

 ### Chapter 771: The Old Academy

As the scorching summer approached, the old locust tree that once provided a cool shade had vanished. The iron well had been sealed off by private owners, leaving the elderly unable to quench their thirst with the sweet well water they cherished. The divine grave was quieter without the chirping of crickets, and the old porcelain mountain, which creaked underfoot, was no longer accessible. Fortunately, the peach blossoms in Peach Leaf Alley still bloomed in vibrant shades of deep and light red.

Life is marked by gatherings and partings, yet there is comfort in both.

At the old academy today, many returnees who had left home were gathering once more.

Li Huai, Lin Shouyi, Dong Shuijing, and Shi Chunjia had arranged to visit the academy together before heading back to the college. There was little to discuss; they simply wanted to take a look around and sit for a while.

Dong Shuijing had asked someone to retrieve the key from the county office's clerk, allowing them to unlock the door. Those unfamiliar with Dong Shuijing’s abilities wouldn’t recognize the name "Dong Bancheng," but his sticky rice wine had already found its way to the capital of the Great Li Dynasty, becoming a source of considerable wealth. It was said even the fairy boats, which flitted like sparrows among the clouds, would carry this wine, a clear sign of its popularity.

The four friends had once studied here together. Li Huai and Dong Shuijing carried buckets and cloths from Li Huai's ancestral home, while Shi Chunjia held a basket filled with their supplies. Lin Shouyi, a wealthy young master back in the day, had little opportunity to engage in such tasks, so when he offered to fetch water, Dong Shuijing chuckled and suggested they go to a nearby well he knew better.

With his hands empty, Lin Shouyi fell into easy conversation with Shi Chunjia.

Both their families had relocated to the capital, with Lin Shouyi’s father having been promoted to a court official, while Shi’s family was merely affluent. To the locals, they were seen as country bumpkins from afar, carrying the scent of mud with them. The Shi family had faced many business setbacks in the past and struggled to find anyone who would listen to their grievances. Shi Chunjia had previously joked about this when they were in Qilong Alley, but now, with just Lin Shouyi around, she opened up, teasing and lamenting about how her family had run into trouble in the capital. They had sought help from Lin Shouyi’s father, only to be met with indifference. It had ended up being just a tea visit, with Lin Shouyi’s father clearly unwilling to assist.

Now married, Shi Chunjia was no longer the carefree girl she once was, but she still valued her friendship with Lin Shouyi. How their parents interacted was a matter of the past; she had left the academy and become a wife and mother, cherishing her formative years even more.

Being able to vent her frustrations was a sign that she held no resentment in her heart.

Lin Shouyi didn't hide anything about his family, sharing, “You know what kind of man my father is and how my family is doing. Who dared to visit my home when we were classmates? Did you see how many times Bao Ping came over?”

The Lin family had always been peculiar in their interactions, preferring not to engage with outsiders. Lin Shouyi’s father, who worked at the construction office, was a completely different person at home—silent and stern. He was strict with Lin Shouyi, almost harsh. While he was well-regarded in his job, having good relationships with several construction officials, at home he came across as somewhat cold and unfeeling.

When Lin Shouyi was away studying at the Dashi Academy, the letters from home were always succinct, almost like accounts being settled.

No matter how well-known Lin Shouyi had become in the Great Li Dynasty, with a large reputation even in the capital, his father never acknowledged him, never once writing to ask him to come home for a visit.

Shi Chunjia recalled something and teased, “Lin Shouyi, even my friends have heard of you! You’ve made quite a name for yourself to be known in the capital. They say you could become a sage of the academy or even a refined immortal on a mountain, especially with such good looks…” 

As she spoke, Shi Chunjia turned to examine Lin Shouyi in his blue robe. “Wow, you really are handsome! I never noticed before; you always had that serious expression like a little scholar, which wasn’t charming at all.”

Lin Shouyi replied, “You should say that in front of Bian Wenmo.”

Shi Chunjia laughed, “I didn’t say you were more handsome than my husband!”

Lin Shouyi shook his head, choosing not to comment further.

Shi Chunjia sighed, “Back then, you and Li Huai always had the latest books. After a year, not much changed. Li Huai was too lazy to read; he would fall asleep as soon as he opened a book, while you were the most careful with yours.”

Lin Shouyi chuckled, “You still remember those little things?”

Shi Chunjia countered, “If I don’t remember these, what else should I remember?”

Lin Shouyi nodded, “It’s a good habit.”

After a moment of hesitation, he said, “If something comes up in the capital, I will seek Bian Wenmo’s help.”

Shi Chunjia was taken aback and then burst into laughter, pointing at Lin Shouyi, “You’ve always been the quiet one, yet you’re so indirect!”

Lin Shouyi didn’t need to rely on Bian Wenmo. This inclination to help others and build bridges was perhaps Lin Shouyi’s unique kindness.

At the academy, Li Huai was busy cleaning while loudly reciting the beginning of a family instruction text, “Rise at dawn, sweep the courtyard!”

Recalling the past, every morning, Mr. Qi would start cleaning the academy early, always doing it himself without letting the servant Zhao Yao do it.

Dong Shuijing chimed in with a smile, “To keep both inside and outside tidy.”

Shi Chunjia was wiping the table and raised the cloth in her hand, saying, “And when night falls, lock the doors.”

From a distance, Lin Shouyi smiled, “I must check everything personally.”

As he carefully wiped the window bars, he thought about studying in the mountains and cultivating his heart and character; it was all interconnected.

Shi Chunjia’s husband, Bian Wenmo, had also returned to Hua Huang County. As the town was both the county and government seat, Bian Wenmo needed to pay a visit to the county magistrate, Fu Yu.

Fu Yu was also of respectable lineage from the capital. The Bian and Fu families had some ancestral ties, both being part of the noble class of the Great Li Dynasty, though the Bian family was still somewhat lesser in status compared to the Fu family. However, the Fu family didn’t share the same level of prestige as the likes of the Cao and Yuan families. Fu Yu had once served as the secretary for the first county magistrate of Longquan, Wu Yuan, and was quite low-key.

After Longquan County was elevated to Longzhou, it governed the districts of Qingci, Baoxi, Sanjiang, and Xianghuo. The magistrate of Yuan County was promoted from within Qingci, while the other three magistrates were all from the capital, hailing from various noble and humble backgrounds. Baoxi County, however, was under Fu Yu’s jurisdiction.

While Bian Wenmo was willing to offer his greetings at the Baoxi County magistrate’s office, he dared not visit the Qingci office due to the weight of the prestigious families.

In fact, although Fu Yu held a position equal to the scion of the Yuan family, both were county magistrates, every time they went to the governor's mansion in the state capital for discussions, neither Fu Yu nor the governor Wei Li found it easy dealing with the Yuan magistrate.

This was not only due to the Yuan family’s background but also to the personal conduct and governance style of the Yuan magistrate.

Yu Lu and Xie Xie had first visited the ancestral home of the Yuan family before heading to the academy, selecting two empty seats.

Both had previously been students at the old Shanyan Academy of the Great Li Dynasty, but they weren’t as close to Mr. Qi as Li Huai and the others. As the remnants of the Lu family, they had only met Cui Dongshan and never had the opportunity to meet Mr. Qi, the founder of the academy and the town’s school.

Coincidentally, Song Jixin and his maid Zhi Gui were also revisiting the old grounds today. They didn’t sit in the academy classroom; apart from Zhao Yao, Song Jixin hardly interacted with Lin Shouyi and the others. Instead, he took Zhi Gui to the backyard, sitting at the stone table where Mr. Qi had taught him and Zhao Yao how to play chess, while Zhi Gui stood outside the north gate as usual.

Song Jixin’s expression was melancholic as he brushed his hand across the table’s surface.

He wondered if Zhao Yao, who had finally lost to him in chess, was doing well in distant lands.

Turning his head, he looked at Zhi Gui, who was idly bending a willow branch.

She stood on tiptoe, gently swaying the branch.

As he gazed at her lovely profile, he couldn’t bring himself to feel anger or resentment; he simply cherished the moment.

She turned her head and seemed to have completely forgotten the candidness of that day, returning to being his devoted maid. Letting go of the branch, she smiled sweetly, “Young Master, are you thinking of playing chess?”

Song Jixin shook his head slightly.

Besides Li Huai and Song Jixin, two unexpected figures from the officialdom arrived at the academy.

The diligent and pragmatic Yuan magistrate and the carefree Cao construction official.

Neither brought attendants—one was intentionally solitary, and the other simply had none.

In fact, both of them were contemporaries from the noble families and had once studied at the old Shanyan Academy of the Great Li Dynasty.

However, like the exiled prince Yu Lu, they had never seen Mr. Qi in person and had never heard his teachings.

Cao construction official leaned against the window, with a bright red wine gourd at his waist. It was made of ordinary material, but having spent many years in the town, it had become polished and cherished—his beloved item, worth its weight in gold.

Seeing the magistrate in a blue robe instead of official garments, Cao construction official exclaimed, “Yuan magistrate, you’re quite the busy person! Always spinning around like a top, never leaving your feet to rest on a chair! Don’t you get dizzy? How many important matters get delayed because of your trips to Hua Huang County?”

Yuan magistrate’s expression remained indifferent. “Talking to you is the real waste of time.”

The Yuan and Cao families of the Great Li Dynasty were the most reputable among the noble families on Baoping Continent. The reason was simple: the ancestral guardians depicted on the door gods were half of their ancestors. In the Huai Huang County, the old porcelain mountain’s Confucian temple and the divine grave’s martial temple also had their ancestors represented as golden statues, enjoying worship.

Cao construction official took a sip from his wine gourd, squinting as though every drink was a moment of fulfillment in life.

Standing tall and straight, Yuan magistrate contrasted starkly with the relaxed Cao construction official. This well-regarded member of the Yuan family remarked, “I wonder if the ever-courteous Yuan magistrate bows down and prostrates himself before the portraits of his ancestors every time he passes.”

Cao construction official was famously down-to-earth, fond of drinking—not excessive but rather savoring small sips, making it seem as though he was always drinking. His life seemed to revolve around purchasing wine, stopping to chat and joke with anyone along the way.

Fortunately, the office was located in the town, a tranquil place that didn’t attract scrutiny from higher authorities. Although nominally under the Ministry of Rites, the Ministry of Personnel in the capital had no power over it. In reality, everyone in the Great Li Dynasty’s officialdom knew just how little oversight the Ministry of Rites had concerning the Longquan pottery industry.

Cao construction official had specifically instructed his assistants to write “good” or “extremely good” for all evaluations of officials and clerks in the office. If someone only received a “good” rating, sending them good wine was essential; otherwise, their rating wouldn’t remain as favorable the following year.

The rules of the pottery office were straightforward: easy to manage, making it so all officials, whether from the noble or humble backgrounds, would be left aghast and eventually pleased, realizing they had found a chief who was easy to deal with. Finding someone of such character was rare.

Cao construction official had long since become adept at speaking the local dialect of the town, and whenever he spoke in the official tongue of the Great Li Dynasty, he felt out of place.

Shooting a sidelong glance at the familiar figure of his peer, he quipped, “I wonder if the ever-polite Yuan magistrate kneels and bows to the portraits of his ancestors every time he sees them.”

Had they not come to this town for their official duties, as a starting point in their careers, Yuan Zhengding would have never exchanged a single word with the laid-back Cao Gengxin, and Cao Gengxin would have likely initiated a conversation with Yuan Zhengding, but it would never have been so “subtle.”

Yuan Zhengding paused for a moment, “If you’re so unfocused, will you have the face to go to Chier Street in the future?”

Cao Gengxin swayed the wine gourd in his hand, chuckling, “Using your face to walk, eh? That’s quite the humorous remark, Yuan Daren! Next time someone in the capital dares to say your only flaw is your lack of humor, I’ll give them two slaps across the face.”

Yuan Zhengding pressed onward, “Do you still remember Guan Yiran and Liu Xunmei? If I recall correctly, those two young lads used to follow you around when we were younger.”

Although those two had not risen to high positions, they were now on equal footing with Yuan Zhengding and Cao Gengxin. The key point was that their political fortunes had taken a turn.

That was the conversion of civil and military identities.

Cao Gengxin smiled, “Yuan Daren, since you don’t recognize me, don’t presume to know who I am.”

Feigning surprise, Yuan Zhengding replied, “Oh? May I ask who you are?”

Cao Gengxin took a sip of wine and said, “When I’m sober, I’m Cao Jiu Gui; when I’m drunk, I’m Cao Da Jiu Xian.”

Yuan Zhengding chuckled, “Indeed, that’s a time-waster.”

Cao Gengxin shook his head, “I came to see Mr. Qi’s direct disciples, especially to ask Brother Dong for some sticky rice wine that doesn’t require credit. You, Yuan Daren, are here to curry favor with the prince; the difference is clear. I’m just a muddy figure in a filthy alley, while you are the shining copper mirror hanging above the door, upright and dignified.”

Yuan Zhengding frowned, “After all these years, have you only learned to talk?”

Cao Gengxin countered, “Have you learned anything yourself?”

Yuan Zhengding’s tone grew serious, “This isn’t a trivial matter!”

Cao Gengxin, holding the small gourd of wine, clasped his hands in a gesture of humility, “Yuan Daren, you just focus on your own rise and don’t worry about whether I’m making progress or not.”

Yuan Zhengding sighed inwardly.

He disliked this man’s style, but deep down, he still hoped this member of the Cao family could take his career a bit more seriously.

Of course, Yuan Zhengding primarily thought of himself.

In any case, whether in officialdom, literature, or the martial world, the affairs of the world are strange; all those who enjoy the spectacle love to see rivals of equal stature, willing to pay more attention to the conflict. If someone rides ahead alone, it might not be a good thing.

The responsibilities of the pottery office were quite significant.

Yuan Zhengding felt envious.

They were responsible for preventing theft and could even catch thieves themselves.

In the town, the four major clans—Song, Zhao, Lu, Li, Chen, and Shi—were all under the purview of the supervisory office, which ostensibly only monitored the production of imperial porcelain. In reality, it held authority over nearly everything, from the Yang family shop to the peaks of Mount Bei Yue, from Lin Lu Academy to the Longquan Sword Sect, and even to the various temples and shrines across the town, including the City God Temple and the Iron Talisman River.

Even practitioners of the Dao with the peace of mind plaques could be inspected by the Cao construction official, for the Ministry of Justice or the Ministry of Rites of the Great Li Dynasty wouldn’t dare question it.

However, this appointed construction official seemed to have chosen not to bother with anything at all.

Yuan Zhengding felt both pleased and worried. He was happy that his neighbor, who would have been a future rival in the Great Li court, was so ineffectual. Yet he was concerned about the ambitious young emperor, who might one day lose patience with Cao Gengxin and simply replace him with someone else. If Yuan Zhengding were to be promoted to the governor of Longzhou in the future, he might find himself tied down.

After all, the lessons of the past were clear: the new construction official would not be easy to deal with.

Not far from the academy.

Ma Kuxuan stood with his maid, Shu Dian.

They exchanged glances with Cao Gengxin and Yuan Zhengding, but neither party seemed inclined to greet the other. They were never on the same path.

Ma Kuxuan remarked, “My grandmother loved to scold people when she was alive, always doing it to their faces—never daring to do it behind their backs. Among those she knew, there were only three people she wouldn’t scold. Mr. Qi from the academy was one of them. My grandmother said Mr. Qi was genuinely a good person.”

Ma Kuxuan smirked, crossing his arms and reclining against a yellow mud wall. “In my hometown, we speak our minds freely.”

Ma Kuxuan chuckled and then said something strange: “When the back is there, it’s okay.”

Shu Dian didn’t understand at all; it was probably a local saying.

She only noticed that the town dialect was quite flat and lacked intonation.

Ma Kuxuan, rarely engaging in harmless conversation, explained with a smile, “It means that when you hear what others say, it’s like carrying a burden—can you bear its weight?”

A young man from the Mud Bottle Alley, passing by Chen Ping’an’s ancestral home, paused for a long time.

Gu Can had initially planned to head straight to the state capital but, after some thought, decided to head toward the academy.

Meanwhile, at the ferry crossing of Niu Jiao Mountain, a tall man who had returned home after leaving for a long time disembarked from a cross-continental ferry heading to the North Ju Lu Continent.

Ruan Xiu smiled and greeted, “Hello, Liu Xianyang.”

Liu Xianyang walked briskly towards her, beaming, “Ruan girl!”

Ruan Xiu nodded and tossed him a sword token, which allowed him to travel freely across Longzhou.

In fact, in just a few years, Liu Xianyang would become a direct disciple at the Longquan Sword Sect.

He was merely borrowing time from the Chen family of the South Posa Continent for twenty years.

After receiving the sword token, Liu Xianyang bid farewell and immediately soared back to his ancestral home, then visited a nearby tomb before finally returning to the town.

At the entrance of Mud Bottle Alley, he ran into Gu Can.

Gu Can didn’t retaliate.

A woman dressed in red, leaping through the clouds, reconsidered her plans. After calculating the time, she decided against heading to the Great Li capital and instead took a detour back to her hometown.

Looking down, she landed near the academy.

Having visited the Qilong Alley for some festive pastries, Ruan Xiu was also on her way to the academy.

Thus, the already bustling academy became even more crowded.

Bian Wenmo left the magistrate’s office and rode his horse-drawn carriage to a street near the academy. He lifted the curtain of the carriage and was surprised to see Cao construction official and Yuan magistrate standing together.

Weighing the pros and cons, he decided it was unnecessary to make formal greetings since both young nobles were present. He dropped the curtain and instructed the coachman to move the carriage elsewhere.

As for the others near the academy, Bian Wenmo either recognized them or had dealings with them before, or they were strangers he had no interest in.

He simply waited for Shi Chunjia to leave the small academy so they could head back to the Great Li capital together.

A frail-looking scholar had a change of heart, taking his brother Long Bo along, and carefully strolled around the town.

Attracted by the “commotion” at the academy, Liu Chicheng gritted his teeth and silently told himself he was just here to take a look, not to stir up trouble. In this little place, if some random brat were to jump up and slap him in the face, he’d still be forced to smile back!

Thus, Liu Chicheng and Long Bo found themselves witnessing a scene at the academy.

Almost everyone began to disperse from the academy at the same time, so at one moment, all of them fell into the view of the pedestrians on the street.

There was Ruan Xiu, with her ponytail and blue attire.

Li Baoping in her red cotton jacket.

Li Huai, Lin Shouyi, Dong Shuijing.

Yu Lu, Xie Xie.

Ma Kuxuan.

Song Jixin with Zhi Gui.

Liu Xianyang and Gu Can.

Those figures caught glimpses of Liu Chicheng, who stood by the roadside.

Especially Gu Can, who wore a playful smile.

Liu Chicheng felt a chill run down his spine, regretting his decision to come. He should never have come here. If the place were deserted, he would have slapped Long Bo across the face by now! How could he not advise him on how to be a good friend?

Without the cultivation of the elder, his vision was still sharp, but he felt even more suffocated than Liu Chicheng. He thought, “With my life in ruins, what’s the harm in it?”

Liu Chicheng humbly asked, “Long Bo, how long do you think you could survive here if you were to make a living?”

Long Bo was at a loss for words.

But as those people moved further away from the academy and closer to the street, Long Bo felt increasingly suffocated.

Liu Chicheng stopped holding back and smiled at Long Bo, “Did you know, I’m a close friend of Chen Ping’an?!”

Long Bo thought for a moment and nodded, “So am I.”

(End of Chapter)

 ### Chapter 772: Another Bowl of Spring Noodles

Inside the Yang Family Shop, the atmosphere felt unusually tranquil. Li Er, Zheng Dafu, Su Dian, and Shi Ling Mountain—these disciples had all set off on their journeys one after another. Old Yang was enjoying his quiet time, while Yang Shu stood guard at the front of the shop, a lad who couldn’t understand human speech. Old Yang couldn’t be bothered to say a word more to him. Of course, Yang Shu also had no desire to be associated with that old man. That stubborn turtle truly thought of himself as important! If it weren't for the old Yang family's sentimental ties, the shop would have barely made a profit throughout the year given its lackluster business. If it were up to Yang Shu to run things, he would have already counted the accounts properly.

Just then, Wei Ban and Ruan Qiong arrived almost simultaneously.

One was the Mountain Lord of North Peak, and the other a local sage, both arriving quietly.

Ruan Qiong was more casual, sitting on the long bench under the eaves, sipping on some wine. This time, he had brought back some fine liquor from his home, which he usually wouldn’t splurge on. 

Wei Ban stood beside the bench, his expression serious.

This long bench had hosted many saints in the past.

Old Yang was seated on the steps outside the main house, shrouded in white mist.

Ruan Qiong put away his wine flask and got straight to the point: “If Xiuxiu hadn’t gone to the school, I wouldn’t have come.”

Old Yang chuckled, “I can’t control her. Ruan Qiong, this is your own fault.”

Ruan Qiong nodded. Having received that answer, as long as it wasn’t Old Yang’s scheme, that was enough. 

However, Wei Ban felt increasingly heavy-hearted. Without Ruan Qiong as a natural ally, this little Mountain Lord had a lot of pressure on him.

To be honest, dealing with this old predecessor was never easy for anyone.

Old Yang tapped his smoking pipe against the steps and said, “The Lord of Baidi City is in the capital of Dali, watching over this place. He might visit at any moment.”

Ruan Qiong frowned deeply.

Wei Ban asked, “What about the National Teacher?”

Old Yang laughed, “If you could guess the intentions of that embroidered tiger, would you really find it easier to do things as a Mountain Lord in the future? I doubt it. Since that’s the case, why think too much?”

Back when Lyzhu Cave Heaven was shattered, numerous opportunities scattered, following people like pieces of broken porcelain falling from a table, landing in all directions.

The biggest five shares of fortune were associated with Ruan Qiong’s only daughter, Ruan Xiu, and the fire dragon bracelet on her wrist.

Gu Can had once asked for a little loach from Chen Ping’an, which he kept in his own water jar. After Liu Zhimiao took it away from the small town, the loach feasted in Shujian Lake and transformed into human form, naming itself Tan Xue.

In the company of Song Jixin and his maid Zhi Gui, there was a four-legged snake with horns on its forehead.

Prince Gao Xuan of the Great Sui bought a golden carp from Li Er, receiving a second one as a bonus, along with a high-ranking Dragon King basket.

Lastly, Zhao Yao, who left the small town early riding an ox cart, was Qīng Jìngchūn’s attendant. Besides that wooden dragon, the young man had also secretly hidden a spring seal as a parting gift from his master.

On the surface, only Zhao Yao was missing from his hometown.

However, Cui Zhan’s arrangements had ensured there would be no such oversight.

The Gao clan of the Great Sui and the Song clan of Dali signed a mountain alliance, a strategic move. As a hostage, Gao Xuan had been learning at the Piyun Mountain Deer Academy for years under the protection of the Gao family's ancestors. The golden carp had been nurtured in the mountain streams for years, and it was clear that the Dali court had secretly instructed the River Dragon and the Iron Symbol River, along with the three mountain gods including Song Yuzhang, not to disclose this matter.

Shujian Lake was another game in motion. Gu Can was at the center of it, while Ruan Xiu followed the Dali alchemist southward, chasing after a young man who was exceptionally fortunate but had been taken away from Dali’s martial realm. Ruan Xiu almost got involved herself. After the upheaval at Shujian Lake, Gu Can’s mother was terrified and chose to move back to her hometown. Eventually, she settled in the state capital, leading a prosperous life again for three reasons: Chen Ping’an’s suggestion, Gu Can’s agreement, and her own lingering fears from the events at Shujian Lake. 

Furthermore, after Gu Can’s father died and became a deity, he first accumulated merit in the haunted mansion of the bride ghost before being promoted to a renowned mountain god of the old Dali peaks. Once they returned to their hometown, life would be much more stable. 

Gu Can hoped her mother would stay away from trouble, and deep down, she couldn’t trust her master Liu Zhimiao, the chief offering of the True Realm Sect.

As for Song Jixin, when did he ever leave the chessboard? When was he not a pawn?

And Zhao Yao, how could he be an exception, truly escaping Cui Zhan’s schemes?

Ruan Qiong departed.

Wei Ban, however, was still reluctant to return to Piyun Mountain just like that.

This gathering felt too sudden and strange. Now that the young Mountain Lord was traveling far along the Sword Qi Great Wall, Zheng Dafu was also absent from Luopok Mountain. Wei Ban was worried that Zheng Dafu might change his mind and not head to the Lotus Root Blessed Land. All of this was this old predecessor's careful planning. Now, the mainstay of Luopok Mountain seemed to rest solely on Zhu Lian. In the Grand Master’s Hall on the Jise Peak, he would always be a guest without a seat.

Old Yang chuckled, “Wei Mountain Lord, why go to such lengths to repay that favor from years ago?”

Wei Ban forced a smile, “I must trouble the old predecessor to speak frankly. This matter is not targeted at Luopok Mountain, and if that’s the case, I won’t disturb your peace any further.”

Old Yang pondered, “There are some connections, but it isn’t directly aimed at Luopok Mountain. Cui Zhan has no need for that, and besides, you don’t trust Cui Zhan; you should at least trust Cui Dongshan.”

Wei Ban looked helpless; he truly didn’t trust that eccentric young man in white.

Old Yang concluded, “You should trust the three portraits hanging in the Grand Master’s Hall of Jise Peak, right?”

Wei Ban suddenly felt reassured, clarity washing over him, and he bowed in thanks.

Old Yang said, “Living amidst mountains and rivers, one seems like a carefree immortal, yet the clouds and water are mere illusions. Wei Mountain Lord, you cannot be blind to this.”

Wei Ban cupped his fists and smiled, “The beautiful scenery of the mortal world is both an illusion and a delight to the eyes. One cannot take advantage and then act coy.”

Old Yang laughed, “Wei Mountain Lord has a good temperament, quite relaxed indeed.”

Wei Ban felt somewhat at ease and took his leave.

Old Yang muttered to himself, “A good exchange of favors; borrowing again isn’t difficult.”

Everything—Cui Zhan’s plans—was to help Zhi Gui obtain a complete true dragon fortune in a manner deemed “justifiable,” without giving the saints from the Three Teachings any room to criticize.

Song Jixin held deep feelings for this maid who had been by his side, and he would surely be willing to pay dearly for the fortune of a mere four-legged snake. 

Ruan Xiu wouldn’t care about the gains or losses of a fire dragon. If she could do something for the Longquan Sword Sect, she would do it without hesitation.

After rapidly growing in Shujian Lake, Gu Can understood the true power of rules and naturally learned how to do business. After all, her parents’ future fates remained Gu Can’s soft spot.

Prince Gao Xuan had studied for many years at the Lin Deer Academy of Dali, and for the sake of the Gao clan’s country and territory, even surrendering a golden carp would feel like a knife to the heart, yet he would do it without hesitation.

As for Zhao Yao, if he couldn’t even keep that spring seal safe back then, how could he safeguard that wooden dragon now? It wouldn’t be easy.

Among the younger generation in the small town, the only one truly distanced from the chessboard was Chen Ping’an—not merely because he was far away at the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Yet, Cui Zhan had the ability to pull Chen Ping’an back into the game, provided Chen Ping’an had a chance to return to his hometown.

But it remained uncertain whether, at that time, Chen Ping’an would be a pawn or the player.

Or perhaps, would he simply replace Cui Zhan?

In front of the pharmacy, Yang Shu saw an old scholar step over the threshold. Yang Shu smiled and asked, “Are you here to see a doctor or to buy some herbs? Did you bring a prescription?”

With such good manners, how well could the Yang Family Shop be doing?

The old man didn’t mind and chuckled, “I can save myself if I’m sick; just looking around.”

Yang Shu was a bit displeased and casually replied, “Herbs are already precious. Nowadays, it’s getting more difficult to gather them from the mountains. Customers are free to browse but shouldn’t go rummaging.”

The old scholar nodded.

He looked around and intended to head towards the backyard.

Yang Shu grew anxious; this old fellow was truly not being polite.

Unexpectedly, in a flash, the old scholar lifted the curtain and headed into the backyard. Yang Shu hesitated, grumbling a few words internally, thinking it would be better to quarrel with Old Yang. Both old geezers, one wouldn’t earn money, the other didn’t want to spend it—old arms and legs, best to be hurt for a hundred days.

Old Yang chuckled, “A rare guest.”

Cui Zhan stood nearby the long bench, not taking a seat, and smiled, “Since I’m a guest, all I can do is try to be less of an eyesore here.”

Old Yang said, “You seem to believe that Chen Ping’an can’t return to Baopingzhou for the time being, making it impossible for him to give that girl a finishing touch, so Dali has no choice but to take a step back and play a trump card?”

Cui Zhan nodded, “It’s a minor issue.”

The contract signed between Wang Zhu and Chen Ping’an back then was quite unstable. If Chen Ping’an’s luck ran out and he died midway, while Wang Zhu would lose her restraints, making it possible for her to re-sign a contract with Song Jixin, she would suffer considerable losses in fate during that transition. Thus, in those years, with her intelligence not fully awakened, Wang Zhu’s actions regarding Chen Ping’an’s life and death were often contradictory. For the greater scheme, she hoped Chen Ping’an would thrive. If one prospered, all prospered. Yet, being neighbors in Mud Bottle Alley meant they spent day and night together, and Wang Zhu, driven by her innate nature, secretly hoped for Chen Ping’an’s demise to solidify her resolve to capture Dali’s dragon vein and the Song clan’s national fortune.

She had been caught in this dilemma for many years, not daring to act recklessly and kill Chen Ping’an, fearing the saint’s suppression, yet unwilling to waste time with someone whose destiny was already broken. She also didn’t want to beg for mercy from heaven. The relationship between Song Jixin and Chen Ping’an, two peers, became a tangled mess. At the moment Chen Ping’an’s longevity bridge was severed, Wang Zhu had already harbored murderous intent, and thus the deal between Song Jixin and Fu Nanhua was secretly laced with danger.

But what happened later was overwhelming, causing Wang Zhu to retract significantly, no longer daring to act lightly.

To make a true dragon’s heart compassionate and empathetic to others was akin to demanding the emperor of Dali to become a moral paragon.

However, both Ruan Qiong and Wei Ban, who had visited earlier, seemed not to see the deeper implications.

The momentum had arrived; opportunities must not be missed. Cui Zhan had to make Wang Zhu condense the true dragon fortune in advance, seeking to restore her peak.

Yet, Cui Zhan’s arrangement for everyone to gather at the small town school was certainly not limited to this.

Old Yang grinned, “As a guest, you should be courteous. As a host, treat your guests kindly. Such a neighbor is indeed a blessing.”

Cui Zhan replied, “According to our agreement, as long as I live, I won’t allow the conflict of fire and water to repeat in this vast world.”

Old Yang asked, “What if you die? Does Cui Dongshan count as you? Will our agreement still stand?”

Cui Zhan chuckled, “You’ll have to ask him about that.”

Old Yang clicked his tongue, “When scholars dive wholeheartedly into business, they truly become more and more astute.”

Cui Zhan said, “I hope the old predecessor will also keep your promises.”

Old Yang nodded, “Of course, fair business has always been my principle.”

Ruan Xiu was born in the Wind and Snow Temple but followed her father to Lyzhu Cave Heaven to cultivate.

Li Liusheng was in Lyzhu Cave Heaven but followed his parents on a journey to Beiju Lu Island’s Lion Peak.

They occasionally crossed paths but would never remain neighbors for long.

Ruan Xiu looked around.

There was Li Baoping, who shared a mutual affinity, Pei Qian, the first disciple of Luopok Mountain, Liu Xianyang of the Longquan Sword Sect, and Gu Can, who had very few friends left in Mud Bottle Alley.

By Li Liusheng’s side was his younger brother Li Huai. Zhi Gui, the true dragon, naturally had an innate affinity with the Dao, so Song Jixin’s choice of camp was very clear. Ma Kuxuan, who was willing to follow Zhi Gui, was also influenced by his grandmother, who had been promoted to a river deity from the River Dragon.

She Lin Shouyi, and the swordsman Dong Shui Jing, both liked Li Liusheng.

Once major issues arose, the two temporarily nascent camps would have their own concerns. If every little matter accumulates, who could remain uninvolved in the end?

That would require someone willing to reason and capable of winning over both sides.

Chen Ping’an.

Cui Zhan’s chess moves didn’t treat those pieces as mere puppets. He had never thought that the lives and deaths of mortals were all in his hands, manipulating their fates like a game. Instead, it was necessary to quietly pave the way for those pieces, ensuring that their paths, though winding, could ultimately appear at key positions when needed.

If he sought the path of eternal life, Cui Zhan would not have betrayed the Confucian lineage.

If he desired power, becoming the Grand Master of the Academy and the Deputy Leader of the Central Plains Confucian Temple was within easy reach, and what difficulty would that pose?

Old Yang exhaled smoke, enveloping the pharmacy, and asked, “What about that matter?”

Cui Zhan rarely showed a hint of helplessness, “Not trusting others means that others also cannot bear this matter. It’s best to separate our souls; I will quietly observe Cui Dongshan. In a day, his thoughts can range from at least two to as many as seventy thousand. If I observe quietly, I’ll have at least three thoughts, and at most eighty thousand. We both have our strengths and weaknesses.”

Old Yang asked, “Have you sorted out those fundamental connections?”

Cui Zhan shook his head, “There’s considerable contention. The three levels of transformation and conversion have fundamental disagreements between us, almost entirely reversed in order, which is quite troublesome.”

Old Yang laughed and asked, “Why have you been deliberately avoiding asking me?”

Cui Zhan smiled, “In terms of age and realm, you’re the senior, and I’m the junior. But when it comes to calculations, we’re equals.”

Old Yang shook his head, “No need to be humble; you are the senior.”

Cui Zhan cupped his fists and smiled, “I dare not be too bold; I fear receiving this.”

Polite words; the Confucian lineage, from the teacher to the disciple to the passing disciple, all seemed quite adept at this.

Old Yang chuckled in amusement, fell silent for a moment, then sighed, “The old scholar has great insight in choosing disciples. The first disciple’s arrangements shine like stars, mastering sword techniques, like a nearly full moon hanging in the sky. Qi Jingchun’s knowledge is the highest, yet he remains grounded, safeguarding the mortal realm.”

Shujian Lake’s True Realm Sect is intertwined with the Yuguizong of Tongye Island.

The crossing ships of the Ghostly Sea Sect have made significant business.

The Mohist patriarch, the merchant clan’s ancestor, along with many still hidden behind the scenes, have all been invited to the gambling table by Cui Zhan. Now, even the Lord of Baidi City has graced Baopingzhou with his presence.

Cui Zhan sat on the long bench, gently resting his hands on his knees, self-mockingly saying, “Even the next game doesn’t seem promising.”

Old Yang laughed, “Cultivating for longevity is precious, while learning and knowledge despise destiny.”

Cui Zhan smiled, “Your words, old predecessor, bring great comfort to my heart.”

Liu Chicheng took Longbo along to accompany Gu Can on a trip to the state capital.

Now, Huai Huang County was well-connected, with numerous large and small roads.

Once the young people from the school dispersed, each heading home, the overwhelming pressure in Bai Fu’s heart suddenly decreased, leaving it hard to articulate.

Liu Chicheng keenly sensed Bai Fu’s change in mood and patted the shoulder of the white-haired youth, “Longbo, I didn’t expect you to have such wisdom; the Dao is promising!”

Bai Fu replied earnestly, “Thank you for your kind words, senior.”

Shi Chunjia boarded the carriage with her husband, Bian Wenmao, heading back to the capital of Dali. Li Baoping said she would find a horse to ride and would soon catch up to the carriage.

Li Huai, Lin Shouyi, and the others planned to return to the Great Sui Academy with Mao Xiaodong.

Cao Gengxin and Dong Shui Jing had made plans to drink at Huang Erniang’s tavern.

Governor Yuan Zhengding accompanied Song Jixin and the maid Zhi Gui, finding an excuse to go to the Old Porcelain Mountain to pay respects.

Ma Kuxuan took a few people to visit the Divine Immortal Tomb’s War Temple.

Liu Xianyang followed Ruan Xiu to the Longquan Sword Sect’s peak. As he wasn’t a direct disciple, he naturally did not need to go to the Grand Master’s Hall to light incense. He was merely there to take a stroll. However, Liu Xianyang mentioned he wanted to stop by Luopok Mountain first, and Ruan Xiu seemed to have been waiting for this suggestion. She proposed they could head to the Longquan Sword Sect first and then go to Luopok Mountain, which Liu Xianyang found reasonable.

Then, the two travelers on the wind saw Li Baoping walking toward the mountains.

The foreign youth from the Sword Qi Great Wall, Zhang Jiazheng, and Jiang Qu, under the secret escort of the sword cultivator Cui Wei, ascended Luopok Mountain.

The housekeeper Zhu Lian had previously mentioned wanting the two to help at the Dragon Alley New Year shop. After Zhang Jiazheng and Jiang Qu discussed it, they thought it would be better to come here first to ask Old Zhu about some important matters.

Cui Wei actually had his own calculations and needed to obtain Zhu Lian’s consent.

Pei Qian happened to return from the Lotus Root Blessed Land with Xiao Mi Li and was delighted to see Zhang Jiazheng and Jiang Qu.

At the very least, she didn’t have to bother with Chen Nuanshu, who had a bag full of seeds. She had to entertain the two boys, who could be considered family.

Xiao Mi Li, clever as always, had previously been scolded by Nuanshu for buying too many seeds at high prices. Yet, she didn’t complain, pretending to be loyal and silent, but she kept glancing at Pei Qian. What was that supposed to mean?

Yuan had previously interacted with Zhang Jiazheng and Jiang Qu and had a good relationship, so they climbed the mountain together.

As for the silly Yuanbao, he was probably busy sparring with the silly Cen Yuankai at the mountaintop.

Li Baoping had come to Luopok Mountain to borrow that horse, which her junior uncle had brought back from Shujian Lake and had been raised in Luopok Mountain all these years.

Her junior uncle was always so sentimental.

Pei Qian, upon hearing that Baoping sister had arrived at the mountain gate, immediately rushed over with a child rubbing his ears.

From over a hundred steps away, Pei Qian leaped high, landing gracefully in front of Li Baoping.

Zhou Mi Li, shouldering a small golden burden and holding a hiking stick, imitated her, suddenly stopping, kneeling slightly, and lightly calling out. Unexpectedly, she exerted too much force and ended up tumbling toward the foot of the mountain's gate.

Pei Qian reached out, pulling her back to her side.

The little girl in black swayed unsteadily, laughing heartily.

Seeing Pei Qian, who had jumped over quickly, Li Baoping pinched the young girl’s cheek, then bent down, clapped her hands on Mi Li’s cheeks, lightly twisting them. The little girl’s sparse, slightly yellow eyebrows suddenly became one high and one low, looking quite amusing.

Under Yuan's lead, Zhang Jiazheng and Jiang Qu explored the Mountain God Temple, a shrine with almost no incense offerings.

Cen Yuankai and Yuanbao were indeed sparring in the square, just as Pei Qian had guessed.

The three boys sat side by side on the railing in the distance.

Zhang Jiazheng merely glanced at the two sisters who stood gracefully as they finished their punches.

He turned his gaze towards the overlapping mountains and rivers outside Luopok Mountain, coincidentally spotting a large flock of birds flying by, like a white river suspended in midair, swaying slowly.

While working as a shop assistant at the tavern on the Sword Qi Great Wall, Zhang Jiazheng had once privately asked Teacher Chen a question.

“Your knowledge is vast, Teacher; did you learn it all from the old Confucian master himself?”

The storyteller, who had shared tales of mountains and rivers while holding a bench and bamboo stick, walked alongside the boy in the streets, shaking his head and laughing, “Not quite. In the beginning, there was a school in my hometown; the teacher’s surname was Qi. Teacher Qi said that principles are in books while being a person is outside of books. If you ever have the chance to visit my hometown, you can check out that school. If you truly want to study, there’s also a new school with a learned teacher.”

At that time, Zhang Jiazheng recalled that saying regarding principles and books.

Teacher Chen raised a hand, pointing into the distance, smiling, “For a child who hasn’t read books, hearing this phrase is like... discovering a mountain of gold and silver. The road might be long, but it’s visible. Carrying a firewood axe, a plow, or a basket, one can earn a lot of money! Suddenly, it offers a sense of hope, as if there’s finally a day when they won’t have to worry about food and clothing.”

In truth, many of Teacher Chen’s words unrelated to principles were quietly remembered by the boy.

In the vast world, there were many impoverished families. The so-called good life was merely being able to put up new door gods and spring couplets each year. The so-called wealth meant having enough money to buy numerous door gods and couplets. However, the places where houses could display door gods and couplets were limited; it wasn’t that they didn’t have money, but rather they were envious yet unable to afford them.

When the boy finally arrived in Teacher Chen’s hometown, Teacher Chen remained far away from the boy’s homeland.

On the second floor of the bamboo house.

Li Baoping, along with the young girl Pei Qian and her companions Chen Nuanshu and Zhou Mi Li, leaned over the railing to admire the scenery.

The taller ones didn’t need to stand on tiptoe.

The shortest, Zhou Mi Li, hung over the railing.

It felt like at any moment, they might suddenly see a returning traveler with a hiking stick and a bamboo box.

Then, upon raising their heads, they would smile and wave at them.

Pei Qian quietly asked, “Today the bright moon is over the river, tomorrow the stars will hang over the fields; does that mean Master will return home the day after tomorrow?”

Li Baoping replied, “It seems junior uncle has been busy for others, not resting since the first day he left home. Staying a bit longer at the Sword Qi Great Wall is quite nice; it’s like a break.”

Chen Nuanshu laughed, “I heard there’s also a tavern over there, with seeds and big bowls of spring noodles.”

Zhou Mi Li nodded vigorously, swinging her dangling feet, “Spring noodles are delicious; the bigger the bowl, the better.”

At the tavern on the Sword Qi Great Wall, Chen Ping’an had just returned for the second time, freshly dressed in clean clothes. He sat at a table, ordered a jug of wine, and enjoyed a bowl of spring noodles alone. Although he had told the child not to add scallions, they still ended up putting in a small handful.

The second shopkeeper rarely came here, so while the bowl wasn’t large, the spring noodles were substantial, and it made sense to put in extra scallions.

Feng Kangle and Tao Ban, two children, sat at the adjacent table, watching the second shopkeeper bend over to enjoy his meal.

Chen Ping’an turned his head, raised his empty bowl, and smiled, “Another bowl, please, and remember no scallions this time, no need for them.”

(End of Chapter)

 # Chapter 773: Turning Over the Old Calendar

Gu Can arrived at the entrance of the state city mansion. At the entrance, two imposing white jade lions, crafted by celestial hands, guarded the gates. Even a starving beggar would lack the courage to approach the door for alms in their presence.

Gu Can did not rush to knock on the door.

Liu Chicheng and Chai Bofu could do nothing but stand outside, braving the chilly wind.

Gu Can ascended the spotless steps and reached for the beast-head door knocker. He paused, his fingers lingering for a moment. This was a golden-painted door knocker shaped like a mythical creature, reserved for nobles. Gu Can sighed inwardly; he shouldn't be so presumptuous. Even though there was a peace and prosperity talisman in his home, it shouldn’t be treated lightly. The governor’s mansion of the state city must have received confidential information from the kiln supervision office, which is why they didn’t scrutinize this matter too closely. Still, it was best to inform his mother about it; there was no need to act so extravagantly at the entrance, as it could easily lead to complications.

Gu Can knocked on the door and took a step back. A well-dressed steward opened the door and, seeing Gu Can in plain clothes, frowned and asked, "Which family’s young master are you? Or are you from the government?"

Gu Can was momentarily taken aback, recalling how much his appearance had changed. It was only natural that the steward wouldn’t recognize him, unlike the elders from Qingxia Island. Years ago, his mother had left Shujian Lake with a close maid, and after many years of cultivation, they had all become Qi practitioners, albeit at a low level, and thus would not involve themselves in the household's affairs. Gu Can had detailed their cultivation progress in letters to his mother over the years and had even helped select several treasures from the mountains. They just needed to cultivate step by step, refine their innate items, and break through their limitations.

The steward quickly glanced at the two individuals standing at the bottom of the steps behind the young man—a frail scholar and a young boy with white hair—and immediately assumed he had gauged the background of the three.

The steward himself was a pure martial artist, concealing his true strength. At the fifth realm, he was indeed skilled in the common martial world. In any small vassal state, he could easily establish a sect. Being a steward and guarding the place was beneath him; he was likely either wealthy enough to afford it or a fugitive seeking refuge. The worst-case scenario was that he harbored ulterior motives, scheming to fish for a big catch, colluding with wild cultivators, and coveting the mansion’s considerable wealth. Gu Can had navigated the martial world for many years, witnessing numerous intertwined scams, and had intentionally observed from a distance, witnessing two con games unfold. One family, known for their wealth and lack of compassion, ended up ruined. Gu Can had appeared when the bandits were dividing the spoils, asking them for advice, but they were secretive and evasive. So, he had let Zeng Yi show off his skills and seize knowledge from them. Another family, appearing to have good morals, Gu Can had casually helped out of trouble.

Gu Can smiled and said, "I am Gu Can; this is my home."

The steward’s expression changed instantly. He bowed his head and stepped aside, saying, "I've seen the young master; I'll go report to the lady right away."

Gu Can crossed the threshold and waved his hand, saying, "No need; it’s just a few steps away. You don’t have to trouble yourself to report."

The steward smiled obsequiously, "At first glance, I almost mistook the young master for a gentleman scholar from the academy."

The steward had already figured out the household’s background. The master was a cultivator who had been away for many years, a matter that was vaguely discussed in the mansion, likely something unspeakable. The young master was a seed of the scholarly world studying outside, so only a wealthy woman remained at home. Every time that lady mentioned her son, she was filled with pride. If it weren’t for the two maidservants beside her, who were also practicing Qi, they would have acted long ago to seize this wealth. So, for this year, they had specifically pulled in a friend from the path to focus on one of the maids.

Gu Can chuckled, "Good eye."

Liu Chicheng nodded, "Indeed, very good."

Chai Bofu glanced at the pure martial artist and thought, Poor guy, truly poor. With so many paths to wealth, he ended up stumbling into this family. A den of self-proclaimed clever foxes, blindly jumping into the dragon's den. What were they seeking, if not death?

Liu Chicheng slapped Chai Bofu on the head, saying, "Long Brother, what’s the matter? Why are you so quiet? Do you think our Young Master Gu isn’t worthy of being a gentleman scholar?"

Chai Bofu felt as if he had been struck by lightning. His vital points trembled, and the Dragon Gate realm he had only just stabilized was now in jeopardy! Chai Bofu quickly said, "Young Master Gu is more than worthy!"

Ordinary rascals would usually try to scare someone first before acting, but this particular senior beside him was the type to act first and reason later.

However, having spent enough time together, Chai Bofu's aspiration to follow the path grew firmer. He was determined to become a disciple of the Bai Di City genealogy in Central Continent.

The steward closed the door but suddenly felt a chill at the back of his neck. It turned out Gu Can had reached out and grabbed him by the neck, pressing his head against the door. Gu Can's fingers were already seeping with blood, demonstrating how ruthless he could be, as he quietly asked, "With the door closed, are you not worried about outsiders laughing at you? Speak! How many people are inside? Who is the highest in cultivation?"

Gu Can suddenly released his grip and turned around, smiling as he looked into the distance, exposing his back to the pure martial artist.

A woman rushed over, stumbling several times on her trailing skirt. Upon seeing her son after so many years, tears welled up in her eyes.

Suffering for survival, working hard for wealth, in the end, wasn’t it all for this ungrateful brat who only sent home letters?

Gu Can quickly approached, and the woman embraced her son, choking with sobs. Gu Can gently patted her back, maintaining a calm demeanor as he smiled at the two maidservants, who were adorned in finery and belonged to him.

The two young women exchanged a glance with Gu Can, immediately lowering their heads, their hands and feet turning cold, as if they had fallen into an ice cavern.

The woman released Gu Can, wiped her tears, and began to scrutinize her son. At first, she felt proud, but then she wondered how much hardship her son had endured alone in the outside world. She covered her mouth and began to sob again, blaming herself, resenting her late husband who had inexplicably become a mountain deity, resenting Chen Ping'an for leaving Gu Can behind, killing that charcoal snow, and resenting the heavens for allowing Gu Can to suffer so much.

After Gu Can and his mother reminisced in the main hall, he stepped into his own study for the first time. Liu Chicheng led Long Brother to wander around the mansion, while Gu Can summoned the two maidservants and the steward, who had been too afraid to act.

Gu Can moved a chair to lean against the window, resting an elbow on the armrest and propping his chin in one hand, asking, "A big tree attracts the wind; it’s inevitable. I won’t be too harsh on you two regarding this matter, especially since my mother also has her faults. However, forgetting one’s roots isn’t a good thing. Does my mother know about outsiders sneaking into the mansion to set traps?"

The two maidservants had already knelt on the ground.

One maidservant looked bewildered.

The other maidservant nodded, saying, "I mentioned it to the lady, but she said to treat it as mere boredom."

Gu Can hesitated for a moment and asked, "Did my father arrange any backup plans?"

The maidservant replied in a low voice, "Master is very concerned about the lady's safety. He not only contacted the local city god but also cast spells on the door gods. There is an older martial artist at the seventh realm in the mansion, who originally served in the border troops and hails from the old mountain region of the Great Li. He has become acquainted with Master and was invited here. Now, he is living in hiding, serving as a guard, keeping a close watch on the steward and his crew."

The steward's mind went blank.

A person who could befriend the city god of Longzhou City and have a seventh realm master as a guard? 

Why was he being belittled by that small-minded woman, who repeatedly called him a useless dead man?

Gu Can felt helpless. What kind of incense and fire was this? The seventh realm masters of the Great Li were all documented, and the court was keeping a close eye on them. They were likely on par with that down-and-out mountain deity, Song Yuzhang. They were indeed protecting the Gu residence, but it was more about keeping a watchful eye. That mountain deity father of Gu Can, whom he had no memory of, would certainly not disclose such inside information to worry her unnecessarily.

Gu Can looked at the pure martial artist, who was still contemplating how to survive, and said without cause, "The person behind this may indeed be a master, but as for you, forget it. It’s still unclear who set it up or whether there was even a setup at all."

Gu Can muttered, "People die for wealth, birds perish for food. How are there so many fools under the heavens?"

A cheerful voice chimed in, "Isn’t this a good thing? In a game of chess, if you throw pieces randomly, how can you talk about having the first move? Only the younger, clever ones can stand out and surpass the predecessors."

Gu Can stood up solemnly. The room was empty, yet he remained respectful, clasping his fists in a bow.

A man in white appeared beside Gu Can, saying, "Pack your things; come with me to Bai Di City. Before we set off, you should visit Huang Lake Mountain with Liu Chicheng and meet that old Daoist named Jia Sheng. If he is willing to appear, you will be my little junior brother. If not, you can rest easy as my named disciple."

The man in white held out a scroll, an old "Mountain Search Map," and handed it to Gu Can. "Take this to Huang Lake Mountain."

Before arriving at this mansion, the man had retrieved this map from Lin Shouyi as a return favor for helping Lin complete a volume of "The Book Above the Clouds," which originally came from Bai Di City, gifting it with the lower two scrolls. Though Lin Shouyi was a scholar, he had made rapid progress in cultivation, quickly reaching the cave realm and focusing on the foundational aspects of "The Book Above the Clouds." His skills were immense, and the thunder techniques contained within were authentic. Yet, this wasn't the greatest essence of "The Book Above the Clouds." Opening pathways and cultivating without hindrance was the core goal of "The Book Above the Clouds." The author of this text was the lord of Bai Di City, who had personally edited and refined it, eliminating many unnecessary details.

Where in the world is the highest cloud above?

Naturally, it is Bai Di City.

As for how the upper volume of the Dao book ended up in Lin Shouyi's hands, it was certainly due to A Liang's involvement, as the literati often borrowed books without returning them. It was no wonder Lin Shouyi took a liking to this text; his fate with it was excellent.

Since it was A Liang's gift, Bai Di City didn't mind Lin Shouyi’s minor "accidental transgressions" against the mountain.

However, Lin Shouyi, after revealing his name, still refused to elaborate on the source of the "Mountain Search Map."

This was the very reason the lord of Bai Di City was willing to gift the final volume of "The Book Above the Clouds." Initially, giving a mid-volume would have meant Lin Shouyi would be reduced to a pawn and suffer a calamity.

Gu Can's expression remained blank, but his heart was shaken. He knew of Jia Sheng!

An honorary worshipper of the Down-and-Out Mountain, a lucky blind old Daoist who could get by in Qilong Alley, had taken two obedient disciples: a young man with a limp, Zhao Denggao, a demon, and Tian Jiu’er, whose blood was the best material for talismans. It was said that Jia Sheng had moved to Huang Lake Mountain to cultivate a few years ago.

The Down-and-Out Mountain had such a person lying low, and how did Zhu Lian and Wei Bo not notice a single trace of him?

"If I hadn't come to this place, no one in Down-and-Out Mountain would ever know about such a person. Jia Sheng would die simply as Jia Sheng, and perhaps during his cultivation journey, he would naturally go to the Fifth Realm. On the day he ascends, he will change his body and reincarnate endlessly, relishing the cycle."

The man in white chuckled, "Don’t overthink it; it's just his usual way of playing with the world. After he put away his sword back then, he completely changed as a person. Good at self-deception, he doesn’t like deceiving others. He has faced countless disasters and misfortunes on the mountain and below, yet he has never once acted to protect himself. In the vast world of righteousness, every continent, he stays for several hundred years. Furthermore, while I am his nominal disciple, Bai Di City was established entirely by me; he has nothing to do with it."

Gu Can suddenly said, "Then I won’t need to visit Huang Lake Mountain. I won’t disturb the old senior’s peace; I’ll just follow the city lord to Central Continent."

The man in white smiled, "If you can say that, then you definitely should meet him."

Gu Can asked, "What about the three people in the room?"

The two maidservants and the steward remained perfectly still.

The man in white glanced at the three, then extended a hand. The three, including the pure martial artist, were forced into a trance, dazed and confused, their feet leaving the ground as they slowly floated to the front of the man in white. He casually pointed at their foreheads a couple of times, and the three spirits returned to their bodies. Gu Can focused his gaze and saw that from the center of each person’s forehead, threads began to spread outward.

Then the three suddenly "woke up." The steward, as a pure martial artist, suddenly burst into tears, kneeling and saying, "Young Master!"

One maidservant kowtowed vigorously, "This servant pays respects to the sect master!"

The other maidservant fell to the ground, utterly heartbroken, "Master, forgive me!"

The man in white waved his sleeve, and the three fainted again. He laughed, explaining, "It’s as if they had a long slumber, waking from a dream. They are still the same people, only with a bit more life experience added."

Gu Can broke out in a cold sweat.

This was the demonic method of Bai Di City!

Only at this moment did he understand why every time Liu Chicheng mentioned this person, there was such reverence.

He could casually turn a person into someone who was no longer who they once were, yet they still firmly believed they were themselves.

Then what of all the grudges and enmities, all the so-called cultivation of the great way? What did they really mean?

The man in white chuckled, "Is life and death the greatest matter? Then what truly is life and death? Once I understood this, some people didn’t want me to leave Bai Di City."

He concluded, "That old man came to this Li Zhu Cave Heaven, not to completely sever karmic ties, but just to wander around? Finally, he has shown a bit of the demeanor of a master; I’m surprised this time."

Beside a thatched cottage on Huang Lake Mountain.

In the depths of the great mountains, water flowed gently.

The blind old Daoist stepped out of the cottage during a break from his cultivation, sighing to himself. After his good brother Chen Lingjun traveled far away, he no longer had anyone to chat with about the mountains. It was truly lonely.

The so-called dedicated cultivation was merely an excuse to find a new place to live. He was no longer cooped up in that shabby place in Qilong Alley, at least it was closer to Down-and-Out Mountain. He could return to Qilong Alley later, and with each back and forth, his identity as an honorary worshipper would become even more solidified. The shopkeeper of the neighboring new year shop would have to treat him with more respect when they next met, wouldn’t they?

Jia Sheng suddenly felt somewhat fearful.

He sensed a ripple in front of him, as if guests had arrived.

Jia Sheng immediately stiffened, raising his voice, "Two guests, visiting uninvited and without a greeting—this isn’t very proper."

Liu Chicheng nearly popped his eyes out.

Sometimes, when observing a person, appearances, souls, and aura can all conceal identities, making it hard for others to recognize someone who is so close. 

But in certain subtle aspects, if one digs deeper, the traces become obvious, such as the blind old Daoist's posture and the curvature of his fingers while forming seals, among others.

Adding to the fact that the senior brother had not explained, Liu Chicheng immediately thought of the most unlikely "what if," crouching down to the ground and trembling as he said, "Disciple pays respects to Master!"

Jia Sheng felt a bit guilty. Where did this wild disciple come from?

Liu Chicheng kept his head to the ground, feeling immensely wronged, "Master, Senior Brother bullied me terribly. First, he drove me out of Bai Di City for a trivial matter, then he let me be chased by the Grand Master of Longhu Mountain with a sword, leaving this poor disciple trapped in this little Bao Ping Island for a thousand years, no one cared for me. Senior Brother showed no regard for our brotherhood; Master, you must seek justice!"

It was not that Liu Chicheng was making things up. The Master had always favored this disciple, and many senior brothers and sisters harbored resentment towards him precisely because of this.

The old Daoist nearly jumped in anger, cursing, "What Bai Di City, what Grand Master of Longhu Mountain? Is there anyone in the world so shameless among my fellow practitioners? If I, Jia Sheng, were really your master, I would be blind to accept you as a disciple..." Jia Sheng suddenly froze, realizing he was indeed blind.

Gu Can admired Liu Chicheng's boldness, truly meeting a high-level individual. He brought up the lord of Bai Di City as his senior brother, and now faced with the true senior brother, he began to mention his master?

Gu Can raised the "Mountain Search Map" in his hand, solemnly saying, "Old Senior, here’s the item returning to its rightful owner."

Jia Sheng naturally opened his eyes and saw the scroll, sighing, "To take on such a big disciple, truly, it seems I haven’t turned over the old calendar."

Then Jia Sheng froze, gently shaking his head. What strange thoughts were these? The old Daoist blinked hard; the world was bright once more, everything in sight.

The odd thunder techniques he had practiced in his own mountain were obscure and cost him dearly—first injuring his organs and then losing his sight, preventing him from seeing anything for many years.

After a momentary daze, the old Daoist, Jia Sheng, retreated, his mind condensed like a mustard seed, falling into a deep slumber while another person took over all his awareness.

The old man lowered his head, tugged at his Daoist robe, then turned his gaze towards the Great Scholar’s Block of Huaihuang County, and then shifted his focus to the True Pearl Mountain and all the dragon kilns within view. His expression grew complex as he ignored both Liu Chicheng and Gu Can, falling into deep thought.

The old man opened his palm, gazed at the patterns in his hand for a moment, and finally muttered, "In this life, a small dream; after waking, Lu Chen has deceived me greatly."

With a single step, the blind old Daoist Jia Sheng stood still, still in deep slumber.

When the old man revealed his true form, he appeared as a tall, thin elder with a refined appearance, reminiscent of a handsome youth with remarkable charisma in his younger days.

The old man's cultivation journey had been like a dazzling meteor in the vast world of righteousness, rising rapidly compared to the long river of time, but falling just as swiftly.

So much so that even the lord of Bai Di City was his first disciple, such a significant matter was known to only a handful of people in the entire world.

The old man was Jia Sheng, and yet he was much more than just Jia Sheng; behind him, Jia Sheng would eventually become just Jia Sheng.

In his lifetime, he would only do one thing, well-known throughout the world.

With a single sword, he would slay the dragons of the world.

Killing until only the last true dragon remained.

In the old calendar of the vast world, because of one person's sword, several pages were ripped away!

When the old man appeared, the giant python that once vied with Gu Can for water in Huang Lake, which had lost, sank abruptly, as if pressured by the will of heaven, submerging into the depths of the lake, trembling in fear, wishing it could bury its head into the mountain's roots.

The old man glanced at Gu Can, stretched out a hand to receive the scroll, tucking it into his sleeve. He then patted Gu Can's shoulder and nodded, smiling, "Good root and bone, a fine seedling. I shall take you as my disciple in place of my master."

Liu Chicheng was struck by lightning, sitting dazed on the ground, no longer howling.

This shouldn't be happening; it absolutely must not happen.

Once Gu Can held such an identity, it would not be long before he, Liu Chicheng, would take a step ahead on the path to the underworld!

The man in white appeared out of nowhere.

The old man glanced sideways at him, saying, "I am now basically a useless person. I can't defeat you, my disciple, but after all, the master-disciple title is still there. What, are you unhappy? Do you wish to betray your master? Just like in swordsmanship, I never taught you this."

The man in white remained silent, a hint of killing intent flickering.

Unexpectedly, the old man pressed forward, seemingly unconcerned about the lord of Bai Di City’s murderous intent, asking, "What are you dazed for? Call me your little master uncle."

The man in white showed no regard for seniority and merely asked, "Are you sure this is for Gu Can's benefit?"

Gu Can knelt on the ground, bowing his head seriously, "Gu Can pays respects to Ancestor Master."

The old man burst into hearty laughter.

Transforming into a beam of sword light, he instantly shot off into the distance, heading north to play with his good brother, Chen Lingjun. 

But the next time they met, he wouldn’t recognize him, and Chen Lingjun would not recognize him either.

The man in white looked up at the sword light vanishing into the north, saying with a smile, "You should treat your closed-door disciple a bit better."

Liu Chicheng let out a sigh of relief. Thankfully, Gu Can was just his little junior brother.

Otherwise, with such a high status, Gu Can, with his lack of regard for old feelings, could do anything heartlessly.

Lin Shouyi sat in the ancestral home, no matter how he tried to focus his mind, he remained restless. He could only head to the ancestral hall, where the divine tablets had already been moved to the capital of the Great Li, to find some peace.

Lin Shouyi lit three sticks of incense, respectfully paying homage to his ancestors.

After completing this, he turned to leave the ancestral hall, just as he was closing the door, he noticed an old scholar standing nearby.

Lin Shouyi, being extremely clever, immediately bowed, "Lin Shouyi from Mountain Cliff Academy, pays respects to Master Uncle."

Cui Zhan smiled, "I am no longer in the direct lineage of the Confucian Sage, so you need not be so polite."

Lin Shouyi straightened his back and bowed again, "A disciple of the Great Li Lin clan, pays respects to the National Master."

Cui Zhan nodded, "In your early years of wandering and studying, your performance was quite remarkable. You were the first to notice A Liang's extraordinary nature and the first to gain opportunities; it was all you, Lin Shouyi, and that was no small feat. Allowing that person to act within the great rules this time was a sign of your academic stability, the accumulation of experience, and a stroke of good fortune."

Cui Zhan led Lin Shouyi through the empty mansion, encouraging the young man to walk alongside him without being overly restrained.

Cui Zhan continued, "Your father has some burdens he will never discuss with you. He was the first to inform Chen Ping'an’s father about the inside story regarding the innate porcelain. Of course, it was out of goodwill, and he also mentioned the consequences to Chen Ping'an's father. The two became close friends despite their differences in status. Your father even helped that man clean up the mess later; otherwise, it would have been difficult for Chen Ping'an to survive. Thus, when Chen Ping'an later traveled to study, he gifted you the 'Mountain Search Map.' There are some fated connections at play here. However, your father, with good intentions, didn’t want you to be too involved with Chen Ping'an, fearing that you might be swept up in the greater tides of fate before you were ready, leading to an early demise. Thus, he acted very indifferent about your journey to the Great Sui Academy."

Lin Shouyi was taken aback.

Cui Zhan said, "Hard to believe? Then think carefully: a man who has served as the deputy for three kiln supervisors wouldn’t be simple, would he? Does he really care about the titles of legitimate or illegitimate sons? Do you know that the current Supervisor Cao, before heading to Huaihuang Town, visited only one person after leaving the late emperor’s study? That would be your father, who remains inconspicuous in the capital. How did your classmate Shi Chunjia's family manage to get through their hardships? Does Shi’s family not know? Are they still harboring some resentment? Do you think your father would care?"

Cui Zhan, with one hand behind his back and the other pinching his fingers as if plucking something, continued, "Shi Chunjia is sentimental, you too should be. If you remember, all your classmates will follow suit. Bian Wenmao has lofty aspirations but only sincerely treats his wife, Shi Chunjia, who comes from humble beginnings. You would understand Bian Wenmao's situation. Once this gentleman from the Great Li capital encounters troubles, you would be willing to help him. If you choose to assist, even if you are still inexperienced and make some blunders, your father will not sit idly by. All these threads are connected, and the web is vast. Just don't forget that if you can think this way, so can everyone else. Whatever level of cultivation one possesses will bring about corresponding karmic consequences. The realm of cultivation is usually useful but can be the least useful at critical times. Lin Shouyi, I ask you: do you still wish to meddle in others' affairs?"

Cui Zhan gently flicked his fingers, as if wiping clean those connections.

Lin Shouyi pondered for a moment before replying, "Since things have come to this, I must manage them one by one."

Lin Shouyi sighed, "But I will meddle less in the future."

Cui Zhan smiled knowingly, "Your father’s tantrums and tricks were not in vain; they helped me come up with such a good name for you."

Lin Shouyi suddenly halted, gathering his courage to bow again, trembling as he asked, "May I ask, Master Uncle, why did you stand by and let our teacher go to his death alone back then?"

This question made Lin Shouyi feel a deep sense of grievance he could no longer suppress. Even if it angered this National Master who did not wish to acknowledge his uncle status, today he had to ask!

Cui Zhan took it lightly, clearly not angered by the young man's audacity; instead, he appeared somewhat delighted as he said, "If you can speak grand principles without paying a great price, what value is there? Anyone can talk about it; what is the meaning of reading? When it comes to righteousness, it is foolish to yield to others. This kind of foolishness is hard to learn without studying. However, the teachings of Confucius are all laid out in plain books."

Cui Zhan gently patted the young man's shoulder, saying, "Thus, while living in the world, one should scold half-hearted scholars more and the sages less."

Cui Zhan looked around, "In your early years of wandering, your poor opinion of your father was noted by Chen Ping'an when he traveled with you. So, even if Chen Ping'an later had enough confidence to bring up old grievances, he would have uncovered many old records about the Ma family in Xinghua Alley. Yet, he stalled at the kiln supervision office with your father, precisely because he trusted you. He feared those rumors that couldn’t be spoken but also didn’t trust the hearts of those he had never met. Most feared that once the truth was revealed, it would cause your friend Lin Shouyi to be bloodied; this is called once bitten, twice shy. After experiencing hardships at Shujian Lake, he truly did not wish to face them again in his hometown."

Cui Zhan smiled, "Although Chen Ping'an misunderstood, it was a good thing. Otherwise, with his temper, once he got serious, even if he uncovered the truth and was able to breathe easily, avoiding you and your father, Down-and-Out Mountain would have early on clashed with the Song clan of the Great Li, suffering severe wounds. They would be stuck in their hometown, seeking answers, making enemies everywhere, naturally harming their vitality, and would never achieve any status as the hidden official of the Sword Qi Great Wall. The Xu family of Qingfeng City, along with many forces, would spare no effort in taking down Down-and-Out Mountain."

Cui Zhan continued, "You don't need to return to Mountain Cliff Academy for now. Inquire with Li Baoping and Li Huai about that 'Qi' character from years ago. Collect any that are still kept, including yours, and then go find Cui Dongshan, giving him all the 'Qi' characters. After that, visit Shujian Lake and retrieve those bamboo slips that Chen Ping'an threw into the lake."

Lin Shouyi was bewildered but still nodded in agreement.

Cui Zhan looked up at the grand sword light that had flashed by, relieved to see it finally leave.

The Great Li Dynasty was busy excavating the grand canal, with construction going on vigorously.

The influential Gongsun family, led by Liu Xunmei, had suddenly become the latest high-ranking figures in the Great Li.

As for the formerly low-profile governor of Qingluan Nation, Liu Qingfeng, once the initial excitement of the Great Li capital's officialdom passed, alongside some behind-the-scenes arrangements, Liu Qingfeng quickly lost people’s interest in probing further.

Coming from a scholarly family in a small nation, it was clear he was not a Qi practitioner and was destined for a short life. In his early years, he had some notable achievements in Qingluan Nation but was infamous, so sitting in this position might lead to some prospects but not great ones, as he was not from the Great Li capital. As for how he suddenly rose to prominence, who knows? In the Great Li capital, there was speculation that this person was merely a puppet raised by the Jiang family of Yunlin, especially since the latest mouth of the grand canal was right in front of the Jiang family’s door.
