A very handsome young man in white squatted in the field, watching from a distance as a local clan fought over water rights, thoroughly captivated. Beside him squatted a frail child with a dull expression.

Liu Qingfeng sat on the field ridge, with his attendants Wang Yifu and the young Liu Suo standing at a distance. Liu Suo was not particularly afraid of the odd young man he had dealt with before; apart from being a bit dim-witted, there wasn't much to say about him. However, Wang Yifu advised Liu Suo to stay away from that "young man."

Liu Qingfeng turned his head towards the boy chewing on a wild grass stalk and asked, "Excavating the grand canal, big and small matters, it should be a step-by-step process. Teacher Cui doesn't need to stay here overseeing it, right?"

Cui Dongshan continued watching the scuffle, observing relatives fighting with shovels and carrying loads. Many of them were uncles and nephews, genuinely going at it, but after the fight, they would still remain relatives, possibly even needing to pay each other for medicine or treatment afterward, all sincere and heartfelt.

Hearing Liu Qingfeng's inquiry, he casually replied, "The grand canal named Qi is the reason."

Liu Qingfeng nodded with a smile, indicating he understood.

A carriage stopped on a rural road. From the carriage emerged Li Baozhen, walking over and bowing, "Teacher Cui."

Cui Dongshan ignored him.

Li Baozhen stood up and looked towards Liu Qingfeng, smiling, "Mr. Liu."

Liu Qingfeng smiled and gestured for him to sit down.

Li Baozhen sat beside Liu Qingfeng.

Cui Dongshan turned his head, jokingly saying, "Don’t let me hold you two back from reminiscing; I’ll find some fun for myself." He stood up, grabbed the child's collar beside him, and left with the wind.

Cui Dongshan quietly landed several hundred miles away in a mountain town, sitting side by side under the shade of a tree with the older brother, surrounded by crowds. They watched roadside wild chess for a good half an hour. It was not Go; the chessboard was simpler. Otherwise, common folks would not be able to attract so many spectators without having played at least half a game of chess.

When the wild chess player won a heap of copper coins and silvers, the crowd dispersed, and they planned to wrap up. This is what they called a one-trick pony. However, when he saw the young man still not willing to leave, observing him closely and appearing like a young master from a wealthy family, he smiled and asked, "Do you like to play chess?"

Cui Dongshan was eager to try, rubbing his hands, "Of course, I can play. I can play this chess, and I can even play Go. But I left home in a hurry, so I don’t have much copper on me. I see some tricks in your game; I’m sure I can win you."

The man playing wild chess laughed. This was one of the top ten wild chess games in the Jianghu, the "Earthworm Drawing the Dragon." He didn’t fear others figuring out the tricks; the more, the better; he was just afraid the opponent would find it unsolvable and not be willing to take the bait.

Cui Dongshan slapped the child's head beside him, "Hurry up and play chess to earn some money."

The man laughed heartily and swiftly packed up his stall, not wanting to engage with this young boy.

Cui Dongshan did not stop him, taking small steps to sit opposite the child. He stretched out his neck, staring at the child, then raised his hands, pulling at the child's cheeks, "How did I figure out you are a chess expert? I didn’t tell that man your surname, Gao."

The child remained expressionless.

Cui Dongshan tugged for a while, feeling it was pointless. He stood up, leading the child to wander around the town. They encountered a not-so-old young man from the capital, who had come to this vassal state to seek treasures, mostly a trusted apprentice from an antique shop owner in the capital, dispatched to places to seek rare treasures and valuable antiques.

Doing this job, one must have sharp eyes and solid character. Otherwise, if one were to stumble upon a priceless treasure, they would run off and establish their own business.

Cui Dongshan followed this young man around the market, weighing and closely inspecting the items he had quietly observed, causing the young man to grumble in frustration, "If you need money, I can give you some; just don’t keep following me around for fun. You think it’s amusing, but you’re ruining my livelihood."

Cui Dongshan looked at the young man’s eyes and expression, feeling inexplicably familiar. He suddenly smiled, "Don’t worry, I guarantee I won’t cause any trouble from here on out."

The young man was skeptical, but as they continued to walk around, the boy remained quiet, which only made the young man more anxious. Could it be that the dangers of the Jianghu were real, and the boy was indeed after him? 

The Jianghu was full of hidden dangers, making it hard to guard against. However, the boy casually bought a porcelain bowl, placing it on the child's head, and bid farewell to the young man, saying he needed to take his silly brother back to the school for a meal. After all, in a foreign land, seeking knowledge, the teacher was the most important; if the student didn’t return for long, the teacher would worry.

The young man let out a sigh of relief.

As the boy took the white bowl off the child's head, he tossed it at the young man from a distance, beaming, "I've learned some fresh tips on buying antiques from you; there's no need for thanks, this bowl is for you."

The young man had intended to refuse, thinking it was just a broken bowl—not worth it, and it would take up space. Moreover, the boy was dressed in finery, yet when he took out copper coins, he counted them one by one, not appearing to be well-off...

But before the young man could speak, the boy had already dragged the child away by an arm, running off quickly. The child looked rather pitiful as they fled.

As the sun set in the west, on a yellow clay road outside the city, houses of various sizes from a village squatted by a river.

Cui Dongshan muttered to himself, "The teacher's reluctance to help others stems from an incident in his youth; he fears being too rash in helping others in need. He thinks that the older Jianghu practitioners should be like this, but in reality, my teacher is too demanding of the Jianghu people."

"Doing good with bad intentions, which is worse? One must make a choice."

"But my teacher is wise, worrying about everything; how can a student dare to speak such things?"

As Cui Dongshan rambled on to himself.

A child herding cattle returned home, riding on the back of a cow.

Cui Dongshan was not to be outdone, jumping onto the child's back.

Cui Dongshan swayed his shoulders, causing the child to stumble along. He said, "Clouds drift in the sky, willows sway by the roadside, the sounds of hawkers selling apricot blossoms fill the streets."

Then, Cui Dongshan clapped the child’s cheek, "Little Gao, my poetic inspiration is surging! Join me in a verse!"

The child blinked.

Cui Dongshan increased his strength, threatening, "You won’t give me face?!"

The child mumbled, "In rural smoke, a herdsman rides a cow, playing the bamboo flute, singing the old peaceful song."

"Little Gao, you truly are a talent!" Cui Dongshan wrapped an arm around the child’s neck, using the other to pat the back of his head, laughing heartily, "What merit do I have to know you?!"

The herding boy turned to look at the two, frightened, and hurriedly urged his cow to quicken its pace.

Cui Dongshan covered the child’s eyes, "Gather your strength, run!"

Finally, with his vision obscured, the child stumbled forward, running straight into the river.

In mid-air, Cui Dongshan released his hands and waved vigorously, his large sleeves fluttering. Just as the two were about to hit the water, the boy laughed uproariously, "The wise enjoy water! Dongshan has come!"

(End of Chapter)

 ### Chapter 774: The Central Martial Artist

Liu Xianyang truly only returned home for a visit. After his stay, he boarded the dragon boat named "Fan Mo" at Luoposhan. This boat didn't go directly to Old Dragon City; instead, it required a transfer at a celestial ferry near the Shuishui Kingdom in the central part of Baopingzhou, following the Longdao southward.

All the direct disciples from the Ancestor Hall of Zhu Chai Island had already relocated from Shujian Lake to the back of the Ao Fish, making it one of the earliest celestial forces to form an alliance with Luoposhan.

The former princess who once ruled with a veil, now the island owner Liu Chongrun, personally took charge of the ferry. It was hard to feel at ease knowing there wasn't a Earth Immortal sitting in on the boat.

Ruan Xiu was at the Niujiao Mountain ferry to see Liu Xianyang off.

The dragon boat was massive, akin to a mountain of gold and silver, which left Liu Xianyang feeling quite emotional. In the past, among the three of them, it was actually Chen Ping'an who wanted to make money the most, not Gu Can. However, unlike Gu Can, who had plans on how to spend the money he wanted to earn, Chen Ping'an was driven by fear of poverty. He needed to earn something every day; no matter how little, as long as his family fortune increased by even a single copper coin compared to yesterday, it could make his unstable days feel more secure, and make the stable days even more so.

During this trip home, Liu Xianyang mostly visited neighbors and friends, chatting with the elderly who remained in the small town. With each passing year, the elderly dwindled in number, and the children who once ran around in open-crotch pants were growing into adults, each with their own marriages. When they saw Liu Xianyang, they might not even recognize him. Those peers from his youth were busy doing business in the state city, so the opportunities Liu Xianyang had to engage in meaningful conversations were few, and it was destined to become even rarer in the future.

Now, in idle chats with the elderly, the likes of Xinghua Lane had become the topic of conversation, with Chen Ping'an, the major landowner who had bought up many hills in his hometown, and Song Jixin, who had mysteriously become a descendant of dragons. There was also Dong Shuijing, who was doing big business with the officials in the state city. These were the most discussed figures among the townsfolk.

Moreover, these elders who had endured hard times seemed particularly fond of praising the feng shui of Xinghua Lane and Niping Lane, claiming it was no worse than that of Fulujie and Taoye Lane.

Liu Xianyang enjoyed listening to the elders ramble about these mundane matters, especially when some of the elders who were not familiar with Niping Lane spoke of Chen Ping'an as if he were a younger relative they had watched grow up. It made Liu Xianyang feel quite pleased. Indeed, in terms of social interactions, especially with elders, Chen Ping'an had always been quite skilled. Though he usually didn't talk much, he would greet people he encountered on the road, never forgetting his manners, even if the other party ignored him. The next time they met, the boy from Niping Lane would still respectfully greet them.

Some people became suddenly rich due to luck and fortune, which was enviable but unattainable. Yet, some successes came from years of hard work and persistence, which seemed easy to learn but was often not.

Liu Xianyang waited for the dragon boat to dock, needing to unload and load cargo. Nowadays, the trade of dragon boats involved connections with the Pima Sect and Chunlu Garden from Beiju Luozhou, something unimaginable to many small-town folks.

Suddenly, Liu Xianyang smiled and asked, “That kid named Xie Ling from the mountain has quite an unusual appearance.”

There was more to his words than met the eye; this was a common way of speaking in the town.

Ruan Xiu responded, “He’s just a kid.”

Liu Xianyang felt a bit schadenfreude.

Ruan Xiu said, “You can't really control Gu Can.”

Liu Xianyang nodded and replied, “If it comes to it, I can just hit him once. Gu Can wouldn’t fight back, but he can't change his fundamentally spoiled nature. I’ve known this for a long time, so I never thought about how to manage him. At least this little brat still has a bit of conscience and knows who truly cares for him.”

Ruan Xiu and Liu Xianyang were old acquaintances. Liu Xianyang had actually entered that sword-forging shop by the Longxu River before Chen Ping'an and had been an apprentice, unlike Chen Ping'an, who later worked there as a temporary helper. Whether it was making porcelain or forging swords, Liu Xianyang seemed to adapt to local customs more quickly than Chen Ping'an. Liu Xianyang liked to pave the way and, when he found a path, he would pull Chen Ping'an along behind him.

On the journey of life, many people are willing to see their friends live well, but they may not want their friends to do better than themselves—especially not by a wide margin.

Liu Xianyang was not like that, nor was Chen Ping'an. This was probably why these two very different individuals could become true friends and, after both their lives had undergone tremendous changes, their friendship only grew stronger.

Ruan Xiu held a handkerchief and picked up a piece of peach blossom cake, asking, “Did you not go to Niping Lane to say hello and chat for a bit?”

Liu Xianyang sighed, “The youthful admiration is all bright and beautiful, but looking back, it’s just a fond memory.”

Once Liu Xianyang finished his sentiment, Ruan Xiu had already finished a piece of cake and picked up another almond pastry, saying, “What did you talk about with my father? He seemed quite happy.”

Liu Xianyang chuckled, “Master Ruan drank, and I scolded Chen Ping'an.”

Ruan Xiu responded with a soft “Oh.”

Liu Xianyang wasn’t exactly lying; there was indeed a serious matter he couldn’t discuss with Ruan Xiu. Years ago, after Chen Ping'an returned from a trip to sea, he had found Liu Xianyang and asked him to go back to his hometown to help convey a message to the Song family of the Great Li in Baopingzhou. Liu Xianyang felt it was more appropriate for Ruan Qiong, the chief devotee of the Great Li and his future master, to discuss matters with the young emperor. This was no small matter; it involved the Chuxian Chen family’s support for the Daxui Mountain Cliff Academy, returning to the ranks of the Seventy-Two Academies. However, the Linlu Academy built on Piyun Mountain by the Great Li was unfamiliar to the Chuxian Chen family and would not be discussed at the Confucian Temple.

At the time, Liu Xianyang had some doubts, so he asked openly why the Chuxian Chen family of the Yasheng lineage wanted to do this, without worrying about potential dissent within the Yasheng lineage.

His concern was not unfounded. A vice chief elder from the Middle Earth Confucian Temple, in terms of both realm and seniority, was on par with Chen Ping'an. To put it simply, Chen Ping'an was a renowned scholar and a pillar of the Yasheng lineage, but within the scholarly traditions of the Yasheng lineage, he was still bound by many constraints.

Chen Ping'an seemed to be in a good mood at the time, telling Liu Xianyang that this was a business deal between himself and Chen Ping'an. If Chen Ping'an relied solely on his identity as a disciple of the Literary Sage's lineage, daring to speak boldly to Chen Xun'an, it would be rather inappropriate. Ultimately, standing atop the stone cliffs by the great river, Chen Xun'an patted Liu Xianyang on the shoulder, saying something refreshing to the young man. He said that we scholars should not be ashamed to discuss interests; our hearts must aspire to lofty ideals, while our actions must be practical and substantial. Scholars should step out of their studies and be among the common folk, discussing principles that even those who have not read books can understand.

At that time, Liu Xianyang blurted out, “We scholars should not only associate with other scholars.”

The old man was greatly pleased, stroking his beard and smiling, “Our Chuxian Chen family’s family traditions and learning styles are quite commendable.”

Suddenly, Ruan Xiu said, “If you’ve already said you don’t care too much, then why take that underground river route? There are ferries that go directly to Old Dragon City, after all.”

Liu Xianyang rubbed his face with both hands and replied, “Back then, the small town was just that small. The pretty girls on Fulujie and Taoye Lane? I didn’t dare to think too much about them. She’s different; she’s Chen Ping'an’s neighbor, living in Niping Lane, and her family is not even as good as my ancestral home. She’s just the maid of the Song family, carrying water and cooking every day. I feel like I’m certainly not worthy of her. If I were to say how much I liked her, well, I do like her a lot, but it’s not to the extent of obsessing over her. Everything is left to fate. Whether we end up together or not, what difference does it make?”

Ruan Xiu asked, “What kind of place is the Sword Qi Great Wall?”

Liu Xianyang thought for a moment, “It’s a place that lacks everything, except for a plethora of sword cultivators. In terms of cultivation, life or death doesn’t seem to be a significant matter there. So, there are many drinkers. Sword cultivators and sword immortals, after all, like to drink. I can even say that in my impression, the Sword Qi Great Wall is the place where the most high-level individuals seem the least like high-level individuals outside my hometown.”

Ruan Xiu nodded.

Liu Xianyang’s expression became awkward. After hesitating for a long time, he finally couldn’t help but say, “Ruan Xiu, I've known you for a long time, right? We have a pretty good relationship, don’t we? But there are some things I really can’t say much about. Chen Ping'an, you two are both my friends, so I can only try not to say those words you might want to hear regarding a certain matter.”

Ruan Xiu looked up at Liu Xianyang and shook her head, “I don’t want to hear those words you think I want to hear, like how Ruan Xiu is better than Ning Yao, or how you are a better friend to me than to Ning Yao.”

Liu Xianyang felt relieved and laughed, “Miss Ruan is just Miss Ruan, after all.”

Ruan Xiu said, “The reason I asked that was not just out of curiosity about what the Sword Qi Great Wall is like now but also to know how he is doing there. If he’s doing well because Ning Yao is there, since we are friends, of course, I would be happy.”

Just as Liu Xianyang was about to follow Ruan Xiu’s words and chat a bit more about how well Chen Ping'an was doing at the Sword Qi Great Wall, he suddenly stopped himself, silently warning himself not to say too much.

In a few years, when Liu Xianyang returns to his hometown again, he would rightfully become a direct disciple of the Dragon Spring Sword Sect. Regarding this matter, after Liu Xianyang ascended the mountain, Ruan Qiong had clearly explained it to both his direct and nominal disciples. However, Ruan Qiong did not mention whether Liu Xianyang would be ranked on the ancestral table after the first disciple Dong Gu or simply placed after Xie Ling. Liu Xianyang did not ask, and it became a topic of amusement among many nominal disciples of the Dragon Spring Sword Sect during their idle chats. The sect members were now quite familiar with the temperament of their sect leader. As long as they practiced swordsmanship sincerely and did not speak out of turn, there would be much speculation regarding Liu Xianyang’s cultivation level. After all, true Confucian disciples were not numerous among sword cultivators.

Ruan Xiu curiously asked, “Why do you still wish to return here to practice swordsmanship in the Dragon Spring Sword Sect? My father actually can’t teach you anything.”

Liu Xianyang replied helplessly, “Chen Ping'an is too good at taking care of others and not very good at taking care of himself. I worry when I’m far away.”

“I’m worried about Chen Ping'an,” Ruan Xiu softly repeated Liu Xianyang’s heartfelt words. She smiled, putting away her handkerchief into her sleeve. With her fingers, which had some cake crumbs on them, she gently pinched the edge of her sleeve, “Liu Xianyang, not everyone is qualified to say such things. Perhaps it was fine before, but it will be very difficult in the future.”

Liu Xianyang replied with a smile, “I’m worried about Chen Ping'an.”

Ruan Xiu smiled, narrowing her eyes, playing dumb.

At the Old Dragon City’s princely mansion, in the study.

On the desk lay several authentic historical texts from different dynasties, collections of literary masterpieces, and painting albums, with no celestial artifacts displayed as decoration.

Behind the desk stood four screens: one was an ancient map of the Great Li, another was a map of Baopingzhou, while the remaining two depicted the distribution of celestial sects in Tongyezhou and Beiju Luozhou.

Song Jixin, who had just returned from his northern homeland to the southern fief, sat alone in the study, shifting the direction of his chair to face the four screens.

With both hands, Song Jixin held a delicate heart-nourishing pot, gently spinning it. The inscription on the pot read "Shan Shao."

As he gently twisted the small pot in his hands, it was a precious item that had been lost and regained, returning to its rightful owner, though the means of recovery were not entirely honorable. However, Song Jixin didn’t care what Fu Nanhua would think.

Years ago, Fu Nanhua had entered the Li Pearl Cave, purchasing this small pot from Song Jixin with a bag of golden copper coins and an old dragon rain talisman. This transaction was actually quite fair; of course, Fu Nanhua had also managed to gain a significant advantage from it. Unlike many treasures from the mountains that were merely rank ornaments but were useless to Earth Immortal cultivators, this heart-nourishing pot was an extremely rare treasure of high rank, most suitable for Earth Immortals to cultivate their Dao hearts and nourish their Qi. Moreover, the pot contained a small cave, making it a compact item. Thus, after Fu Nanhua acquired it, he had someone verify it, feeling overjoyed and treasuring it deeply.

Yesterday, after reminiscing with the young prince, Fu Nanhua had mentioned this small pot, and today he had someone deliver it.

Song Jixin wasn’t truly coveting the heart-nourishing pot; it was more about this homecoming journey allowing the seemingly diligent but actually indifferent young prince to unknowingly regain a sense of ambition, finally beginning to see himself as the Great Li prince "Song Mu." This small pot, which had fallen back into his hands, was a reminder of the power dynamics below the mountains.

Since ancient times, celestial beings have looked down upon princes.

However, the current Great Li Dynasty was different; it had already suppressed, constrained, and intimidated all the mountain forces to the extent they could hardly breathe. No matter how powerful sects like the Shengaos and the Zhenjing Sect were, with their connections to other continents, in the small morning meetings in the emperor "Song He’s" imperial study, they still had to act like half-subjects, carefully observing others' expressions, sitting down obediently, and standing up dutifully.

Song Jixin casually tossed the invaluable small pot, alternating between catching it with both hands.

There were two confidential documents on the table, both of which Song Jixin had requested the copper men at the Penglu Terrace to collect. He completely distrusted the spies from the Green Wave Pavilion, because the original owner of the Green Wave Pavilion was the Great Li Empress, who was also Song Jixin’s biological mother. Although the Green Wave Pavilion and the Niujiao Lane both belonged to the National Master now, Song Jixin knew very well that many of the elderly who had not been eliminated from the Green Wave Pavilion knew how to navigate the delicate balance between the emperor Song He, the empress dowager, and the weak prince Song Mu.

On the other hand, the Penglu Terrace was the military’s unique intelligence agency, only listening to orders from the emperor’s uncle Song Changjing, and had never been interfered with by National Master Cui Zhan.

Song Jixin turned his head and glanced at the two documents. One was a detailed list of five-bound cultivators in Beiju Luozhou, while the other was a brief file regarding "Young Cui Dongshan."

The Fire Dragon Real Person from the Pile Peak, Li Yu from the Tai Xia lineage, had already perished. The Yuanling Hall of Zhixuan Peak was also affected, and fortunately, one of the individuals was merely at the Nascent Soul level; otherwise, the Fire Dragon lineage would have been far too intimidating.

Tianjun Xie Shi.

The Pima Sect’s head, Zhu Quan, alongside two old ancestors.

The Ghost Valley of Jingguan City, Gao Cheng.

There were Taoist temples and monasteries hidden within the peach forests, but the specifics of their foundations were currently unknown.

Fuping Sword Lake, female sword immortal Li Cai. She had already traveled far to the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Taihui Sword Sect, head Han Huaizi, old ancestor Huang Tong, and new Jade Purity Realm sword immortal Liu Jinglong. Han Huaizi had also been at the Sword Qi Great Wall for many years.

The first sword immortal of the northern region, Bai Shang, the mentor of Xu Xuan.

Yuan Ti Mountain, Ji Yue, had perished in battle, exchanging lives with the tenth realm martial artist Gu You. This was a significant loss for the entire Beiju Luozhou.

Shuilong Sect, with the northern sect led by Sun Jie and the southern sect by Shao Jingzhi.

The head of the Qionglin Sect.

In the Great Source Dynasty, the Chongxuan Bureau's Yunjiao Palace was led by the Yang family head.

Qingliang Sect’s He Xiaoliang.

The whereabouts of the wild cultivator Huang Juran remained unknown.

In addition, there were many entities similar to the Taoist temples and monasteries in the peach forest, as well as numerous high-level individuals who lived in seclusion, making it extremely difficult for the Great Li Dynasty’s intelligence to penetrate deep into Beiju Luozhou to uncover the long-buried truths. There were also some secret histories regarding all the living and deceased sword immortals’ journeys at the Sword Qi Great Wall.

As for Cui Dongshan, the Penglu Terrace only provided a blank page.

However, two pages of documents had been relayed from the Ministry of Justice to this study. One briefly explained where this person had previously appeared, lingered, and his words and actions. Most notably, his first appearance was in the still unshattered Li Pearl Cave. He then took the deceased prince of the Lu family and a girl named Xie Xie to the Great Sui Academy, where he clashed with the esteemed Gao family’s patron, Cai Jing, in the capital, creating a magnificent downpour of treasures. Later, he teamed up with Ruan Xiu to hunt down a bottleneck sword cultivator of the Zhu Ying Dynasty, successfully killing him on the borders of the Zhu Ying Dynasty.

The closing remarks on the first page of the Ministry of Justice’s file noted that this person had broken through extremely quickly, possessed numerous magical treasures, and had a rather strange temperament.

The second page was filled with detailed descriptions of those treasures.

Song Jixin withdrew his gaze and turned back to the four screens, pondering that the individuals from the mountain who frequented the prince’s mansion were a mixed bag, many of whom had concealed identities. If the other party did not reveal them, even Song Jixin would find it impossible to guess, including some secret worshippers from the Tongye Sect who had been hidden in Baopingzhou for many years, as well as the business manager of the Qionglin Sect in Baopingzhou.

At first, Song Jixin acted like a fool, trying his best to say appropriate words. However, upon reflection, he realized that what he had considered appropriate were actually the most inappropriate words, likely making many high-level outsiders who risked revealing their identities feel like conversing with this young prince was akin to talking to a cow.

Because all this time, Song Jixin hadn’t figured out what he truly wanted.

Reverting to the name Song He? Competing for the throne with his brother? Song Jixin had no interest in that, or rather, he feared treading the same path again; anyone who had read a few history books knew that fratricidal conflicts in royal families often resulted in numerous deaths. Whether it was the current emperor or the empress dowager, they were ultimately his closest relatives. Song Jixin realized that his life had been muddled and unclear, loving and hating others seemed difficult to be pure, and in the end, he would repay his debts to each one, be it Supervisor Song Yuzhang, neighbor Chen Ping'an, or maid Zhi Gui...

This couldn’t go on any longer.

Song Jixin tightened his grip on the heart-nourishing pot and suddenly stood up.

At the entrance of the study, Zhi Gui had actually been standing quietly for quite some time, and at this moment, she finally spoke, “Young Master, someone has been waiting to see you for a long time. It’s the eldest daughter of the Jiang family from Yunlin, Fu Nanhua’s nominal wife. Um, that girl looks a bit plump. But it’s just a high-level person using an illusion spell; her true appearance is okay.”

Song Jixin smiled and walked toward the door.

As he walked alongside her, Song Jixin quietly asked, “How much snake gallstone and golden copper do we need?”

Zhi Gui’s eyes brightened as she responded, “Young Master, of course, the more the better, just like the silver from years ago. However, these materials are now strictly regulated by the court, and the imperial treasury in the capital won’t casually release them.”

Song Jixin chuckled, “Don’t worry; I can find a trivial reason. I can make a deal with the Lord of the Southern Yue Mountain, using Fan Junmao as a pretext to try and secure half for you.”

Zhi Gui seemed surprised and stole a glance at Song Jixin, realizing that the young master was somewhat different now.

She continued to look around, not revealing any secrets.

Currently, in Baopingzhou, there were only a handful of figures she felt apprehensive towards, and there happened to be one who was the least desirable to provoke.

After Song Jixin left the study.

From behind the four screens emerged a young man in white clothing, and in the corner squatted a wooden, expressionless child who had not breathed throughout.

Cui Dongshan held a folding fan in one hand, lightly tapping his back with it, while in the other hand, he flipped his wrist, conjuring a brush, and began drawing circles on a screen, writing the names of several five-bound cultivators in Beiju Luozhou. Then he leaned over the table and flipped through the three pages of documents regarding himself, adding names to many entries of unnamed magical treasures listed on the two pages of the Ministry of Justice, and finally wrote on the blank page: “Cui Zhan is an old bastard; ask him if you don’t believe me.”

After finishing, he felt quite satisfied.

He waved his hand, beckoning Gao Laodi to come over. Cui Dongshan bent down and began drawing on the child’s face with his brush.

Without looking up, he smiled and said, “Maku Xuan, you’ve gotten used to not following rules, but one day, you’ll pay a big price for it.”

Maku Xuan revealed his form, leaning against the study door, “What kind of big price? Death, loss of the Dao? National Master, it’s fine if others don’t understand, being a frog at the bottom of a well. But how could you not know? I’m most afraid of that.”

Cui Dongshan finished his drawing, nodded, and said, “You say you’re not afraid of death, and I believe that. However, you don’t even understand the severity of entangled fates. What qualifications does a frog at the bottom of a well have to tell me whether they’re afraid or not? Just look at the Mulan flower matter; whose arrangement was that? I’m not scaring you. Just relying on a high realm doesn’t mean you’re capable. How many people can kill me? Even if you gain an extraordinary realm in the future, I can still make you worry for a thousand years, just by doing it casually. So, be smart and let me save some effort. Otherwise, when the day comes that you truly are scared, what benefit would that be for me? The fundamental principle of merit and learning is to avoid letting people make foolish mistakes, ensuring that those seeking benefits actually receive benefits.”

Maku Xuan nodded, “That makes sense.”

Cui Dongshan sat back in his chair, twirling his folding fan, and joked, “It hasn’t been long since I’ve been beaten up, so I decided to bully a poor beggar. What do you think—fun or not?”

Maku Xuan laughed, “Being able to bully a poor beggar today means there might be a chance to bully a wealthy man tomorrow. People must have some aspirations; otherwise, why not just live as a beggar for a lifetime?”

Cui Dongshan suddenly realized, vigorously nodding, “That makes sense.”

Maku Xuan clasped his fists, “I hope to continue hearing the National Master’s teachings in the future.”

After Maku Xuan left, Cui Dongshan leisurely swayed his fan, feeling quite content, with four large characters written in running script on the fan: “To win hearts through virtue.”

Cui Dongshan extended a finger and casually waved it, seemingly writing something as he gleefully said, “Three inches of vertical strokes, a thousand fathoms high. A single white line, a long rainbow piercing the sky…”

Turning around, he looked at the child silently standing by the desk, “Whose child is this? So handsome.”

The entire face of the child, covered in scribbles, suddenly spoke, “Sir, I want to learn chess.”

Cui Dongshan rolled his eyes, “Teach you boxing and stepping, starving the master. What benefit would I gain from teaching you chess?”

The child replied, “I can accompany you to play chess.”

Cui Dongshan shook his head, not giving an answer, only saying something confusing: “Lost hairpin and old sword, will surely return one day.”

Carving a boat to seek a sword is not foolish, nor is it laughable to be worried like Qi people.

Cui Dongshan began to close his eyes to rest.

The child started to daydream.

Half an hour later, Song Jixin returned to the study alone, while Zhi Gui mentioned wanting to stroll around the city.

Upon seeing the white-robed young man occupying the space, Song Jixin halted his steps, then continued forward, choosing a chair to sit down. “Cui Xiansheng, you really are quite at home here.”

Old Dragon City was not a place where cultivators could act as if it were a lawless land.

Cui Dongshan opened his eyes and asked, “Do you know who I am?”

Song Jixin nodded, “I have some guesses.”

Cui Dongshan tapped his shoulder with his fan, “Gao Laodi, tell him who I am. I’m afraid he might guess wrong.”

The child recited accurately, “My master is Dongshan.”

Cui Dongshan suddenly burst into laughter, almost tipping his entire chair over.

Then he abruptly restrained his expression, standing up.

Under the pressure of his imposing aura and invisible pull, Song Jixin involuntarily stood up as well.

Cui Dongshan said solemnly, “At this point, I won’t baffle you any longer. I am Cui Dongshan, and that Cui Zhan is the most incompetent of my nominal disciples.”

Song Jixin bowed and said softly, “Why must you belittle yourself, National Master?”

Cui Dongshan used his hand as a fan, a gentle breeze brushing against his face, “What can relieve worries? Only self-deprecation.”

The three pages of documents on the table turned to ashes, scattering with the wind.

Cui Dongshan walked around the table, approaching a nearby windowsill, and said softly, “Qing Jingchun has high expectations for you. Why haven’t you taken it seriously over the years?”

Song Jixin remained silent.

Cui Dongshan sighed, “Song Jixin, do you know that with your kind of fate, in many novels, you’d be either the first character to appear at the beginning or the last at the conclusion? Why can’t you just strive a bit harder? Your brain isn’t working well? Look at that Maku Xuan from Xinghua Lane, bringing along a cat. You’re even more impressive, taking along a Wang Zhu before you set out, and adding in that Xie Ling from Taoye Lane, your own ancestors could walk out from the first few pages of the genealogy. People like you are all destined to be little heavenly deities!”

Song Jixin’s expression darkened. What in the world was this all about?

The white-clad youth lifted his head, pretending to cry, seemingly feeling the atmosphere was lacking, and snapped his fingers.

The child Gao Laodi understood the cue and began to sing a cheerful little tune about how delicious stinky tofu was.

In Cui Dongshan's view, a person could live in two ways. One was to be rewarded by heaven with food, having minor worries without major concerns, living comfortably day by day. The other was to be favored by ancestors, having a skill to rely on, not worrying about the winds, sun, or rain. With money, one could eat candied hawthorns, enjoy stinky tofu, and savor both in one hand, one bite after another.

The young prince stood there, unsure of what to think.

Outside the gate of the Ancestor Hall on Jise Peak, a grand martial arts conference was being held. To show importance, a table and four long benches were set up, filled with fruits and pastries.

Of course, the door of the Ancestor Hall wasn’t casually opened, nor could things just be brought outside, so the tables and benches were specially transported from the ancestral mountain of Luoposhan.

All those present were now leaders of the Donghua Mountain branch under the Dragon Spring Sect.

Pei Qian, the branch leader, sat in the main seat, back facing the door of the Ancestor Hall, arms crossed. In front of her stood a wooden plaque, the alliance token of the Dragon Spring Sect, which had been kept by Bao Ping for many years.

Recently promoted to deputy branch leader, the right protector Zhou Mili was present, along with the branch's offering, Chen Nuanshu. However, Chen Lingjun was absent, and Pei Qian had already noted this in the ledger.

The girl in a pink skirt, who held the keys to all the doors of Luoposhan, and the little girl in black, carrying a golden shoulder pole and a green bamboo staff, sat side by side on a long bench.

Li Huai, the little branch leader of a certain academy under the branch, was squeezed among Liu Guanhua and Ma Lian on a long bench. Liu Guanhua and Ma Lian were not only classmates at the Daxui Mountain Cliff Academy but also good friends from the same academy. Liu Guanhua was a descendant of the Han clan, while Ma Lian came from a prominent family in the Great Sui. The Ma family was even related by marriage to the Gao family of the Great Sui, and both Liu Guanhua and Ma Lian were highly regarded as seeds of the Great Sui in the academy.

There was also the recently promoted right protector of Qilong Lane, a small person from the former Mantou Mountain and later the Longzhou City Hall, who had been allowed to sit at the table due to his small stature, giving him the rare opportunity to face the branch leader directly.

The left protector of Qilong Lane was slumped beneath the long bench.

As the leader of the martial arts alliance, the head of the main sect was Li Baoping. The honorary head of the branch, the Great White Goose Cui Dongshan, was absent from this meeting.

Pei Qian cleared her throat, scanning the crowd, and said, “I’ve gathered you all today to discuss three serious matters… Zhou Mili, put the sunflower seeds back. Liu Guanhua, sit properly.”

The little girl quietly set down the handful of sunflower seeds she was holding. Liu Guanhua reluctantly sat up straight.

The branch leader was indeed stern, showing no favoritism.

Pei Qian proceeded with the three matters. The first was to announce some rules for the branch, all fundamental principles of navigating the martial world, which Pei Qian had copied from martial arts novels, mainly revolving around her master’s teachings. For example, having a skill was the foundation for a martial person, acting with righteousness was the martial ethics expected, and how to discern right from wrong, break through obstacles accurately, and end matters without flaws were things that a true hero needed to contemplate. When encountering injustice, one must shout, but that alone isn’t enough.

The next matter involved a series of changes and promotions within the branch.

Lastly, she was about to go to Beiju Luozhou with Li Huai, marking the first serious venture down the mountain for the branch. Therefore, they needed to pool their experiences of navigating the martial world, with Chen Nuanshu responsible for taking notes, which would later be compiled into a book, ensuring everyone would have a copy in the future.

After discussing the serious matters, Pei Qian waved her hand, “Time for sunflower seeds!”

The atmosphere on Jise Peak was lively and cheerful.

Accompanied by the great winds and flying birds above, the cross-continent ferry of the Pima Sect smoothly docked at the Bone Beach ferry. There were two named offerings from Luoposhan, along with the sect leader Zhu Quan, stationed at the Qinglu Town of Ghost Valley: the Nascent Soul cultivator Du Wensi and the direct descendant sword cultivator Pang Lanxi from Mu Yi Mountain. Chen Lingjun, holding his hiking staff and carrying a bamboo box, stepped off the ferry. Many cultivators who had traveled south to explore Baopingzhou finally returned home, bustling and noisy, leading to disputes with several ferry cultivators, which left Chen Lingjun wide-eyed. The martial artists from Beiju Luozhou were indeed as renowned as they claimed, brimming with heroic spirit and quite generous. If this were in his own Niujiao Mountain ferry, how many would have been knocked down by the Dragon Spring Sect and the Great Li cultivators?

Chen Lingjun first visited the increasingly deserted Mural City, purchasing a set of the Goddess painting as a gift for the Pima Sect. The expenses had already been pre-paid by the Luoposhan Ancestor Hall, but Chen Lingjun didn’t use a single snowflake coin from that small treasury. For jokes, would Chen Da-ge lack that little bit of money? Back in the days when he was roaming the Jiang territory, his pockets jingled with the sound of celestial coins clinking together, like thunder. However, upon arriving in Dragon Spring County, Chen Da-ge had become a bit kinder to others; otherwise, with his fiery temper… he would have likely killed someone with a punch long ago.

Sometimes, the whimsical thoughts of Chen Lingjun made him wish that every qi cultivator in the world should reside in small towns for a while, humbly seeking advice on martial experiences.

Within the solemn Pima Sect, the sect leader Zhu Quan didn’t make an appearance, and neither did the two elders. One had been traveling for many years, while the other, the law elder Yan Su, had been busy reinforcing the mountain protecting formation with the elder from Middle Earth who came to the Pima Sect. Pang Lanxi was in seclusion, and Du Wensi was still at Qinglu Town dealing with those skeletons. Not seeing any familiar faces, Chen Lingjun grumbled about his master’s lack of stature, feeling rather disappointed that there wasn’t even a welcoming feast thrown by the sect leader to honor him. He had to maintain a demeanor as someone who had seen the world while cautiously glancing around. Years ago, at the blacksmith shop in the small town, he had nearly fallen for Ruan Qiong’s tricks, disguised as a farmer. Wasn’t that just blatant trickery? So, he felt it would be prudent to take it easy on this trip.

After greeting and receiving Chen Lingjun, the one welcoming him was a man named Wei Yusong, who was quite amiable, claiming to be the accountant who daily dealt with grievances and had the least persuasive speech. Chen Lingjun felt he had met a kindred spirit, yet he constantly reminded himself not to easily call anyone brother during this trip. Along the way, Chen Lingjun had flipped through many books, mostly about the precautions in treacherous mountainous areas. For the Pima Sect and Chunlu Garden, which his master had visited and formed ties with, he hadn’t looked closely at them. At this moment, he found Wei Yusong quite agreeable, a suitable candidate for executing important tasks. Chen Lingjun hurriedly took the chance to temporarily cling to a lifeline, secretly pulling out a booklet from his master and flipping to the section on the Pima Sect. Sure enough, he found Wei Yusong mentioned, noted by his master as a very good businessman, considered the financial god of the Pima Sect, reminding Chen Lingjun to respect him when he met him and to avoid speaking loosely.

Since he learned that the other party was a significant figure managing the sect’s finances, Chen Lingjun quickly grasped the situation. In a celestial sect, there are three types of people not to provoke: those managing sect rules, who surely are formidable; those managing finances, who won't be easy to deal with; and lastly, the young descendants of the Ancestor Hall.

After bidding farewell to Wei Yusong and refusing his invitation, Chen Lingjun set off down the mountain alone. On the way, he encountered an ordinary-looking woman who seemed to gaze at him strangely. Chen Lingjun felt a bit uncomfortable; he wasn’t Wei Bo, so why was she staring? The woman, lacking in perception, followed Chen Lingjun all the way to the foot of the mountain. At the gate, when that woman, wearing a knife at her waist, introduced herself as Zhu Quan, Chen Lingjun’s knees buckled, and he nearly lost his balance.

Zhu Quan smiled, saying, “Wei Bo has already sent a letter via flying sword to Mu Yi Mountain. If you encounter any trouble during your travels, you can report on behalf of the Pima Sect's Zhu Quan. It might not guarantee your life, but it will surely help you take revenge. Of course, it’s best if there’s no trouble. However, it will be quite difficult; if we wander through Beiju Luozhou without encountering a pile of trouble, what kind of experience would that be?”

Chen Lingjun trembled as he expressed his thanks. Zhu Quan waved her hand, and after he bid farewell, she suddenly asked, “When will Chen Ping'an return from the Sword Qi Great Wall?”

Chen Lingjun shook his head, “I’m not too sure. My master never gives a precise time of return when he travels.”

Zhu Quan glanced at Chen Lingjun’s bamboo box and hiking staff, laughing, “You all from Luoposhan travel the martial world dressed like this?”

Chen Lingjun nodded vigorously.

Zhu Quan suddenly sighed, “I somewhat envy that guy’s… freedom.”

Chen Lingjun didn’t understand the bizarre words of these high-level figures hidden in the clouds, but he could at least tell that this renowned female sect leader held a rather good impression of his master. Otherwise, she wouldn’t have specifically returned from Ghost Valley to Mu Yi Mountain just for him. Generally, celestial beings from the mountains value equality and propriety, with complex rules. The fact that Wei Yusong treated him well was already quite gratifying.

A sect leader at the fifth realm, still daring to tussle with Gao Cheng from Ghost Valley for so many years, was indeed a remarkable woman. After leaving Mu Yi Mountain, Chen Lingjun walked with a slight bounce in his step.

Following the planned route, Chen Lingjun boarded a ferry from Chunlu Garden heading to the eastern sea entrance of Jidu. The ferry operator was Jin Dan cultivator Song Lanqiao, who had now secured a position in the Chunlu Garden Ancestor Hall. After visiting Song Lanqiao, Chen Lingjun was treated with excessive courtesy. Not only was he directly arranged in a top-tier guest room, but Song Lanqiao also personally accompanied him for a long chat. In their conversation, besides the genuine warmth he felt for Chen Ping'an and Luoposhan, his humility also put Chen Lingjun in a more awkward position.

Now, Luoposhan, Piyun Mountain, Pima Sect, and Chunlu Garden had formed alliances. Among them, Wei Yusong and Tang Xi from Pima Sect were responsible for the various matters. Song Lanqiao and Tang Xi were allies, and to become a member of the Chunlu Garden Ancestor Hall, they owed their thanks to the young sword immortal Chen Ping'an. What’s more, the latter was also the mentor of Song Lanqiao’s own mentor, and they had an affinity. Song Lanqiao had almost never met his own master, yet his unrelenting thoughts on an outsider had gone beyond mere relations.

The farther Chen Lingjun traveled from home, the more he missed it.

Everyone missed it, even the old blind Daoist who had been cultivating on Huang Lake would often think of it.

During the farewell from the ferry, Wei Bo had said that for cultivators, using techniques to kill or pressing people with power was not too difficult; the challenge lay in winning the hearts of others.

It was the first time Chen Lingjun carefully reviewed the contents he had previously overlooked. Then he went to the observation deck, leaning against the railing, gazing blankly. The bright moon hung high in the sky, half-hidden behind the sea of clouds, appearing both far and near, as if the ferry could crash into it with just a slight change of direction, just like a traveler passing through an archway.

Whether his master was in Luoposhan made a significant difference, which Chen Lingjun had sensed long ago. 

Only by leaving Luoposhan and embarking on this journey could he understand why it felt different and what made it different.

When living with his master, it was easy to overlook his realm and status. But as Chen Lingjun walked along the paths his master had once walked, he discovered that the boy from Niping Lane he had reluctantly followed back then had indeed changed and become quite formidable.

Chen Lingjun collected his thoughts, packed his belongings, greeted Song Lanqiao, and then midway left the ferry, heading to Sui Jia City, straight to the Fire God Temple.

Under the secret planning of the Dragon King of Cangjun Lake, the Fire God Temple, which had once fallen into ruin, was rebuilt. The local government spent heavily to recreate a painted statue, and the incense offerings were abundant. Chen Lingjun chose to visit late at night, respectfully knocking on the door. Upon seeing the man, who appeared to have a low realm, Chen Lingjun presented many celestial wines. The man, upon revealing his true self, was quite pleased; however, when it came to matters concerning Chen Ping'an, he didn’t ask a word.

Chen Lingjun felt that this older brother suited his taste; he was very much like him, brimming with the spirit of the martial world!

Thus, both sides drank, without needing any persuasion.

Not only had his master noted this in books and documents, but he had also specifically reminded Chen Lingjun verbally that this local deity was a friend of his and owed him a drink.

On the side of Cangjun Lake, upon receiving the report from the Fire God Temple’s priest, the Dragon King, Yin Hou, immediately rushed over at night without bringing any confidants. For a lake king whose domain encompassed the entire Sui Jia City, this was just a few extra steps in his own courtyard.

Seeing the rosy-faced child, who was flailing his hands and legs while chatting, the lake king was momentarily stunned. How did the Chen sword immortal come to have such a friend?

Just a meal, and they both felt satisfied.

However, after Yin Hou arrived, the man from the Fire God Temple treated him with respect but was not particularly enthusiastic, while he enjoyed drinking with Chen Lingjun.

In the morning, Chen Lingjun departed from the Fire God Temple and visited the Golden Crow Palace, paying a visit to the Golden Core bottleneck sword cultivator, Liu Zhiqing.

He was again treated with great courtesy, respectfully escorted to the mountain where Liu Zhiqing was in closed-door cultivation.

When Chen Lingjun saw Liu Zhiqing, the handsome young man’s celestial demeanor, adorned with a golden hairpin and clad in a snow-white long robe, made it seem as if all the renowned mountains and rivers in the world were waiting for such a cultivator’s visit.

Liu Zhiqing smiled and inquired if Chen Lingjun wanted tea. Chen Lingjun declined repeatedly. Liu Zhiqing didn’t insist; in fact, there wasn’t much for them to discuss. Liu Zhiqing was not one of those adept at socializing among mountain cultivators. The two exchanged polite words; when Chen Lingjun had nothing to say, Liu Zhiqing didn’t press him to stay longer. As Chen Lingjun stood up to leave, Liu Zhiqing offered to see him to the foot of the mountain. Chen Lingjun realized this person was in closed-door cultivation, so he hurriedly rejected the offer, dashing down the mountain. Upon reaching the foot of the mountain, when the palace master awaited him, Chen Lingjun also refused the banquet invitation, expressing his apologies, gratitude, and promising to meet again, all in one breath, growing increasingly adept.

Afterward, he went to Chunlu Garden without taking the celestial ferry again.

After all, it was his nature to be close to water. Chen Lingjun chose a common boat, sailing through the painted landscape, amidst the calls of monkeys on both banks, as he visited the myriad mountains.

Upon reaching the territory of Chunlu Garden, Chen Lingjun didn’t rush to find his acquaintance Song Lanqiao to chat but instead followed the atlas, first strolling along the scenic spots of the river entering the sea, then going to Chunlu Garden to explore Yuying Cliff. After that, he visited the Ant Shop established by his master, which was well-run by the steward, thriving with business. Chen Lingjun worked there as a shop assistant for two days.

That night, the entire Chunlu Garden suddenly held a sword festival.

The entire place lit up brightly, and Chen Lingjun quickly opened the shop, looking up to see the bustling street below. It was said that a sword immortal had fallen at the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Far away from his hometown, Chen Lingjun thought of the master who was even farther away and sat on the threshold, resting his chin on his hands, his expression dim.

On the southern battlefield of the Sword Qi Great Wall, the golden river appeared for the third time.

A young man carried a sword box filled with borrowed swords from the sword shop.

Chen Ping'an stood atop the city wall, gazing at the battlefield momentarily. In a single step, he leaped down, plunging towards the ground. During the descent, he rolled up his sleeves. Just as he was about to land, he slightly bent his knees, stepping on the void. As he shot forward, the ground erupted beneath him, creating a massive pit, rumbling from deep within.

He didn’t ride the sword but instead rode the wind.

Like an arrow, he suddenly soared over a hundred feet away from the city wall, pressing down on the heads of two demon cultivators, effortlessly pushing their decaying corpses away.

When Chen Ping'an floated to the ground, all the sword cultivators around instinctively vacated the area, automatically making way for the young hidden official who was going out for the third time to kill.

The Sword Qi Great Wall no longer bore any traces of resentment, for the young hidden official was originally a sword cultivator, and he could kill even more effectively.

A martial artist from the demon clan, clad in heavy armor and wielding a spear, charged straight at him. The young hidden official advanced in a straight line, casually smashing the spear with his head, shattering the opponent's body with a punch. When he stepped heavily on the ground, his fists were not yet raised, but the intent of his punches surged forth.

Within a dozen feet around Chen Ping'an, the intent of his punches flowed like a raging tide. Furthermore, a second, even larger punch aura emerged from afar, stirring vigorously, with layers of punch frames and divine intent, radiating like overlapping halos of the moon.

In the center stood the martial artist, at the peak of his power. 

(End of Chapter)

 ### Chapter 775: A Sparrow in a Cage

Chen Ping'an journeyed southward alone, and wherever he went, spells and spiritual artifacts poured down like a torrential rain.

It wasn't long before he encountered a formidable opponent—a short man clad in resplendent crimson armor, wearing a phoenix-winged golden crown adorned with two long peacock feathers, reminiscent of the flamboyant costumes seen in the bustling theaters of the world. 

Only someone unafraid of death, or perhaps qualified to be unafraid, would dare to flaunt themselves on the battlefield of the Sword Qi Great Wall. This practitioner of the demon race was exceptionally swift, almost as if using a teleportation spell, appearing at Chen Ping'an's side in an instant. With a single fist, he shattered the dense martial intent protecting Chen Ping'an, striking him directly on the temple and sending him flying dozens of yards.

Chen Ping'an slapped the ground with his palm, performing a graceful spin before standing firmly. The opponent, like a shadow, mirrored his movement and exchanged a punch with him.

Both combatants slid backward nearly simultaneously, carving a trench in the earth that barely reached their knees. The demon warrior shook his right wrist, removed a feather with two fingers from his left hand, and spoke in the local dialect of the Sword Qi Great Wall, "You must be the new Hidden Official? Have you stepped into the realm of martial arts? Your punches pack quite a wallop; no wonder you lost three times to Cao Ci before winning three against Yu Juanfu."

He raised his right hand, signaling the surrounding demon army to step back and leave the battlefield to himself and the young Hidden Official from the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Chen Ping'an gave a thumbs-up, wiping the blood from the corner of his mouth, then rubbed his temple with his palm. The force behind that blow was considerable; his opponent was likely at the Mountain Peak realm among demon warriors, relying on a naturally resilient physique, making him harder to deal with. Yet, as a ninth-tier warrior, equipped with martial luck, he shouldn't have been this reckless. The way he dressed and fought was far too "carefree."

Understanding quickly, Chen Ping'an took the unusual step of speaking with his adversary on the battlefield. "Are you the strongest eighth-tier warrior from the wild world? Looking for a chance to break through and gain martial luck?"

The short man let go of the feather in his hand, which bounced up, and he nodded with a smile. "What do you say? How about a friendly spar? If I say no, no one will believe me. I can’t guarantee that some sneaky sword cultivator assassins won’t join in, but it’s fine—just give me your nod, and anyone who interferes, including you, will be my enemy, and I’ll deal with them all."

Chen Ping'an extended a hand, pointing toward the Sword Qi Great Wall. "Inside the city, there's a senior in the ninth realm who taught me some boxing techniques. You can go ask him."

The short man's expression darkened; he had shown sincerity, yet this highly reputed young Hidden Official was proving to be quite unreasonable.

Chen Ping'an continued, "Let me put it to you this way: as a martial artist, no matter who you lose to—even if it's Cao Ci—there’s no such thing as losing with honor. A loss is a loss. This shows that the strongest wandering realm martial artist from the wild world, regardless of how tough his fists may be, lacks the spirit and ambition expected of a martial artist. If you are to be called 'the strongest' and step into the ninth realm, that would be a huge joke."

Their exchange bore little substance.

Each was calculating their own interests. The short man feigned bravado, wanting to use the young Hidden Official as a stepping stone for his martial path. Should he succeed in breaking through, he could gain not only the martial luck from the wild world but also a portion of the martial luck legacy from the Sword Qi Great Wall. 

As for Chen Ping'an, he was secretly searching for the first swordsman of the wild world. Previously, the Three Teachings Sage had cultivated the golden river twice, and after two encounters outside the city, Chen Ping'an had crossed paths with that individual. Their exchanges had appeared tentative, as if neither was using their full strength, but the subtleties intertwined. The first one to slip would be the one to perish, and death would come in ways too unremarkable to impress the observing sword cultivators of lower realms.

The short man seemed to lose interest in their mental sparring, lightly kicking the gravel beneath his boots. "We can chat standing up, but soon, I’ll give you the chance to lie down and talk. By the way, I’m called Hou Kuimen."

Chen Ping'an rested his hand on his back, slightly turned his head, and pointed to his temple, indicating he was ready for another punch.

An idea struck him; it was time to test the waters. The precondition for this was to let his opponent have a go first.

Hou Kuimen, of course, was not polite.

After throwing a punch, Hou Kuimen hesitated for a moment, choosing not to pursue the advantage. He stood still, watching the young man he had just sent flying. 

The young man, who hadn't dodged or countered, landed heavily on the ground, stopping his momentum, and smiled back at Hou Kuimen, a hint of mockery in his expression.

Hou Kuimen had just been wary of a trap, so he had held back a little.

A young Hidden Official renowned for his cunning wouldn’t be foolish enough to just stand there and let himself be killed.

Thus, after his successful punch, he felt a twinge of regret. If that punch had not been simply a probe but a full-force strike, would that young man still be standing?

But why had his opponent taken that punch head-on?

Chen Ping'an pointed to his chest. "Again."

Hou Kuimen raised both arms, his fingers gripping the feathers. His attire, the bright crimson armor, the golden crown, and the two shimmering feathers, were not ordinary mountain artifacts but a complete set of ancient treasures. After refinement, they had changed appearances, but their quality remained intact—a semi-divine weapon, both offensive and defensive, named the Sword Cage, capable of restraining a sword immortal's flying sword for a moment. Without their life-sustaining flying sword, sword immortals were forced to compete based on physical ability when approached.

Hou Kuimen released the two feathers, and with a flash, he appeared in front of the young man who sought death, extending his fist. The young Hidden Official was sent tumbling away.

Chen Ping'an stood up, spitting out blood, and shot a glance at Hou Kuimen, cursing under his breath in his hometown dialect.

He had intended for this eighth-tier peak warrior to help him break through the seventh-tier bottleneck, yet Hou Kuimen had been sluggish in both his punches, making Chen Ping'an, who was used to the weight of Li Er's fists on Lion Peak in North Ju Lu Prefecture, feel as if he had just received two slaps from a woman.

Now, the Sword Qi Great Wall was circulating a fair saying: whether watching the young Hidden Official strike or being struck, it was always a delightful sight.

Hou Kuimen's expression was complex.

Chen Ping'an inquired in the refined dialect of the wild world, "Are you trying to kill the Hidden Official for merit, or are you here to spar with a martial artist to break through?!"

Hou Kuimen took a deep breath, lightly tapping his fists together, and said solemnly, "The last punch—if you don’t die, I lose. Chen Ping'an, I know you have your own ambitions too. It’s fine; let’s see whose boxing skills are superior! You can just counter."

Chen Ping'an furrowed his brows.

Vaguely, Hou Kuimen's overwhelming martial intent coalesced around him, creating a hazy atmosphere akin to a sage presiding over a small world.

Years ago, at the Shujian Lake, during his travels with Zhang Ye of Qingxia Island, Chen Ping'an had already noticed he could catch glimpses of such signs.

He shook out his sleeves, rolling them up lightly.

In that instant.

On the battlefield, dust swirled, obscuring the sky and blocking the sun.

The swirling sand was mixed with the piercing martial intent that shot out in all directions, chaotic like countless tiny flying swords scattering.

Moments later, the earth trembled, and the sand dispersed, revealing Hou Kuimen clutching his neck with one hand, blood seeping between his fingers, while the other hand formed a fist, glancing around.

Finally, Hou Kuimen spotted a demon race practitioner behind him, as the young Hidden Official’s left hand plunged a short knife into the back of a sword cultivator’s heart, while his right hand gently swept across their neck.

Hou Kuimen could hardly articulate, his voice slurred, "Chen Ping'an, I’ve personally experienced your abilities as a Hidden Official, but as a pure martial artist, I’m truly disappointed—so very disappointed."

It turned out that during their previous spar, the young Hidden Official had taken Hou Kuimen's punch head-on but had drawn a knife from his sleeve, stabbing upwards directly into Hou Kuimen's neck. Not only that, but with a swift motion of his left hand, he had slammed the knife's handle, forcing Hou Kuimen—had he not stomped and lifted himself up, then retreated a few steps—to nearly have his tongue sliced by the blade before it could have punctured his skull.

If he were a pure martial artist from the wild world, without a naturally resilient physique to support him, being thus injured would have rendered him incapable of uttering a single word.

Chen Ping'an gently pushed aside the corpse of the sword cultivator behind him, gathering sound into a line, and smiled at Hou Kuimen. "In your three punches, which one was worthy of a pure martial artist? If your first punch had been pure enough, I wouldn’t have minded exchanging three punches with you. Who knows, we might even break through together—that would be a true contest of life and death, solely dependent on skill."

After Chen Ping'an made his appearance, a large space opened up on the battlefield.

The young Hidden Official gripped his short blades with both hands, loosening and then firmly grasping them again.

This was a small habit he had learned from Yu Lu. As for the posture of holding the blades, it was inspired by a knife-wielding stance he had observed at the Sword Water Mountain Villa in the Shuishui Kingdom. Indeed, in the world below, assassins and knife-fighters also employed this stance, but to Chen Ping'an, it seemed insufficient—merely a lifeless form.

Hou Kuimen, knowing only the young Hidden Official from the Sword Qi Great Wall, was unaware of Chen Ping'an's habits in combat.

When he began to act hesitantly, it was surely in pursuit of some follow-up.

Otherwise, all words would only come after life and death had been decided.

Hou Kuimen did not retreat; instead, his martial intent intensified. Good.

Chen Ping'an sheathed the dual blades he had taken from the assassin at the Deer Cutting Mountain in North Ju Lu Prefecture, standing his ground.

Hou Kuimen, employing some secret technique, halted the blood flow from his neck, his arms hanging down, completely motionless.

This was the true essence of a martial artist's spar, the mindset that should be present.

After that, wherever the two figures went, it was bound to bring calamity upon the fish in the pond.

The two pure martial artists, each at their martial bottlenecks, were like two flying swords, cutting through the battlefield recklessly, leaving behind a trail of dismembered limbs and corpses.

As Hou Kuimen’s punches became increasingly “light,” the weight of his martial intent grew heavier.

Every strike bore the essence of a ninth-tier warrior, signaling a momentous opportunity for breakthrough.

For reasons unknown, the young Hidden Official, widely recognized as a sword cultivator, had yet to summon his flying sword, not even touching any of the blades in his sword case behind him.

Far across the battlefield, a “middle-aged man” who was a comrade of the young Hidden Official seemed swept along by the demon army, advancing toward the Sword Qi Great Wall. He had been keeping a close eye on the clash between Chen Ping'an and Hou Kuimen, sensing some underlying hints. He hesitated, contemplating whether to disrupt Chen Ping'an’s plans.

However, after scanning a few locations and weighing the distance, he chose to refrain from intervening, unwilling to compete for military merit with the talented figures at the Jia Shen camp.

Hou Kuimen, bloodied and battered, a dignified eighth-tier peak warrior adorned with precious treasures, found himself in an utterly inconceivable situation against a younger warrior of a lower tier.

Standing there, covered in blood, Hou Kuimen suddenly halted, chuckling softly to himself, raising his head to fixate on the equally startled young man who had just retracted his fists.

Hou Kuimen seemed to say: once I reach the ninth tier, with martial luck at my side, it will be time for me, Hou Kuimen, to be unreasonable. All your elaborate plans—will they still prevail? Will you escape this battlefield alive? If you have the capability, why not break through yourself, Chen Ping'an?!

This exchange, where the higher realm should have had the upper hand, had fallen to an unexpected disadvantage. The crux lay not in Hou Kuimen’s lack of physical prowess or the lightness of his fists; rather, it was that Chen Ping'an seemed to anticipate every move.

At that moment, witnessing Chen Ping'an’s wary demeanor, Hou Kuimen felt a thrill of exhilaration. Throughout his life of training in martial arts, he had never felt such a rush during a breakthrough. Today, Chen Ping'an would help him break through; afterward, he’d leave him whole, provided he could withstand the punches he would deliver once he attained the ninth tier!

The martial luck from the wild world surged forth, descending upon the battlefield and wildly rushing toward Hou Kuimen.

Chen Ping'an smiled knowingly; they had finally arrived.

Hou Kuimen's punches were too light, incapable of shattering his bottleneck; at most, they would help him temper some crucial muscles and bones—merely an embellishment. 

Considering the potential impact on future battles, many ninth-tier punches targeted key acupoints. Should they strike him, Chen Ping'an was not afraid of injury, but rather of the martial intent creating chaos within his small world. Thus, he could not afford to endure all of it, needing to offload the majority. While Hou Kuimen may have enjoyed throwing punches, Chen Ping'an felt no satisfaction in countering them.

It was fine; he had experience in fending off martial luck, having done so more than once in the Old Dragon City.

Moreover, Chen Ping'an had endured heavenly tribulations twice in North Ju Lu Prefecture, and had faced off against true opponents at the Sword Qi Great Wall.

With a tip of his toes, Chen Ping'an shot into the sky, ascending straight upward without throwing a punch, merely striving to rise higher, as if he wouldn’t stop until he reached the highest point of the firmament. Even without striking, he met the surging martial luck from the wild world with a punch intent akin to clouds rising over a vast marsh.

The “middle-aged man” paused in his tracks, looking up and muttering to himself, “Can martial luck be snatched? Is business really done this way?”

Because that young Hidden Official had employed some strange method, he seemed to be pulling all the martial luck white rain into the sky, making him appear as if he were ascending with the white rain.

In essence, martial luck in the world was a profoundly ethereal existence; otherwise, even the central Confucian temples of the Great Harmony world would have been unable to intercept it, leading to a situation where they could only let it flow among the talented martial artists across the nine continents.

In the wild world, even the Moon-Touching Mountain could not restrain such matters.

The most awkward position belonged to Hou Kuimen, who could not access the martial luck that had come his way.

With his knees slightly bent, Hou Kuimen also ascended, chasing after the young man whose figure had become as small as a mustard seed, hoping to get closer to the martial luck.

The sword cultivator self-identifying as a "middle-aged man" still refrained from launching a surprise attack on Chen Ping'an. It was not out of respect for rules or righteousness; in the heat of battle, he and Chen Ping'an shared similar styles. Each attack, and indeed each exchange of injuries with opponents, felt like a meticulous transaction.

This young sword cultivator, regarded as superior to Li Zhen and Zhuo Jie in the Sword Immortal rankings, sensed a hint of profound truth from the Dao.

If he struck now, even if successful, it would only bring him losses in his pursuit of the Dao, because in this life and this world, he would only attract the invisible weight of martial luck from heaven and earth.

If he were a pure martial artist, honing his martial path in this way would be beneficial, but alas, he was ultimately a sword cultivator.

No!

That Chen Ping'an's martial intent and motives were all a façade.

Suddenly, he extended his right hand, directly summoning a long sword from a nearby demon sword cultivator. With a gentle shake, he shattered it into dozens of sword fragments. Simultaneously, his left wrist twisted, forcibly shattering several veins with his own sword intent, blood oozing out, which he then smeared across the shards of the sword.

The young sword cultivator, employing one of his many hidden techniques, flicked his sleeve, sending the fragments shooting skyward, aimed straight at Hou Kuimen.

Almost simultaneously, Hou Kuimen's view blurred as the figure a hundred yards away first used a ground-shrinking talisman, then drew two refined flying swords, Song Zhen and Ke Lei, as a guiding force.

Holding his blades in both hands, he struck Hou Kuimen's jaw, piercing through his cheek, and then stabbed into his heart. After landing the hit, he used the ground-shrinking talisman to vanish instantly.

In the next moment, the sword fragments hovered around Hou Kuimen, forming a miniature sword formation, shielding this temporarily ambiguous eighth or ninth-tier martial demon.

Had they not arrived in time, Chen Ping'an would have been able to cleanly sever Hou Kuimen's head.

Gritting his teeth after taking two blows, Hou Kuimen's figure "ascended," momentarily stalling as he continued to soar into the sky, while the martial luck was once again being drawn higher by that young Hidden Official.

Once it was confirmed that Hou Kuimen's life was secure, the sword fragments quickly flickered away, returning to the “middle-aged man.”

The two pure martial artists crashed through two layers of expansive cloud seas.

One layer was just slightly higher than the city walls of the Sword Qi Great Wall, while the higher cloud sea towered far above the city.

Suddenly rising above the cloud sea, Chen Ping'an furrowed his brow again, but this time, it was not about the authenticity or deceit of Hou Kuimen’s actions.

He sensed a genuinely ominous aura of conspiracy.

The martial luck at the higher altitude was undeniably real.

Though Hou Kuimen was unaware of why the young Hidden Official had paused, he still approached the undulating martial luck like a dragon moving through water.

After a moment of contemplation, Chen Ping'an decided to abandon all previous plans and plunged back down into the cloud sea, returning to the ground.

Hou Kuimen would gladly accept the martial luck that was rightfully his. Above the cloud sea, the sun shone brightly, making Hou Kuimen appear like a divine being.

But in an instant, his eyes turned pitch black. After struggling for a moment, he began following Chen Ping'an, dragging the martial luck along with him back toward the ground.

The martial luck surged into Hou Kuimen's body, propelling him toward Chen Ping'an.

Chen Ping'an changed his retreat trajectory three times but still could not evade.

Upon the earth's surface, a massive pit was created, resembling the explosion of a sword immortal's life-sustaining flying sword.

Hou Kuimen, a ninth-tier martial artist, along with all his martial luck, was utterly obliterated.

At the Jia Shen camp, five sword immortal prospects from the wild world no longer concealed their presence, appearing at the edges of the vast pit, each taking their position.

Zhuo Jie, Li Zhen, Yu Si, Liu Bai, and Tan.

The middle-aged man sighed, hiding his figure and departing.

It seemed that a great demon, using its innate divine powers, had possessed the soon-to-breakthrough Hou Kuimen, sacrificing a sure ninth-tier martial artist to heavily injure the young Hidden Official, Chen Ping'an.

Zhuo Jie spoke, “Be cautious; this may be a trap.”

A soft, smiling voice echoed in everyone’s hearts simultaneously, “How could that be possible?”

*(End of Chapter)*

 **Chapter 776: Surrounding One and Being Surrounded by One**

Only the sound could be heard, but the person was nowhere to be seen.

Liu Bai had been closely observing the battlefield situation around her. She communicated swiftly through her mind voice, "This situation has arisen suddenly, and there are currently no Sword Immortals to assist us. We must resolve this quickly."

This woman swordsman, who had emerged from the same lineage as the Sword Immortal Shoucheng, had been serving as the vice commander under the main officer in the Jia Shen camp and had yet to draw her sword.

The young swordsman Tan was the first to summon his life-bound flying sword, which flew low and traced a long shimmering sword light around the edge of the pit that remained for a long time.

"We must force the opponent to reveal themselves!" 

With two swords hanging at his waist, Tan pressed his hands on the sword hilts and focused intently on the dusty bottom of the pit. The fine dust could not obscure a swordsman's vision, yet he could not discern what clever tricks the opponent had employed to hide the figure of the young Hidden Official. However, Chen Ping'an had definitely not left this place. Tan communicated with his friends through his mind voice: "It doesn’t matter. Since I can’t see him, I’ll go down to investigate directly. We won’t give him a chance to recuperate. Zhu Ke, pay attention to the movements at the mountain's base beneath the ground. Liu Bai, be on guard for any strikes that might intercept Chen Ping'an."

With that, Tan leaped down, using his life-bound flying sword "Jia Qi" to pave the way. As the sword light dissipated at the edge of the pit, thousands of tiny iron cavalry appeared, densely packed and arrayed. Although each was only the size of a palm, they looked comical; in truth, every single one was like a flying sword. In an instant, countless miniature iron cavalry surged down the slope from the top of the pit, like a tide pouring into a depression.

The flying sword "Jia Qi" took the lead, advancing in a manner most suitable for probing the subtle traps set by the young Hidden Official.

If Tan were a swordsman from the Sword Qi Great Wall, relying solely on this life-bound flying sword, he would at least be rated as a second-tier by the Hidden Official lineage, on par with Yue Qing's hundred-foot spring and Lark in the Sky, as well as Qishou's Jumping Pearl.
