Should this life-bound flying sword possess more mysteries, it might even be comparable to Wu Chengpei's "Ganlin."

Zhu Ke, as the first disciple of Liu Cha, would have been the only true inheritor if Liu Cha had not taken in a group of named disciples during this battle.

However, since the war began, Zhu Ke had not taken action, remaining more enigmatic than Liu Bai, the female swordsman in the same military tent. Apart from his widely known lineage, the details of his flying swords, life-bound supernatural abilities, and swordsmanship were all unknown. Behind him, a massive sword rack bore six long swords that now detached, encircling the pit. Eventually, the sword tips turned downwards, and each sword plunged into the ground, forming a formation deep underground that would not allow the already injured young Hidden Official any chance to escape. Even if he had the strength to break through the sword formation, he would leave traces behind. At that time, the young Hidden Official would face the interception of fierce flying swords, and there would definitely be more than one.

Yushi wore a black robe, with only a snow-white silk ribbon tying back his hair, looking like a dashing noble.

His thoughts stirred slightly, and several broken weapons on the nearby ground suddenly flew off in different directions before crashing to the ground. Where they passed, there was not a ripple of movement, indicating there were no formations or traps. Logically speaking, from the moment Chen Ping'an clashed with the bait, Hou Kuimen, to the point where Hou Kuimen was possessed by the great demon of the Throne, wielding immense power, even risking mutual destruction with Chen Ping'an, Chen Ping'an had been caught in one unexpected situation after another. Even clad in a magical robe of celestial rank, he should have suffered greatly.

Yet, Yushi still felt something was amiss.

Li Zhen squatted down, pinching a handful of soil and lightly rubbing it. The dust scattered and flew, clinging to a trace of sword intent. Looking around with a smile, Li Zhen said, "Indeed, something is odd. This is a forbidden place similar to a small world. In our last skirmish, he didn’t display this level of skill. Good, very good; now I can accept losing."

As it turned out, the dust that drifted ten zhang away ignited like a wick, instantly turning to ash.

Yushi again manipulated some shattered instruments and the remnants of the demon race, sending them flying into the distance. 

Sure enough, they crashed down like hitting a wall.

The young Hidden Official was both a swordsman and a pure warrior, making him particularly troublesome to kill. Even if he exhausted a breath of pure qi, he could switch to swordsmanship to kill. Once his spiritual energy needed replenishing, he would resort to his martial prowess. The interchange between martial qi and swordsman's spiritual energy was endless. Therefore, in the second skirmish outside the city, when the Jia Shen camp recorded the battle merits of both sides, the young Hidden Official ranked highest among the swordsmen from the Sword Qi Great Wall, having participated throughout the entire battle. This was certainly related to the Sword Immortals needing to guard the Golden River; the Sword Immortals stationed at the city would either defend a given area or shield the younger swordsmen. True opportunities for the Sword Immortals to draw their swords would be limited.

During that battle, the young Hidden Official had constantly concealed his identity and shifted his aura, employing myriad tactics. Unlike the first skirmish outside the city, where Ning Yao protected the formation, allowing him to openly array as a pure warrior, the second time on the battlefield resembled more of a scavenging assassin. Only when absolutely necessary did he resort to using fists and swords for combat. Thus, in the various military camps of the Wildlands, this swordsman from the Sword Qi Great Wall earned a fresh title: Southern Shoucheng, Northern Hidden Official.

Finding Chen Ping'an on the battlefield had become increasingly difficult. Even if they found him, injuring him would be even harder. Even if they were willing to exchange injuries with Chen Ping'an or even risk death for an injury, the other party's retreat was exceptionally decisive. The key was that Chen Ping'an’s combat capabilities were astonishing, making the young Hidden Official, who operated in such a sneaky manner, the most infuriating opponent compared to the more straightforward and powerful Sword Immortals from the Sword Qi Great Wall.

"Goodness, I nearly fell for it. Everyone, I apologize; it was my oversight earlier."

Yushi was inwardly furious as he pressed down on the sword he wore, condensing sword intent into substance. Strands of white sword energy swirled around his arm and sword hilt, creating a chilling aura as a thin layer of frost spread across the entire sword sheath. "But from this, we can see he’s been seriously injured. Otherwise, with Li Zhen's ploy, our Hidden Official would have continued concealing himself and wouldn’t have exposed his flaws this quickly. As an apology, my last strike will be the one!"

Those not in the Jia Shen camp would certainly find Yushi's last remark utterly baffling.

Zhu Ke furrowed his brow and asked, "Li Zhen, how did this small world come to be? Did it borrow from the Saints? Can small worlds even be borrowed?"

Among them, only Li Zhen could claim to be the foremost expert on small worlds.

Li Zhen had already begun strolling about, just as he had during his initial confrontation with Chen Ping'an. Every few steps, he tossed out a treasured item from the mountain. Being the door disciple of the Moonlit Mountain, he lacked for magical treasures.

Moreover, Li Zhen's formation technique was exceptionally profound.

Li Zhen did not trust Zhu Ke's underground sword formation and felt he had to lay down another formation himself to be at ease. This would both prevent Chen Ping'an from breaking out and slightly impede the Sword Immortals' rescue.

Li Zhen smiled, "Heaven knows how it came to be. The urgent matter is to ascertain the mysteries of this small world. Can it assist Chen Ping'an in rising a realm, or is it a place specifically targeting Qi Practitioners that cannot be traversed? Or is it merely a trick to delay the battle, allowing the Sword Immortals to arrive in time to rendezvous with Chen Ping'an?"

Yushi was already inspecting the matter. Around him, the remnants of limbs and broken bodies hovered in the air, bumping into that invisible wall nearby. Yushi glanced into the pit, where the dust had already been dispersed by him; the scene at the bottom remained shrouded in white fog. "Aside from the barrier that severs heaven and earth, the situation at the pit bottom is still uncertain. It seems there’s nothing strange surrounding us. Why don’t we just strike and break this small world?"

Li Zhen shook his head, squatting down to press the final magical treasure deep into the ground while responding with his mind voice, "Not much meaning in that. Chen Ping'an wouldn’t mind if we left now. Don’t forget what our goal is: to surround and kill Chen Ping'an. I’ve already tested him with flying sand and have my answer. Just as you suspected, Chen Ping'an is indeed seriously injured. Through this small world’s tricks, ultimately, he’s still stalling for time. Let’s see what result Tan achieves with his strike."

Yushi felt quite helpless.

With the encirclement in place, they couldn’t find the person, which was quite frustrating.

In the pit, the iron cavalry army had spears attached with colorful banners, vibrant and colorful.

The colorful flags and tassels attached to the spears were the second aspect of Tan's life-bound supernatural ability.

Refining swords required various rare materials, among which the most crucial was soil from the roots of the five great mountains in the Wildlands. It wasn’t merely for show that the "Iron Cavalry Army" had manifested.

Tan, feeling slightly unsettled, focused again and realized he was hovering above a sea of clouds, where several peaks faintly rose above the clouds like islands.

The heavens were vast.

Tan immediately stopped riding the wind and hovered in the air, looking down at the ground, which resembled a battlefield with iron cavalry charging, yet they were all like headless flies, the geographical situation completely illogical. Many iron cavalry that were initially far apart suddenly collided with each other in an instant.

In his line of sight was a troop of verdant iron cavalry, crushing past a crimson army adorned with colorful banners.

Yet Tan did not retrieve his life-bound flying sword "Jia Qi." As long as the iron cavalry trod upon the earth, even in this illusory small world, all the spears attached to banners of the iron cavalry would remain unharmed. In fact, the battlefield was just like this: the iron cavalry continuously shattered and yet continuously regenerated, tirelessly launching one charge after another. Tan quickly discovered the subtlety of this battlefield, as if it were a series of thin chapters of paper, intricately folded by someone behind the scenes, making the marching routes of the iron cavalry entirely within the opponent’s control.

Tan realized that his voice could no longer communicate with Zhu Ke and the others. Trapped in a predicament, the young swordsman still maintained a clear mind, drawing out his twin swords and vanishing in a flash.

After one sword disappeared, a curtain of lightning interwove across the sky, surging wildly, continuously unfolding breathtaking scenes.

One sword transformed into a rainbow, flying urgently toward the farthest point, trying to ascertain the size of this small world.

Tan reached out and grabbed what should have flown thousands of zhang away—a second sword—only for it to stab straight into his back, caught in the young man's hand.

Tan sneered, "Sneaky tricks, relying on some flashy maneuvers to wear me down?"

Atop a peak, a figure as small as a mustard seed suddenly grew as large as a mountain, the towering figure in a blue robe, bearing a sword box.

The law form stood tall on the mountaintop.

It was as if a person stood atop a roadside stone.

Chen Ping'an smiled, looking down at the sword-wielding youth, raising a hand to produce a jade bamboo fan gifted by a student, and swiftly slapped it down. The surrounding sea of clouds was pulled by that overwhelming force, rolling as if boiling, with faint sounds of thunder.

Tan remained utterly still, allowing the great fan to strike down upon him, ultimately passing through.

Tan sneered, "Your true self is indeed heavily injured, relying solely on illusions to delay things."

Chen Ping'an raised a hand again, palm cradling a law seal, flipping it over. The seal appeared like a mountain, once more heading toward Tan.

Tan swung a sword, cleaving the mountain seal in two without a ripple of energy, only the brilliance of the sword.

Once again, it was a false manifestation born from intent.

Tan shook his long sword and beckoned towards the young Hidden Official who was putting on a show.

That "Chen Ping'an" smiled slightly and produced a golden talisman. Due to the immense size of the talisman held by the law form, it appeared overwhelmingly large in Tan's eyes, resembling a golden lightning pool, filled with thunderous energy, drifting toward the young swordsman.

At the same time, Chen Ping'an's law form raised his left hand gently. On the ground, a mountain range was directly uprooted, rising from below, complementing the golden talisman that overshadowed Tan, soaring down toward him.

Tan touched the sword body with his fingertip, pressing the tip of the sword, which burst forth with dazzling brilliance, ultimately creating a large circle of sword light centered around the young swordsman, crashing into the talisman and mountain.

This time, the young Hidden Official's action indeed involved real objects!

Tan’s heart surged with inspiration and he leaned back abruptly, fingers forming a seal. The magical robe on his body radiated a dazzling rainbow of colors, revealing numerous charming celestial musicians, their figures small and adorable, immediately shielding all the vital points of the youth.

Tan directed his sword away from the original spot, and in the next moment, a golden-bodied law form appeared behind him, a stunningly beautiful celestial maiden who slightly bent over, cradling the young man’s figure with her hands.

A long string of blood droplets slowly oozed from Tan's neck.

The long sword beneath the young man's feet trembled slowly, seemingly suppressed by the underlying principles of heaven and earth.

The golden-bodied law form protecting the young man began to show signs of deterioration, the originally flawless dazzling golden form corroding rapidly.

Holding the sword, Tan lightly wiped away the blood from his neck.

It was evidently a place of "impossibility" targeting all Qi Practitioners.

He had nearly lost his head to that fellow's blade.

The youth finally understood the feelings of those who had battled against the young Hidden Official.

Illusions and realities, truth and falsehood, all were matters of the heart and calculations.

On the battlements of the Sword Qi Great Wall, Wei Jin asked the old Sword Immortal, "Do you really not need me to intervene?"

Chen Qingdu smiled, "Intervene? Whose rescue are you talking about, Chen Ping'an or you, Wei Jin? Do you think the other side has no backup plan? Just those five excellent Sword Immortal candidates—who will be responsible for escorting them away? If any of them dies, the Jia Zi camp will suffer."

Wei Jin replied, "With Lu Zhi helping to stabilize the situation, I can give it a try."

Chen Qingdu shook his head, "Just wait and see. Whoever strikes last will gain the upper hand."

Chen Qingdu gazed toward the numerous demon military tents in the south. Even if Zhou Mi were to intervene, it would be manageable. However, Liu Cha, if he found an opportunity to draw his sword, would cause some trouble for the Sword Qi Great Wall. 

For instance, if a disciple he held great hopes for were to die.

At that time, Chen Qingdu would find it inconvenient to draw his sword.

Then who would stop him? Dong San was held back at the Golden River. Lu Zhi? Far from enough. Even with that old deaf jailer who had also found a reason to draw his sword, it still wouldn’t suffice.

At the foot of a mountain far from Tan, Chen Ping'an, who had just returned to his original position, now stood on a relatively slender "mountain range."

Beneath Chen Ping'an was the corpse of Hou Kuimen, who had revealed his true demonic form after death. As for the black armor, purple gold crown, and two feathers, they were damaged but not shattered after the previous collision. According to logic, they should have been picked up as scraps and collected by the Hidden Official, but this time, Chen Ping'an did not collect all of it; he simply took the feathers and the item borrowed from Yan Ming in exchange for one. Moreover, that item’s previous contents had also been cleared out.

As for Hou Kuimen's armor and purple gold crown, Chen Ping'an had used the Mountain Moving technique to place them far from Hou Kuimen's corpse.

At this moment, Chen Ping'an was severely injured, his face pale, to the point that his entire right arm was uncontrollable, trembling slightly—a rare occurrence for him.

Previously, Hou Kuimen's attack had been too vicious; Chen Ping'an had essentially endured a full-force punch from a tenth realm warrior. If he hadn’t evaded slightly, he would have been instantly pierced through the heart by Hou Kuimen's punch.

If it had been on a training ground, taking a peak punch from the tenth realm and surviving would have been an exhilarating experience. 

But now, while it appeared that the young swordsman was toying with the youth, in reality, Chen Ping'an still found it hard to escape the encirclement, which was an extremely unpleasant experience.

The earlier failed strike against that young swordsman left Chen Ping'an feeling extremely helpless. If he had been at the peak of his strength, the head of that genius swordsman should have been placed in a small item by now.

However, the longer this young man remained here, unable to forcibly break out of the small world, the more Chen Ping'an could recover.

Chen Ping'an gazed at the posture of the young man, who was protected by the divine being, without withdrawing his sight for a long time.

Tan did not look at the law form that pretended to be meditating atop the mountain.

The young man stared intently at a lingering breath in the distance. Although he could not clearly see the scene at the foot of the mountain, he was certain that the young Hidden Official was hiding over there.

The majestic law form atop the mountain opened its eyes, fingers forming a sword seal, and from behind the sword box, countless massive flying swords surged forth towards Tan.

The celestial maiden law form that protected the youth turned her body, turning her back to the colossal flying swords resembling celestial ferries.

Tan gritted his teeth and spat blood.

The sword interlaced with lightning suddenly hovered in mid-air, with sword light bursting forth between its tip and hilt, shooting straight toward the sky and the ground.

Chen Ping'an, employing the power to fold heaven and earth, attempted to alter the trajectories of the two beams of sword light. Once he slightly changed the course, the sword light would no longer travel in a straight line, allowing him to prevent the young swordsman from detecting the boundaries of heaven and earth.

Unexpectedly, the young man detonated the flying sword directly, causing the sword light to suddenly expand, filling the heavens as if a beam of support had been raised.

That flying sword was, in fact, Tan's second life-bound flying sword.

Simultaneously, his life-bound flying sword "Jia Qi" transformed from the iron cavalry army back into a sword, returning to Tan's vital point.

The celestial maiden law form clasped her hands together, protecting Tan, even at the cost of destroying a flying sword.

The law form of the celestial musician, unlike an ordinary one, seemed almost alive. Earlier, it had braced itself against the flying sword from the peak's blue-robed figure and now showed a hint of emotional change.

At this moment, she looked down at her master, her expression warm.

That "Yushi," coming and going in haste.

Zhu Ke's long sword, at the previous entrance, flashed with sword light and then vanished.

In the deepest layer of that small world, Chen Ping'an covered the wound on his ribcage caused by the flying sword, smiling ruefully.

What a Liu Bai.

As long as she had shown a slight mercy, even if she were cautious and heartless, according to Chen Ping'an's expectations, lightly injuring "Yushi" to determine the truth, then a distance of over ten zhang would have been enough to allow Chen Ping'an to close in. Once close, whether to kill her or that young man, there would have been ample opportunity.

Unexpectedly, that Liu Bai's life-bound flying sword directly aimed for "Yushi," targeting the core vital points of all swordsmen, forcing Chen Ping'an to slightly shift his body, retreating with a light injury instead.

It was a case of attempting to steal a chicken only to lose the rice.

As for the long sword from Zhu Ke that followed closely, dodging it was not difficult for Chen Ping'an, who quickly "sent it out of the boundary" with ease.

Within the small world where Chen Ping'an resided, Yushi's situation was far more dire than Tan's.

Because Chen Ping'an was gradually recovering from his injuries, he no longer performed any flashy maneuvers. Within the small world, flying swords were everywhere.

In the Jia Shen camp, swordsman Yushi, familiar with the secret archives from the Summer Palace, had more detailed information than Zhu Ke and Liu Bai.

His life-bound flying sword "Waterfall."

After summoning the flying sword, it felt as if the world had turned cold, enveloping him in a swirling cloak.

Thus, even while surrounded by those interweaving and freely flying swords, he was still able to hold on.

If Liu Bai and Yushi had switched places, Liu Bai would likely have already perished.

Chen Ping'an's two life-bound flying swords’ supernatural abilities completely outmatched and countered that strange flying sword of Liu Bai.

It was unfortunate there was no such "good if" circumstance; today's battle had mostly brought about bad accidents and unforeseen events.

The martial artist Hou Kuimen had been similarly tampered with in three crucial treasures. The young swordsman's decisive actions, and Liu Bai’s ruthlessness toward a fellow comrade…

As for within his own small world, folding mountains and rivers like origami was a technique Chen Ping'an had been inspired to develop years earlier when witnessing Mao Fuzi trapped in a law formation in the Great Sui capital city.

It was just that Chen Ping'an had not yet mastered it completely. Otherwise, Li Zhen and Zhu Ke's strong formation breaking wouldn’t have taken merely a single incense stick's time, as the flying sword "Caged Sparrow," unlike the lifeless mountain and water formations, differed from the territories governed by the Saints in academies, temples, or battlefield ruins. The latter's territorial mountains and rivers were nearly fixed, but Chen Ping'an's reliance on "Caged Sparrow" allowed him to manipulate the very essence of heaven and earth. Likewise, as the Hidden Official, Chen Ping'an was unable to truly devote himself to cultivation or sword refinement, otherwise, the levels of this nested world would be even more rounded and seamless.

Such is the nature of the world; benefits are rarely obtained without cost.

If not for becoming the Hidden Official of the Sword Qi Great Wall, Chen Ping'an would have never been able to refine these two life-bound flying swords that resonated with the "Dao of the Sword Qi Great Wall."

Yushi could assure that he would not die temporarily, yet it was still far from comfortable.

The young Hidden Official, aside from using flying swords to kill, would also rely on the "impossibility" that suppressed the opponent's flying swords while allowing his own to flow more smoothly, using pure martial arts to strike with fists, wielding blades that appeared and disappeared.

Yushi's cheek bore a large chunk of flesh that Chen Ping'an had sliced away, his body riddled with injuries.

Fortunately, since it was neither a critical qi point nor a key vital area, Yushi was ultimately still a swordsman, with no fatal injuries.

However, he was a far cry from the elegant figure he had been upon his arrival.

An abrupt sword cleaved through the heavens.

The long sword was sent out of heaven and earth, and Zhu Ke, relying on the remaining strands of sword intent, found the place.

Chen Ping'an's figure vanished, manipulating heaven and earth, having intentionally left that trace of sword intent.

The elusive life-bound flying sword of Liu Bai was hard to trace, but for Chen Ping'an, the sword intent from Zhu Ke’s flying swords was akin to fireflies flickering close by in the dark of night.

Unable to move Yushi, who was protected by the waterfall of sword energy, Chen Ping'an reversed heaven and earth, positioning Yushi—busy resisting over a hundred flying swords from "Moon in the Well"—exactly in the path of that sword light.

Zhu Ke spoke through his mind voice, "Yushi!"

Zhu Ke said no more, as that was not enough to reveal heavenly secrets.

Only a glance of mutual understanding was needed.

Yushi did not disappoint Zhu Ke, reaching out to grasp the sword light.

The sword light bent like a rope, and Zhu Ke, channeling his mind and sword intent, suddenly yanked, attempting to pull Yushi out of the small world that resembled a great prison. 

To prevent Chen Ping'an from taking advantage of the situation and attacking Yushi as he retreated—leaving a trace for him to follow—Liu Bai needed no reminder from Zhu Ke, and summoned her life-bound flying sword that seemed to not exist in this world.

When Zhu Ke struck, he stood atop the celestial maiden's shoulder.

Chen Ping'an sighed slightly, allowing Zhu Ke to rescue Yushi while he aimed to kill the young man, with both sides not impeding one another.

You save your people, I’ll kill your people; it’s a fair trade.

Since Zhu Ke had already anticipated this, they could only settle for second best.

The flying swords that had traversed countless mountains and rivers with Chen Ping'an—initially arriving and departing—finally manifested at the same time.

Then, behind that celestial maiden, a far larger and more imposing blue-robed law form appeared, both hands intertwining into a fist, smashing down towards her head.

Zhu Ke, holding the sword, swept it through the air.

The crescent sword light reappeared, directly slicing through Chen Ping'an's law form that had been holding onto its fist.

Since they could not kill the most vulnerable among the encircled swordsmen, they would return the favor with an unexpected blow, taking down the strongest among them.

Chen Ping'an forcibly changed the thickness of heaven and earth, placing himself within the folded mountains and rivers even more quickly than the pine needle thunder, combined with a shortcut talisman, and instantly arrived behind Zhu Ke.

Zhu Ke was struck hard in the center of his back, falling from the celestial maiden's shoulder and crashing into the distant ground.

Chen Ping'an was then stabbed in the abdomen by Zhu Ke’s retaliatory sword, receiving a solid blow. Zhu Ke had the option to evade but chose not to, clearly intending to exchange injuries with Chen Ping'an.

The two swords, First and Fifteenth, had collided with Liu Bai's life-bound flying sword no less than a hundred times.

The means did not stop there; between heaven and earth, two rivers of talismans emerged, glowing with golden light, surging toward Yushi.

Even after being blasted away by a punch, Zhu Ke still controlled that sword light, drawing an arc in the air, striving to pull Yushi toward himself.

Liu Bai grasped Tan's shoulder, continuing to steer her life-bound flying sword to obstruct First and Fifteenth, while she took Tan to a distance, leaving no chance for Chen Ping'an to engage in close combat.

Indeed, that young Hidden Official closely followed after Yushi.

Yushi, however, roared, "Liu Bai!"

The female swordsman was momentarily blank, instinctively releasing her hold on the young Tan. She was about to self-destruct her golden core and control her life-bound flying sword to pierce her heart, hoping to kill herself before that young Hidden Official.

But the opponent's fingers gripped her neck, yanking her backward, pulling her away from her original position. Then, with a heavy twist, Chen Ping'an directly snapped Liu Bai's entire neck.

Moreover, a punch heavily struck Liu Bai's spine, the force penetrating her body, fracturing her energy channels and even affecting her thoughts, forcing her life-bound flying sword to stutter in its previous trajectory.

Chen Ping'an was about to deliver another punch, trying to shatter Liu Bai's entire back, intending to destroy both her spine and her golden core on the spot, as well as to completely sever her path to immortality.

Unexpectedly, it was as if a heavy hammer struck Chen Ping'an's forehead, forcing his figure to vanish.

Although Liu Bai's physical form was destroyed, she managed to protect half of her Dao foundation. Yet, her chances of ascending to the Fifth Realm—especially the realm of immortals—were now bleak, as difficult as climbing to the heavens.

Chen Ping'an quickly glanced at the area near the young woman’s head.

There was a talisman left behind by that young man, who had quietly inscribed it on her.

To utilize that life-saving talisman, the young man, already wounded more than once, coughed up blood, his face smeared with blood and his vision blurred. He still exerted himself to reach out, wrapping the broken talisman around the golden core and soul of the young woman before pulling it into his sleeve. After completing this, Tan nearly fainted, clinging to the last shred of clarity in his mind, and reached out again, determined to retrieve Liu Bai's skin.

Unexpectedly, beams of light appeared in the sky, whether sword light or star light, enveloping Zhu Ke, Yushi, Tan, and Liu Bai's lifeless body.

Chen Ping'an narrowly avoided Liu Bai's beam but found himself unable to escape within his own small world, unable to evade the second beam that struck him.

As for Liu Bai's physical form, it had already been utterly obliterated by the light beam.

Chen Ping'an was slammed to the ground, staggering in the air and rolling, narrowly dodging a shadow-like beam, and then folding heaven and earth, swiftly retreating hundreds of zhang.

Li Zhen hovered in the sky, resembling an ancient deity traversing through the river of time, raising his hands to what should have been the Northern Dipper hanging in the night sky.

The starry constellation slowly shifted, and within the small world, the four seasons flowed, thunder shook in spring, summer heat blazed, autumn winds howled, and heavy snow fell. The operation of the Dao moved like a grinding mill, grinding all things to dust.

During this period, the countless sword energies previously laid down by Zhu Ke became increasingly fierce. Between heaven and earth, drops of condensed sword essence formed a river of sword energy that continuously expanded, inundating everything.

Chen Ping'an had the option to retract the life-bound supernatural ability of "Caged Sparrow," or he could plunge into a grueling battlefield of pure spiritual energy consumption against Li Zhen.

Chen Ping'an's figure appeared and vanished repeatedly within the small world.

Chen Ping'an slid sideways for over ten zhang and came to a stop.

The manifestation of the "Caged Sparrow" small world condensed into a sword, darting into his vital point.

The small world dissipated.

Chen Ping'an stood on the slope of the pit, while Li Zhen hovered above, only ten zhang away. Zhu Ke, bearing the sword rack, was situated at the very center of the pit, while Yushi supported Tan at the edge of the pit.

The sword formation buried underground by Zhu Ke was about to make a move.

The heavens shifted once more.

This time, the small world was considerably narrower than before, appearing cramped.

Only a few dozen li in diameter.

A landscape filled with strange burial mounds, yet surrounding the mounds were willow trees swaying gently.

Was this truly the young Hidden Official's inner world?

Zhu Ke, who had always been calm, unexpectedly displayed a hint of anger.

Yushi protected himself and Tan with the "Waterfall" flying sword, gritting his teeth with deep resentment.

Why was this Chen Ping'an so hard to kill?!

Li Zhen casually lifted a hand, easily touching the heavens, and chuckled, "The Hidden Official who values his life the most, are you really not planning to flee this time?"

Next, all that Chen Ping'an could kill would simply be Tan's remaining half-life, and possibly Yushi.

As for Li Zhen himself and Zhu Ke, amid this chaotic and smoke-filled attempt to encircle, they possessed plenty of killing flying swords but lacked the ability to unleash them fully.

Chen Ping'an, trapped in the encirclement, swayed his figure. It was evident that having summoned "Caged Sparrow" twice, and facing five opponents alone, his martial body was nearing its limits, and his spiritual energy was nearly depleted.

Li Zhen shook his head, his eyes filled with pity. "Fishing in a dried-up pond, seeking the path to death."

Yet his expression remained relaxed, while his heart was utterly frustrated.

Had he known earlier about the supernatural abilities of Chen Ping'an's two flying swords, their five-person team would never have fallen into such a miserable state. With a little preparedness, not to mention Li Zhen, even the other four Sword Immortal candidates would have had no shortage of magical treasures at their disposal. Many of the offensive treasures and secret methods they had prepared earlier had never had the chance to be employed. As a result, now they were unable to encircle Chen Ping'an, leading to Liu Bai and Tan's paths being obstructed, limiting their future achievements.

But in the path of cultivation, it is often said that knowledge comes at a price.

Chen Ping'an clapped his palms together heavily, smiling, "I’ll send you all on your way; rest in peace."

From all directions of the heavens and earth, from the boundaries of the small world at the round place, innumerable flying swords "Moon in the Well" began to slowly advance toward the four Sword Immortal candidates.

Once again, it was an unreasonable life-bound flying sword!

Li Zhen's heart filled with horror.

This madman really intended to exchange lives?!

Zhu Ke furrowed his brow tightly. Did this young Hidden Official refuse to be killed even in death? Choosing instead to risk his life and Dao, seeking to take one more life?

Moments later.

Chen Ping'an leaned back and fell.

Both "Caged Sparrow" and "Moon in the Well" flew back to their vital points in an instant.

Thus, after discovering the truth, Li Zhen couldn't help but curse.

It turned out that the place where Chen Ping'an leaned back and fell was at the very corner of the Sword Qi Great Wall.

This meant that all of them had been tricked by this damn young Hidden Official.

Using the two life-bound flying swords to gamble with them was a ruse; folding heaven and earth and changing the battlefield was the truth.

However, the subsequent series of events would bring enormous surprises to the Wildlands and the Sword Qi Great Wall.

First, a Hidden Official from the Throne, concealed on the battlefield, revealed himself. With a wave of his large sleeve, he gathered Zhu Ke, who had already drawn his sword, and Li Zhen, who was attempting to retreat, into his cosmic sleeve, simultaneously flicking his fingers.

Sword Immortal Wei Jin from the Wind and Snow Temple cleaved at the great demon aimed at Chen Ping'an with a sword.

Lu Zhi was just about to leave the city walls.

A burly man with a long beard and a sword at his waist directly repelled two Sword Immortals from the Sword Qi River, approaching the battlefield near the Sword Qi Great Wall, pressing down on the sword hilt and looking up at the female Sword Immortal Lu Zhi.

As long as Lu Zhi did not draw her sword, he would not unsheathe his own.

And that was not even the "great" surprise.

Chen Qingdu looked up and smiled.

An elder in gray robes from the Jia Zi camp stepped out from the military tent, seemingly wanting to witness a certain scene in person.

In the shared sky of the Wildlands and the Sword Qi Great Wall.

A beam of light, as large as a mountain, smashed through the grand restrictions of the entire world, striking straight down onto the battlefield, deliberately avoiding the Sword Qi Great Wall and, instead, directly choosing the heart of the demon army south of the Golden River.

On that vast battlefield of hundreds of miles, the earth instantly split apart, sending countless demons flying, resulting in massive casualties.

A man from beyond the heavens, slightly bending his knees, stood on the battlefield, raising both hands to press against his forehead, slowly brushing back his hair.

That man straightened his back, surveying the surroundings filled with demons, and laughed heartily, "You are all surrounded by me." 

(End of Chapter)

 ### Chapter 777: Departing and Returning

The man spread his arms wide, palms facing upwards, and gave a gentle shake. After a long separation, he gestured to the members of the Sword Qi Great Wall, especially to the good girls he had been thinking about, hoping for a sign of recognition.

The once-silent Sword Qi Great Wall suddenly erupted with whistles and jeers from atop the city walls.

The female Sword Immortal, Lu Zhi, lowered her gaze, too lazy to look at the man. She truly found it embarrassing.

With his back to the city wall, the man nodded in satisfaction; it felt good to still be this popular. Outside the battlefield, the Sword Qi Great Wall was like a roadside child, and upon encountering a drunken gambler, along with a carefree bachelor, they would shout, "Damn that A-Liang!"

On the battlefield, that man was just A-Liang, nothing more.

A-Liang's gaze wandered, glancing at the scattered military tents, and he called out loudly, "Don’t hesitate! Bring me a few who can fight!"

A burly man with a thick beard turned around, fixed his gaze on A-Liang, and said in a deep voice, "I’ll come."

Without turning his body, A-Liang merely turned his head to look at Liu Cha, who stood alone by the golden river. In the past, they had been quite compatible, being both friends and foes. A-Liang slowly turned around, rubbing his hands together with a smile, "How about we negotiate, good brother? Let’s start with a few who aren’t that strong, just to warm up my hands. With someone like you, I can’t handle too many at once!"

Liu Cha, with his sword and dagger at his side, wore a stoic expression. "I’ve been waiting for you. Why can’t you find a decent sword yet?"

A-Liang pressed his palms together and lightly twisted his wrists. Since the first battle would be tough, he would have to warm up himself.

Liu Cha gently pushed the hilt of his sword with his thumb, and in an instant, he had crossed the golden river, standing before A-Liang with a single downward stroke.

From then on, the two figures disappeared from the battlefield, only to leave behind ripples like a mountain crashing into a great lake, each layer of ripples spreading outward as if a dense array of flying swords had been unleashed, countless in number.

Once A-Liang descended, the remaining demon army within a hundred miles, those who had not perished, were all in a frantic retreat, with the supervising officers of the military tents offering no obstruction whatsoever.

With the sound of thunder cracking, massive pits appeared scattered across the ground.

As all the pits suddenly caved in, life was drained from the surroundings. The bodies and souls of the demon cultivators, upon hitting the ground, were reduced to powder, weapons, and treasures, all enveloped by a condensed sword energy, forming natural sword formations that emerged from thin air, a chilling sword intent slaughtering all.

This was merely the residual sword energy from the clash between the two sword cultivators.

Each standing at the pinnacle of swordsmanship, they forcibly created a phenomenon in the world.

A certain military tent, relatively close to their battlefield, was instantly split in half, leaving several cultivators caught completely off guard, not knowing how they had met their demise.

Liu Cha stood atop the divided tent; the tent beneath him remained intact, while the cultivators inside had already scattered like birds and beasts.

Several miles away, A-Liang halted, reaching out to grab a flying sword wielded by a fifth-tier sword cultivator. He first tightened his grip, then positioned his fingers against the sword’s tip and hilt, applying pressure to bend it into an exaggerated arc.

This flying sword was as thin as a hair, extremely delicate, and crucially, it could conceal its movements through the currents of time, indicating it belonged to a sword immortal highly skilled in assassination.

In the blink of an eye, the flying sword was nearly bent into a crescent moon by A-Liang's fingers. Just as it was about to snap, a barely perceptible grunt echoed from afar. At a huge cost, the wielder forcibly retrieved the sword that A-Liang had restrained, then swiftly retreated, intent on escaping the battlefield. However, to his surprise, a man appeared behind him, pressing down on his head. Sword intent poured forth like water, and A-Liang yanked back, forcing the man to lean back. A-Liang looked down at the face of the slain sword immortal, "I told you, it wouldn’t be that little bastard Shoucheng. As long as I’m on the battlefield, he’ll never have the guts to draw his sword."

Gently pushing the body aside, it fell a dozen yards away, hitting the ground heavily.

In another direction, a brilliant white beam of light shot up from the earth, the soul of a demon sword immortal abandoning its corporeal form. Along with the tightly wrapped golden core and nascent soul, it was swept away by the beam infused with boundless sword intent, leaving no trace behind.

During this brief pause, A-Liang glanced around. The white mist enveloped him, indicating he had fallen into a small world created by some great demon.

"A little trick, trying to scare me? How did you know I’m easily frightened? Well, it’s true; I do turn red whenever I see a girl." A-Liang seemed to warm his hands, and the white mist gradually dispersed around him.

In the battlefield of black and white, a colossal demon in its true form loomed over, dominating the space, looking down at the sword cultivator as small as a black dot.

A-Liang looked up, momentarily taken aback. "What a big one!"

He asked a very sincere question, "I don’t even know you. How dare you come?"

The reasoning was simple: aside from those with ancient thrones in the Hall of Heroic Spirits, other demons who had never crossed paths with A-Liang in battle did not qualify to be called great demons. Since they weren’t great demons in A-Liang's eyes, were they even worth his attention?

The massive demon, deemed "unknown" by A-Liang, was just about to unleash its divine powers and attempt to crush the renowned A-Liang in the wild world.

Unexpectedly, a straight white line appeared from above, as if cleaved in half by a long sword.

In this small world of a celestial demon cultivator, although it was instantly injured to its core and could easily shift the battlefield, it had just managed to stabilize its momentum and barely fend off the overwhelming sword intent brought by that bright line. It ended up on the edge of its small world, trying to increase the distance from A-Liang. Yet, it had no idea that within the entire realm, not only along the boundary of its small world but even outside it, countless rays of light pierced through the heavens and earth, making it seem as though the entire small world had turned into A-Liang’s domain.

A forest of swords, with thousands of swords embedded into the ground.

Ultimately, the great demon, pinned down by dozens of sword lights, could barely move its body. Even the slightest thought would inflict excruciating pain. It was horrified to find itself trapped in a tragic situation, where escape was impossible even within its own small world.

A-Liang paid no heed to this celestial demon.

The small world was as fragile as porcelain, as if a sword immortal could shatter it with just a light tap of their sword tip.

Once the world regained clarity, starting from A-Liang’s position, countless beams of sword light surged forth, expanding like a gigantic circle, sweeping away everything within several dozen miles.

Liu Cha, who had previously been atop the military tent, found it no difficulty to withstand the sword lights. Now suspended in mid-air, he became the only one confronting A-Liang on the battlefield once more.

He said calmly, "A word of advice: don’t get involved."

Even if one was willing to die, at the very least, they should inflict a bit of injury on A-Liang.

Liu Cha sheathed his sword, reached behind him, and drew it again, gripping the sword firmly.

In the wild world, opportunities for swordplay were almost nonexistent, which is why Liu Cha had looked forward to reuniting with A-Liang. He had thought it would happen in the majestic world, never expecting this man to break through two major realms and return directly to the Sword Qi Great Wall.

A-Liang reached out, retrieving a standard long sword from the battlefield north of the golden river. After weighing it in his hand, he sighed; it felt slightly too light, indicating even the sword makers were forced to cut corners. This battle was indeed quite brutal.

When Liu Cha had first met him, he had slashed at A-Liang’s face. That was hardly the way of the martial world.

A-Liang retaliated with a strike against the burly man.

After their respective blows were exchanged, A-Liang was sent crashing into the sky. The entire sea of clouds above the Sword Qi Great Wall was torn apart, scattering like tattered threads.

With a heavy step back, A-Liang stomped down hard in mid-air, halting himself.

Liu Cha crashed into the ground, his body sinking deep into the earth, disappearing from sight as a series of muffled thunderclaps sounded from below.

The two men each rapidly prepared for a second strike, A-Liang descending from the sea of clouds, while Liu Cha reappeared on the ground.

Both attacks were straight and direct.

This time, they retreated even further apart.

A-Liang was directly pushed back into the highest part of the Sword Qi Great Wall's sea of clouds, dispersing a flurry of sword flowers, casually shaking off the residual sword intent lingering on Liu Cha’s blade. He smiled at an old Daoist man who had settled in the heavens, "Old buddy, it’s been twenty years! Those girls from the Sword Qi Great Wall who used to have runny noses have all grown into stunning young ladies, right? Do they know they have an uncle A-Liang who travels far and wide?"

The old Daoist, holding a whisk in one hand, switched it to the other, resting it against his severely damaged staff with a smile. He cursed lightly in the dialect of the Qingming world.

After a round of "polite" pleasantries, A-Liang vanished in a flash.

The whole sea of clouds trembled as sword intent was drawn forth, and the seated sage of the Daoist sect, somewhat helpless, extended a hand, gently pressing down on the sea of clouds, halting its tumultuous motion.

A-Liang raised his arm high, resembling an untrained child with a sword, merely swinging it down.

He struck Liu Cha once more, causing both the man and his sword to vanish into thin air, retreating deep into the ground.

This time, however, A-Liang didn’t take a single step back, though the long sword in his hand shattered into nothingness.

In this battlefield, even with just two opposing figures, neither was willing to close the distance.

Unless the old man in gray standing outside the tent commanded the several demon kings to launch a siege against the man.

Yet the old man merely watched coldly from the sidelines.

Some demon kings, who had initially been eager to act, immediately dismissed their intentions to strike first.

After all, Liu Cha had yet to unleash his full strength.

With no sword in hand, A-Liang formed hand seals. Two torrents of sword energy surged crazily toward the retreating Liu Cha, each carrying the true essence of the sword paths from the Sword Qi Great Wall and the wild world, thick and unmatched. The two sword energies rushed forth like two flooding dragons, crashing into the earth below.

The ground within a hundred miles rumbled and collapsed.

A-Liang, who had only been a few yards above the ground, now found himself suspended in mid-air.

The fifth-tier demon cultivators looked down from above.

Liu Cha stood atop the "earth," which was a hundred yards below the battlefield, one hand behind his back, his other hand forming seals with two fingers. Although the burly man did not hold a sword in his hand, a snow-white jade plate appeared before him, thin and translucent, emanating brilliant light like a moon rising in the human realm, blocking the two torrents of sword energy descending from the heavens.

The two cascading waterfalls of sword energy smashed against the shining white plate.

Behind Liu Cha, the soil of the mountain roots continued to crack and splinter.

The sword energy scattered, and many low-tier demon cultivators watching the mountains and rivers from afar felt their eyes burn as if they were commoners staring directly at the sun. They had to retract their divine senses, no longer daring to continue gazing at the "small world" that had been forcibly created by both sides.

Liu Cha, dressed in coarse hemp garments, his sleeves fluttering in the wind, looked up and said, "After going to the outer sky and killing some otherworldly demons, is this all it amounts to? Or is it that the second Daoist is not as capable as he claims?"

A-Liang laughed, "I’m only saying this as a friend. If you truly think so, then you’re going to die."

Liu Cha shook his head and surprisingly sheathed his sword, allowing the two torrents of sword energy to crash into him.

The burly man gathered no strength, intentionally restraining the sword energy.

Steady as a mountain, he stood firm, allowing the sword energies to collide against him. Liu Cha’s own sword path was like towering mountains, and after the two sword energy torrents collided with his form, they wound around him, creating waves of sword energy that soared dozens of yards high.

While having heard of many sword energies or witnessing them firsthand, Liu Cha had certainly traveled across several realms. After honing his skills at the Sword Qi Great Wall, he had even been able to condense his pure sword intent into a tangible form.

However, at this moment, Liu Cha was solidifying his sword path into his very essence.

A-Liang chuckled.

Then, between him and the burly man, an ethereal river of time appeared, shimmering with a beautiful, glass-like color.

This entire river twisted like a colossal flying sword, wrapping Liu Cha within it, as if he were placed inside someone else's sword sheath, and that person was now returning the long sword to its sheath.

Originally the river of time was most harmonious with the principles of the world. Yet, after being pulled by A-Liang, it began to face rejection by the laws of the wild world, causing countless divine truths to clash with it. At the junction of the two, colorful shards of the river of time shattered like broken ice. But even though the river of time was being compressed, it grew tighter and stronger, as if a long sword forged from the glass-like golden body of ascendance had appeared between heaven and earth.

The old man in gray exclaimed, "Good technique."

In a certain military tent, a scholar who had devoted himself solely to teaching his disciples, oblivious to the outside world, lifted his head to carefully observe the distant battlefield.

A-Liang looked up.

Liu Cha, whose true form was temporarily restrained and whose sword path was gradually being worn down, certainly would not simply resign to fate.

A figure, standing tall within the heavens, revealed only half of its body above the earth. With both hands gripping a sword, it fell toward A-Liang, the sword tip aimed directly at him.

At the ruins of the previous military tent, another Liu Cha appeared, his fingers pressed together, forming a long sword with sword intent.

Earlier, A-Liang had jokingly said he couldn’t handle many opponents like Liu Cha.

However, Liu Cha—now divided into three forms, with his sword path embodied, his yang spirit manifesting, and his yin spirit wandering—was not equivalent to three peak Liu Chas.

A-Liang never fought battles where he could only be hit.

Even with opponents like Dong Sangeng from the Sword Qi Great Wall, this current Liu Cha from the wild world, and that shameless true invincible from the Qingming world.

In the next instant, an exaggerated and towering manifestation emerged behind Liu Cha’s form, pressing down on his head and forcing it into the ground.

Before leaving the Sword Qi Great Wall, A-Liang had always wanted to tell Liu Cha that whether or not he possessed a suitable sword mattered little, as long as his opponent also lacked a celestial sword, it didn’t matter much.

In the past, A-Liang hadn’t mentioned it during their encounters on the battlefield, as they were friends, making it awkward to say.

Being too direct with words could easily lead to losing friends.

At the same time, the "A-Liang" pressing down on Liu Cha’s head wielded a sword in his other hand, striking down decisively. In a single line, eight military tents were located.

Three demon kings—Bai Ying, the old man with a long staff, and the golden-armored deity—each took action to block that strike.

A-Liang cheekily remarked, "Gotta run!"

The river of time that A-Liang had condensed into a long sword shattered.

A streak of sword light inexplicably collided with the wall of the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Even the golden river was pierced by a sword.

Once the sword light dissipated, a man was seen lying atop the city wall, slowly sliding down.

The old man in gray arrived at Liu Cha’s true form, glancing at the burly man with blood seeping from his mouth, and said with a smile, "So, the next time you strike, don’t be so timid."

Liu Cha nodded.

The yin spirit manifestation that had traveled far and the yang spirit that had just returned A-Liang a sword both returned to one.

The man who had been "sent" onto the city wall initially found himself at the top of the word "fierce," sliding all the way down to the ground. During this time, he didn’t forget to secretly spit into his palm, his head turning left and right, carefully smoothing his hair and sideburns. When fighting, one must have aspirations. What aspirations? Naturally, it was about style.

He remembered a little girl selling wine in the Huángliáng Fudi, who had once said that upon seeing his face, it was as if a little deer had suddenly jumped out of her heart, running wildly on her path.

Such heartfelt words could be accepted, but as for the admiration of the girls? That could be passed.

The man halted mid-slide, suddenly stepping forward. He greeted an old sword cultivator with a strange expression, "Isn’t this our Brother Yin? What are you staring at? The more you look, the more you can improve your realm!"

He slapped the shoulder of the old sword cultivator, Yin Chen, and complained, "Brother Yin, I’m not saying this to you, but during the years I’ve been away, have you only been watching pretty girls? Otherwise, how come you haven’t reached the fifth tier yet?"

With a slight tilt of his shoulder, Yin Chen felt a twinge of pain. The other party’s hands were unceremonious, and despite being known for his standoffish nature at the Sword Qi Great Wall, Yin Chen remained tight-lipped.

A-Liang clapped both hands hard against the old sword cultivator's cheeks, eyes wide open, shaking him vigorously, "Brother Yin, Brother Yin! Can’t you even recognize me? Are you stupid…?"

Yin Chen helplessly replied, "I do recognize you. I’m just a bit too excited to speak right now."

A-Liang released him, restraining his laughter. "At least a few familiar faces remain. It’s my fault for arriving late. It’s always like this, passing by and missing out."

Yin Chen sensed something was wrong and, as expected, the next moment, A-Liang had him in a headlock, trapping him under his arm. He struggled to break free while enduring A-Liang's spittle. "Brother Yin, seeing you still a bachelor pains my heart."

Suddenly, A-Liang let go of the old sword cultivator and stepped off the wall, floating toward the city wall, finally arriving beside the Grand Sword Immortal.

On the city wall, Wei Jin clasped his fists and smiled, "Senior A-Liang."

A-Liang patted Wei Jin on the shoulder, lamenting, "What’s there to see? I’m still a bachelor."

A-Liang sat cross-legged, facing south, his expression turning solemn for once. Even with his disruption, it was but a momentary peace; the battle would continue, and people would continue to die.

On the battlefield, the slaughter persisted.

Chen Qingdu stood beside A-Liang, smiling as he asked, "Is there really no beautiful yellow-crowned Daoist in the White Jade Capital of the Qingming world to keep people from leaving?"

A-Liang pointed at the clouds above, then rested his chin on one hand, gazing at the battlefield. He pressed a hand against his chest, silently nourishing his energy, though his words were not entirely sincere, “Oh, of course there are! But only a glimpse beneath the White Jade Capital; just that old buddy’s two junior sisters looked at me like they wanted to eat me. And don’t get me started on the other celestial maidens. Traveling the world, that’s the most frustrating thing.”

Chen Qingdu chuckled.

A-Liang then asked, "How's that kid's injury? I only caught a glimpse from afar; it looked rather strange, so I couldn’t see it clearly."

Chen Qingdu casually replied, "Well, as long as Ning girl carries him back, he won’t die. Half-dead situations are something one gets used to."

A-Liang said, "After all, he’s just a young man, still an outsider. Grand Sword Immortal, as an elder, should protect him a little. This kid, aside from liking Ning girl, really doesn’t owe the Sword Qi Great Wall anything. Relying on age to bully the young isn’t a good habit."

Chen Qingdu laughed, "Are you teaching me how to live or how to wield a sword?"

A-Liang stood up, whispering, "I’m not one to teach others, but if the Grand Sword Immortal insists on learning, I suppose I could reluctantly impart a lesson."

Wei Jin was greatly impressed.

Whether it was during the previous sword strike or in their current conversation, A-Liang was indeed the senior he admired.

The old man cast a sidelong glance at A-Liang.

With a tremor of the city wall, A-Liang was already gone, slipping away quickly.

But was the direction in which Senior A-Liang fled the wrong one?

Even Wei Jin was left dumbfounded and couldn’t help but ask, "Grand Sword Immortal, what’s going on?"

Chen Qingdu glanced at Wei Jin, "Can’t you tell? They’re fighting."

Wei Jin had no words to retort.

Chen Qingdu took another look at the suspended rainbow starting from the city wall. A-Liang’s retreat was far too rapid, and he smiled, asking, "When he traveled to the Baoping Continent, didn’t he mention how much he loved being surrounded and beaten by a group of ascended beings?"

Wei Jin paused for a moment, looking strange. "Back then, A-Liang told me he was among the strongest in the Sword Qi Great Wall, certainly ranking in the top fifty. He even urged me not to think he was bragging—he was very… emphatic about it."

That’s why Wei Jin initially thought he had met a fraud, but thankfully A-Liang’s insights and understandings of swordsmanship, while seemingly nonsensical, genuinely benefited Wei Jin. He held back from testing his skills at that time, and after that, he participated in A-Liang’s so-called little betting game, losing the sword-nourishing gourd, and then entered seclusion. Indeed, he successfully ascended to the fifth tier. After emerging from seclusion, Wei Jin naturally became enamored with the Sword Qi Great Wall, wanting to see for himself what a place with fifty A-Liang’s truly looked like.

Chen Qingdu suddenly remarked, "Besides always presenting himself as a swordsman, A-Liang is also a scholar."

As the man’s figure receded, he crossed over the golden river, and after heavily landing, the surrounding demon army, after a moment of shock, immediately retreated like a tide, frantically fleeing, some using wind to ride their swords, others merely running.

"Damn it, he’s back again!"

The man raised his head high, running his hands through his hair, and mused aloud, "Can I be any more handsome? Honestly, I can’t help but brag!"

As he spoke, a land-based whirlwind began to form around him, growing larger and larger until it blotted out the sun, a formation of flying swords coalescing.

The sword formation was entirely unaffected by the dominating laws of the wild world.

After distancing himself from the Sword Qi Great Wall, A-Liang ascended to the outer sky, killing countless otherworldly demons, and even engaging in a life-and-death struggle with the second Daoist. He had already reached the pinnacle of swordsmanship and was now on another level, able to touch the heavens.

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 778: Drunkenness

The great demon, Huang Luan, who had just employed a technique to manipulate the world within his sleeves and forcibly whisked away the Bamboo Baskets and their entourage from the base of the Sword Qi Great Wall, was known for refining countless immortal ruins into his own courtyard.

Lu Zhi left the city wall with sword in hand, determined to kill this peak demon reputed to possess the most ethereal aura in the wild lands. Despite the efforts of the sword immortal Mi Hu from the Golden River, who intervened with a strike, Huang Luan managed to escape with the cost of losing half of his right sleeve and a portion of his sleeve-world, thanks to the timely assistance from his ally, Yang Zhi, who helped him return to the Jia Shen camp.

Standing on the increasingly sparse Golden River, where sword immortals were becoming few and far between, Lu Zhi chose not to return to the Sword Qi Great Wall but to remain and guard her territory.

Previously, her sword strikes had been rather restrained, constrained by the battlefield's location between the river and the city wall, where their side had too many sword cultivators.

The old sword cultivator Yin Chen sat cross-legged within the strokes of a large character, shaking his head with an expression of disdain. He scoffed, muttering, “If I had such cultivation, Huang Luan wouldn’t have escaped. This battle has reached such a stage, yet you still don’t know how to account for it. How can you, Lu Zhi, call yourself a great sword immortal? Women are just women, sentimental at heart.”

It was perhaps this very attitude that earned Yin Chen his esteemed reputation at the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Outside the Jia Shen camp, Huang Luan shook his right sleeve, and like beans scattering on the ground, several young sword cultivators, no bigger than mustard seeds, appeared one after another.

The Bamboo Basket thanked him for taking back his sword, while Li Zhen’s expression was grim, and Yu Si looked utterly disheveled, supporting the unconscious youth, Tan.

As for Liu Bai, who had suffered the most, thankfully her soul had been gathered back by Tan.

Not a sword cultivator, but the young leader of the Jia Shen camp, Mu Ji, upon realizing Liu Bai’s predicament, though anxious, still bent deeply to express gratitude to the senior.

Huang Luan smiled, “Mu Ji, you all are the fortune of our world. The Dao is long; there will always be a chance to repay this life-saving grace.”

Mu Ji's expression was resolute as he replied, “I will never forget this great kindness.”

Once a sword immortal progeny died in the Jia Shen camp, Mu Ji, as its leader, would not only face consequences on the ledger but also on his conscience. Thus, Huang Luan's actions were tantamount to saving his life.

Yang Zhi waved her hand, directly apprehending Yu Si and forcing him back, then stood in the place Yu Si had occupied, gently cradling the young boy in her arms. She extended a finger to press against Tan’s forehead, and a stream of the purest water energy flowed from her fingertip, nourishing the boy’s vital points. Simultaneously, she rubbed her fingers together to condense a gleaming white short sword, an ancient relic she had treasured for years. Pressing it to his forehead, she thought that if Tan had lost his life-bound flying sword, she would give him another.

Moments later, Tan slowly regained consciousness and, upon seeing the familiar face of the woman in the imperial crown and black dragon robe, his eyes suddenly turned red as he trembled, “Master.”

Yang Zhi spoke softly, “A little setback; don’t let it weigh on your heart.”

After all, Tan was still young at heart. This calamity had severely injured him; although his Dao heart remained intact, it was truly a challenge. Yet heartbreak was genuine, and he choked out, “That guy was too treacherous. The five of us seemed to always be fighting against him. What will happen to Sister Liu Bai?”

In the end, the boy’s concern was still for Sister Liu Bai.

Yang Zhi laughed, “As for Liu Bai, Master originally thought her appearance was not handsome enough to match you. Now, it’s good; let Mr. Zhou simply replace her with a better appearance, and you two can become Dao partners.”

Tan quickly shook his head, for that was not his intention.

Yang Zhi affectionately ruffled the boy’s hair, “It’s all up to you.”

Huang Luan was greatly surprised; when did Yang Zhi take in a direct disciple?

The sword immortal Shou Chen hurriedly arrived at the Jia Shen camp, taking away his junior sister’s soul. After confirming that Liu Bai’s Golden Core and Nascent Soul were not severely harmed, Shou Chen let out a sigh of relief, still thanking everyone before carefully using his technique to gather Liu Bai’s soul and promptly took a detour to find his master.

As for the reason for taking the detour, it was naturally because of that Ah Liang.

Huang Luan departed on the wind, returning to the palace of jade towers, choosing a secluded spot to begin her breathing exercises, swallowing a copious amount of spiritual energy.

In this battle, she had suffered the greatest losses; her carefully nurtured disciple, Hou Kui, had been used as a puppet on the battlefield to target the young hidden officials. Not only had she lost an important piece, but she also received a sword strike each from Lu Zhi and Mi Hu, shattering half of her robe’s sleeve and a portion of her small world, leading to a needless loss of three hundred years of her cultivation.

Huang Luan’s heart stirred, and she saw a building appear before her, made from the carcasses of numerous serpentine dragons, serving as beams and corridors. She immediately removed the restrictions and absorbed it into her own realm.

Huang Luan smiled, “Thank you, Ancestor, for the gift.”

Mu Ji had already returned to the military tent.

The Bamboo Basket and Li Zhen stood side by side, observing the battle from a distance.

In the earlier encirclement against the hidden official, the two of them had not had the chance to unleash their full power, and neither had sustained injuries. However, compared to Liu Bai, Tan, and Yu Si, they were likely the most frustrated.

Li Zhen voiced his thoughts to the Bamboo Basket, “I didn’t expect to lose due to a life-bound flying sword’s abilities. If it hadn’t been for that, even if Chen Ping An had two more life-bound flying swords, he would still have died!”

The Bamboo Basket replied, “Complaining is fine, but I hope you don’t vent your anger on Tan and Yu Si.”

Li Zhen scoffed, “If you hadn’t reminded me, I would’ve forgotten they were part of the fight. Three useless people; what have they done besides dragging us down?”

The Bamboo Basket frowned, “Li Zhen, I dare say that in a hundred years, even the most severely injured Liu Bai will achieve a higher level of sword Dao than you.”

Li Zhen fell silent for a moment, then mocked himself, “Are you sure I can live for a hundred years?”

The Bamboo Basket countered, “Does it really matter? Are you sure you’re a sword cultivator? Can you even draw a sword for yourself?”

The Bamboo Basket was greatly puzzled; the previous Li Zhen from Tuo Yue Mountain, though unruly and arrogant, had shown a kind of sharp spirit. Yet now, ever since Li Zhen had 'died' once, his temperament seemed to have become increasingly extreme, even disheartened.

Li Zhen rubbed his cheeks, muttering to himself, “Have you personally walked through the River of Time? Perhaps you haven’t, or maybe you have, but you surely haven’t seen the riverbed. I have walked through it; that is fate.”

The Bamboo Basket listened to Li Zhen’s murmurs, frowning deeply.

Yu Si stood alone, even more dejected than the morose Li Zhen. 

Solitude often breeds a sense of loneliness, while loneliness can often arise in the midst of bustling crowds.

A figure suddenly appeared beside him, a young woman with crimson eyes. Her robe was woven with fine, dark green threads, rivers and streams she had refined over the long years.

She softly comforted, “Young Master, it’s alright; I’m here.”

Then she fixed her gaze on the elegant Yang Zhi, confronting her; they were the new and old River Lords.

Yu Si brushed away the young woman’s hand and stepped forward, saying indifferently, “Let’s go.”

The woman followed behind him.

Tan was taken aback by this scene.

Mu Ji, sitting inside the military tent, raised his head and then lowered it again.

Mu Ji had always known the sects of Li Zhen, the Bamboo Basket, and Liu Bai, but today he learned the true backing of Tan and Yu Si.

The youth scratched his head, unsure when he would be able to take in disciples and become their support.

Chen Ping An suddenly awoke, sitting up in bed. Fortunately, it was the small residence in Ningfu he hadn’t returned to for a long time, not the corner of the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Chen Ping An pressed his hand to his forehead, feeling a splitting headache as he exhaled a heavy breath. Such a small action caused the small world within him to tremble violently; it should not be a dream, given the multitude of divine techniques on the mountain and the countless strange occurrences in the world that required caution.

Chen Ping An stared blankly toward the door.

Sitting on the threshold was a man, lifting a wine jug to his lips.

The strong scent of herbs in the room couldn’t mask the fragrant aroma of the wine.

The man stood up, leaning against the door, and smiled, “Don’t worry; a person like me should only appear in the dreams of young ladies.”

At this, the man wiped his mouth and began to chuckle to himself.

Life is as fleeting as a spring dream, leaving no trace; like a spring dream, unripe millet, the deer runs away…

The scholar recalled some beautiful verses from his readings, sounding quite serious indeed.

Chen Ping An felt a weight lift from his shoulders; he was definitely dealing with a real person.

Chen Ping An and Ah Liang locked eyes for a long moment, and the first words out of his mouth were an utterly unromantic question: “Ah Liang, when are you leaving?”

He hoped Ah Liang would return to the Sword Qi Great Wall, but he didn’t want him to stay there; it would be fatal.

In this war, the only one who could confidently say he would definitely not die was the old man in gray from the Jia Zi camp in the wild lands. Even the great demons like Yang Zhi and Huang Luan, lords of the wild lands, did not dare to assert such certainty.

On the side of the Sword Qi Great Wall, no one was exempt.

“I want to leave. A whole group of ascendants won’t stay; if I don’t want to leave, the old sword immortal can’t chase me away. You think you can persuade me?” 

Ah Liang sighed, swaying his wine jug. “As expected, it’s the same old story. Why think so much when you can’t manage it all? The boy back then was unlike any boy; today’s youth is still unlike young people. Do you think that once you pass this threshold, you’ll be able to live a comfortable life? Dream on.”

The outcome of today’s events may seem to stem from yesterday’s causes, but they often turn out to be the causes of tomorrow’s events.

Why do people cultivate on the mountain? It’s not just about taking up a good feng shui spot.

Ah Liang pointed the wine jug at the young man. “You shouldn’t have started practicing martial arts and cultivation so early. This senior brother of yours is unfit for the role, and I’ll talk to him next time we meet.”

Cultivators labor with their minds, not their bodies, while pure martial artists labor with their bodies, not their minds. This kid, however, managed to do both, which is just asking for trouble.

But Ah Liang didn’t say anything too harsh; his own words were a bit insensitive, but at least it was better than standing around complaining all day, or else a man’s life would be without hope.

Ah Liang gestured for Chen Ping An to rest and cultivate, while he sat back on the threshold to continue drinking. This jug of immortal wine was borrowed from the sword immortal Sun Juyuan on his way here; he didn’t have anyone at home, so don’t blame him for not inviting.

Chen Ping An curiously asked, “Did you get into a fight?”

Ah Liang faced the courtyard, looking lazy, his back to Chen Ping An, “Not much, just two times. If it went on longer, I reckon the Jia Zi camp would be in total chaos. I’ve been afraid of hornets since I was a child, so I hurried here to drink a few sips to calm my nerves.”

He wasn’t the one getting beaten, so Ah Liang couldn’t muster any enthusiasm.

Yet, after a long-awaited return to familiar ground, the taste of the wine remained the same, but many friends had turned into old acquaintances, and the sadness lingered more.

It seemed that his life had always been this way; no matter how much he drank, it was hard to find joy.

Ah Liang casually asked, “Did you promise the old sword immortal something?”

Chen Ping An replied, “The Sword Qi Great Wall can hold for an additional three years.”

Unknowingly, he had already spent a few years at the Sword Qi Great Wall. If he were in the Hao Ran world, it would have been enough time for Chen Ping An to finish another tour of Shujian Lake. If he traveled alone, he could have traversed either North Ju Lu Prefecture or Tongye Prefecture.

Since taking on the role of hidden official, every day in the summer retreat palace felt like a year, and the only act of leisure was to escape to the cold retreat palace to teach those children martial arts.

“You’re really foolish.”

Ah Liang shook his head, saying, “Have you considered that if Qiu Miao were to be the hidden official, taking on a deputy would be much easier for you? The outcome for the Sword Qi Great Wall wouldn’t differ much. Now that the fifth world has been opened, have you discussed the details of the mirage city to the north with the old sword immortal?”

Chen Ping An intentionally overlooked the first question and softly said, “He mentioned it. The entire mirage city is a replica ascending platform that has been constructed over several millennia, combined with the summer retreat palace and cold retreat palace of the hidden official lineage, forming an ancient Three Mountains formation. At that time, it will carry a batch of sword seeds from the Sword Qi Great Wall to break the sky and head to the newest world. However, there is a major issue; the mirage city is like a small temple and cannot accommodate the higher-level sword immortals, so those leaving must be sword cultivators beneath the middle fifth realm. Moreover, the old sword immortal doesn’t trust certain sword immortals to guard it.”

Ah Liang clicked his tongue in amazement, “The old sword immortal is truly deep; I didn’t even know about this. In the past, while roaming around, I only guessed the general idea. The old sword immortal doesn’t mind pushing all local sword immortals to their demise, but one thing he does well is that he is always lenient with the young, ensuring they have a way out. Now that you mention it, it makes sense; in the newest world, for five hundred years, no upper fifth realm cultivator will be allowed in, lest they be reduced to ruins.”

It was indeed the case that in the courtyard of any great family, one could find a jar or two of silver.

For such an extraordinary plan to ascend, who would protect the formation? Naturally, it would be the old sword immortal himself taking action.

Ah Liang couldn’t help but take a hearty swig from his wine jug, sighing, “Our old sword immortal is the most unsatisfied sword cultivator, half-dead, languishing for ten thousand years, just to give out two sword strikes. So, in some matters, the old sword immortal may act unscrupulously; you can scold him, but don’t harbor any hatred.”

Chen Ping An shook his head, “I won’t hate; I wouldn’t dare to scold.”

Ah Liang laughed, “Every now and then, a few curses won’t hurt.”

Chen Ping An sighed, “The old sword immortal holds grudges; if I curse him, I can’t escape.”

Ah Liang nodded gravely, “When drinking and chatting, buttering him up, rubbing his shoulders and back, regardless of the situation, you should say thank you to the old sword immortal for his hard work. You’ve suffered such serious injuries; just limping over to the thatched cottage on the city wall to enjoy the view, that’s enough silence to speak volumes. Do you need to feign pity? You’re already pitiful enough. If it were me, I’d borrow a straw mat from a friend and sleep outside the old sword immortal's cottage!”

Chen Ping An laughed and then, feeling drowsy, peacefully drifted back to sleep.

Ah Liang remained sitting on the threshold, showing no intention of leaving, slowly drinking his wine while muttering to himself, “In the end, there is only one truth: the child who cries gets the candy. Chen Ping An, you’ve never understood this since you were little; you’ve been at a disadvantage.”

Those who are capable take on more work, and over time, it inevitably leads others to take it for granted.

The lineage of the Literary Sage.

The old scholar has a share of merit in the fifth world.

The first disciple, Cui Zhan, stationed at the Treasure Bottle Prefecture.

With sword in hand, he stands at the Tongye Prefecture.

The closed-door disciple, Chen Ping An, has been at the Sword Qi Great Wall for two and a half years as the hidden official.

And all the sword cultivators of the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Whether strong or weak, everyone’s reasoning contributes to this shaky world, bringing about real good and bad.

Moments later, Chen Ping An awoke from his dreams again, sitting up suddenly, drenched in sweat.

Ah Liang didn’t turn around, saying, “This won’t do. You’ll have inner demons later.”

Chen Ping An raised his arm to wipe the sweat from his forehead, his expression grim, and lay back down, closing his eyes.

Ah Liang remained silent.

Still alone, he continued drinking.

Perhaps feeling uncomfortable sitting on the threshold, he changed positions, squatting down to drink.

Years ago, on the Treasure Bottle Prefecture, the man in the bamboo hat tricked that muddy-legged boy into drinking.

In truth, there are never carefree wine immortals; there are only drunks who are dead drunk and those not yet dead drunk.

On the city wall of the Sword Qi Great Wall, the swing was no longer present.

A certain sword immortal no longer hesitated to eat a bowl of plain noodles.

When the foreign sword immortal Yuan Qingshu fell in battle, he was spirited and proud.

Before and after the death of Han Huizi, the head of the Taihui Sword Sect from North Ju Lu Prefecture, there were no words.

An old white-haired woman stood at the entrance of Ningfu, murmuring softly, “Old dog, old dog. Come back and guard the door.”

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 779: Two Swordsmen

A-Liang stood up, hearing the distant sound of a horn echo across the battlefield—the wild lands had called back their troops.

Both sides began to clear the battlefield, marking the end of this grand conflict, perhaps without the need for a horn to signal the next. 

A-Liang made his way to the pavilion at Dragon Slaying Cliff, loosening his grip on the empty wine gourd in his hand. He spun around once, let out a loud shout, and kicked the gourd out of the pavilion, where it shattered on the training ground below. 

With the battle momentarily over, the sword cultivators atop the city walls returned home like migratory birds, their sword lights painting a picturesque scene. 

They would retreat to their secluded meditations, nurse their wounds, forge swords, and indulge in wine.
