The deceased had passed, and the survivors’ sorrows would gradually dissolve in their cups, whether through heavy drinking or subtle sips, all would be resolved over the table.

A-Liang recalled an esteemed figure once saying at the table that a person's belly is the best wine vat in the world; the stories of old friends are the finest raw wine, mixed with the bitterness of life, allowing the joys and sorrows to brew the most exquisite of wines, rich in flavor.

After a moment of contemplation, he patted his thigh and realized that this esteemed figure was none other than himself.

It’s no good being overly modest; he needed to change that.

Before long, a group of sword cultivators flew back from the city walls to Ning’s residence. Ning Yao suddenly dropped down swiftly, landing at the main entrance to converse with the elderly matron.

The others—Chen Sanqiu, Diezhang, Dong Huafu, Yan Zhuo, and Fan Dache—continued straight to the pavilion, gracefully landing and sheathing their swords.

A-Liang leaned against a pillar of the pavilion, one foot poised on the ground, watching the tall and graceful woman with a sigh, “Diezhang has grown into quite the young lady.”

Diezhang smiled and called out, “A-Liang!”

Back in her youth, Diezhang often accompanied A-Liang on the streets, both worrying about their circumstances. The men fretted over how to scrape together money for wine, while the young girl was troubled by how to avoid being sent to buy it. Each purchase would yield just enough coins for a bit of travel money—copper coins clashing in a ragged pouch. If she could add even a couple of silver pieces, it would create the most delightful sound in the world. Unfortunately, A-Liang had borrowed too often, and many tavern keepers feared her presence.

Dong Huafu asked, “What do you mean she’s grown?”

A-Liang grinned, “Ask your mother.”

Dong Huafu chuckled, “Diezhang, my mother says you helped her choose that name—clearly with ill intent.”

A-Liang sighed, “What does that even mean? Your mother should read fewer of those frivolous novels. With all the books in your family’s library, who knows how many unscrupulous merchants in Nan Bosuo have been supported. The printing is poor, and the content is crude—none of those ten books can be read a second time. And your sister, what was she thinking tearing out all those important pages? Using them for toilet paper?”

Dong Huafu fell silent. He was complicit in that matter; his sister had flipped through the books with reckless abandon while he merely helped tear them, and then she secretly bound them into volumes.

Chen Sanqiu kicked off his boots and sat cross-legged, appearing relaxed as he leaned against the railing.

He liked Dong Huafu, while Dong Huafu liked A-Liang. Yet, that didn’t deter Chen Sanqiu’s admiration for A-Liang’s carefree spirit, nor his gratitude for A-Liang’s past actions.

For instance, A-Liang had once had a fierce argument with the great sword immortal on Chen Sanqiu's behalf, lambasting the Chen family head, Chen Xi. However, he never mentioned it to Chen Sanqiu, who only learned of the behind-the-scenes events later, long after A-Liang had left the Sword Qi Great Wall, wearing a bamboo hat and carrying a sword, quietly returning to his homeland.

Some sword immortals, though skilled in swordsmanship, lived constrained and uneasy lives.

Ironically, the freest of them all, A-Liang, often said that true freedom had nothing to do with being unburdened.

“Fat Yan” was busy giving a shoulder rub to one of the men, then quietly asked, “A-Liang, how’s my swordplay now? If I go to the lofty realm, will I make the fairies’ hearts leap? You once said, as long as it’s a sword immortal, even if they’re not that handsome, once they draw their sword, it’s the best makeup for women. When they see skilled swordplay, they react like they’ve put on blush. Is that for real?”

A-Liang nodded, “Of course it’s for real. How could it not be? I know the lofty realm quite well. If you ever get the chance to travel there, I’ll give you a map marking all the mountain peaks with fairies. Don’t go asking about swords; just fly to the foot of the mountain, circle it once while showing off your swordsmanship, finish your display without saying a word, and leave a gourd for the fairies to drink from while you walk away. Only after that, you can recite a poem loudly and exit gracefully…”

Yan Zhuo looked distressed, “A-Liang, I can’t recite poetry.”

A-Liang replied, “I have a book with over three hundred verses, all tailored for sword immortals like us. Want to buy it at a friend’s price?”

Dong Huafu chimed in, “Haven’t you already worn out the verses in that book?”

A-Liang sulked a little.

Fan Dache was the most reserved.

He wasn’t familiar with A-Liang. Even though A-Liang was approachable, Fan Dache still felt he was on a different level—close yet distant.

It’s like how many young sword cultivators felt towards veterans like Dong Sanqian and Lu Zhi; while the elders might not look down on the younger generation, the juniors often felt inferior.

A-Liang smiled, “You must be Fan Dache, right?”

Fan Dache nodded eagerly, feeling flattered.

A-Liang continued, “You’ve entered the Golden Core realm earlier than both me and the great sword immortal expected.”

Fan Dache couldn’t believe it. Did he really catch the eye of A-Liang and the great sword immortal?

A-Liang smiled, “Actually, the great sword immortal has been watching every child grow. It’s just that he’s rather shy and doesn’t enjoy pleasantries.”

That was a tricky statement to respond to.

After all, he wasn’t just a simple tavern keeper.

Once Ning Yao parted from Bai Momo, she walked along the stone path of Dragon Slaying Cliff. Upon reaching the pavilion, she found A-Liang already seated with everyone.

Ning Yao looked a bit weary and asked, “A-Liang, is he alright?”

“That kid has been restless, so I knocked him out. He’s better now, snoring like thunder,” A-Liang explained honestly. “Chen Ping’an should find it hard to get back into the fray any time soon. You should have stopped him from fighting in that last skirmish; it was too dangerous. We can’t let him develop a habit of gambling with his life.”

Ning Yao shook her head, “He’s set on his path; I can’t dissuade him.”

A-Liang clicked his tongue in amazement, “Is the Ning girl still the same Ning girl I knew?”

Ning Yao sat silently, leaning against the pavilion pillar.

She carried a sword case and wore a flowing white robe.

Inside the pavilion, casual chatter ensued.

Mostly it was Dong Huafu asking A-Liang about the exploits of the Qingming Realm, while A-Liang boasted about how remarkable he was there, claiming that his punches against the second-tier Daoist were no big deal since no winner was declared, but that he had dazzled Bai Yujing without even drawing his sword—a feat not everyone could achieve.

His lighthearted talk concealed deeper issues that were hard to let go of.

Finally, A-Liang gave some pointers on swordplay, addressing the bottlenecks and obstacles each young cultivator faced, then stood to take his leave. “I’m off to find someone for a drink; you all should hurry home.”

Ning Yao stood to see A-Liang and all his friends depart on their swords.

She walked down Dragon Slaying Cliff alone to her small residence. Gently, she pushed open the door and stepped over the threshold, sitting beside Chen Ping’an’s bed. She softly grasped his left hand, which was inexplicably protruding from the blanket, still trembling slightly—a sign of his unsettled spirit and lingering unease. Ning Yao moved gently, placing his hand back beneath the covers. She bent down, wiping the sweat from his forehead with a finger, smoothing the slightly furrowed brow.

Chen Ping’an liked her, and that made Ning Yao happy.

But for Chen Ping’an to like her, it meant he had to carry this burden, which made Ning Yao a bit angry with herself.

Thus, just as Chen Ping’an’s brow relaxed, hers furrowed again.

What to do? She couldn’t not like him, and she couldn’t bear for him not to like her either.

These feelings of melancholy settled over her brow and into her heart.

A-Liang returned directly to the city walls, but instead of heading to the straw hut, he sat down next to Wu Chengpei, who was diligently practicing swordsmanship.

Wu Chengpei gazed out at the battlefield, where the golden river had been gathered by the three Daoist saints. On the ground, there were still some sporadic skirmishes.

His expression bore no trace of sorrow; humans often carried unspoken grief.

For many of the newly arrived sword cultivators exploring the outer lands, the local sword immortals of the Sword Qi Great Wall often appeared eccentric and hard to approach.

A-Liang remained silent.

Finally, Wu Chengpei spoke, “I heard from Mi Hu that before Zhou Cheng died, he said, ‘Living isn’t much fun, so let’s die and see.’ Tao Wen said it was refreshing to die, a rare moment of ease. I envy them.”

A-Liang replied, “Indeed, not everyone gets to choose how they live; often, they can only choose how they die. But I must say, a good death is not as good as a bad life.”

Wu Chengpei said, “In the years you were away, all the foreign sword cultivators, whether dead or alive now, regardless of their realms, have left a deep impression on me. I have no more grievances with the lofty realm.”

A-Liang took out a jar of celestial wine, uncorked it, and gave it a gentle swirl. The aroma wafted up, and he leaned down to sniff it, smiling, “A year of autumn passes in the wine; its taste outshines that of osmanthus every year. The wines of the lofty realm and Qingming Realm can’t compare to that of the Sword Qi Great Wall.”

Wu Chengpei suddenly asked, “A-Liang, have you ever truly liked a woman?”

A-Liang thought for a moment and was about to respond when Wu Chengpei shook his head, “No need to answer; I regret asking already. I’d probably regret even more after hearing your answer.”

A-Liang chuckled, “Traveling the world, what’s the point of not having a bit of romance? Look at those infatuated folks; aren’t they all just drunken fools steeped in wine? In matters of love, everyone’s a coward.”

Wu Chengpei was surprised; this rare moment of seriousness from A-Liang was unexpected.

Lu Zhi made a rare appearance, sitting on the other side of Wu Chengpei.

A-Liang tossed the wine gourd over, but Lu Zhi batted it back with a hand. A-Liang complained, “What’s with the formalities with your older brother A-Liang? It’s just a jar of wine.”

Lu Zhi raised her arm.

A-Liang sighed, took out another jar of new wine, and tossed it over, “Women warriors shouldn’t sweat the small stuff.”

After drinking, Lu Zhi asked, “I’ve heard that there’s a long-standing lineage of sword immortals in the Qingming Realm. How do their sword techniques compare to that of the Grand Master of Longhu Mountain?”

A-Liang rubbed his chin, “You’re referring to the head of the Grand Xuandu Sect, right? I haven’t crossed paths with him; it’s a bit of a regret. The female Daoists from the Xuandu Sect… oh wait, no, it’s the peach grove of that temple—whether it’s crowded or not, it’s always a stunning sight. As for the Grand Master of Longhu Mountain, I’m quite familiar with him. The nobles from the Tianshi Mansion are always exceptionally warm when it comes to hosting guests—quite a spectacle.”

It’s customary to start with a thunderous greeting before any conversation.

A-Liang shifted Wu Chengpei’s head aside and grinned at Lu Zhi, “If you’re interested, when you visit the Tianshi Mansion, just mention my name.”

Lu Zhi scoffed, “Mention your name? Isn’t that tantamount to asking for a duel with Longhu Mountain?”

A-Liang laughed heartily, “The Sword Qi Great Wall knows me best, and no one knows me better than Lu Zhi.”

Wu Chengpei said, “Both of you, I’m here to practice sword techniques, drink, and chat. I’ll take my leave now.”

Lu Zhi replied, “When the heart dies before the person, no good sword can be forged.”

Wu Chengpei said, “No need for you to worry about me. I know that even if I stop forging, my flying sword ‘Ganlin’ will still rank in the top three. Your master sword ‘Dacheng’ only places in the second tier. The records from the Summer Palace are quite clear.”

Lu Zhi replied, “Just let me finish my drink first.”

Wu Chengpei urged, “Please drink quickly.”

Sword immortal Wu Chengpei isn’t adept at dueling, but he’s known for not fearing anyone within the Sword Qi Great Wall. In his time, A-Liang had suffered quite a bit under Wu Chengpei’s hands.

A-Liang waved his hand dramatically towards two elder sword cultivators sitting at the north and south ends of the city wall, calling out, “Place your bets! Cheng Quan, Zhao Ge Yi, come place your bets!”

But Lu Zhi had already stood up, tossing the wine gourd over the city walls before taking off on her sword.

After Lu Zhi departed, A-Liang remarked, “Lu Zhi used to see everyone as outsiders, but she’s changed a lot. You rarely get to hear her speak to you like that; how come you don’t appreciate it?”

Wu Chengpei looked lost in thought, “Hearing familiar words can be painful.”

A-Liang nodded, “That’s true.”

Wu Chengpei said, “You’ve heard about Xiao Shen, right?”

A-Liang reclined, resting his head on his hand, and crossed his legs, “Everyone has their ambitions.”

Wu Chengpei suddenly said, “For the past events, I never got to say thanks or offer an apology. Today, I’ll do both. I’m sorry, and thank you.”

A-Liang replied, “In other realms, sword cultivators like us, skilled in swordplay and good-looking, are highly sought after.”

Wu Chengpei was indeed a handsome man, often paired with Mi Yu as “the twin jewels” in the conversations of many foreign women.

One was infatuated, while the other was sentimental.

Having seen the appearances and poise of the two jade-purity realm sword cultivators, many foreign women felt they had not wasted their journey, realizing that men could also be this handsome. Beauty is not solely for women.

Wu Chengpei placed his sword across his lap and gazed at the distance, softly saying, “Walk to where the water ends, and sit to watch the clouds rise.”

Wu Chengpei then asked, “What if I add ‘mountain’ in front of ‘watch the clouds rise’? Would it resonate better with the water?”

A-Liang casually replied, “No, too many words dilute the meaning.”

Wu Chengpei pondered for a moment, then nodded, “That makes sense.”

A-Liang smiled, “Since when did you start to appreciate elegance?”

Wu Chengpei replied, “I had some free time and flipped through the poem collection of the Hundred Swords Immortal; it was quite interesting.”

A-Liang asked in confusion, “What's that?”

Wu Chengpei chuckled, “You don’t recognize the character for ‘bi’? How can you call yourself a scholar? Didn’t your father die of anger from your ignorance?”

A-Liang grinned, “Your father is the one close to death.”

Wu Chengpei stretched lazily, smiling slowly as he said, “A gentleman's heart is as clear as the autumn sky; a gentleman’s friendship is united in purpose and parting without harsh words. A gentleman’s actions are like wild grass in the morning dew—coming and going, all delightful.”

A-Liang blinked, “Did I say that?”

Wu Chengpei laughed, “Those are words of learned men.”

When Chen Ping’an regained consciousness, he could move freely and learned that the wild lands had ceased their siege, yet he still didn’t feel much lighter.

Unable to find Ning Yao, he found Bai Momo teaching martial arts at the Summer Palace. Chen Ping’an then flew his sword to the Summer Palace, only to discover A-Liang sitting at the threshold, chatting with Chou Miao.

Chou Miao and Dong Bu De were familiar faces to A-Liang, but for outsiders like Lin Junbi, A-Liang was merely a name—everyone had heard of him, but no one had seen him.

A-Liang had spent over a hundred years at the Sword Qi Great Wall, so for the younger cultivators in the lofty realm, all they had were tales passed down orally.

Jiang Shangzhen from the Northern Jiulu Continent had many stories, but A-Liang, having traversed three realms, had even more.

The two landscape paintings spread out in the Summer Palace could not reach the battlefield beyond the golden river, so during A-Liang’s earlier two sword strikes, none of the sword cultivators from the Hidden Official lineage had witnessed them, only feeling the aura from gathered information, leading the younger cultivators like Lin Junbi and Cao Jun to be even more restrained upon seeing A-Liang in person compared to Fan Dache.

Song Gaoyuan, from Fuyun Continent, was even more excited, his face flushed, yet he didn’t dare speak.

Since childhood, he knew that his lineage’s female ancestor had deep feelings for A-Liang. At that time, young Song Gaoyuan, naive and bold, had asked many taboo questions. The female ancestor shared many old stories, and he remembered well how she felt both grievances and anger whenever she talked about A-Liang. It wasn’t until much later that he understood that expression was what true affection looked like.

Guo Zhujiu squatted beside the threshold, resting her chin on her hands as she stared intently at A-Liang.

She was too young and had never seen A-Liang before.

Today, she wanted to steal a few more glances to make up for it.

Occasionally, Guo Zhujiu would turn to glance at the old girl and then look at Deng Liang, who had affections for the old girl.

A-Liang felt a bit unnerved under the gaze of the little girl who refused to forget to carry her bamboo box.

The young girls at the Sword Qi Great Wall were no longer timid.

Whenever their eyes met, the little girl would immediately grin, making A-Liang feel a rare sense of awkwardness, and he couldn’t help but smile back.

This made A-Liang think of that little rascal, Li Huai—the epitome of innocence in a small town.

Guo Zhujiu noticed Chen Ping’an and immediately bounced over, her expression turning anxious, wanting to say something but hesitating.

Chen Ping’an smiled, “It’s fine; take your time to recover.”

Guo Zhujiu nodded vigorously, then pointed at the threshold and whispered, “Master! He’s alive, A-Liang is alive!”

Chen Ping’an ruffled the little girl’s hair, “Forgot? I’ve known Elder A-Liang for a long time.”

A-Liang gave a thumbs-up, grinning, “You’ve got a good apprentice.”

Guo Zhujiu returned the gesture, then felt it wasn’t enough and raised another thumb, “My master has met a good senior!”

A-Liang echoed, “Little girl has a good eye.”

Guo Zhujiu maintained her gesture, “Sister Dong has a good eye!”

A-Liang said, “Sword Immortal Guo has good fortune.”

Just as Guo Zhujiu was about to continue talking, she received a playful smack from her master and had to withdraw her hands, “Senior, you win.”

Finally, Guo Zhujiu strutted into the house.

Chen Ping’an and A-Liang sat side by side at the threshold.

Two swordsmen, two scholars, began to drink together.

*(End of Chapter)*

 **Chapter 780: Not a Character in the Book**

Two outsiders, sipping on local wine.

Ah Liang was the first to speak, teasingly saying, “Recovering this quickly? The physique of a pure martial artist is indeed impressive.”

The healing of muscles and bones, the stabilization of a chaotic soul, and the nurturing and repairing of his life sword—all three processes were happening at an astonishing speed that even Ah Liang had not anticipated.

Chen Ping'an sighed, “Hanging by a thread, I still feel a bit anxious.”

It wasn't just the sword cultivators of the Sword Qi Great Wall who would, for various reasons, secretly send messages to the military camps in the wild lands; among the demon army, there were also cultivators who would leak information to the Sword Qi Great Wall.

After this battle, the five talented sword cultivators from the Jia Shen Camp had already provided a detailed assessment of their combat strength to the Summer Palace.

Of course, the young Hidden Official had two life swords as his trump card, and it was certain that many military camps in the wild lands were already aware of that.

Ah Liang joked, “You can’t just look at the thieves eating meat and ignore the thieves getting beaten; I understand that.”

For any outsider, finding a foothold in the Sword Qi Great Wall was no easy task.

Ah Liang knew this well from his own experience.

He stood up and stretched lazily. “Let’s go. I’ll take you around the city. One's heartstrings can’t always be taut.”

Beside him, Chen Ping'an, without realizing it, had been breathing according to the “rules” since he started gathering herbs as a child.

To breathe is to live—that's a fundamental principle. Almost all cultivators start their journey toward longevity by diligently practicing the art of breathing.

The elder from the Liyu Cave Heaven, a highly respected figure, had taught Chen Ping'an a breathing technique in his early years. It wasn’t particularly sophisticated or high-ranking, but it was steady and orderly, akin to food supplementation rather than medicinal supplementation. Though it became second nature to Chen Ping'an and didn’t burden his physique, it brought long-term benefits, like a gently flowing spring nourishing the heart. 

However, cultivation remained cultivation, and being human remained being human. The distinction between the two was clear, as if every step taken adhered strictly to the rules, ensuring daily harvests. Such restraints on the heart could be a good thing, but they could also make a person seem dull. Thus, the young boy from Mud Bottle Alley had always given an impression of being mature beyond his years.

After learning fist techniques, every time Chen Ping'an traveled alone in the Jianghu (rivers and lakes), he liked to deliberately control his breathing and footsteps, masquerading a high level of skill with a low level of ability. He could always handle it effortlessly, appearing more seasoned than the old veterans—not merely due to talent.

Chen Ping'an stood up and asked with a grin, “Can I bring along a little follower?”

Ah Liang nodded, “Then one for each of us.”

Chen Ping'an called over Guo Zhujiu, who still considered herself his little disciple. However, at just thirty years old, Chen Ping'an was still young for a cultivator, almost like a child in the bustling world. It was unlikely that Guo Zhujiu would become a disciple of the Falling Star Mountain.

Guo Zhujiu hoisted her book box onto her back, holding a hiking staff.

Ah Liang then called for the young sword cultivator Song Gaoyuan from the Deer Antler Palace on Fuyao Continent. The Deer Antler Palace was the top immortal sect of Fuyao, where several of the living founding masters were women, leading to a multitude of female cultivators. As a result, the male cultivators from Deer Antler Palace were particularly envied by others.

Known for their water-based magical powers, the Deer Antler Palace controlled a large part of a river flowing into the sea. Within their jurisdiction were the well-known tourist spots of Jealous Woman Ferry and Rouge Ferry, where women would disrobe their makeup and don plain skirts and wooden pins to cross the waters, lest the water goddess stir up trouble. Conversely, at Rouge Ferry, women were required to apply makeup to appear stunningly beautiful before they could safely cross.

The Deer Antler Palace never interfered, as long as the two waters didn’t harm anyone; the two whimsical water goddesses were allowed to establish their odd rules based purely on personal preference.

Having traveled through the Deer Antler Palace for several years, Ah Liang had, of course, visited both places and found the two water goddesses to be amiable companions—one lively and the other shy, both good girls.

As for the chance encounter at the Deer Antler Palace, it occurred one moonlit night when Ah Liang had promised to bring a gift to the water goddess of Jealous Woman Ferry, helping that poor girl restore her broken appearance. He ventured into the forbidden Lotus Pond, where every lotus leaf had extraordinary uses. Countless dissatisfied female cultivators had longed for a single lotus leaf from the Deer Antler Palace, which was priceless and could not be bought.

The restrictions within Deer Antler Palace were quite interesting; at that time, Ah Liang could only crawl along, twisting and turning to sneak to the pond’s edge. With his rear in the air, he was about to pluck lotus leaves when he suddenly spotted a girl sitting on a massive green lotus leaf, staring wide-eyed at the scruffy man who was foraging for lotus seeds. Noticing her, Ah Liang extended his hand, asking if she wanted to try some.

The girl was hospitable, and a magnificent water spell came crashing down upon him.

Old memories could be recalled.

The four of them left the Summer Palace on foot. Chen Ping'an, always observant, noticed a subtle shift in the expressions of Dong Buding and Pang Yuanji among the group earlier. He wondered what Ah Liang had discussed with them before his arrival.

As they exited the main gate, Song Gaoyuan, gathering his courage, asked with a flushed face, “Ah Liang, will you come to our Deer Antler Palace again in the future?”

Ah Liang chuckled, “Speak up. Which of your senior masters still remembers me after all these years? I can’t guarantee whether I’ll go to the Deer Antler Palace or not.”

Out of respect for his elders, Song Gaoyuan quietly communicated with Ah Liang, “It’s the Master Rongguang who often mentions you.”

In fact, that elder who had distanced herself from the mortal world for over a hundred years would always visit the lotus pond every time she exited her seclusion, frequently murmuring that lotus seeds had a bitter taste that could nourish the heart.

Indeed, indeed. Ah Liang sighed, “It’s her, huh?”

Song Gaoyuan hesitated for a moment and softly said, “Before my travels, Master Rongguang instructed me to say one thing to you if I saw you at the Sword Qi Great Wall.”

Ah Liang was silent.

Song Gaoyuan continued, “Master Rongguang wants to convey to you, ‘At that time, it was thought to be ordinary.’”

Ah Liang scratched his head and didn’t say much more.

Song Gaoyuan didn’t dare press Ah Liang. 

Some things simply couldn’t be reasoned; making it difficult would only complicate matters further.

As they casually wandered towards the city, they passed by two private residences of sword immortals. Ah Liang introduced one residence, saying its foundation was a plaque made from the refined jade of a poetical inscription by a sword immortal, while the owner of the other residence loved collecting ancient inkstones from the Haoran world. However, both of the former owners of these residences had passed away; one was completely deserted, while the other housed three young disciples who had been taken in by a sword immortal. They weren’t allowed to leave the residence until they achieved the Nascent Soul stage. 

Ah Liang gazed at the walls of that private residence and sighed, “Such earnest care, indeed.”

Chen Ping'an had an odd expression.

The three Golden Core sword cultivators within that residence were all men and could not leave. It was said they were even forced to wear women’s clothing, an oddity of the Sword Qi Great Wall. They had once sent a message requesting to go out and fight, but the Hidden Official lineage discovered that the deceased sword immortal had made a written agreement long ago with the Summer Palace, which bore the name of the late sword immortal and a tiny palm print—likely the work of the previous Hidden Official, Xiao Xian.

Chen Ping'an could only give up, politely declining the request of the three Golden Core sword cultivators.

In the Sword Qi Great Wall, the rules regarding the entrusted affairs of fallen sword immortals were paramount; once it was set down on paper, it had to be upheld, with no room for negotiation.

On the other side of the wall, a young sword cultivator peeked out, sporting a young face but a scraggly beard, and began cursing at Ah Liang.

Ah Liang shot back, saying he had merely shared an anecdote with their master, and it was not his fault if their master wanted to imitate him.

The young sword cultivator angrily retorted, “You dare not come in and have a fight?”

Ah Liang jumped up and spat in that direction.

Chen Ping'an rubbed his forehead, unable to bear watching.

He suspected that the quarrel techniques of the old sword cultivators Cheng Quan and Zhao Ge in the city were learned from Ah Liang.

Then the man noticed Guo Zhujiu, who was wide-eyed beside him, and Song Gaoyuan, as if frozen in place. He quickly tidied his hair and muttered to himself that he had lost his composure.

When Chen Ping'an inquired, he finally unraveled the mystery behind the Sword Qi Great Wall’s case; it turned out that the old sword immortal had a peculiar magical ability, adept at identifying seeds of swordsmanship. In reality, nearly half of the young talents currently thriving in the Sword Qi Great Wall were recognized by that old sword immortal. The prestigious families like Tai Xiang Street and Yu Hu Street were fine, but in the alleys of Lingxi and Suolisi, should a promising sword cultivator sprout up, they would inevitably be overlooked. It was not only sword cultivators in the world; all Qi practitioners, in fact, would achieve greater success the earlier they embarked on their cultivation journey. 

Take Diezhang, for instance; he was discovered as a good seedling through the techniques taught by that sword immortal. Many future sword immortals had initially appeared inconspicuous and hidden, not revealing their talents at a young age.

Once, while drinking with the gravely injured old sword immortal, Ah Liang casually recounted a story about a scholarly family in the Haoran world. The ancestor repeatedly failed the imperial examinations and returned home in frustration, personally teaching his family’s male descendants, forcing them to wear women’s clothing and study hard. If they failed to gain a title before the age of forty, they had to wear women’s clothing continuously, which initially became a subject of ridicule but eventually resulted in the remarkable achievement of six scholars and three received honorary titles.

Ah Liang chuckled, “Doesn’t that sound ridiculous? It caused those three young talents to be ridiculed for decades, to the point where they thought that as long as they could go out and wield their swords, they would be willing to die on the battlefield to be freed from it.”

Ah Liang continued, “The sword techniques of that elder lineage were always about harming others and oneself, making it easy for them to have short lives. Becoming a sword immortal is quick, but dying after becoming a sword immortal is just as quick. When the elder was alive, he could still protect some of his disciples, but once he was gone, it didn’t matter if he had three disciples or thirty; with such a fighting method, the situation would be the same as the desolate house ahead—no one left.”

“To take in disciples is to regard them as one’s own children, which becomes a burden; every master or preacher must bear some responsibility for their disciples’ lives.”

Ah Liang took down the wine jug and took a sip, smiling, “By the way, let me tell you an old tale: an elder sword immortal once approached my master and asked if that technique could be made public, so that the Sword Qi Great Wall could discover more young talents. My master refused, saying that this technique could not be passed on. Even when Chen Qingdu personally left the city to plead with him, it was in vain. In the end, he sent that elder sword immortal away with a single phrase: ‘Who the hell said that only becoming a sword cultivator is a good thing? Is that what Qi Tingji decided?’”

At this point, Ah Liang laughed, feeling more cheerful than melancholic. “When I privately asked him if it was true that the old sword immortal had come seeking, he replied that it was impossible. If the old sword immortal came seeking, how much face would he have to show? After discussing matters, he would invite the old sword immortal for a drink, and that would be his life’s satisfaction. When I asked what if it was Dong Sangeng who came knocking, he said he would just pretend to be dead.”

Ah Liang finally sighed, “In the Haoran world, there are sword immortals like that, but they’re too few.”

Song Gaoyuan nodded in agreement.

After that, Ah Liang spoke less. 

In truth, he used to dislike discussing serious matters with younger generations. Being young, they shouldn’t have too many worries; the major affairs of the Sword Qi Great Wall should be shouldered by those with higher sword skills.

But times had changed; the future would be an unprecedented situation after ten thousand years. Almost every young person in the Sword Qi Great Wall, even children, was now deeply involved. Each of them had to grow up quickly; the momentum was immense, and worries came regardless of age.

The group arrived at the entrance of the Guo Family on Yu Hu Street. Chen Ping'an asked Guo Zhujiu to go home and then had Song Gaoyuan, who had voluntarily taken his leave to return to the Summer Palace, greet all the sword cultivators of the Hidden Official lineage, allowing them to wander freely for the next two days to relieve their minds.

Song Gaoyuan glanced back at their figures.

That Ah Liang had quite a name in the Deer Antler Palace. When he had been pursued by Master Rongguang and her junior sister, he had never fought back but had kept shouting that he was a close friend of the great sword immortal Xu Dian from Fuyao Continent, requesting the immortal masters of the Deer Antler Palace to spare Xu Jianxian some face. Xu Dian came from the second largest sect in Fuyao and was considered a prominent rising star, having become a Nascent Soul sword cultivator at a young age. However, the cultivators of the Deer Antler Palace were known for their independence. Despite Xu Dian’s promising future, he was still not a true sword immortal, and his status was not high. Furthermore, the palace master was one of the ten most respected figures of Fuyao, known for her kindness to her junior sister Rongguang, so the man’s desperate plea for help was utterly useless. In the end, he managed to escape without leaving his name, but he certainly didn’t hold back on poetry.

Afterward, the Deer Antler Palace sent a flying sword to Xu Dian's sect, along with a portrait of the man, demanding to know his origins and whereabouts.

Xu Dian was bewildered, having faced an unwarranted disaster as a swordsman, and quickly replied that he did not know the man in the portrait.

Consequently, an ancestor from Xu Dian’s sect, who frequently mingled with mortals, although appearing youthful, had long since returned to a simple state, actually possessing a cultivation level higher than that of the palace master. After learning of this matter, he hurriedly flew to the Deer Antler Palace, saying, “Xu Dian doesn’t know him, but I do! I’m good friends with Ah Liang!”

Outsiders only knew that this elder had come down the mountain with a red and swollen face, cursing loudly, and after leaving the gates of the Deer Antler Palace, he shouted, “Ah Liang, you owe me a drink!”

As a child, Song Gaoyuan could no longer hold back and boldly asked Master Rongguang what it was that Ah Liang did to endear himself to her.

Master Rongguang pondered for a moment, shook her head, and said he hadn’t done anything, yet she simply liked him.

After Guo Zhujiu and Song Gaoyuan departed, Chen Ping'an shared some of his own stories from the mountains and rivers, chatting sporadically about whatever came to mind.

His first visit to the Sword Qi Great Wall involved taking the old dragon city ferry to Osmanthus Island, passing through the Dragon River, and nearly dying, all thanks to his senior brother who saved him with a sword strike.

He lost three matches against his contemporary, Cao Ci, unable to counterattack at all.

In Tongye Continent, he accidentally entered the Lotus Flower Blessed Land, having a genuine adventure in the Jianghu, taking in Cao Qinglang and Pei Qian as disciples, yet he wasn’t sure how to impart his knowledge to Cao Qinglang and worried that Pei Qian was too eager to grow up.

Years ago, he and Diezhang had run a tavern, selling bamboo sea cave wine, which did quite well. It was slower than sitting on a property, but it was steady income. No one believed that the wine had anything to do with the Green God Mountain, so Ah Liang, you have to help speak a few words of truth for the tavern. You’re acquainted with the lady of Green God Mountain; we’re friends, so how can my wine have nothing to do with the bamboo sea cave?

The great demon caught and released in the Catch-and-Release Pavilion on the Upside-Down Mountain had latched onto a young sword cultivator named Bianjing, who was subsequently hunted down and slain by the Hidden Official lineage at sea.

Now, Falling Star Mountain not only had bamboo buildings but also, as per their agreement, established a founding hall at Jisec Peak. Ah Liang, you must visit it sometime.

The two walked through the bustling streets.

Ah Liang was well-acquainted with every corner, listening to the young man’s stories, more often than not just listening and occasionally asking questions that piqued his interest, such as which was more beautiful, the female immortal Huang Ting from Taiping Mountain or Yao Jinzhi from the Great泉 Dynasty.

Chen Ping'an laughed, saying they were all beautiful, but in his eyes, combined, they were still not as good-looking as Ning Yao.

Ah Liang said, “Ning Yao isn’t here right now. Why don’t you say something manly?” Chen Ping'an glanced around, thought for a moment, chuckled softly, but still said nothing.

With the war paused, business in the taverns within the city flourished.

Along the way, Ah Liang and the young Hidden Official passed by some sword cultivators they were familiar with but didn’t exchange much more than nods.

Those who knew Ah Liang weren’t necessarily willing to interact with the young Hidden Official; patrons of Chen Ping'an’s tavern might not dare speak to Ah Liang.

Though the two outsiders shared many commonalities, in the eyes of the local sword cultivators of the Sword Qi Great Wall, the dogged Ah Liang and the dogged second tavern owner didn’t seem alike at all.

Ah Liang didn’t head to Diezhang’s tavern but took Chen Ping'an to a tavern on a street corner.

The place was packed.

All because the tavern keeper was a beautiful woman.

She was a woman whose life sword had been destroyed long ago.

Upon seeing Ah Liang, the woman was very warm, personally bringing wine to the table and scolding the man playfully, saying he was heartless.

Then, she smiled at the young Hidden Official, speaking very casually, “Oh, isn’t this our second tavern owner? Tired of drinking your own wine and looking for a change in flavor? Encountering beautiful women and getting knocked out in one punch—really, what’s the deal?”

Chen Ping'an felt a headache coming on and could only smile in silence.

Ah Liang raised his wine bowl and clinked it with Chen Ping'an’s, then inexplicably sighed, “When I was young and read miscellaneous books, I once saw a famous saying that the heavier the grain head, the lower it bows. But not walking the Jianghu, I didn’t truly grasp it. Only after genuinely traversing the Jianghu did I realize that the full grain head bows low; it truly is wisdom.”

Chen Ping'an had an odd expression.

Ah Liang placed a foot on the bench, grinning mischievously, “What are you thinking? You’ve misinterpreted a good principle, haven’t you?”

Chen Ping'an asked, “What about the rumors between you and the lady of Green God Mountain? Wei Ban spoke very confidently about it; how much of it is true and how much is false?”

Ah Liang laughed, “That little mountain deity from Qizhu Mountain knows nothing.”

Chen Ping'an said, “Outside the bamboo building, once when I mentioned you, Wei Dajun rarely showed genuine emotion and spoke highly of you.”

Ah Liang quickly changed his tune, “As the old mountain deity of the former Shu state, Brother Wei is quite something, and his insights are profound. No wonder when we first met, I felt an instant connection with him.”

What Ah Liang referred to as an instant connection was likely just giving Wei Ban a bamboo sword strike.

At this point, Ah Liang suddenly put down his wine bowl. “The emergence of Liyu Cave Heaven is intricately linked to the many inner workings of the ancient Shu state, not to mention your neighbor from Mud Bottle Alley. Have you thought about it?”

Chen Ping'an nodded, “I have thought about it.”

“That means you’ve thought about it but haven’t pulled the thread of that hidden connection.”

Ah Liang glanced at Chen Ping'an, feeling helpless; some of the inside information was something Chen Ping'an would never guess, no matter how hard he tried. Ah Liang couldn’t help but shake his head and asked a question, “In your Falling Star Mountain, have you ever seen a seemingly unremarkable outsider cultivator, excluding the monsters and spirits, who definitely has a low level of cultivation, especially one you can be sure has a low level, and this person has a good relationship with Chen Lingjun, whom Lu Chen has his eye on?”

Chen Ping'an mentally reviewed and nodded, “Yes.”

Ah Liang laughed, “Then it seems that your journey from Falling Star Mountain to the Sword Qi Great Wall isn’t all bad.”

Chen Ping'an asked curiously, “Can you tell me why?”

Ah Liang hesitated for a moment, “It’s not that I can’t say, and besides, it's just my guess, so it’s not certain. I suspect that the one who has killed the most dragons might have already placed himself around Falling Star Mountain.”

Ah Liang took a sip of wine. “This person is quite easy to talk to. As long as it doesn’t involve the dragon, any Qi practitioner from the lower five realms could kill him without retaliation. At worst, he could change his identity and continue wandering the world. However, once it involves the last true dragon, he will become a very difficult person to deal with. Even the slightest hint of cause and effect will lead him to slaughter everything in his path. Three thousand years ago, dragons were still the masters of the water transport in the Haoran world, protected by merit. Unfortunately, under his sword, everything is illusory. The Wen Temple has intervened before, but there was no negotiation, no discussion. Lu Chen could be saved, but the same goes for not being saved. In the end, what could be done? It was hard to come up with a compromise. The saints of the Three Teachings could only help this fellow clean up his mess. When your cultivation level is low, you can be stable. However, the higher your level, the more perilous it becomes.”

Ah Liang laughed, “Of course, in this world, there’s no such thing as a truly invincible person. It’s better to know about the more significant matters than to be oblivious. Just know that this person exists; that’s enough. I still say what I’ve said; you can’t handle it.”

Chen Ping'an nodded.

On one hand, it was about matters beyond his comprehension, and on the other, the worst outcomes had not come to pass. Moreover, he was destined not to return to the Bottle Continent, so overthinking was pointless.

Then Ah Liang seemed to start boasting, giving a thumbs-up to himself, “If a conflict really arises in the future, just report my name, Ah Liang. The higher the opponent's level, the more effective it will be.”

In general, those who were actively called “brothers” by Ah Liang, like that sword cultivator Xu Dian from Fuyao, were typically those who had been thoroughly taken advantage of by him and were people he didn’t particularly like.

After that incident, whenever Xu Dian ventured down the mountain, he would find no one willing to befriend him among the female cultivators of Deer Antler Palace. The female Qi practitioners there had a wide social circle, leading to most of the female cultivators across half of Fuyao disliking Xu Dian. As his mischievous master once said, those who had been doused with a bucket of filth by Ah Liang would be remembered as such, even if they cleaned up afterward.

However, if one were to report their name and dare to claim to be friends with Ah Liang, then in almost every sect of the Haoran world, they might still be unwelcome, but that name could ward off many disasters and unexpected events.

Ah Liang inexplicably exclaimed, “You and Ning Yao are looking more and more like a couple.”

Chen Ping'an raised his wine bowl and suddenly turned to ask the tavern keeper, “Do you have any complimentary side dishes to go with the wine?”

That didn’t sound much like Ning Yao at all.

Regarding Chen Ping'an and Ning Yao, Ah Liang had long felt that they were a perfect match. Back then, one was still Ning Yao of the Sword Qi Great Wall, while the other was a young boy just starting out in the Jianghu.

A girl who didn’t want to think too much encountered a boy who wanted to think of everything; could there be a more fitting situation than this?

Not all men realize that the beloved person beside them is their one and only match in the world over millennia.

The tavern keeper smiled, “Our little business can’t compare to the flourishing trade of the second tavern owner. Besides, the second tavern owner not only runs the tavern but also sells wine and picks up treasures everywhere; would he lack money?”

Chen Ping'an could only smile in response.

Ah Liang looked at Chen Ping'an across the table and slowly said, “When a person can only do a few things, they can’t possibly express deeper reasoning. Even if they’ve read books and can articulate it, if others don’t listen, doesn’t that mean they haven’t spoken at all? Isn’t that the case?”

Chen Ping'an nodded, “The times we need to reason with others are often precisely when reasoning has become ineffective; the latter stealthily precedes the former, leading to helplessness in worldly matters.”

Ah Liang laughed, “Isn’t that boring?”

Chen Ping'an shook his head, “Not at all. It’s interesting. The more like this it is, the more we should live well and strive to make the world a little more stable.”

Then Chen Ping'an took a big swig of wine, his demeanor calm and his eyes bright, “Just like a person, as long as their drinking capacity is good enough, they can drink away the worries in their wine bowl without needing to drunkenly speak to others.”

Ah Liang laughed heartily, very pleased.

Because, in the now-present Chen Ping'an, he saw the shadow of another person.

The one who hadn’t traversed the Jianghu—the young man with hope placed upon him—had already helped traverse quite a distance.

Chen Ping'an suddenly said, “Although I haven’t been to the Wild Lands, I know that on the battlefield, many of the demon race who died under my fist and sword are, beyond the battlefield, a substantial portion of them are weaklings—truly powerless weaklings.”

Ah Liang laughed, knowing what the kid was trying to say. Chen Ping'an seemed to be speaking about himself, yet he was actually comforting Ah Liang.

Chen Ping'an continued, “Once the Sword Qi Great Wall is breached, those genuine weaklings from the Wild Lands will also become powerless strongmen.”

Ah Liang, on the contrary, was less appreciative, laughing as he asked, “Then should they die?”

He was, in fact, one of the people who understood the customs and practices of the Wild Lands the best.

Ah Liang even had friends like Liu Cha out there beyond the battlefield; apart from Liu Cha, Ah Liang knew many cultivators from the Wild Lands, who had long since become no different from ordinary people.

Chen Ping'an had already downed two bowls of wine and filled a third. The tavern's wine bowls were slightly larger than those in his own tavern; he had known to buy them by the bowl.

Chen Ping'an finished the third bowl in one gulp, shook his head, and said, “I just lack the ability; otherwise, who would dare approach the Sword Qi Great Wall? All the great battlefield monsters could be killed with one punch or sliced down with one sword. To hell with the great monsters… If I ever have the chance to return to the Haoran world, for everyone who harbors compassion for the Wild Lands while having the luck to remain uninvolved, I see one…”

He burped, then began refilling the wine again. The habit of drinking had originally been instilled by Ah Liang. As for what would happen if he saw one, he didn’t finish his sentence.

Ah Liang didn’t stop him.

He merely smirked and said, “What do you think you can do when you see those people? They have their own reasoning; after all, no one forced the Sword Qi Great Wall to kill so many people.”

Chen Ping'an paused drinking, hands in his sleeves, leaning against the wine table. “Ah Liang, tell me, what would you do? I want to learn.”

Learning from others’ strengths had always been Chen Ping'an’s strong suit.

When it came to accounts, he had learned a thing or two from Zhong Kui at a small inn on the border of the Great泉 Dynasty.

As a package dealer, secretly picking up scraps was an actual skill. What sort of realm should it be, he had seen broad horizons while traveling with Daoist Sun on Bei Ju Lu Continent.

Even long ago, a casual remark by Lin Shouyi, implying that when out in the world, one can manage affairs but shouldn’t meddle too much, had increasingly resonated with Chen Ping'an as time went on.

Even earlier, many experts regarded Chen Ping'an’s handwriting as “overly crafted, lacking spirit,” unknowingly, it all stemmed from the three pieces of paper that Lu Chen had gifted him.

Back then, Lu Chen had mentioned three matters, but only clearly stated two, including the advice to pick up snake gall stones and try his luck. When Chen Ping'an had asked a question, Lu Chen hadn’t revealed the last point, which turned out to be learning to write.

Ah Liang laughed, “I don’t care at all.”

Chen Ping'an was left speechless, recalling those “heart voices” he had heard in the Dragon River and the subsequent events after the heavenly tribulation in Suijia City.

Chen Ping'an reached out from his sleeve, took a sip of wine, and with one hand holding the bowl and the other scratching his head, he mused, “That’s a bit hard to learn.”

Ah Liang laughed, “No need to learn.”

Once one ascends the mountain to cultivate, looking up, the sky isn’t far away.

For a cultivator, the closer they get to the mountain peak, the less patience they have for worldly matters.

There were exceptions, but they were few.

Ah Liang also worried that Chen Ping'an would become one of those mountain deities.

Just like regarding Chen Ping'an's learning to write, Ah Liang wasn’t unaware of Lu Chen’s deeper intentions in gifting him the prescription. He merely wondered why Chen Ping'an’s talisman drawing was so smooth. It felt as if there were no barriers, as if he leaped right over them. 

One should know that the talisman path, regardless of whether it was a Taoist Qi practitioner, was seen as a chasm, akin to sword cultivators—failure was failure.

However, this matter was something Ah Liang couldn’t openly disclose; Chen Ping'an had to figure it out on his own.

Just because one is skilled in swordsmanship doesn’t mean they find all worldly affairs easy. There’s no such good fortune, and Ah Liang was no exception.

As the two drank, the pace slowed; Ah Liang wasn’t in a hurry, as he had a good capacity for alcohol, and Chen Ping'an wanted to drink more.

That tavern keeper had a long-standing relationship with Ah Liang and sent a platter of side dishes over from the tavern, jokingly saying she wouldn’t charge him.

Thus, the two ended up drinking until the sky darkened and the surroundings became increasingly sparse. During this time, several sword cultivators, who had been proactive in their pleasantries, came and went, sitting down to drink, ensuring they remembered to settle their bills.

So, by now, all they needed to pay for was a jug of wine on the table.

At the Sword Qi Great Wall, no one judged a sword cultivator’s ability to drink based solely on innate capacity.

Ah Liang’s face was already flushed as he pointed at one of the bright moons in the sky and smiled at the tavern keeper, saying, “Thank you, sister! I’ve been there; believe it or not?”

When out in the world, it’s acceptable to call someone younger “sister” or “girl.” For women older than oneself, regardless of whether they’re a few years or several hundred years older, one should always call them “sister”—that’s a good habit.

The tavern keeper glanced at the bright moon and directly replied, “Is there a mother?”

Ah Liang waved his hand, “You little girl, always saying playful things.”

The tavern keeper retorted, “It’s closing time. Finish this jug of wine and get lost quickly.”

After finishing their last jug of wine, Ah Liang and Chen Ping'an got up to leave. Chen Ping'an took out money to pay the bill, but the tavern keeper, who was somewhat of a rival, smiled and waved, saying, “Chen Ping'an, let this one be on me.”

Chen Ping'an didn’t ask why and pocketed the snowflake coins, thanking her.

The two walked on the dimly lit streets late at night, their steps somewhat swaying, unable to shake off the alcohol’s effects.

Approaching the Ning residence.

Ah Liang said, “Chen Ping'an, remember, we are not in the White Paper Blessed Land, and the people around us are not characters from a book. Remember, this doesn’t count as a skill, and you must remember it even more in the future.”

Chen Ping'an responded affirmatively.

Ah Liang suddenly declared confidently, “I won’t tell Ning Yao about the fact that I didn’t spend money on the wine. And about how beautiful Huang Ting and Yao Jinzhi are—I'm even less likely to mention it.”

Chen Ping'an clasped his hands behind his head, “You think I’ll be scared if you say that? What a joke! Ah Liang, I’m really not bragging…”

At the entrance of the Ning residence, a figure appeared, and the young Hidden Official immediately took a deep breath, dispelling his drunkenness and instantly shaking off the effects of the alcohol. He hurriedly ran up the steps, a hand behind his back, signaling the man behind him to cool off on his own, and ran up to her, standing still. “I’m sorry for being late! I didn’t drink much, really; Ah Liang kept persuading me, and I said it didn’t matter that I was injured, but it didn’t work. I won’t do it again next time!”

Ah Liang stood there, ears perked to listen to the exchange, his jaw dropping in disbelief. The second tavern owner was certainly not just a name; he had surpassed expectations.

Ning Yao turned to look at Ah Liang.

She had dismissed him.

Ah Liang turned to leave, muttering, “It’s the first time I’ve ever had a drink without paying at the tavern of a lady from the Sword Qi Great Wall. I can’t believe it!”

At the entrance, Ning Yao didn’t speak.

Chen Ping'an felt a bit guilty.

Ning Yao completely ignored Ah Liang’s complaint, merely staring at Chen Ping'an.

He seemed to have grown a bit taller.

She stood on her tiptoes, aligning her eyes with his.

Chen Ping'an tilted his head, squinted, and smiled, “Quick, tell me who you are. If you keep being this cute, I might just start disliking Ning Yao for liking you.”

Ning Yao remained silent.

By the time Chen Ping'an finally understood, Ning Yao had already turned to leave.

On the walls of the Sword Qi Great Wall, Wei Jin was compelled to use the technique of observing the mountains and rivers, with the scroll depicting the entrance of the Ning residence. Ah Liang pounded his chest in frustration, “What a foolish kid, just dazed.”

The great sword immortal stood with his hands behind his back, bending slightly to gaze at the scroll, nodding, “He truly is foolish.”

Originally somewhat reluctant, Wei Jin now chuckled in agreement, “The second tavern owner really lacks emotional intelligence; he’s truly ruining the atmosphere.”

Ah Liang cleared his throat and gently pushed Wei Jin’s hand aside, “Wei Jin, you, a dignified sword immortal, are doing such things? Isn’t that a bit lacking in chivalry? Does your conscience not hurt?”

The great sword immortal turned to leave, “It shouldn’t be.”

Leaving behind just a sword immortal who had been diligently practicing in the Frost and Snow Temple.

On the walls of the Sword Qi Great Wall, Ah Liang sat cross-legged, “Can we swap someone else in, perhaps me?”

Chen Qingdu shook his head, “No.”

Ah Liang retorted, “Isn’t my realm higher?”

Chen Qingdu replied, “At our level, having a realm means nothing. It’s excusable if you didn’t understand before, but do you still not understand now?”

Ah Liang fell silent.

The great sword immortal spoke plainly but with profound meaning.

The two were quiet for a long time, with Chen Qingdu sitting beside Ah Liang.

Ah Liang was somewhat surprised.

The great sword immortal rarely did this.

Chen Qingdu softly said, “I'm a bit tired.”

But the elder smiled and added, “Sword cultivator Chen Qingdu is fortunate to meet all of you sword cultivators.”

Ah Liang laughed heartily, “Say that loudly! Say it louder!”

Chen Qingdu glanced sideways.

Ah Liang immediately acted mischievous, “If I’m drunk, I can’t say such things, can I?”

Chen Qingdu softly remarked, “I wonder what the scene will be like ten thousand years from now.”

Ah Liang replied, “It’ll always leave people disappointed yet hopeful, I suppose.”

Chen Qingdu nodded, “That’s very comforting.” 

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 781: Shoulders and Hearts

Under the bright moon, wealth and poverty hold no significance. The moonlight visits without knocking at the door, wandering through Jade Staff Street (Yuhu Street) and Beauty and Ugliness Alley (Yanchi Lane) alike.

The sun chases away evil spirits, especially during the warm winter days that feel like cotton jackets, as it shines upon Beauty and Ugliness Alley and Jade Staff Street.

Chen Ping'an sat alone in the pavilion at Dragon-Slaying Cliff for an entire night, but ultimately, he lacked the courage to knock on Ning Yao's courtyard door. Damn that liquid courage—what good was it if it didn’t help?

By the time the sun reached its zenith, Chen Ping'an flew out of the city on his sword, heading towards the Summer Retreat Palace. The local sword cultivators, including Chou Miao and Dong Bu De, were absent. Besides Pang Yuan Ji, who was no longer around, the foreign sword cultivators like Deng Liang had gone to pay respects to their respective sword immortal seniors back in their hometowns, or to catch up with old friends. In the end, only Lin Jun Bi and Pang Yuan Ji remained to play chess together. Chen Ping'an observed silently, knowing Lin Jun Bi's skills were a notch above Pang Yuan Ji's, and the outcome was inevitable. After watching for a while, he went to the archives to rummage around. 

Eventually, Lin Jun Bi approached him, saying that the great sword immortal Mi Hu had specifically requested to see the Hidden Official. However, this great sword immortal was quite respectful and showed no intention of entering.

Chen Ping'an gestured for Lin Jun Bi to continue their game while he went to the entrance, where he met Mi Hu. Mi Hu was the elder brother of Mi Yu, the leader of their Hidden Official lineage, and the latest and youngest sword immortal of the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Chen Ping'an clasped his fists and smiled, “What a rare guest.”

Without much pleasantry, Mi Hu got straight to the point, saying, “Let’s walk and talk.”

As they walked side by side, Mi Hu candidly stated, “Chen Ping'an, I’m looking for you today because I have a favor to ask. It’s both a public and a private matter.”

Chen Ping'an replied with a smile, “Feel free to speak.”

Mi Hu continued, “I hope that once the war is over, my brother, who is currently in the Upside-Down Mountain, can go wherever he wishes, such as your Haoran World.”

Chen Ping'an replied, “His military achievements should be sufficient. However, Mi Yu is still a Jade Purity Realm sword immortal. According to unwritten rules, every sword immortal's fate needs to be acknowledged by the top sword immortal. Only then can our Hidden Official lineage finalize it, and at that point, outsiders would have nothing to say.”

Mi Hu said, “The top sword immortal has already given his nod.”

Chen Ping'an smiled, “Since the top sword immortal has agreed, then Mi Hu doesn’t actually need to discuss this with me. Mi Yu’s path is secure. In the Haoran World, a sword immortal of such rare worth can go anywhere they please, as long as they wish to. In the immortal ancestor hall on the mountain or the Golden Luan Hall in the royal dynasty below, they would be honored guests wherever they go.”

Mi Hu responded, “I still can’t help but worry about my brother. If he has no one to look after him in that foreign land, I won’t feel at ease. Cultivating on the mountain in the Haoran World is different from sword training in our Sword Qi Great Wall. Although I’ve never been there, I’m well aware that it’s fraught with intrigue and deception, a real den of thieves. Mi Yu’s dealings with women are decent, but if he gets entangled in some nonsense argument over the Dao with a cultivator, my brother is too naive and would suffer greatly.”

Chen Ping'an understood that this sword immortal was asking him, as an outsider to the Haoran World, to pay more attention.

Yet, there were certain things, such as the agreement with the top sword immortal and his own future circumstances, that Chen Ping'an couldn’t reveal in advance. So he had to carefully consider his words.

As for whether Mi Hu’s words were indirectly insinuating something about him, Chen Ping'an was magnanimous enough to treat it as the wind passing by his ears.

Mi Hu added, “As long as you’re willing to give your approval, I will be extremely grateful. Think of it as a business deal; I trust you, the shopkeeper.”

There was some misunderstanding there.

Chen Ping'an didn’t clarify, saying, “Let’s set aside the gratitude. Mi Yu has accumulated quite a bit of military merit during his two years in the Hidden Official lineage. You don’t need to offer anything extra. However, the success of this matter ultimately hinges on what Mi Yu thinks as well.”

Mi Hu frowned, “With the connections the Hidden Official has in the Sword Qi Great Wall, even if my brother is unwilling to leave, you could easily find a few sword immortals to knock him unconscious and take him to Haoran World.”

Chen Ping'an asked, “If he gets to Haoran World but can’t let go of his burdens, wouldn’t that complicate his cultivation journey? Holding the identity of a sword immortal from the Sword Qi Great Wall while cultivating there might not lead to many incidents, but even one could be a significant problem.”

Mi Hu firmly stated, “Living is more important than anything. To live even one more day is worth it. Besides, don’t underestimate my brother’s resolve; it’s not as fragile as you think.”

Chen Ping'an nodded, “That’s true.”

He continued, “Let’s send Mi Yu to North Julu Continent, to the Taihui Sword Sect or to the Floating Water Sword Lake of Sword Immortal Li Cai. Both places need a sword immortal to serve, and Mi Hu wouldn’t have to worry about fighting there. Eventually, let Mi Yu choose where he wants to go.”

Mi Hu expressed confusion, “Why not send him to your mountain?”

Chen Ping'an shook his head, “I have a pile of old debts. Even if Mi Yu leaves Upside-Down Mountain to go to Ruined Mountain, he wouldn’t find peace in a few days, so there’s no need for that.”

Mi Hu insisted, “Then let Mi Yu go to serve at your Ruined Mountain, paying respects and putting up offerings.”

Chen Ping'an sighed, “Mi Hu, you’re a straightforward person, so I’ll speak plainly. If it were just a simple transaction, only a fool would refuse a sword immortal’s service. I consider your brother a friend and don’t want him getting involved in murky waters in Baoping Continent. In North Julu Continent, where the ties to the Sword Qi Great Wall run deepest, Mi Yu’s identity will serve as the best protection; no other continent offers such an advantage.”

Mi Hu retorted, “Stop rambling like a woman. Mi Yu will go to Baoping Continent, end of discussion!”

So much for reasoning with the great sword immortal Mi Hu—he had to resort to insults?

Just as Chen Ping'an was about to speak some words of moderation, he was taken aback when Mi Hu suddenly began to complain, “A bunch of drunken old bachelors who don’t know what it means to have a woman, how dare they laugh at my brother? They’re like a bunch of men who’ve been run over by a cart! How can they compare to my brother? These bachelors can’t take their eyes off women’s ample chests and backsides. What pathetic creatures…”

Chen Ping'an turned to look at Mi Hu.

How could Mi Hu have the audacity to say that about others?

Realizing the younger Hidden Official’s gaze, Mi Hu, being a great sword immortal, quickly adjusted his tone, saying, “There are some people who aren’t bachelors but act worse than one. Before I came here, I heard someone was drinking with A Liang at Miss Xie’s tavern without spending a dime. I also heard that after opening for business today, Miss Xie was smiling brightly, as if she had become a different person.”

Chen Ping'an smiled back, pretending he didn’t understand, while inwardly he took out a small ledger, recording this little debt against Mi Yu. He would definitely send a letter back to Ruined Mountain, demanding that Mi Yu endure a whole year of illusions and not earn a decent amount of spring rain money before being allowed to leave the mountain.

The two of them arrived at a nearby private residence of a sword immortal called the Zongyu Immortal Pavilion, which had an unusual foundation. The former owner was a sword immortal who had refined a piece of poetic inscription from the Flying Moon. However, the private residence had been abandoned for many years. Most sword immortal residences outside the Sword Qi Great Wall were like this; when a sword immortal passed away and their direct disciples also perished, leaving no descendants to maintain the lineage, it would become a vacant lot. It would then be reclaimed by the Hidden Official lineage according to regulations, to be rented out or gifted to new sword immortals.

For instance, the private residence of the Taihui Sword Sect, known as the Armor Library, was acquired through military merits. The female sword immortal Li Cai first rented the former residence of a sword immortal, known as the Wanhe Residence, but she eventually desired the nearby Pavilion of Floating Clouds, which was entirely carved from a piece of immortal jade. She was willing to pay a sky-high price to acquire it, but the Summer Retreat Palace refused initially due to regulations, infuriating her. She directly flew her sword to send a message to the young Hidden Official, scolding Chen Ping'an thoroughly.

Later, when the war escalated and divine money became scarce, Chen Ping'an instructed Dong Bu De to notify Wanhe Residence that if the price was doubled, they could purchase the entire Pavilion of Floating Clouds.

When the ferry from Osmanthus Island reached Upside-Down Mountain, it brought along several boxes of divine money from the Jiang family of the Yu Gui Sect.

Mi Hu stopped, noticing someone flying down from a distance, seemingly looking for the young Hidden Official beside him. 

It was the middle-earth sword immortal, Ku Xia.

Mi Hu then conveyed his thoughts through their shared consciousness, “Chen Ping'an, thank you for the task today.”

Chen Ping'an replied, “I will do my best.”

Having received the promise, Mi Hu glanced at the sword immortal Ku Xia, then tossed a sword nurturing gourd to Chen Ping'an, saying, “Crafted using ancient methods, its quality is decent,” before soaring away from the city.

Chen Ping'an took the ice-cold sword nurturing gourd and decided to pass it along to Mi Yu later.

Ku Xia approached Chen Ping'an, his face troubled, which only intensified his frown.

Chen Ping'an hung both sword nurturing gourds at his waist, a good omen, and asked the sword immortal from the Shao Yuan Dynasty, “Is Lin Jun Bi leaving?”

Ku Xia nodded, “I realize it’s not the right time. So within half a month, a ship from Central Continent will express some goodwill to the Summer Retreat Palace. It’s a gesture from our Shao Yuan Dynasty.”

Chen Ping'an felt a bit helpless.

Indeed, sword immortal Ku Xia was a straightforward person.

To be honest, if Lin Jun Bi hadn’t chosen to stay with the Hidden Official lineage, he could have left the Sword Qi Great Wall long ago.

If Lin Jun Bi were to leave, any sword cultivator from the Summer Retreat Palace would think it perfectly reasonable.

However, with Ku Xia’s words, it felt as though Lin Jun Bi’s departure would paint him as ungrateful, to the point that the national teacher from the Shao Yuan Dynasty, who was also Lin Jun Bi’s mentor, would have to spend money to appease the Sword Qi Great Wall for Lin Jun Bi’s return home.

But as for the heavenly materials and earthly treasures and divine money from the Shao Yuan Dynasty, Chen Ping'an welcomed it without hesitation, the more the better.

Thus, he didn’t take advantage of the honest person and directly suggested going to the Summer Retreat Palace to call Lin Jun Bi out to meet with sword immortal Ku Xia.

However, Ku Xia didn’t move, looking toward the Zongyu Immortal Pavilion’s main door, asking, “Hidden Official, do you know the origin of this residence’s name?”

Chen Ping'an replied, “Not quite.”

In truth, during his years as the Hidden Official, he had enjoyed perusing the many sealed archives of the Summer Retreat Palace as a form of leisure. 

The last owner who renamed the residence to Zongyu Immortal Pavilion was a woman—a rare literate sword immortal from the Sword Qi Great Wall who shared a fondness for planting immortal flowers, much like Guo Jia. She had once entrusted the Upside-Down Mountain to purchase a elm tree from Fu Yao Continent, which was then transplanted into her small garden. It unexpectedly bloomed high above the eaves, delighting the sword immortal, who then decided to name the residence accordingly. However, once the sword immortal passed away and there were no disciples, the residence fell into disrepair over the years. The Zongyu Immortal Pavilion, with its additional layer of immortal prohibitions, would not allow outsiders to intrude. As such, no one knew whether the interior had withered or flourished, whether flowers bloomed or withered.

Ku Xia said, “The first time I traveled to the Sword Qi Great Wall with a friend, my friend admired a disciple of this sword immortal. Yet, due to the rigid customs, they couldn’t become immortal partners.”

Chen Ping'an asked, “If your friend had stayed, wouldn’t they have been able to become a couple?”

Ku Xia’s expression darkened further as he sighed, “How many sword cultivators in the Haoran World are unencumbered mountain and wilderness cultivators? Even if they start out that way—like Deng Liang from Aiai Continent—they will ultimately be taken in by the grand sects’ ancestral halls. Moreover, my friend has been heavily relied upon since childhood as a lineage teacher. The weight of their sect’s favor is not something they can simply discard. Within the sect, there are elders that my friend respects greatly.”

Chen Ping'an replied, “It’s indeed difficult to have it both ways.”

Ku Xia said, “That’s why my friend and I both hold the Hidden Official in high esteem.”

Chen Ping'an chuckled, “Sword immortal Ku Xia, if you can’t lie, then don’t.”

There were no friends or sword immortal disciples; it was clearly Ku Xia himself who was the one infatuated with the female sword immortal.

Ku Xia, feeling helpless, said, “During that farewell trip to Nan Po Sha Continent, everyone urged me, including Yu Juanfu and Jin Zhenmeng, among others, as if I had accomplished some great feat. I genuinely felt guilty and didn’t deserve their admiration.”

Chen Ping'an said, “If sword immortal Ku Xia speaks up, do you think Yu Juanfu and Zhu Mei would respect you even more?”

Ku Xia appeared bewildered at first, then slowly realized, and finally felt somewhat relieved. “It’s better not to say anything. As an elder, discussing such romantic matters with juniors is inappropriate.”

Chen Ping'an posed a question, “The owner of Zongyu Immortal Pavilion, back then, aimed to accumulate military merits but ended up dying in battle. Do you harbor any resentment towards the top sword immortal, or towards the Sword Qi Great Wall?”

Ku Xia shook his head, “Without the Sword Qi Great Wall’s soil, how could I have met someone like her?”

This was Ku Xia’s heartfelt truth. He bore no hatred towards the Sword Qi Great Wall; if there was anyone to blame, it would be his own helplessness.

Chen Ping'an nodded.

With Lin Jun Bi and Ku Xia present, Chen Ping'an's impression of the Shao Yuan Dynasty improved a little.

A Liang had unraveled a mystery yesterday, and now sword immortal Ku Xia had solved another enigma today.

Suddenly, Ku Xia asked, “Hidden Official, didn’t you say you were unfamiliar with this place?”

Chen Ping'an replied earnestly, “I previously said, ‘not quite clear.’ As a Hidden Official, it’s my duty to know a little about the Zongyu Immortal Pavilion right under the nose of the Summer Retreat Palace.”

Ku Xia felt exasperated.

If he were dealing with scholars from the Ya Sheng lineage, things wouldn’t be like this.

Leading sword immortal Ku Xia back to the Summer Retreat Palace, Chen Ping'an called out, and the white-clad youth Lin Jun Bi gracefully stepped out, exuding an aura of immortality.

Upon seeing sword immortal Ku Xia, Lin Jun Bi immediately understood the purpose of their visit and clasped his fists in silence.

At this moment, leaving the Summer Retreat Palace and the Sword Qi Great Wall, shedding the burdens of the Hidden Official lineage, would inevitably raise suspicions of shirking responsibility. For instance, Deng Liang and Cao Gun would likely feel this mental burden. However, Lin Jun Bi would never entertain such thoughts.

Chen Ping'an patted Lin Jun Bi's shoulder, saying, “Parting on good terms isn’t easy. Take care.”

Lin Jun Bi stood tall and clasped his fists again, saying, “In the years spent beside the Hidden Official, I’ve learned a great deal and benefited immensely. Jun Bi will remember this. A gentleman must focus on his foundation; once the foundation is established, the Dao will naturally arise!”

Chen Ping'an smiled, “Let’s skip the pleasantries and focus on doing practical things. As for the agreement from years ago, I will certainly fulfill it for you.”

Lin Jun Bi instantly understood, his face filled with sincerity as he said, “Hidden Official, your expertise in chess is renowned. The chessboard and box shall remain at the Summer Retreat Palace.”

Chen Ping'an gave Lin Jun Bi a hearty slap on the shoulder and smiled, “It seems Jun Bi has learned some real skills.”

Sword immortal Ku Xia felt a sense of relief.

He had previously worried that the young Hidden Official might intentionally make things difficult for Lin Jun Bi due to the connections with the national teacher of the Shao Yuan Dynasty and the young sword cultivators.

It appeared he had underestimated the young Hidden Official’s character.

Ku Xia took out a sealed letter and handed it to Lin Jun Bi, saying, “Jun Bi, barring any unforeseen circumstances, you should leave tomorrow on a returning ship from Nan Po Sha Continent. This letter was just sent by your teacher via flying sword to Chun Fan Zhai at Upside-Down Mountain.”

Lin Jun Bi would definitely remain at the Summer Retreat Palace today; otherwise, there wouldn’t be anyone familiar at the residence of sword immortal Sun Ju Yuan in the city. Moreover, sword immortal Sun currently had a very poor impression of the young sword cultivators from the Shao Yuan Dynasty. After the frontier incident, it wouldn’t make sense for Lin Jun Bi to go and make a fool of himself.

Furthermore, Lin Jun Bi had maintained good relations with all sword cultivators from the Hidden Official lineage, especially with the cheerful Cao Gun and Xuan Can, with whom he had grown very close.

Guo Zhu Jiu had been urging the three of them to cut off chicken heads and burn yellow paper, saying she had prepared everything and was just waiting for the three of them to bow!

Before leaving, Ku Xia reminded Lin Jun Bi to be cautious on his journey back.

Instead of directly returning to the city, sword immortal Ku Xia strolled over to the Zongyu Immortal Pavilion.

With a face full of distress, the elder gazed at the residence, lost in thought for a moment before breaking into a smile.

Lin Jun Bi returned to the Summer Retreat Palace and continued the unfinished chess game with Pang Yuan Ji, which had already been decided.

Pang Yuan Ji chuckled, “Is this our last game?”

Lin Jun Bi asked, “Shall I let you win this time?”

Pang Yuan Ji replied, “If you let the Hidden Official help you with chess, there’s no need to let me win.”

Chen Ping'an, observing from the side with his hands tucked into his sleeves, remarked nonchalantly, “I’ve played proper chess with others and have never lost a single match.”

Pang Yuan Ji asked, “How many matches have you played?”

Chen Ping'an shot him a sideways glance, “Why do you care?”

Pang Yuan Ji gently returned a piece to the box, saying, “I’ll just leave it.”

Lin Jun Bi’s eyes brightened, “Sounds good.”

Chen Ping'an also felt relieved and took out the sword nurturing gourd gifted by Mi Hu to examine it carefully. For now, he was still its owner.

At the bottom of the sword nurturing gourd, the words "Hao Liang" were inscribed.

The material of the sword nurturing gourd was unknown, and it was unclear what Mi Hu meant by “decent quality.” 

Pang Yuan Ji turned to Chen Ping'an and said, “If I recall correctly, Mi Hu picked this up from the corpse of a Nascent Soul realm demon on the battlefield years ago. After acquiring it, Mi Hu never had anyone verify its quality, so it’s hard to say.”

Chen Ping'an stared intently at the sword nurturing gourd, nearly pressing his face against it, casually stating, “I can’t say how good a good thing is, but if it’s not good, I can tell as soon as I hold it. You wouldn’t understand; this is a matter of talent and expertise.”

Pang Yuan Ji didn’t want to continue that topic and changed the subject, “How did you survive that ambush by five people? Even sword immortal Chou Miao said he might not have escaped.”

The five who had surrounded him were top talents: Zhu Zhen, Li Zhen, Yu Si, Tan, and Liu Bai.

The curiosity surrounding the young Hidden Official wouldn’t be limited to Pang Yuan Ji alone.

Many things about the young Hidden Official remained a mystery; knowing only the surface, even if you had seen it with your own eyes or heard it with your ears, didn’t mean you understood.

For instance, many speculated that Chen Ping'an’s life-bound flying sword could isolate a small world, but even if it was a small world, there were distinctions, with varying divine abilities.

Chen Ping'an put away the sword nurturing gourd and hung it back at his waist. After Lin Jun Bi put away the chess pieces, he was drawn into Chen Ping'an’s proximity.

Chen Ping'an didn’t elaborate on the specifics of the ambush but merely told Pang Yuan Ji and Lin Jun Bi about the flying swords and methods of the other five.

If they needed to fight side by side and leave the city for a battle, Chen Ping'an wouldn’t mind sharing more inside information. Since it wasn’t necessary, however, saying more would be pointless.
