After all, being honest with someone doesn’t mean pouring out your heart all the time. If one side opens up too much and the other fails to catch it properly, it could hurt both parties.

Lin Jun Bi asked, “So, it seems that Liu Bai’s life-bound flying sword is the most dangerous?”

Chen Ping'an nodded, “If you encounter her in the future, be extra cautious. Once she reaches the upper fifth realm, her life-bound flying sword will be deadly; it could be quite troublesome.”

If that ambush had purely been a contest of strength, several of them would have perished there.

Speaking of which, Chen Ping'an chuckled, “But for now, we’re unlikely to meet her. So in that transaction, I didn’t gain much, but I didn’t lose too much either.”

Lin Jun Bi lamented, “This strange and bizarre flying sword, I’ve never heard of anything like it before. Previously, I only knew that some sword immortals have particularly delicate life-bound flying swords, but nothing as extravagant as Liu Bai’s.”

Chen Ping'an remarked, “In this vast world, there’s no shortage of wonders.”

Using his ability to traverse space, Chen Ping'an directly moved from the Summer Retreat Palace to the Cold-Weather Palace.

He didn’t find Grandma Bai, who usually taught boxing, but instead encountered an unexpected guest.

It was Guo Zhu Jiu, who had brought a bamboo box. Instead of staying home, she had come to the Cold-Weather Palace early in the morning, and now she was on the training ground, enthusiastically describing the thrilling ambush.

Guo Zhu Jiu hadn’t witnessed the ambush herself, and since Chen Ping'an had been recuperating at Ning’s residence, he hadn’t spoken a word to her, so her storytelling was purely fictional and fabricated.

However, Chen Ping'an didn’t stop her. He sat far away on the railing, allowing his disciple to play the role of a storyteller.

When it came to boxing, Guo Zhu Jiu was indeed a true disciple.

With one leg raised in a pose of a golden rooster standing on one leg, she spoke solemnly, “The situation was dire—five sword cultivators were bloodthirsty, each wielding life-bound flying swords of the highest quality, at least as tall as two Yuan Creation realms! Were you afraid? I know I was! Just think about it—Li Zhen is a disciple from Tuo Yue Mountain, and Zhu Zhen is the top disciple of Liu Cha, while Liu Bai is a direct disciple of the old fox Zhou Mi! What kind of backing do these three have? Not to mention Yu Si and Tan, who were able to stay at that Jia Shen tent—they must not be simple characters, right? Otherwise, at such a young age, how could they rise to the ranks of the hundred sword immortals of the barbaric world? But it’s fine; it was just a drizzle, nothing major. My master remained calm in the face of danger; just like that, his aura was intimidating! You all are martial artists; you should know that every stance of a martial arts grandmaster carries great significance…”

Chen Ping'an truly couldn’t listen any longer. Moreover, his disciple’s posture lacked any semblance of grandeur or masterful demeanor.

He quickly rose, leaped to the training ground, and cleared his throat, reminding this well-meaning but unhelpful disciple that it was time to wrap up.

Guo Zhu Jiu turned to see her master and worried that he might be too high-minded to let her speak a few words of truth, so she hurriedly maintained her stance and accelerated her speech, rattling off a few hundred words about the subsequent developments of the battle.

Chen Ping'an walked up beside Guo Zhu Jiu and gently pressed her head down.

Guo Zhu Jiu assumed a posture of deep breathing, “I won’t say anything more; after all, I can only express a fraction of my master’s magnificence. What a pity, what a pity.”

A child named Jiang Yun crossed his arms and asked, “Chen Ping'an, did Sister Guo say you crushed that female sword cultivator named Liu Bai with one punch? Is that true? What’s wrong with you? Facing five sword cultivators, four of whom are male, why didn’t you just take them all down and instead only target the girl? Are you picking soft persimmons to squeeze?” 

At this point, Jiang Yun chuckled, raising his eyebrows repeatedly. “Squeezing soft persimmons? Where did you aim your punch? I’ve heard that the battlefield was quite strange, obscured as if covered by a blanket. Outsiders couldn’t tell who was lying beneath that blanket…”

Guo Zhu Jiu shook her head with a sympathetic look, “Jiang Yun, it seems our relationship is now set in stone.”

Fearless Jiang Yun unexpectedly felt a little anxious, “Sister Guo, don’t! We’re sworn siblings of good fortune; don’t let an outsider spoil our bond! Even if we do have our differences, please don’t come banging on my window later!”

Chen Ping'an chuckled, “Alright, let’s start practicing. Guo Zhu Jiu, you watch from the side.”

Guo Zhu Jiu obediently stepped aside.

Chen Ping'an frequently came here to help the children practice boxing for an hour.

The so-called “feeding boxing” meant that the children were allowed to strike at him without worrying about any specific techniques.

Jiang Yun glanced at the Hidden Official, “You look like you’re not healing well from your injuries. I’m worried that my punch might knock you down. Be careful; don’t try to act tough. You haven’t seen me in a few days, right? My boxing skills have made great progress, and my punches can cause the heavens to collapse and the earth to shatter!”

Chen Ping'an looked at this child, who had the best martial arts aptitude and an exceptional talent for talking back.

Jiang Yun immediately retreated several steps, taking a stance to prepare for an attack. He kicked off the ground, darting in and out, leaping high to reach the young Hidden Official, and threw a punch.

Chen Ping'an kept one hand behind his back, tilted his head, and with the other hand, gently pushed Jiang Yun's head, sending him crashing to the ground, rolling several times before getting back up.

Following Jiang Yun’s lead, a girl named Yuan Zao Hua followed up with a sweeping kick from behind Chen Ping'an, but he sidestepped and elbowed her down, sending her sprawling as she slid across the ground.

Chen Ping'an’s “feeding boxing” naturally required some pressure, and he had never missed a target.

According to their agreement, whenever Chen Ping'an was hit by a punch, it meant the children were ready to go home.

One child was gently pushed by Chen Ping'an and crashed into another, sending both flying.

One child, who got too close, had his face grabbed by Chen Ping'an, twisting his wrist until both his feet were off the ground, sending him flying.

“Form follows intention, energy flows from the dantian, and intention permeates the whole body. We martial artists stand tall in the world; our punches are as fast as flying swords, and our intent in our punches doesn’t lose to that of sword immortals.”

Chen Ping'an walked slowly, casually punching one child in the neck, causing their head to tilt. He then transformed his punch into a palm, with his palm facing down, slapping the child on the shoulder, making the latter stumble and fall. With a light kick, he sent another child flying, while simultaneously blocking another child's punch, who was now off balance.

“Powerful and vigorous, unbreakable, think carefully about your punches. The intention of your punch must be as fine as a needle; you must think before striking.”

Chen Ping'an stepped aside and punched another child at the back of the head, sending them sprawling to the ground, blood pouring from their nose.

Another child changed trajectories several times, their elbow overlapping their front hand, palms flipping quickly as they combined their moves, closing in on Chen Ping'an with some minor momentum in their punches.

Once again, Chen Ping'an countered every move with his elbows and palms, pushing the child back to their starting position.

Jiang Yun, seeing an opportunity, kicked at Chen Ping'an but was met with a swift kick in the chest, sending him to the ground. As he lay there, Jiang Yun was about to curse Chen Ping'an for taking advantage of his height when he realized that the young Hidden Official had kicked him while leaning back. Jiang Yun wiped the blood from the corner of his mouth, bracing himself to get back up.

Any child who approached Chen Ping'an was effortlessly knocked back. One was sent rolling from an elbow to the abdomen, and another was shoulder-checked and sent flying. When the children got back to their feet, they felt as if half their bodies had disintegrated. Still, they gritted their teeth and got back up; generally speaking, punches delivered with a hint of hardship wouldn’t slow them down. 

However, not just them, but all the children practicing martial arts here, along with Jiang Yun, remembered the young Hidden Official’s saying: a martial artist’s body must endure some injuries, or they would be seeking death themselves. If they could get hurt and still punch faster, that was the mark of a true martial artist.

Yuan Zao Hua lunged like an arrow. 

Some children threw wild punches, while others, familiar with one another, tried to work together to land a punch on Chen Ping'an.

One child after another was knocked back by Chen Ping'an, and while they weren’t severely injured, it definitely wasn’t pleasant.

Chen Ping'an continued to walk slowly, “As long as your intention isn’t alive, even if you can forget life and death in martial arts, you’re still dead.”

Chen Ping'an crouched slightly, positioning his hands above a leaping child’s jaw, gently lifting him, sending the child flying ten or more feet away. “Punches must originate from the ground. No matter how good your techniques are, if your stance isn’t steady, how can you leave the ground?”

After a stick of incense had burned, most of the children lay on the ground, with only a few able to sit up; not a single one was standing.

Chen Ping'an stood still and said, “Continue. Punches can be slow, but your intent must be heavier. Otherwise, I won’t hold back.”

The children nearly all swayed as they got back up.

On the side, A Liang and the old woman watched Chen Ping'an teach boxing, with A Liang softly laughing, “The boxing is practical and not difficult, yet it’s hard to execute so beautifully. If they reach the Haoran World in the future, once they throw a punch, it’ll be like entering a garden of a hundred flowers.”

The old woman smiled, “The son-in-law's boxing is indeed quite splendid. His punches and appearance complement each other well. It’s normal for girls to be fond of him; after all, he’s not someone who’ll easily get involved, which makes people feel secure.”

A Liang chuckled, “Does this kid have any shortcomings?”

The old woman thought for a moment and shook her head.

A Liang looked at the children and sighed, “Carrying a burden on the shoulders is just physical labor. But carrying a burden in the heart—what’s the end of that?”

The old woman readily agreed and softly said, “This is something the son-in-law isn’t quite good at.”

Another stick of incense later, all the children lay on the ground this time.

One sharp-eyed child, lying on the ground, caught a glimpse of A Liang from a distance and quickly began to whisper excitedly with the others.

Chen Ping'an turned his head and smiled, “A Liang, why don’t you take over and teach boxing for a while?”

A Liang was eager to try.

His boxing skills were still quite commendable.

He propped himself up on the railing, stood gracefully, took a deep breath, and with a shake of his shoulders, shouted before moving straight ahead, showcasing his exceptionally flowing boxing techniques and footwork between the corridor and the training ground.

Jiang Yun jumped up, wearing a rare serious expression, saying, “Chen Ping'an, let’s continue; you can teach boxing now.”

The other children nodded in agreement.

A Liang stood there, rubbing his chin, thinking this wasn’t right.

My boxing is both beautiful and solid; the Dao Old Second has suffered greatly from it!

Guo Zhu Jiu comforted him gently, “Senior A Liang, your sword techniques are already so high; there’s no need to feel ashamed if your boxing isn’t as good as my master’s.”

A Liang asked, “Did you all see that my boxing skills weren’t high?”

Guo Zhu Jiu vigorously shook her head like a rattle drum.

A Liang tentatively asked, “Is it that I didn’t look good?”

Guo Zhu Jiu sighed, “Senior A Liang, do you want to hear the truth or a lie?”

A Liang replied, “A lie!”

Guo Zhu Jiu immediately beamed with excitement, enjoying the banter with Senior A Liang, which didn’t hurt their feelings and saved her from getting scolded by her master. She raised both thumbs enthusiastically, loudly praising, “Senior, your boxing is incredible, truly incredible, just as good-looking as your appearance!”

A Liang was unconcerned, happy just to hear something pleasant, and asked, “Zhu Jiu, do you want to learn sword techniques? Uncle A Liang isn’t boasting; my boxing skills might not be as good as your master’s, but my swordsmanship, tsk tsk tsk…”

Guo Zhu Jiu shook her head, “I won’t learn.”

A Liang asked, “Why not?”

The little girl took a step in place, swaying her shoulders, her little bamboo box bobbing, “Because I only have one master!” 

*(End of this chapter)*

 ### Chapter 782: The Hairpin

On the training ground, the children once again lay sprawled on the ground, each one bruised and battered. The initial training in martial arts was certainly not comfortable. When it was time to endure hardships, they were enjoying comforts, and when it was time to enjoy, they had to endure.

Having been born in the Sword Qi Great Wall and entering this cold refuge palace to learn martial arts, they had to adapt to the suffering and master a skill.

Not every hardship in the world leads to sweet rewards. The pure martial heart of a martial artist can only be forged through the trials of suffering.

The Hidden Official, dressed in a long blue robe, remained calm and composed, saying, “Take a break for two incense sticks’ worth of time.”

Chen Ping’an sat cross-legged, placing his hands palm-up in his lap, and began to meditate. The children struggled to rise, forming a circle around him, mimicking the young Hidden Official’s posture, closing their eyes, and slowly adjusting their breathing.

When Chen Ping’an opened his eyes, he assessed each child’s punches, commenting on their strengths and weaknesses. He wouldn’t favor Xu Jun just because he came from a prominent family, nor would he scold Zhang Pan for his slow learning due to his weak physique. Every well-executed punch would earn praise, while a tired one would be met with criticism. He wouldn’t go easy on Sun Qu and the tomboy just because they were girls.

In short, Chen Ping’an wanted all the children to remember one fundamental truth: in martial arts, one must first confront oneself.

Learning martial arts begins with becoming a better person. Those who teach, regardless of whether they hold the title of master or teacher, must first educate others. Teaching is not just empty talk; even a village schoolteacher’s nuances can leave a lasting impression on a poor child, while one flattering word from a wealthy man could be dismissed as mere flattery. Everything is remembered, and thus, the profound teachings become overshadowed.

There are truths in both books and life; everyone can be a teacher.

Chen Ping’an fell silent.

According to the rules, it was now time for the children to ask questions.

The child named Xu Gong from Mumen Alley was the first to speak up, “Mr. Chen, a punch travels in a straight line, so it should be the fastest. If practicing stance training is to strengthen the body, why then are there so many different punches?”

Chen Ping’an raised a hand, thrusting out a punch suddenly before suspending it mid-air. “Xu Gong, are you saying that a punch traveling in a straight line reaches the target the fastest, correct?”

Xu Gong hesitated, unsure of his own words.

Jiang Yun chuckled, “One punch and he’s down.”

Who in the Sword Qi Great Wall didn’t know that the young Hidden Official was particularly “gentle” with the fairer sex? Otherwise, how could he have earned the nickname of “One Punch to the Second Shopkeeper”?

As for why he was so ruthless with the wildlings, it was probably because the female sword cultivator was less attractive than the male.

However, Jiang Yun suddenly recalled the scene of Yu Jianfu being pressed down and banged against the wall, sighing as he felt he might have wronged the second shopkeeper.

Xu Gong’s expression turned anxious; he had never meant that. He wouldn’t dare show the slightest disrespect to Mr. Chen.

In Xu Gong’s eyes, Chen Ping’an was like a deity, immaculate and unblemished. When he chatted with his two good friends, they all admired him greatly. Therefore, when Guo Zhujiu was telling stories earlier, they were the three who believed the most.

Coming from Mumen Alley, Xu Gong knew he wasn’t from a prominent family like Jiang Yun. Lacking Jiang Yun’s talent and background, he, along with his friends Zhang Pan and Tang Qu, often practiced their stances secretly at night, sometimes encountering that tomboy Yuan Zao Hua. However, too much practice almost harmed their health.

Chen Ping’an maintained that punching stance, then raised his left hand, using his punching right arm as a path, pointing out the flow of pure energy that travels in a straight punch—from the fist, to the wrist, forearm, shoulder, back, and waist—highlighting each pressure point, thoroughly explaining how this straight punch channels energy. Every muscle, every bone, every tendon was accounted for, and he explained it all to the children, breaking down the various techniques and their subtleties. He clarified how and why to generate force, providing insightful yet accessible explanations.

After retracting his fist, Chen Ping’an rested his hands on his knees and smiled, “Thus, the punch techniques are foundational, the intent of the punch is central, and the principles of punching are celestial.”

Jiang Yun furrowed his brow, “The punch techniques are the least important? But I think the stance and form must come from the techniques; they are very important.”

Chen Ping’an chuckled, raising a fist, twisting his wrist to change the punch into a palm, only an inch from the ground, and suddenly slapped the training ground.

The earth trembled, and all the children almost simultaneously bounced up, varying in height and twisting in the air. 

Then, as if crushed by an unseen force, they fell back down, gasping for breath, feeling nearly suffocated, their backs curved, unable to straighten up.

“The punch techniques are foundational; this only refers to position and order. It doesn’t mean they are unimportant; on the contrary, all techniques begin low. Only by building layers upon layers can our techniques rise to the heavens.”

As Chen Ping’an withdrew that intangible essence of the punch, the children immediately felt relieved. He turned to Yuan Zao Hua and Zhang Pan, “Training in martial arts requires constant focus and caution. This is the essence of the teacher leading the way while the student must be vigilant. Yuan Zao Hua, Zhang Pan, you both did well just now, showing that while resting, you were still practicing your stances, though not high off the ground, your sitting posture was stable. Jiang Yun, despite being the lowest off the ground, had a scattered posture.”

Jiang Yun rolled his eyes; he was already used to the Hidden Official’s cold remarks.

The shy Zhang Pan looked excited, while the tomboy’s expression was resolute, her lips pressed tight. After learning martial arts, the girl had changed dramatically. A few years ago at the Sword Qi Great Wall, when she first met the second shopkeeper, who had yet to become the Hidden Official, she was just a cheerful little girl.

Chen Ping’an’s gaze swept over everyone, leaning slightly forward as he spoke, “Learning martial arts is not merely about throwing punches on the training ground. Breathing, footwork, diet, even observing flying birds may seem tiring at first, but with practice, it becomes second nature. Your bodies are a small universe, filled with treasures that belong to you alone. Unless one day you must contend with others for life or death, no one can take them from you.”

Chen Ping’an squinted, “Now the question arises—when your punches are strong, and you decide to strike, how should you face your opponent in a fair contest of life and death?”

Jiang Yun shouted, “One punch to take them down!”

Chen Ping’an smiled, “You little rascal, are you not done playing yet?”

With crossed arms, Jiang Yun replied seriously, “Hidden Official, this isn’t a joke. When a martial artist throws a punch, they must carry the demeanor of being the best in the world. My pursuit of martial arts lies in making my opponent tremble before my fist even leaves my hand.”

Chen Ping’an stood up, “Alright, then I’ll teach you. Hearing you say this reminds me of a match I had. I faced a six-realm opponent with my ten-realm skill. Now, you can use your three-realm against my seven-realm. It’s a four-realm difference; don’t say I’m bullying you.”

Jiang Yun immediately sprang to his feet.

Chen Ping’an pointed to a corner of the training ground, “You stand over there against the wall.”

Jiang Yun swaggered over, turning his back to the others. The children secretly gritted their teeth, wishing they could slap themselves. They could only remind themselves to lose gracefully and not let their faces show defeat.

Chen Ping’an walked to the opposite side of the training ground but suddenly changed his mind. “Everyone, come over here, stand side by side, and don’t lean against the wall—stand three steps away from it.”

The lives these children would lead wouldn’t be regimented; they would only face opponents of similar strength or those a realm or two higher.

Whether it’s him or Granny Bai, in the future, they would help the children strengthen their bodies step by step, but on the path of cultivation, such good fortune wouldn’t always be there. No one wants to be anyone's stepping stone; they all aspire to climb higher and higher, reaching for the peak.

Chen Ping’an had demonstrated how to punch from the peaks of the three to the seven realms.

He had also shown them the punches of the eighth, ninth, and tenth realms.

However, the children, including Jiang Yun, felt that Granny Bai, having dropped from the tenth to the ninth realm, was currently at a higher level, but in terms of the “meaning” behind the punches, the young Hidden Official was still more captivating.

But the previous training had truly been practice; the children were merely spectators.

Today, Chen Ping’an wanted the children to stand on an opposing front, to personally experience what a punch felt like.

Years ago in North Julu Prefecture, the elder Gu You had blocked his path and had once asked for a spar.

The punch had come without warning, and the response had been unprepared. Gu You’s sudden strike had arrived in an instant, and at that moment, Chen Ping’an could only await his fate.

After stopping, Chen Ping’an centered himself, immersing in focus, forgetting the world around him, with no one in front of him.

Jiang Yun, facing Chen Ping’an from a distance, began to sweat profusely, subconsciously warning everyone, “We must bite our teeth and hold our ground; no one can back down, and no one can lean against the wall. Even if we’re scared, we must stand still!”

The girl from Yuhua Street, Sun Qu, trembled, “I’m scared right now.”

Initially, like Jiang Yun, Sun Qu had been one of the children least willing to learn martial arts because she had a sister named Sun Zao, a sword cultivator.

Yuan Zao Hua whispered, “Then just focus on your stance and don’t think about anything else!”

Chen Ping’an didn’t rush to throw a punch.

For those children standing against the wall, this was even more torturous. Since they would eventually face danger, it would be better to get it over with than to be slowly intimidated.

A Liang said, “Guo Zhujiu, when your master teaches others, he’s also practicing himself and refining his mind. This is a good habit; using a shell to create a dojo isn’t a derogatory term.”

Chen Ping’an’s previous martial arts training had been too diverse, and he needed this opportunity to reflect and forge his own path. Sometimes, he needed to think of nothing, as one does when sleeping, to calm his mind. Teaching martial arts, practicing, and cultivating the heart—these seemingly singular tasks were, in truth, three intertwined endeavors.

Teaching martial arts to the martial students of the Sword Qi Great Wall was crucial, but it was even more vital to provide all the children with a relatively stable path of cultivation. For a Hidden Official responsible for the state of affairs, this was a significant distraction. Yet in the end, it turned out not to be a loss.

Guo Zhujiu had long since placed her book box at her feet and had been imitating her master’s punches, remaining busy from start to finish. Upon hearing A Liang’s words, she paused her punches and said, “With so much knowledge from my master, I will learn it all.”

Granny Bai stood by, softly saying, “If your master throws this punch, many children will likely crumble on the spot.”

A Liang laughed, “To truly understand where one’s punches stand is a great thing.”

Back then, Gu You, as the ancestor of the Mountain Shaking Fist, had seen this pure martial artist from another continent, who happened to have his foundation in the Mountain Shaking Fist, and had thrown a peak ninth-realm punch at him.

Chen Ping’an stepped forward, silent as a whisper.

With six steps of stance practice, in the blink of an eye, as swift as thunder, the entire training ground began to tremble, ripples spreading outwards, the air thick with martial intent.

Sun Qu, who had been hoping to resist her fears with a firm stance, found herself shaken back to reality. Her stance faltered, her mind was thrown into chaos, and her face reflected sheer panic.

Jiang Yun felt the overwhelming martial intent enveloping the space, and with a sharp shout, he stomped down hard, setting his stance while using his own martial intent to counter the overwhelming force. Seeing Sun Qu about to fall, he gritted his teeth, shifted sideways, his face contorted in pain, but still stood protectively in front of her. After all, she was a girl, and he felt it was his duty to protect her.

Xu Gong and Yuan Zao Hua called out simultaneously, “Six-step stance!”

All the children seemed to share a connection, almost instinctively advancing instead of retreating, attempting to counter the incoming force with their own stances.

A fierce wind swept over them, martial intent pressing down upon them.

They quickly found that retreating was not an option; they could barely take two steps before stumbling back.

Sun Qu, summoning courage she hadn’t known she had, bypassed Jiang Yun and chose to face the punch directly.

In an instant, together with Jiang Yun, all the others leaned against the wall, their faces pale, sweating profusely, while some of the weaker children had already collapsed against the wall.

Standing in the center of the training ground, Chen Ping’an rested one hand behind him and the other in a fist against his abdomen, exhaling a breath of turbid air.

He quickly turned to wipe away the blood trickling from his nose. Despite the strain of his present physique, even just half a punch was no easy feat.

Chen Ping’an turned and smiled, “Get up, everyone; today’s practice ends here.”

The children were momentarily stunned, some dazed.

After a brief silence, Chen Ping’an suddenly laughed, “After this punch, I must say, my eye for selecting martial seeds is indeed sharp. In the future, should you walk the rivers and lakes and encounter fellow martial artists, you can proudly say your teacher is the tenth-realm martial artist Bai Lianshuang from the Sword Qi Great Wall, and the one who fed you martial arts is Chen Ping’an of the Great Harmony World, with the observer being the sword master A Liang.”

After bidding farewell to Granny Bai, Chen Ping’an and A Liang, along with Guo Zhujiu, left the cold refuge palace on foot.

A Liang said, “Zhujiu, earlier your master mentioned the observer but only referred to me. Did he forget you? Are you hurt?”

Guo Zhujiu replied with confusion, “Master mentioned it; didn’t you hear?”

A Liang was taken aback, “How could I not hear?”

Guo Zhujiu, serious, said, “I said it to myself in my heart on behalf of my master.”

A Liang admired her, “Your sword heart is impressive, Zhujiu.”

Chen Ping’an chuckled, “A Liang, can you teach me the Sword Qi Eighteen Stops? I’d like to learn.”

A Liang sighed, “I said I’d teach earlier, but Zhujiu didn’t care.”

A Liang ruffled his hair, “But since Zhujiu said my looks and martial skills are both good, such heartfelt words mean I should stubbornly impart this ultimate skill. But no rush; I’ll visit the Guo residence later.”

Guo Zhujiu exchanged a knowing glance with Chen Ping’an, both smiling.

Master, you understand.  
Master, I understand.

Guo Zhujiu didn’t linger; she had sneaked out over the wall today and needed to return home.

After bidding farewell to her master and A Liang, the girl, carrying her hiking staff and a small bamboo box, dashed off.

A Liang and Chen Ping’an made their way toward the stacked hills where a tavern stood.

A Liang asked, “After Tao Wenjian died, did we receive extra celestial coins for his military achievements?”

Chen Ping’an didn’t hide anything, replying, “I took out some too.”

At the tavern, taking stock of the wealth Chen Ping’an had accumulated over the years at the Sword Qi Great Wall from the gambling den and the sales of seals and folding fans, not a single snowflake coin remained. All had been returned to the Sword Qi Great Wall under the name of Tao Wen’s legacy. Of course, it wasn’t because Tao Wen requested it; it was simply Chen Ping’an’s original intention.

This was also the reason Tao Wen entrusted his posthumous affairs to the young Hidden Official.

To catch the eye of a sword saint can never be achieved by merely raking in a fortune or speaking pretty words.

A Liang continued, “With so many celestial coins, that’s no small sum. Are you just going to leave them on the table in the courtyard for sword cultivators to take at will? Can you really trust that?”

With the war currently at a lull, cultivating swords was of utmost importance, and sword cultivators were notoriously unreasonable with money.

This was why so many sword saints at the Sword Qi Great Wall were financially struggling.

The higher the rank of their life swords and the higher their cultivation, aside from a few wealthy families on Tai Xiang Street, no one dared claim they had enough money.

Only when they weren’t in a state of cultivation would sword cultivators have some spare change, drinking and betting casually.

Thus, while most sword cultivators might only take what they needed from Tao Wen’s house, some would inevitably pocket extra celestial coins.

Chen Ping’an shook his head. “No one is watching over there. Tao Wen didn’t care; I don’t either. It’s not a business deal; there’s no need to fuss.”

A Liang nodded. “That’s the way to think about it—be more relaxed.”

Chen Ping’an took off the white jade hairpin from his bun.

A Liang took it, his mind lost in thought, then burst into laughter, “What a sly scholar; you even fooled me back then.”

Chen Ping’an couldn’t be bothered to use his inner voice for this and said directly, “This hairpin changed the tide of battle during my confrontation with Li Zhen. Otherwise, I wouldn’t have won without being a sword cultivator then.”

The white jade hairpin had been unsealed, and A Liang could see its nature clearly. 

Chen Ping’an continued, “Time flows differently here compared to many cave heavens; a month here is like a year in the outside world.”

The white jade hairpin was a peculiar cave heaven, small in area, able to accommodate only over a hundred people, and its spiritual energy was average, hardly qualifying as a treasure land. In fact, it was unsuitable for cultivators to practice.

A Liang sighed, “That old scholar truly cared.”

The old scholar had gone to great lengths for his disciple, Qi Jingchun. 

Using it as a shelter, it could serve as a study—a place to read peacefully. After hundreds of years, as the world changes, perhaps the next time they return to the Great Harmony World, it will be a different scene.

The old scholar’s initial intention was likely to wait until the wild world attacked the Sword Qi Great Wall and for Confucianism to open up the fifth world, creating a new vast realm, expanding the board, providing more space for his disciple Qi Jingchun.

When the old scholar left the Grove of Merits, he had probably made this plan. He was willing to exchange the merits of opening a world for Qi Jingchun to find his place in the mortal realm.

Chen Ping’an said slowly, “If the master is such a master, how could I dare to treat my own disciples carelessly? Brother Mao once said that the most precarious task in the world is to teach, to cultivate, and to educate. Because you never know which of your words will be remembered by a student for a lifetime.”

A Liang returned the white jade hairpin to Chen Ping’an.

Chen Ping’an reinserted it into his hair.

Eight small seal characters read, “In memory of the gentleman, warm as jade.”

A Liang held his hands behind his head, basking in the gentle sun.

The young man beside him, clad in a blue robe, with the white jade hairpin in his hair, wearing layers of cloth shoes, and a sword-gourd hanging from his waist.

Chen Ping’an suddenly asked, “A Liang, did you get hurt in the last two fights?”

A Liang had gone out of the city twice. The first time was fine; even the sword saint stationed at the city wall had seen something.

But during the second return to the battlefield, a powerful demon had attacked with full force, isolating the heavens and earth.

Chen Ping’an couldn’t help but worry.

Unexpectedly, A Liang shook his head, “Not much of an injury; just used some of my secret skills. Next time I go to the battlefield, I’ll definitely be targeted. Just like your two life swords' key techniques, outsiders don’t know, but they are critical. Knowing them, it will be hard to use them again. After all, it’s not like drifting in the Great Harmony World, where I encounter strangers; on the battlefield of the Sword Qi Great Wall, it’s quite large yet small. I've become acquainted with those demons; I know their tactics very well. We are contending against the entire wild world, and the issue is that they are not short of magical treasures. Even if they don’t have them, they can borrow them.”

Chen Ping’an was surprised, “You didn’t get hurt at all?”

A Liang chuckled, “Want to see a trick? After witnessing it, you’ll understand why I could escape unscathed.”

Chen Ping’an looked around, “Not in the street, though.”

A Liang complained, “There’s no one around; what’s the point of showing off if it’s just you and me staring at each other?”

Chen Ping’an nodded, “If you dare to show it, I dare to learn.”

A Liang halted, lightly tapping the ground with his toes.

Chen Ping’an was puzzled and stopped, waiting expectantly.

Suddenly, from the second floor of a nearby tavern, someone shouted angrily, “You bastard, pay up! I’ve seen scams before, but I’ve never seen someone run off after losing money!”

In an instant, patrons at various tables cheered loudly, clinking chopsticks against bowls and slapping tables, creating a ruckus.

Chen Ping’an, with his hands in his sleeves, remained composed, treating this as a small matter.

A Liang shouted back, “I’m not paying! I’m just helping you save money. Saving money means saving wine—what nerve you have to scold me!”

The old sword cultivator was momentarily speechless.

In a fit of anger, the old sword cultivator was about to spit in that bastard’s face.

But A Liang lightly stomped his foot.

At his toes, golden characters appeared, linking together to form a small circle at A Liang’s feet.

All were teachings from the sages.

Starting with a phrase from the Confucian sage, the first golden circle emerged.

Next came the profound principles of yin and yang as expounded by the Daoists.

After that came the Confucian classics regarding heaven, earth, and humanity, followed by larger circles of poetry and prose reflecting the seasons.

The five elements.  
The twelve hours.  
The twenty-four solar terms.  
The fundamental teachings of the seventy-two sages worshipped in the central land’s literary temple.

Layers upon layers of golden characters arose, innumerable.

The teachings of three religions and a hundred schools, each one representing the words of countless poets, moral sages, famous ministers, generals, sword saints, and heroes, all manifested in writing.

Chen Ping’an looked down, taken aback by the rapid appearance of each golden character, each carrying immense meaning, leaving even him feeling overwhelmed.

In moments, the entire city was covered with dense golden letters.

Chen Ping’an even recognized many of the beautiful phrases he once inscribed on bamboo slips.

He saw many words from Buddhist scriptures and Legalist texts, as well as words written by Li Xisheng on the walls of bamboo buildings.

A Liang’s heart stirred, and the strange phenomenon vanished as he smiled, “Just learn the gist of it. After all, no one can become someone else, nor do they need to. I, A Liang, am A Liang; Xiao Qi is Xiao Qi; you, Chen Ping’an, are just Chen Ping’an.”

Chen Ping’an nodded.

A Liang then turned to the second floor, “What were you shouting just now?”

The old sword cultivator, sincere, said, “A Liang, want to drink? My treat.”

A Liang retorted, “What do you take me for? Am I the type to owe someone money and then ask for a drink?!” 

Yet his eyes were glued to the old sword cultivator, clearly unwilling to leave.

“Absolutely not!” 

The old sword cultivator declared, shaking a hand vigorously. A friend quickly tossed over a jug of wine, which the old sword cultivator caught with both hands, gently tossing it out of the window, “A Liang, my brother, it’s been too long since we’ve seen each other. I’ve missed you. When you have time, I’ll set up a big table at the Second Shopkeeper’s tavern and we’ll drink to our heart’s content!”

After Chen Ping’an and A Liang left with the bottle of wine, the old sword cultivator settled back down, stroking his beard as he chuckled, “Who in the entire Sword Qi Great Wall can demand debts like I can, making A Liang put on such a show just to dodge repayment? You lot are just riding my coattails, so today I won’t spend a penny; who’s paying the bill?”

As A Liang walked down the street, sipping the wine that others insisted on giving him, he suddenly asked, “Have you talked about that big matter with Ning girl?”

Chen Ping’an nodded, “I’ve told her everything—the reasons and results. I feel that the closer we are, the more we should clarify things.”

A Liang laughed, “No wonder you’re not single; it’s not without reason.”

Chen Ping’an smiled but didn’t reply.

When they arrived at the tavern, it was thriving, far surpassing others. Even with many tables, there were still no empty seats. Countless people were squatting or sitting by the roadside, drinking.

A Liang and Chen Ping’an squatted by the road, a bowl of noodles and a small plate of pickles in front of them.

The surroundings were noisy; the patrons at this tavern were all carefree souls. If they weren’t, they likely wouldn’t return, so they treated A Liang and the young Hidden Official as if they were no big deal.

A Liang cradled his wine bowl, took a bite of the pickles, shivered at the saltiness, and quickly rolled a large bite of noodles.

Listening to some boasting about how good the wine and dishes were, many newcomers eventually felt that the taste of the wine was indeed quite nice.

A Liang wondered, “Am I now a waiter who collects no fees?”

Chen Ping’an held his wine bowl with both hands, sipping slowly, gazing into the bustling street.

People came and went, walking and stopping, some lingering, some rushing.

Those beside him might leave tomorrow.  
Travelers might return home tomorrow.

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 783: Three out of Four

Lin Junbi never expected that Pang Yuanji was also a big mouth; the news of his departure had already spread among the other sword cultivators of the Hidden Official lineage.

At dawn, Lin Junbi simply packed his belongings and strolled through the Summer Retreat Palace. He eventually returned to the main hall, glancing at the tables arranged within. For cultivators who were unaware of the changing seasons in the world below, a few short years felt like a fleeting moment. Yet Lin Junbi felt as though he had lived through a grand dream here, and he was somewhat reluctant to wake up from it.

He shook his head to dispel these thoughts, feeling that leaving without saying goodbye might not be such a bad thing after all.

To his surprise, several sword cultivators arrived, all of them mounted on their swords. Aside from the young Hidden Official, everyone was present, including Guo Zhujiu, who had brought a gong and drum along.

Lin Junbi straightened his collar and bowed in thanks to the crowd.

It was customary for friends to drink together when seeing someone off from the Sword Qi Great Wall, so the group headed to the tavern run by the second shopkeeper to drink. Even at this early hour, there were still seats available. Everyone had a small drink, as farewell toasts were generally more subdued, taken in moderation. Lin Junbi requested a plaque from the tavern owner, and as a golden dan sword cultivator, he wrote a phrase: “Lin Junbi has had this drink, and in three years, he shall break through three realms.” He personally hung it on the wall.

The wooden plaque seemed to resonate with the sword cultivators.

Gu Jianlong remarked, “Junbi’s words truly reflect the style of the Hidden Officials. The phrase ‘and only’ is simply exquisite.”

In the end, Lin Junbi raised his drinking bowl and downed its contents, smiling as he said, “It has been a pleasure spending time with all of you in this Orchid and Bamboo Chamber.”

Turning to Guo Zhujiu, he added, “When I return to my hometown, if I venture out again, I must have a bamboo box and a bamboo staff.”

Finally, everyone stood up, clasping their fists in farewell, but they did not accompany Lin Junbi far. Guo Zhujiu, a bit regretful, found that the gong and drum had gone unused.

Thus, the white-clad youth with a small bag slung over his shoulder left the tavern alone and headed towards the great gate leading to Mount Inverted. This entrance, located between the city and the mirage, was much further from the city and considerably more lively. The trade routes involving Chunfan Pavilion and Haoran’s Eight Continents ferry were becoming increasingly smooth. Chen Chunan from South Posa Island, the Yu family from Yujia, Zhou Shenzhi, the master of the Bitter Summer Sword Immortal, Jiang Shangzhen, the newly appointed sect leader of Yuguizong from Tongye Island, and several major sects from North Julu Island, along with many wandering sword immortals who had established connections in their respective continents, evidently contributed, either directly or indirectly. Therefore, the worst-case scenario that the young Hidden Official and Chou Miao Sword Immortal were concerned about did not occur. The Central Plains Confucian Temple did not support the new structure created by the Eight Continents ferry, but it had also not explicitly opposed it.

Lin Junbi’s small bag contained only ordinary items: a finely printed manual of the Bi Sword Immortal, a jade bamboo fan purchased from the Yan family shop, and some small gifts from friends like Pang Yuanji. The gifts were light in weight but heavy in sentiment; Lin Junbi felt genuinely happy. Their relationship had not yet reached the point where he needed to be overly polite about gifts; true friends were more casual with one another.

As he proceeded, he remained vigilant. At the gate, Lin Junbi saw the young Hidden Official, who had not concealed his face, standing next to a woman of moderate stature. A natural fragrance of grass and wood surrounded her, indicating she must have employed an illusion technique to conceal her true appearance. Such actions were rare among the sword immortals of the Sword Qi Great Wall; sword immortals generally considered them beneath them. However, it was an exception for the Hidden Official, who, when serious, could mask even a woman’s face. According to Gu Jianlong, in battle, the young Hidden Official had disguised himself as a woman to attack, and his figure was surprisingly graceful. Since Guo Zhujiu had heard this, it might as well have been said to the Hidden Official, which was why Gu Jianlong had to limp for a month.

Lin Junbi quickly guessed the woman’s identity: she was the mastermind behind one of the four private estates of Mount Inverted, the Plum Blossom Garden's Lady Toh Yan.

Regarding matters at the borders, Lady Toh Yan had not only escaped unscathed but somehow switched allegiance to Lu Zhi. This renowned figure in Haoran was a top-tier enchantress of the Fifth Realm, who had compensated for her past misdeeds, and after the incident at Plum Blossom Garden, all its assets were confiscated by the Summer Retreat Palace. If one were to speak of beauty as a strategy, it could work on anyone, but it had no effect on the young Hidden Official. As for the complicated backstory of the changes at Plum Blossom Garden, the young Hidden Official did not elaborate, and no one was willing to ask further.

Chen Ping’an mentioned that he was just on his way to Chunfan Pavilion.

Lin Junbi had no objections.

Currently, the Hidden Official was frequently traveling between Mount Inverted and the Sword Qi Great Wall and no longer needed to go out of his way to conceal his identity. Those who should know would pretend not to, and it was better that those who shouldn’t know remain unaware. With the current vigilance of the Sword Qi Great Wall, anyone who knew too much could land in serious trouble. The power of the Hidden Official lineage was immense; sword strikes could kill without a need for explanation or justification. Even the wealthy mansions on Taixiang Street and Yuhuo Street could be targeted if they attracted suspicion from the Summer Retreat Palace, and the lineage’s sword cultivators could act as if they were in an uninhabited realm.

In the past two years, following numerous intelligence reports that only the Hidden Official had access to, many operations had been carried out, with Lin Junbi personally participating in two encirclements aimed at the “merchants” over in the Mirage. They had been executed flawlessly, like cutting through melons and vegetables. One incident involved a highly respected old Yuanying who had been operating in the Mirage for many years, disguised so well and with excellent connections that the Hidden Official lineage did not wish to elaborate on the reasons. The situation nearly escalated into chaos in the Mirage. Ultimately, six sword immortals, including Gao Kui, flew into the air on their swords, while the young Hidden Official remained silent, standing outside with his hands tucked in his sleeves. Only when Chou Miao dragged the body out did he turn to leave. That day, twenty-three shops in the Mirage closed down, and the Sword Qi Great Wall did not intervene, allowing them to relocate to Mount Inverted. However, the next day, all the shops had new owners.

Sword cultivators of the Hidden Official lineage, from Chou Miao to Dong Buduo, and even Guo Zhujiu, still a young girl, were all swift and decisive in their actions.

However, many of the more sordid matters could not simply be resolved by drawing swords. Lin Junbi remembered the young Hidden Official spending ten days at the sword workshop, and upon returning to the Summer Retreat Palace, he remarkably did not confide in the sword cultivators about the events that had transpired, only stating that he had resolved a significant hidden danger.

Sometimes, Lin Junbi would indulge in whimsical thoughts: if our Hidden Official lineage and this Summer Retreat Palace were to establish themselves as a sect in the Haoran world, what would it be like?

The young Hidden Official would be the mountain lord, Chou Miao Sword Immortal would oversee the laws, the sword immortal Mi Yu would be in charge of the genealogy, Wei Wenlong would handle finances, while the other sword cultivators would practice diligently, each managing their own peak and lineage, branching out as they pleased and accepting disciples.

It would surely be magnificent. Within a century at most, the entire Haoran world would have to pay attention. Unfortunately, that was merely Lin Junbi’s daydream.

Lady Toh Yan remained silent, glancing at the youth several times. This “border” had been mentioned by her respected senior, who held this junior disciple in high regard.

Upon arriving at Mount Inverted, Lin Junbi followed his master's secret instructions to visit an old friend of a certain gentleman at the Yuan Ruo Mansion, and then that night, he would take a cross-continental ferry back to the Central Divine Continent.

At the entrance of the Yuan Ruo Mansion, Chen Ping’an took out a wooden box from his belongings and said, “This contains some relics of old friends who have visited the tavern. Treasure it well; you might find it useful in the future. I only hope that you can honor the relics inside and not let me down by sending them to the wrong person.”

Lin Junbi accepted the wooden box with both hands, guessing that it contained the plaques taken down from the walls of the tavern. This farewell gift was immensely significant.

As long as Lin Junbi had the heart, as soon as he returned to the Central Divine Continent, he could immediately convert it into cherished connections, public reputation, and even tangible benefits.

With a serious tone, Lin Junbi said, “Rest assured, Hidden Official; I will be more prudent in my actions from now on.”

Chen Ping’an replied softly, “One thing at a time, focus on the matter, not the person. Once you return to the Shao Yuan Dynasty, I hope you can balance your studies and cultivation. Once you mingle with the masses, it’s easy for the pure to become muddied. Junbi, you must think carefully.”

Lin Junbi took a step back and bowed, “I bid farewell to the Hidden Official.”

Chen Ping’an returned the gesture.

Chen Ping’an and Lady Toh Yan headed to Chunfan Pavilion, while Lin Junbi watched their retreating figures and suddenly called out, “A gentleman loves wealth, but takes it through righteous means. I have never seen Mr. Chen conduct business so straightforwardly.”

Chen Ping’an did not turn around but waved his hand.

Lin Junbi watched as the two departed.

As they neared Chunfan Pavilion, Lady Toh Yan smiled charmingly, speaking to the young Hidden Official with her heart’s voice, “Lin Junbi has left. What about the other foreign sword cultivators of the Hidden Official lineage? Will they also be fleeing?”

Chen Ping’an replied with a grin, “Fleeing?”

Lady Toh Yan turned to the young Hidden Official, her face full of apology, yet she spoke with an unrepentant tone, “Perhaps my wording was inaccurate; that’s the essence of it. Anyone who leaves the Sword Qi Great Wall alive is technically fleeing, right? Of course, Mr. Lu is an exception.”

Referring to a woman as “Mr.” in the Haoran world is a significant form of respect.

Chen Ping’an said, “Lady Toh Yan, if even the entire Plum Blossom Garden can run away, how can you accuse the foreign sword cultivators of our Hidden Official lineage?”

Lady Toh Yan switched her tone, “To be honest, I truly admire the means and spirit of these young people. Once they return to the Haoran world, they will surely become formidable figures, outstanding heroes. I make such comments out of envy; they are sword cultivators, with great potential ahead, making it hard not to feel a twinge of jealousy with every glance.”

Upon entering Chunfan Pavilion, Chen Ping’an asked, “Do you know why I wanted you to visit Mount Inverted?”

Lady Toh Yan, with a melancholic look, bit her lip and said, “How could I possibly guess? The Hidden Official’s position is so high that whatever you say goes.”

Chen Ping’an stated bluntly, “Find a time when there are fewer people, and move the entire Plum Blossom Garden to the Sword Qi Great Wall. It will be beneficial, and the Summer Retreat Palace will remember your contribution.”

Lady Toh Yan complained, “Hidden Official, you even want to take away an empty Plum Blossom Garden? Isn’t that a bit much? Can’t you leave me with a memory? When I arrive at South Posa Island, I should at least be able to contribute a little to ensure Mr. Lu has a peaceful place to cultivate, right?”

Chen Ping’an said, “Whether or not you have that conspicuous Plum Blossom Garden, with Lu Zhi’s temperament, he would actively help you sever past grudges, allowing you to cultivate in peace. So, you don’t need to complicate matters. As long as you can reach the Celestial realm, you will have the means to protect yourself in the Haoran world. Even if Lu Zhi is not around, no one will dare to underestimate Lady Toh Yan, and other academies will treat you with respect.”

Lady Toh Yan lamented, “There are no more romantic nights, just the mundane struggles of life. I am but a pitiful traveler in this world.”

Chen Ping’an replied, “A self-aware person does not blame others.”

Lady Toh Yan gave him a sidelong glance, her charm radiating, “Mr. Chen, you become quite unromantic when you speak of reason.”

Chen Ping’an frowned, “Are we that familiar?”

Lady Toh Yan pretended to be pitiful, “Isn’t Mrs. Xie from the tavern familiar with Mr. Chen?”

Chen Ping’an chuckled, realizing he had been thoroughly tricked by Ah Liang and Mrs. Xie.

Lady Toh Yan composed herself, her curiosity piqued. “I’ve only heard that Mrs. Xie was once a Yuanying sword cultivator, but later her path was interrupted; her flying sword broke, her sword heart shattered. Why does she look at you with such new eyes? There must be a story there, right? If Mr. Chen is willing to share, I will gladly assist with moving the Plum Blossom Garden.”

Chen Ping’an feigned ignorance, never having encountered such a boring enchantress from the Fifth Realm.

In another room, Wei Wenlong and the others—Shao Yunyan, Mi Yu, Yan Ming, and Nalan Caihuan—were discussing business matters with a group of ferry managers in the meeting hall.

In the adjacent room, several of Shao Yunyan’s disciples were assisting with accounting.

Lady Toh Yan dropped her illusion, adopting a languid posture as she leaned against the doorframe. With her bare face devoid of makeup, she naturally exuded a rustic charm.

Unfortunately, Wei Wenlong glanced at her but quickly turned away, his heart unmoved. Though the woman was beautiful, she couldn’t compare to the allure of the accounting books.

After Chen Ping’an took a seat, he randomly picked up a book from the towering pile of accounts, flipping through it while inquiring about the recent trade conditions from Wei Wenlong.

Lady Toh Yan, with nothing to do and unable to casually sit and flip through the accounts, sat on the threshold, her back to the room, leaning forward with her hands propping up her chin.

Once Wei Wenlong finished answering the young Hidden Official’s questions, he inadvertently glanced at Lady Toh Yan’s back, and found it hard to pull his gaze away.

Beyond the accounts lay different scenery.

Chen Ping’an noticed Wei Wenlong’s unusual behavior but chose not to interrupt his moment of admiration.

After all, Wei Wenlong was a single man; a few glances wouldn’t hurt. Perhaps after some time, he might even come to his senses.

Yet after only two pages of accounts, Wei Wenlong seemed to regain his composure, as if he found the accounts on the table more interesting.

Mi Yu returned from the meeting hall, cursing and swearing angrily at the ferry managers who had been blinded by greed. Unexpectedly, upon seeing Lady Toh Yan, he instantly became lively and spirited.

To his surprise, Lady Toh Yan had already risen, keeping him at a distance and not giving Mi Yu the chance to get close. She turned to Chen Ping’an and said, “If the Hidden Official trusts me, I will handle the relocation of the Plum Blossom Garden myself.”

Chen Ping’an nodded.

Lady Toh Yan flashed away.

Mi Yu stood at the door, lightly waving his hand to create a breeze, and smiled at Wei Wenlong, “You dimwit, have you had enough of looking? If I were you, I would have sincerely asked Lady Toh Yan if she needed my hands as a little stool.”

Wei Wenlong had no words to respond.

Chen Ping’an stood up and strolled with Mi Yu through Chunfan Pavilion. Today, two groups of merchants were scheduled to visit, and Chen Ping’an planned to listen in on the second meeting, waiting for the first group of ferry managers to leave before heading to the meeting hall.

Mi Yu remarked unexpectedly, “That Lady Toh Yan from the Plum Blossom Garden is also a woman of misfortune. Thus, when she sees someone like me, she finds it most repugnant.”

Chen Ping’an did not bring up the Sword Nurturing Gourd, and since the affairs of the Mi brothers were their own, he saw no need to interfere with Mi Yu’s decision.

Suddenly, Mi Yu said, “I’ve always been hesitant to return to the Sword Qi Great Wall because I didn’t know what to say.”

Chen Ping’an realized that this Yuanying sword cultivator, infamous in the Sword Qi Great Wall, had already understood his elder brother Mi Hu’s intentions.

After a moment of silence, Mi Yu said, “But I must go back; I can’t keep avoiding it.”

Chen Ping’an then took out the Sword Nurturing Gourd and handed it to Mi Yu.

Mi Yu merely glanced at it and shook his head, “This was given to you by my brother. What does it mean for me? Hidden Official, you should keep it. My brother would feel more at ease. Besides, I no longer need the Sword Nurturing Gourd to nurture my life sword.”

Previously, as a sword cultivator of the Hidden Official lineage, Mi Yu had fought alongside other sword cultivators several times. While he had fought with all his might, he had never truly forgotten the weight of life and death. The reason was simple: once he found himself in a desperate situation, the first to die would be his brother.

Chen Ping’an kicked Mi Yu lightly, “Then go ahead and make haste.”

Mi Yu left Chunfan Pavilion.

After the first group of ferry managers left the meeting hall, Shao Yunyan and the others needed to see them off. Only then did Chen Ping’an enter the empty main hall.

When Shao Yunyan, Yan Ming, and Nalan Caihuan returned, Chen Ping’an chose not to sit in the main seat but instead sat in Mi Yu’s position, closer to Yan Ming and Nalan Caihuan.

Shao Yunyan casually took a seat across from him.

Nalan Caihuan reported in detail on the trade developments regarding the Eight Continents ferry. The matter concerning the Divine Money from the Ai Ai Continent was still the most challenging, as the Liu family had yet to make a clear statement. When Nalan Caihuan mentioned this, she appeared worried and then somewhat frustrated, saying, “Why don’t we just seize the Yuan Ruo Mansion? What if it’s not something like the Plum Blossom Garden or Chunfan Pavilion? We can dismantle it. Those pavilions and towers, all made of divine money! After all, the Liu family hasn’t considered moving; with people gone and buildings left empty, it’s practically unowned. At worst, we can have the Nanji ferry send a private message to the Liu family, saying we owe them a favor, and later have sword immortals like Xie Songhua help to repay it.”

Shao Yunyan could only smile wryly at such a fanciful idea.

“Just one thing, can any of us persuade sword immortal Xie Songhua?” 

Unexpectedly, Chen Ping’an interjected, “No rush; dismantling is inevitable. The Liu family from the Ai Ai Continent is likely waiting for us to dismantle the Yuan Ruo Mansion. They’re just sitting at home, waiting for us to deliver this favor. However, friends are friends, and business is business. We need to consider what we’ll offer in return for the help of sword immortals, including Xie Songhua. You three should work together on this; by the time we reach an agreement, we won’t need to consult the Summer Retreat Palace anymore—just give a direct response.”

Yan Ming asked, “Does the purchase of the Cloud-Drifting Pavilion by Li Cai from Floating Duck Lake mean we can establish an additional ferry route? Connect with the Yuguizong of Tongye Island? Tongye Island is rich in resources, and if we can have the ferries from Old Dragon City fully operate towards Mount Inverted, we might even increase our resources by twenty percent.”

Chen Ping’an shook his head, “It can only stop here. Jiang Shangzhen sent those divine coins in his capacity as the head of the Jiang family, which in itself is a statement.”

Although Jiang Shangzhen was now the newly appointed head of Yuguizong, the newly ascended Xuanyuan from Tongye Island would never agree to this move, and Jiang Shangzhen wouldn’t be foolish enough to act recklessly.

If Jiang Shangzhen dared to prioritize personal matters over public good, he might soon lose his position as sect leader. Xuanyuan would be capable of making such a decision, and the Jiang family might even be replaced, with the Yunkong Blessed Land changing masters.

To act upon one’s position and seek benefits for oneself is an undeniable principle for all genealogical immortal masters.

Mountain and wild cultivators have their own advantages and disadvantages, while genealogical immortal masters have their own gains and losses.

Suddenly, Lady Toh Yan appeared outside the door, holding a potted plant. Inside the pot were miniature pavilions and lush trees, each detail vividly rendered.

This small potted plant was essentially the entire Plum Blossom Garden. The contrast with Chen Ping’an’s impression of moving an entire estate was immense.

Perhaps this was what they called a pure and serene place, a small mountain in the palm of one’s hand.

Standing at the entrance, Lady Toh Yan lightly tossed the potted plant to the young Hidden Official and playfully asked, “Is this related to Mr. Shou?”

Shao Yunyan and the others were utterly confused.

Chen Ping’an accepted the potted plant within his reach and said, “Honestly, I’m not sure. You can ask Lu Zhi.”

After the gracefully departing Lady Toh Yan left, Shao Yunyan remarked, “With this, it seems the four private estates of Mount Inverted only have the Water Crystal Palace of the Rain Dragon Sect left unclaimed by us.”

Yan Ming’s expression was indifferent as he casually said, “Since you enjoy watching the spectacle and making sarcastic remarks, then enjoy it to your heart's content.”

Nalan Caihuan looked towards the entrance, recalling the expressions of the Rain Dragon Sect cultivators and sneering, “So many innocent cultivators, and we won’t help them? If we don’t intervene, we’ll definitely be criticized; it’s unbecoming of a sword cultivator, unworthy of a sword immortal. If the Hidden Official doesn’t intervene, I’ll go to the Water Crystal Palace and earnestly persuade them to relocate their sect elsewhere for a more peaceful existence. A little financial loss is far better than losing one’s life.”

Chen Ping’an refrained from getting involved.

When Shao Yunyan stood up to receive the second wave of ferry managers, Nalan Caihuan noticed that the young Hidden Official had already vanished.

Even though she knew he was nearby, as a Yuanying sword cultivator, Nalan Caihuan did not perceive his presence, failing to detect even a ripple of his aura.

After that, a meeting dragged on for an hour and a half, largely consisting of both sides bickering.

Shao Yunyan took the role of the harsh critic, Nalan Caihuan being the villain, while Yan Ming leaned towards one side.

In fact, Chen Ping’an had been quietly standing behind Mi Yu’s chair, watching the back-and-forth negotiations unfold.

The smaller the space of the cage, the stricter the rules within it.

When Chen Ping’an condensed the divine powers of this life sword into a small space, even a Yuanying sword cultivator like Nalan Caihuan remained oblivious.

Against the troublesome foes outside of the four major obstacles, for any cultivator below the Fifth Realm, utilizing pine needles, thunderous coughs, or spirit runes combined with physical strength, one could control the wind and the sword, instantly bridging the distance, and display the cage bird technique, closing in, face to face, delivering a punch to conclude it all.

One ferry manager who had not participated in the first meeting at Chunfan Pavilion grew agitated during the arguments. He slammed his palm on the table, causing the teacups to jump, and angrily shouted, “How can you conduct business like this? The price-cutting is utterly heartless! Even if the Hidden Official were sitting here facing us, I would still say this: the goods on my ferry, buy them if you want. If Chunfan Pavilion keeps cutting prices, it’s like killing me! I’m not afraid of you sword immortals; no way! At most, I’ll just stab myself first and take a break here, so that both Chunfan Pavilion and my sect have a proper explanation…”

Yan Ming leaned back slightly in his chair, his back against the seat. In reality, the deal could still be negotiated; according to the price offered by Chunfan Pavilion, the other party would still make a good profit. This was just pure nonsense on their part; the joy of trading lay in this.

Yan Ming didn’t hate the interaction; after all, it was business. However, the same old cunning foxes kept coming in waves, and it was tiring.

Nalan Caihuan wore an amused smile.

Then, dozens of ferry managers all turned toward a certain spot, where a tall figure appeared out of thin air.

Everyone instantly rose to their feet.

Across from them stood a young man with his hands clasped over the top of the chair, smiling, “One knife isn’t enough; I have two. After I’m done, remember to return them.”

Though Nalan Caihuan had harbored great resentment toward the young Hidden Official, she couldn’t help but admit that sometimes, Chen Ping’an’s words did refresh the spirit.

A ferry manager who had crossed paths with the young Hidden Official bowed respectfully, introducing himself, “I pay my respects to the Hidden Official!”

The manager who had been shouting about stabbing himself seemed struck by lightning, left speechless.

Chen Ping’an did not actually put the ferry manager in a difficult position but instead, actively offered a concession before leaving the hall.

This time, after exiting Chunfan Pavilion and returning to the Sword Qi Great Wall, Chen Ping’an did not take the usual longer route but instead walked through the original grand entrance.

Once again, that young disciple sitting on the meditation mat reading did not lift his head upon seeing Chen Ping’an.

The sword-wielding man on the other side of the door did not show himself, and Chen Ping’an did not greet the familiar sword immortal named Zhang Lu.

(End of Chapter)

 ### Chapter 784: Today, Tomorrow, the Day After Tomorrow

Chen Ping'an found Ah Liang at the corner tavern. 

Ah Liang was currently leaning against a swordsman, joking, "What are you sad about? Even if Nalan Caihuan has won your heart, can she claim your body? Not a chance; Nalan Caihuan doesn’t have that kind of ability." The swordsman didn’t feel any better; instead, he wanted to drink even more. He swayed a bit, reached for the wine jug on the table, only to find it empty. Ah Liang quickly ordered another jug of wine. Just then, a series of hisses sounded as Madam Xie twisted her waist and wound her way out from behind the counter, her eyes sparkling with mischief as she smiled at the street outside. Upon hearing the commotion, Ah Liang turned around and saw Chen Ping'an had arrived. "At the Sword Qi Great Wall, it seems that us scholars are quite precious; we are welcomed wherever we go."

After Chen Ping'an took a seat, he smiled and said, "Ah Liang, I'm inviting you to dinner at Ning Mansion. I'll cook myself."

Madam Xie placed a jug of wine on the table but didn’t sit down. Ah Liang nodded in acceptance of Chen Ping'an's invitation. At this moment, he tilted his head to look at the woman, his eyes blurry from the effects of the wine. "Sister Xie, what’s going on? I can barely see your face."

Madam Xie scoffed, "Are you going to ramble on again about how every time you get drunk, you can see two upside-down mountains? You’re not being original, Ah Liang; you’re getting old. You should read more of the Bi Jian Xian's Imprint Compendium; that’s the kind of conversation a scholar should be having."

Ah Liang felt a pang of sadness at her disdain for novelty.

After the two left, Chen Ping'an walked a little distance before saying, "I read in the archives at the Summer Palace that Xie Yuan was gravely injured, and ever since, this Madam Xie has been selling wine to make a living."

Ah Liang shook off the haze of alcohol and slapped his cheeks. "It’s not right to call her 'Madam Xie' since she has never married. Xie Yuan is from Yangliu Lane, incredibly talented in swordsmanship, and stood out at a young age, younger than Yue Qing and Mi Hu, and is on the same level as Nalan Caihuan. Plus, she’s the one that Cheng Quan and Zhao Gezi have been thinking about; she was one of the most outstanding young women at the Sword Qi Great Wall back in the day."

Ah Liang sighed, "In the drizzling rain, as the world turns hazy, a handsome scholar sees a woman holding an umbrella, her azure robe fluttering like flowers blooming on the roadside, resembling a willow swaying in the spring rain—absolutely breathtaking."

Chen Ping'an replied, "Remove ‘handsome scholar,’ and just picture the woman alone; that scene would indeed be beautiful."

Ah Liang laughed, "Without that handsome scholar's perspective, how would you even know such beauty exists?"

He continued, "Xie Yuan exchanged her life-bound flying sword with a junior sister of the sword immortal Shou Chen on the battlefield, both of them shattered their swords, and she was gravely injured. Unable to escape in time, Shou Chen caught up and struck her again. If she hadn’t suffered that calamity, Xie Yuan would have easily reached the upper five realms. So, with Xie Yuan’s connection to the Wenhai lineage, it's no surprise there’s a deep-seated grudge; she naturally feels grateful to you for beating that Jia Shen account nearly to death."

Ah Liang chuckled maliciously, "In such matters, a simple thank you when they meet is sufficient; no need to make a fuss about it."

Now it dawned on Chen Ping'an why Ah Liang had invited him for a drink at the tavern—it was to help Xie Yuan untangle a knot in her heart, and of course, Ah Liang was enjoying a free drink himself.

When they reached Ning Mansion, Chen Ping'an indeed went to the kitchen to cook, with Granny Bai helping out as they chatted about trivial matters.

In the guest room of Chen Ping'an's residence, Ah Liang rummaged through the famous Bi Jian Xian's Imprint Compendium, with several blank fan surfaces and ordinary materials spread across the table. However, it seemed he wouldn’t be putting pen to paper anytime soon.

Ning Yao sat nearby and asked, "What’s the deal with the outer heaven demons of the Outer Sky? Is it true that even the White Jade Capital can’t completely suppress them?"

The origins of the outer heaven demons remained an ambiguous topic in the vast realm. As for the sword cultivators at the Sword Qi Great Wall, they hardly cared.

Ah Liang only provided a rough overview, "Isn’t it the case that troubles are brought upon us by us cultivators ourselves? We can’t clean up our own mess and choose to deceive ourselves instead, letting it go on unchecked. Year after year, as floods ravage the land, the Qingming realm can only resort to the most primitive methods of building dikes to block the water, raising them higher and higher over time. Eventually, it becomes a perilous scene of 'floodwaters hanging overhead.' We can’t blame the White Jade Capital for merely treating symptoms and not the root cause; every Qi practitioner bears some responsibility. It is said that the second Daoist’s senior brother is dedicated to seeking fundamental solutions. Both the second Daoist and Lu Chen have their own strategies, but one is too deliberate and harsh, while the other is too casual; I suspect the Dao Ancestor is not fond of either, and more hope rests on the eldest disciple."

The three heads of White Jade Capital are akin to the three teaching ancestors under the Dao Ancestor in the Qingming realm, but the title of teaching ancestor is self-bestowed by the Daoists, and the various schools of thought do not acknowledge it.

Ah Liang smiled, "Don’t blame me for being vague; it’s not my intention to keep secrets from you. The truth is, one often speaks unconsciously, while the listener takes it to heart. When cultivators get earnest, it often becomes a great obstacle, especially with these outer heaven demons—talented individuals find it hard to deal with them. Of course, there are exceptions, and you, Ning Yao, are one such case. But once I tell you, it may not be appropriate; it’s better to let things unfold naturally."

Ning Yao nodded.

The reason she inquired about the outer heaven demons was that she worried about Chen Ping'an's future in achieving the Golden Core and Nascent Soul.

As for herself, it seemed she had no concerns at all. Reaching the Golden Core and Nascent Soul—she was merely a step away from the Jade Purity realm. For Ning Yao, breaking through would be easy whenever she decided to.

Ah Liang further disclosed a bit of insight, "The Daoists of the Qingming realm are bustling and busy, not at all relaxed. It’s a different battlefield from the Sword Qi Great Wall, but the level of brutality is comparable. The Western Buddhist Kingdom is similar; beneath the Nine Springs, resentful souls and vengeful spirits gather like the sea. Who are you going to blame?"

Ning Yao asked, "People?"

Ah Liang replied, "Life is a source of worry from the moment one learns to read. So when a person cultivates, naturally, they worry even more, facing more hidden dangers."

Ning Yao queried, "Ah Liang, you should discuss these things with Chen Ping'an; he can keep up with the conversation."

Ah Liang chuckled, "I won’t add to his burdens. You, Ning Yao, can forget what you've heard, which is why it’s right to talk to you."

Ah Liang was twisting a plain, jade-like stone with no inscriptions, slowly saying, "In the end, cultivation is ultimately suppressed by the heavens and the great Dao. Plus, on the path of cultivation, one gets used to only taking and not giving, leading to endless troubles. The sages of old climbed mountains to cultivate, quenching their thirst with poison—they had no choice. We juniors are merely greedy for cups of wine, but our thoughts and ideas have changed; the ancient and modern individuals are two entirely different people. That’s why there’s a saying: those of old externalized without internalizing, while today’s people internalize without externalizing. This is a truth that the elders could no longer suppress, voicing their heartfelt words in frustration. However, deep down, the elders actually hope that the younger generation can prove them wrong."

Ah Liang put away the stone, returning it to its place, and cheerfully declared, "No matter what, we must recognize the characters, read the books, cultivate the Dao, walk the path, and most importantly, eat!"

Ning Yao said, "Just don’t encourage Chen Ping'an to drink."

Ah Liang stood, saying, "A little sip is fine; I promise not to overdo it, but I must drink. A tavern keeper who doesn’t drink is definitely a black-hearted one; I must help the second tavern keeper prove his innocence."

Today at Ning Mansion, the four of them gathered around a table for a meal, all home-cooked dishes.

Chen Ping'an could only have a bowl of wine.

Ah Liang made himself at home, sitting at the main position, and asked with a grin, "Your senior brother hasn’t visited Ning Mansion yet?"

Chen Ping'an sighed, "I mentioned it. My senior brother said since the teacher has never visited Ning Mansion, what kind of student would I be to go there first and act all high and mighty? After some back-and-forth, during that sword practice on the city wall, my senior brother used quite a bit of force; he must have been blaming me for not knowing better."

Ah Liang took a sip of wine and shook his head, "You’re being foolish; you don’t know to talk to the right people. In the end, will you give up the main seat for the old scholar? The old scholar is like he has already taken a seat; how can this student not accompany him? Even if the teacher isn’t physically present, he’s always in the heart."

Chen Ping'an found some wisdom in that and felt a deep sense of regret. With his senior brother's temperament, he believed invoking the teacher’s name would work, regardless of whether the teacher was there or not.

Ah Liang was indeed an old hand at this; he was still far behind in terms of experience.

Granny Bai complained, "Your son-in-law is an honest man, not as scheming as you, Ah Liang."

Ah Liang quickly raised his wine bowl, "Miss Bai, I’ll take a self-punishment; you drink a bowl with your brother Ah Liang."

Bai Lianshuang shot a glare at Ah Liang, ignoring him as she helped Ning Yao and Chen Ping'an pick up some dishes.

She, an old woman, being called ‘Miss’ in front of the young lady and son-in-law—does that make sense?

Ah Liang looked at the white-haired elder and couldn’t help but feel a bit melancholic. He remembered when he first met Bai Lianshuang; she was still a tall and graceful girl, a pure warrior woman, after all, not comparable to a female Qi practitioner—she was at a disadvantage.

Among the sword cultivators of the Sword Qi Great Wall, it was hard to discern a woman’s true age based solely on her appearance.

When Nalan Yexing, the steward of Ning Mansion, first saw the young Bai Lianshuang, her appearance did not seem aged; she looked like a man in his early forties. Yet later, Bai Lianshuang transitioned from a girl to a young woman, then to one with white hair, while Nalan Yexing fell from the Immortal Realm to the Jade Purity realm, making him look considerably older. In his prime, Nalan Yexing, as Ah Liang would say, had some charm; in the Qingming realm, he was quite the sought-after catch!

And the once extremely beautiful Bai Lianshuang, though she came from the Yao family as a maid, had no trouble finding a husband among the many sword cultivators, where male warriors were rare at the Sword Qi Great Wall.

However, Bai Lianshuang had high standards, excellent martial arts talent, and did not settle for any sword immortal, so year after year, the young girl grew into an old maid, and the old maid inadvertently became an old woman.

Ah Liang chuckled, "Miss Bai, you might not know, but Nalan Yexing’s grandfather, Jiang Yun, nicknamed Stone, is about the same age as you. There are several other old drunks who are still single. In their youth, they wouldn’t dare say a word to you, but when they met secretly later, they would all curse each other for being shameless.
