Jiang Yun especially loved to mock Nalan Yexing for being unashamed, saying how old he was, and yet he still acted like a senior. Nalan Yexing’s skills in cursing are truly pathetic, but luckily he’s good at fighting; I once saw him sneak into Jiang’s house at midnight while Jiang Yun was asleep, and hit him with a blunt weapon. After one hit to knock him out, he followed up with several strikes to the face, all in one go. The weapon didn’t break, and the man didn’t leave. Each time Jiang Yun woke up, he never understood how he ended up with a bruised face. In the end, he even bought several talismans from me to ward off evil spirits."

The old woman merely smiled at this, but her peripheral vision caught sight of an empty spot near the entrance.

Ning Yao felt a little anxious and glanced at Chen Ping'an.

Chen Ping'an gently shook his head, signaling her not to worry.

Some words were better left to the family elder, while Chen Ping'an, being a junior, didn’t want to speak out of turn.

Ah Liang was the right person to say them.

Ah Liang and Bai Lianshuang reminisced about the past.

Granny Bai hardly spoke, just listening.

There were many people and events related to her that she still didn’t understand because she had never paid attention in the past, perhaps more so because she was deeply entrenched in this mountain.

Chen Ping'an noticed Ning Yao paying close attention, which made him feel helpless.

Ah Liang suddenly asked, "Chen Ping'an, in your hometown, don’t you have any female peers you care about or who like you?"

Without hesitation, Chen Ping'an replied, "No. They were too young and didn’t understand these things. Besides, I went to the Dragon Kiln to become an apprentice at a young age. According to the old customs in my hometown, girls weren’t allowed near the kiln."

Ah Liang countered, "That’s not right. I heard from Li Huai that there’s a family next door to you in Mud Bottle Lane, and there’s a little girl there who is quite cute. That’s what they call a childhood sweetheart; how could the relationship be bad? Li Huai said you got up early every day just to help fetch water, and he even said your family had a wall that was dug out with a pit, as if you were just one window away from opening a door."

"Every day, you and your grandpa," Chen Ping'an thought to himself, but he said, "Liu Xianyang likes her; I don’t. Besides, when Li Huai saw you, Ah Liang, he hadn’t even been to Mud Bottle Lane. His family fetches water from far away, never going to the Iron Lock Well. My wall has one side next to an empty house, and the other side is next to Song Jixin's place. Li Huai is just talking nonsense; anyone who believes him is a fool."

Ning Yao chimed in, "I’ve seen her; she’s quite pretty. She’s just not very tall, and if she doesn’t stand on her toes while peeking over the wall into Chen Ping'an's courtyard, I can only see half her head."

Ah Liang rubbed his chin, clearly wanting to continue the conversation, but Chen Ping'an raised his wine bowl and downed it in one go, saying, "After finishing this wine, I’ll eat."

At this meal, it was mostly Ah Liang boasting about his past exploits in the jianghu, recounting interesting encounters with mountain gods and water spirits, along with some eerie encounters with ghosts and spirits. He told of a ghostly scholar who "gained weight by eating characters," claiming that if one consumed books, their cultivation would increase. He also recounted a stroke of luck, where he accidentally attended a banquet called the Hundred Flowers Feast in the mountains and met a little girl crying in a corner. It turned out she was a banana spirit, lamenting that poets rarely wrote about bananas, which hindered her cultivation level, leaving her unloved by her peers. Ah Liang was indignant and joined her in cursing the scholars, then spontaneously wrote several poems on leaves to give her, but she didn’t accept a single leaf or poem and ran away, crying even harder. Ah Liang even mentioned how he once watched a few skeletons in a graveyard and recognized one of the spirits, which no one believed.

He spoke of seeing a woman known for her icy demeanor in the mountains, twirling her skirt when she thought no one was around, and how he encountered a group of gossiping female ghosts in the overgrown wilderness, which scared him half to death. He also recalled a lonely little girl he met at a dilapidated grave, who, in a daze upon seeing him, screamed "a ghost!" and ran around erratically, unable to leave the area around the grave. Ah Liang had to explain that he was a good ghost who meant no harm. Eventually, the little girl, regaining her senses, felt sorry for him and asked how long it had been since he last saw the sun. Before parting, Ah Liang helped the girl settle in a small nest, a cozy place that could shield her from wind and gather water, allowing her to see the daylight.

As he continued to talk, the spirited man gradually grew somber, taking a big gulp of wine. "Later, when I passed by again, I wanted to check on the little girl and see if she had grown up. But I didn’t find her. It turned out that a passing immortal, without asking for any reason, had casually killed her. I remember when the little girl happily bid me farewell, she said, 'Haha, we are ghosts; now I’ll never be afraid of ghosts again.'"

Ah Liang picked up a peanut, chewing it slowly, "If only I had thought a bit more, even just a little, like not treating a small ghost with such indifference, why must I have taken her to a certain mountain spirit to settle? Moving her home, getting some incense to burn, and achieving a bit of stability, would it also make her less happy? I pondered in places where I shouldn’t have, but I didn’t think enough about the cultivators on the mountain who focused solely on their paths and never overthought it. In this world, there’s always the potential for the unexpected, and yet I didn’t think enough."

Ah Liang murmured, "Years have gone by, yet I still want to know, as this little girl with no one to rely on leaves this world, will she still remember that swordsman and want to say something to him? If she does, what would she say? I’ll never know."

Ah Liang turned to Chen Ping'an, "What I’ve been saying, the nonsense you ignore, and you didn’t heed my advice—good, that’s the Chen Ping'an I know, regarding everything as a grand matter. You wouldn't see Ah Liang as a sword immortal; why should you cling to such trivial past events at the dining table?"

Ah Liang raised his wine bowl and drank it all by himself.

The parting of the strong feels magnificent, while the farewells of the weak are silent and indistinct, with no clear sound of weeping.

Ning Yao and Granny Bai left the table first, saying they wanted to go sit at the Dragon Slaying Cliff Pavilion together. Ning Yao asked Chen Ping'an to keep Ah Liang company for a bit longer, and Chen Ping'an said he would tidy up the dishes afterward.

After the two finished their drinks, Chen Ping'an walked Ah Liang to the door.

Suddenly, Chen Ping'an remembered that Ah Liang seemed to never have a proper place to settle down at the Sword Qi Great Wall.

He only knew that after every drinking session, Ah Liang would sway on his sword, casually living in the abandoned residences left by the sword immortals outside the city. 

On the city wall, he could lie down and sleep without a care.

Ah Liang said, "In the next six months, you won’t be able to engage in combat in the city anyway, so you should plan well for yourself—nurture your sword, practice your fist, refine your materials; you have plenty to keep yourself busy. Over at the Summer Palace, there’s Chou Miao holding down the fort; even if a few young outsiders leave, those from the Hidden Official lineage can fill in the gaps and continue their duties. The Spring Banner Studio still has Yan Ming and the others, so neither side will falter. Here’s my suggestion: you can visit the old deaf man’s prison more often; whether you have business or not, personally experiencing the pressure from the great demons of the Immortal Realm would be beneficial. It’s a pity that the ascended being was beheaded; otherwise, the effect would have been even better. I’ll give the old deaf man a heads-up and keep an eye on things for you; there won’t be any surprises. Your life-bound divine ability from the caged sparrow and the bottleneck of the seventh realm martial artist can all be polished in this time."

Chen Ping'an hesitated to respond.

Ah Liang said, "There’s no need to delay any longer; it’s only six months, enough time for the old sword immortal to arrange a retreat."

Chen Ping'an nodded.

Ah Liang smiled, "For these six months, I’ll be here with you."

Ah Liang suddenly remarked, "The old sword immortal is a kind person, proficient in swordsmanship, good character, with a kind face, thick brows, broad shoulders—quite the handsome figure…"

Chen Ping'an was left bewildered, not understanding why Ah Liang's flattery felt so forced. Then, Chen Ping'an found himself atop the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Near the thatched cottage, he was surrounded either by the old sword immortals or the great sword immortals.

The mischievous Yuan Zao Hua once listed the top ten sword immortals in the minds of these children.

The old sword immortal, Dong San Geng, Ah Liang, the Hidden Official, Chen Xi, Qi Ting Ji, Zuo You, Nalan Shao Wei, the old deaf man, and Lu Zhi.

At this moment, Chen Ping'an's senior brother, Zuo You, was already in Tongye Continent, replaced by Ah Liang returning to the Sword Qi Great Wall.

As for the Hidden Official, he remained, but had swapped identities with Chen Ping'an.

For some unknown reason today, all ten individuals needed to gather at the city wall.

The old sword immortal Chen Xi smiled slightly at the young Hidden Official, and Chen Ping'an returned the gesture with a clasped fist.

Chen Qingdu, hands behind his back, asked with a smile, "Hidden Official, it seems you are the only one here who isn’t a sword immortal."

Chen Ping'an nodded helplessly.

Nalan Shao Wei cast a sidelong glance, chuckling.

Chen Ping'an chose to ignore him, hearing nothing.

Ah Liang and the old deaf man were chummy, whispering to each other, while the old deaf man nodded vigorously at the young Hidden Official.

Chen Qingdu said, "Once everything is discussed, everyone may disperse."

Most of the sword immortals used their swords to return.

Even Ah Liang didn’t say much and walked away with the old deaf man.

Chen Ping'an was left in a daze. What was going on?

Chen Qingdu waved his hand, saying, "Bringing you here was just to make up the numbers."

Chen Ping'an tentatively asked, "Old sword immortal, is there really nothing for me to do?"

Chen Qingdu shook his head with a sympathetic look.

Chen Ping'an could only summon his talisman boat, puzzled, and return to the city.

Earlier, on the north city wall, he had seen Fengxue Temple Sword Immortal practicing swordplay and greeted him, mentioning that Wei the Great Sword Immortal was basking in the sun.

Wei Jin smiled, his gaze mirroring that of the old sword immortal’s—filled with sympathy—as he looked at the departing talisman boat, seeming a bit foolish and naive.

Upon returning to Ning Mansion, he found only Granny Bai at the pavilion and could not see Ning Yao. The old woman simply smiled and said she didn’t know where the young lady had gone.

With nothing to do, Chen Ping'an was at a loss for what to occupy himself with, so he flew on his sword to the Summer Palace to find something to do.

Ning Yao sat in her room, earnestly writing the character "Chen."

After finishing, she rested her head on the table, dazed.

On the table beside the mountain and water travelogue gifted by Chen Ping'an were several books, each page filled only with the name "Chen Ping'an."

Today she wrote "Chen," tomorrow she would write "Ping," and the day after, "An." 

She wrote one character a day, completing the name "Chen Ping'an" in three days.

Unlike Chen Ping'an, who had traversed mountains and rivers after meeting her, accumulating numerous stories, her reunion with Chen Ping'an after the Upside-Down Mountains seemed to yield a singular story: merely that of Chen Ping'an.

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 785: Pressed by the World

On the battlements of the Sword Qi Great Wall, a paper kite soared high in the sky. 

The kite glided gracefully above. 

Zhao Ge Yi and Cheng Quan were unusually seated side by side instead of opposite each other. These two close friends, bonded through life and death, sat together on the northern battlement, gazing into a small alleyway of the city.

Zhao Ge Yi turned his head to glance at the kite in the sky, knowing that only that scoundrel, A Liang, would be foolish enough to fly a kite up here. In the past, that man always had a bunch of hangers-on around him. Among the last group of children were Chen Sanqiu, Dong Bu De, Dong Hua Fu, and a couple of others like Chou Miao, Gao Ye Hou, and Luo Zhen Yi.

Zhao Ge Yi withdrew his gaze, continuing to lament Cheng Quan's lack of talent, claiming that his efforts to refine the mountains were moving too slowly, wasting the protective formation that had once moved mountains.

Cheng Quan held tightly onto a stamp inscribed with the words "not small" in Liuyebiao script, as if he needed to carefully protect that "not small." Instead of countering his old friend's complaints, he asked, “Is it true that the sword immortals of the Haoran world don’t have much love and affection?”

Zhao Ge Yi chuckled, “Not necessarily. Take Wei Jin from the Wind and Snow Temple, for instance — he’s a heartbroken romantic. I've heard rumors that he has some ties with Chen Ping An. However, there are indeed few sword immortals like him who get entangled in such emotional messes. More often, you have people like Pu He and Xie Zhi, who don't care much for romantic entanglements.”

Cheng Quan fell silent for a moment and spoke in a low voice, “If we were to tally our battle achievements, I reckon we could each leave. I’m quite familiar with the second shopkeeper; should I go greet him?”

Zhao Ge Yi scoffed, “What has that brat done to you to make you feel this way? When did you, Cheng Quan, go from cursing people to asking for favors?”

The Sword Qi Great Wall was filled with many disappointed sword cultivators. 

For instance, there was Mi Hu, whose talent was even better than Yue Qing’s. Even though he was now a grand sword immortal, he still felt a sense of regret. Mi Hu should have been the most likely to join the ranks of the Ten Great Sword Immortals. 

Then there was his brother, Mi Yu, who was stuck at the Jade Purity realm and couldn't break through. Along with Cheng Quan, who had fallen to the Nascent Soul realm, and Yin Chen, who had never managed to reach the upper five realms, many sword cultivators at the Great Wall felt the weight of their limitations. 

“I'm not joking with you,” Cheng Quan insisted.

Zhao Ge Yi laughed, “Do you think it's easier for a Jade Purity realm sword immortal who can stabilize a sea than for a worthless Nascent Soul cultivator to go to the Haoran world? It’s all relative.” 

Sword cultivators accumulate battle achievements primarily to nurture their swords; this endless pursuit often leads to a slim balance on the Hidden Officer lineage's ledger of merits. The same goes for sword immortals. The more significant their battle achievements, the higher the quality of their flying swords, but the consumption is equally great. For example, the grand sword immortal Yue Qing had almost exhausted his merits. Mi Hu, too, squandered his on behalf of his brother Mi Yu, delaying his own cultivation. In contrast, very few like Lu Zhi would see their achievements grow without any dwindling.

Cheng Quan said, “You should strive for the Haoran world, take on a few disciples, and find a compatible partner on the mountain. If you’re generous, at least hang up a portrait of me in the ancestor hall.”

At some point, a man had squatted down behind them. The wind was strong on the battlements, and the paper kite danced above their heads.

A Liang grinned, “Why hang a portrait of Cheng Quan? Two grown men sitting close together would easily lead to misunderstandings. Better to hang one of Cai Yun; what a beautiful girl! Brother Zhao could tell his disciples every day, ‘This is the master’s wife, the ancestor’s grandmother. Once upon a time, there was a scoundrel named Cheng Quan who practiced swordsmanship poorly, with an ugly mug, yet dared to covet your ancestor's beauty for many years...’”

Cheng Quan cursed, “Shut your mouth! Last time Zhao Ge Yi helped me move mountains, he let it slip that he himself admitted Cai Yun liked someone who...”

At this point, Cheng Quan fell silent, unable to continue.

A Liang said, “If one can leave, let him be.”

After saying this, A Liang stood up and resumed flying the kite. 

He paused briefly at an empty spot, letting the kite go, which immediately floated away into the sea of clouds.

As he strolled along the battlements, A Liang chatted with familiar sword immortals stationed there.

He approached a bustling spot where three sword immortals were teaching three younger sword cultivators. They sat cross-legged, engaged in lively conversation.

A Liang hurried over, and just as one of the female sword immortals was about to leave, A Liang’s presence made her shy. She quickly wanted to walk with the female sword immortal, taking in the breathtaking view from the high battlements, where the clouds gathered and dispersed beneath them, and the evening glow painted the horizon. Such a scene was perfect for a talented scholar and a beautiful maiden to share their hearts, resembling celestial couples in their affections.

Seeing that escape was impossible, the girl resigned herself to sit back down, preferring to avoid being alone with A Liang.

Among the three sword immortals were Xie Zhi from Fuyou Island, a wild cultivator who had remained solitary for life, having only recently changed her mind about taking on a couple of disciples to carry on her legacy. However, she was not looking for the exceptionally talented but rather those with great resolve and potential, as Xie Zhi herself was not the most outstanding in terms of innate talent.

Song Ping, the female sword immortal from Jinjia Island, was stunningly beautiful, her adornments crafted with exquisite skill, drawing attention. Unlike most female cultivators who favored gold and silver ornaments, Song Ping went against the trend, dressing in striking gold, captivating yet not gaudy.

Pu He from Liuxia Island was an elderly, lanky man known for his eccentric temperament. He was a proper lineage sword master but acted more freely than even Xie Zhi, a wild cultivator. Pu He had remained at the Sword Qi Great Wall after suffering defeat in a duel, often residing at the sword immortal villa “Cui Yu Pavilion” outside the city.

When Pu He saw A Liang, his expression turned sour.

The reason was simple: when Pu He first traveled to the Sword Qi Great Wall, it was this scoundrel who goaded him into challenging Mi Hu, claiming that Mi Hu’s realm was low despite his fame. Defeating Mi Hu would bolster his reputation immensely! The key was that defeating Mi Hu would also mean defeating his brother Mi Yu, who was even more renowned. Not seizing such an opportunity would be foolish. Yet, when Pu He finally challenged Mi Hu, he discovered that Mi Hu’s battle prowess was comparable to that of an immortal.

The three young sword cultivators hailed from the hometowns of the three sword immortals: Song Gaoyuan from the Deer Horn Palace, Cao Jun from Liuxia Island, and Xuan Can from Jinjia Island.

The three had previously met A Liang at the Summer Retreat Palace, and Song Gaoyuan had completed his task assigned by his ancestor. He had conveyed a message to A Liang that he had no further desires for this journey.

As for the three sword immortals, they had all once visited the Upside Down Mountain Spring Flag Pavilion alongside the young Hidden Officers, thus establishing a bond with the younger sword cultivators of the Hidden Officer lineage.

Otherwise, Xie Zhi and the others would not have gathered to meet and invite the three young cultivators to practice their swordsmanship.

Even if they hailed from the same region, these senior sword immortals, who stood tall on the peaks of their respective islands, had no need for such trivial friendships. To put it bluntly, if they “knew how to behave,” none of them would have ended up at the Sword Qi Great Wall, putting themselves in such peril, but rather would have established their own sects back in their respective hometowns in the Haoran world.

Becoming a practitioner of the upper five realms is a different matter than leading a sect; the latter is universally acknowledged as far more challenging.

A Liang sat beside Song Ping, saying wistfully, “Miss Song, how can you bear to part after such a literary romance?”

Once upon a time, a poet from Fuyou Island, while traveling, encountered a female sword immortal from Jinjia Island and became infatuated, penning many heartfelt poems. Unfortunately, he failed to win her heart.

Xie Zhi, not particularly close with A Liang, joked, “Senior A Liang, that famous line of poetry, ‘I have seen you in dreams, your eyes shining bright,’ alongside the line ‘Half for the Dao, half for you,’ is indeed a perfect match.”

Song Ping frowned slightly, “Xie Zhi, mind your words.”

Xie Zhi promptly fell silent.

Women who have risen to the upper five realms, especially sword immortals, are no lightweights; their presence often rivals that of men. Song Ping, along with Xie Songhua from Aiai Island and Li Cai from Beiju Lu Island, are all formidable in battle, each wielding their swords with fierce intent. 

In contrast, local Nascent Soul sword cultivator Nalan Cai Huan’s swordsmanship, though ruthless, lacks the same purity of heart when compared to these three foreign female sword immortals.

Xie Zhi suddenly recalled the late female sword immortal, Zhou Cheng, not out of affection but difficult to forget.

Such women, like deer fleeting through the forest, are rarely seen in the Haoran world.

Song Gaoyuan and the other two felt an immense curiosity about the past entanglements of these senior figures. Hearing tales from the higher realms was like a treasure trove.

Especially Song Gaoyuan perked up, as Song Ping had once made an impression during a peak ceremony in the Deer Horn Palace, leaving a lasting impression on him.

Unbeknownst to them, A Liang shifted the topic, inquiring about the recent happenings in Fuyou Island. He entrusted the three sword immortals with a message to relay to a Confucian sage at the Deer Ming Academy on Fuyou Island if they happened to return home.

Before leaving, A Liang imparted the “Eighteen Stops of Sword Qi” technique to the three young cultivators and agreed that while they could teach it to others in the future, they must be careful in their selection.

The three stood up, bowing in gratitude to the senior.

After A Liang rose, he only bid farewell to Song Ping, who, with a high realm and a thin skin, showed no reaction. Understanding, A Liang swiftly departed, heading to one end of the Sword Qi Great Wall, where he met the Confucian sage stationed on the battlements.

The sage gazed up at the sky, where the three moons of the wild world were faintly visible, and slowly said, “What have you heard to come this way, and what do you see as you leave?”

A Liang replied, “Not meeting in person is like the Tathagata.”

Once a disciple of Buddha, the Confucian sage’s words echoed the literary lines of the Haoran world, while A Liang’s response was a Buddhist saying.

Now a sage of the sub-saint lineage, the Confucian sage smiled, “In a daze, it feels like wandering a familiar path, as if meeting an old friend.”

A Liang remained silent, reclining back.

Earlier, at the Ning residence during a banquet, he had shared only half of a small story.

But Chen Ping An would surely understand the latter half of the unspoken tale, for he was a scholar who had traversed many rivers and lakes just like A Liang.

A lineage sword master, traversing mountains and rivers, slaying demons and monsters, yet mistakenly killing innocents—who could A Liang seek revenge against? How would he take that revenge? If he were to draw his sword, surely he would need to wield many swords to make his point. If he acted out of sheer indignation, how could he ensure the person belonged to a sect that didn’t have a certain girl glaring at him, asking why... If he sought reason everywhere, how could he voice the grievances bottled up in his heart? Drinking would be of no use; how could he find peace?

The reason A Liang didn’t continue was that he feared Chen Ping An would dig deeper, asking what the outcome would be.

So, every heart-wrenching story has a warm beginning.

In the northern part of the city, Yan Ming rarely returned to his residence, sitting in his study with his eyes closed. The little cunning spirit, adept at accounting, flipped through the pages of the ledger, venting to the man about the family's financial troubles, lamenting that they should really negotiate with that young Hidden Officer for relief; otherwise, the entire Yan family would become destitute. 

This little sprite plopped down on the ledger, looking up to ask, “Is it true we can’t reclaim that item? It’s not just any ordinary item; we can’t just let it go like that. The Hidden Officer should at least give our Yan family an explanation.”

Yan Ming opened his eyes and smiled, “Difficult.”

Earlier, during a meeting at the Spring Flag Pavilion, Chen Ping An had mentioned this matter, stating he had been caught in a deadly ambush by five sword cultivators from the Jia Shen realm. The situation was dire, and the item had suffered some damage, needing repairs before it could be returned; otherwise, it would be quite unreasonable.

Yan Ming truly couldn’t be bothered with that.

Yan Zhuo knocked on the door, entered, and was at a loss for words, still intimidated by this father. 

In fact, Yan Ming was not adept at conversing with his son either. When silent, the head of the Yan family commanded a certain authority, causing the little sprite to cough repeatedly and signal discreetly.

Finally, Yan Ming said, “Stop listening to A Liang’s nonsense. Honestly, you’ve always looked like me since you were young; you just need to be a bit slimmer, and you won’t be lacking.”

As soon as Yan Zhuo sat down in a chair, it creaked loudly.

The little sprite burst into laughter, holding her belly.

Yan Ming initially maintained a stern face but couldn’t help but chuckle.

Yan Zhuo scratched his head, feeling a bit at a loss. This kind of father was something he wasn't used to.

In a small alley, beside a tilted stone tablet, two busy children squatted — Feng Kang Le and Tao Ban, who worked as waitstaff at the tavern. The second shopkeeper had taught them the method for taking rubbings, providing them with the necessary items, allowing the kids to run errands and earn some copper coins. Afterward, they would settle accounts based on the number of characters, and as long as they were nimble and quick on their feet, they could earn quite a bit, enough for a bowl of spring noodles with an extra fried egg.

Feng Kang Le said he wanted to learn from Chen Ping An, becoming a itinerant trader, collecting scraps to exchange for money. At that time, his piggy bank would surely not be enough, and he would need to switch to a bigger one.

Tao Ban declared he would also open a bustling tavern in the future, not as a worker, but as the shopkeeper, collecting money without doing any work.

The two children busily chatted about their distant dreams.

On the wall facing the battlefield at the Sword Qi Great Wall, the old sword cultivator Yin Chen sat on a worn-out mat. Having no relatives or connections, the old sword cultivator didn’t even know what he was living for.

Sword Immortal Sun Ju Yuan had kicked off his shoes, sitting in his own corridor, leaning against an incense burner, holding a wine cup, drinking by himself. His sleeves brushed the ground, and a graceful paper talisman beauty danced in the courtyard, charming and lovely.

Sword Immortal Guo Jia watched his daughter gobbling down food beside him, while his wife nagged her to eat more slowly, saying there was no need to rush as if they were starving. She wondered how her daughter would manage to marry if she behaved like this. Would she end up like Dong Bu De, an old maid who was happy?

Guo Zhu Jiu looked up, grinning, then quickly closed his mouth, his cheeks puffed out.

Having bought the Ting Yun Pavilion, Li Cai stepped outside for some fresh air and arrived at the now-empty gate of the armor storehouse.

The sword cultivators from the Tai Hui Sword Sect had retreated after their leader Han Huai Zi fell in battle, returning to the Haoran world.

Li Cai stood still, recalling a time when she was invited to the armor storehouse by the late Han Huai Zi, who had once playfully suggested that there were many female sword cultivators in the Floating Duck Sword Lake, while the Tai Hui Sword Sect had too many melancholy men; perhaps the two sides could arrange some marriages. At that time, the sword cultivators from the Tai Hui Sword Sect had all looked at her, the Floating Duck Sword Lake’s master, with eager eyes, and she had promised to facilitate interactions between the young men and women of the two sects, providing them with chances to travel together. As long as both parties were willing, she would gladly play the matchmaker.

Lu Zhi, who was tall and skinny, was quite plain-looking, but due to A Liang's influence, she had inexplicably been celebrated as a beauty at the Sword Qi Great Wall.

In Lu Zhi’s private residence, the blushing lady was brewing tea. This upper five realm spirit had just handed over a plum blossom garden to the Summer Retreat Palace, and she regarded Lu Zhi as a peer, yet beneath the surface, she still acted as a servant, currently kneeling on a bamboo mat and handing Lu Zhi a cup of tea.

The blushing lady gently asked, “Did the Grand Sword Immortal summon many sword immortals including you earlier?”

Lu Zhi shook her head.

The blushing lady took the hint and refrained from asking more. 

Unable to resist, the blushing lady spoke in secret, “Lu Zhi, the more sword cultivators die in battle, the more sword path fortune remains in the Sword Qi Great Wall. Once the wall falls and a new owner arrives, who benefits the most? Naturally, it would be the sword cultivators from the wild world. Does that young Hidden Officer not realize this, or is he feigning ignorance? If he truly doesn’t know, it’s acceptable; exhausting himself for the position of Hidden Officer is indeed commendable. But if he’s aware, isn’t he just a pawn... an accomplice? How can such a person be worthy of your regard, Lu Zhi?”

Lu Zhi retorted, “It seems you have some biases against Chen Ping An?”

The blushing lady shook her head, “I just can’t believe that a young man could do something like this simply because a woman he loves is at the Sword Qi Great Wall.”

Lu Zhi hesitated, then said, “I can only tell you that this was the Grand Sword Immortal's intention, and Chen Ping An is merely following it.”

The blushing lady’s eyes suddenly lit up, “Lu Zhi, is there a possibility that one day in the Haoran world, we could have our own sect? One that only accepts female cultivators?”

Lu Zhi chuckled, “Women don’t stay put. Even if there are only female disciples on the mountain, will they not venture down for experience? Once they leave the mountain, they will inevitably fall for men, and you will still be troubled.”

The blushing lady sighed, fanning herself, “Blame men like A Liang and Chen Ping An for stirring up romantic debts.”

Lu Zhi questioned, “A Liang is one thing, but what about Chen Ping An? Are there any women in the Sword Qi Great Wall who like him?”

The blushing lady held her forehead, “Oh, my Lu Zhi, there are plenty! Just talking about the Summer Retreat Palace, I’ve noticed that the girl named Luo Zhen Yi doesn’t even realize her own feelings. She acts as if she looks down on everyone, yet she clearly dislikes that man’s every word.”

Lu Zhi pondered for a moment, recalling an impression of a fairly attractive young woman.

Lu Zhi said, “Why doesn’t she like Chou Miao? They’ve been together for some time, so logically, she should like him.”

The blushing lady’s eyes gleamed as she felt a surge of conversation coming on, “Lu Zhi, let me tell you, there’s a great deal of complexity in this.”

Lu Zhi regrettably thought to stop this pointless topic, but the blushing lady lamented, “Lu Zhi, just consider it a diversion.”

Lu Zhi drank tea as if it were wine, finishing each cup in one go and passing her the teacup.

The blushing lady poured another cup of tea, smiling softly, “Many men in this world think that their charm ruins women, yet don’t realize that women aren’t blind. It’s those truly devoted souls who make women quietly open their hearts. Besides, the unattainable is always more desirable. As for someone like Mi Yu, who’s all about flattery and actively courting, he’s truly beneath contempt. How can he boast of being a god among flowers?”

Lu Zhi suddenly said, “It seems Mi Yu has a good relationship with Chen Ping An.”

The blushing lady scoffed, “Neither of them are anything good.”

The children practicing martial arts in the Summer Retreat Palace were also rarely permitted to return home. 

On Taixiang Street, Jiang Yun returned home, boasting to his grandfather about how impressive martial artists were, explaining that sword cultivators couldn’t compare.

When it was just the two of them, Jiang Yun practiced the Six Steps Stance and demonstrated several martial techniques taught by the young Hidden Officers, asking his grandfather for his opinion.

Jiang Shu had initially only been indulging his most cherished grandson with casual compliments, but when the old sword cultivator witnessed his grandson execute a technique known as the Top Heart Elbow, he genuinely looked at him with newfound respect.

The old man hesitated a moment, allowing his grandson to continue practicing, casually inquiring about the old woman who taught him the martial arts. Jiang Yun remarked that the old lady's martial arts were just average, but her temper was poor; she seemed to target him on purpose.

Hearing this, Jiang Shu didn’t get angry but rather laughed, feeling quite pleased. In the old man’s heart, Ning Fu Bai Lian Shuang had never changed, always appearing as that cold-faced young girl. He had met her years ago and had been quite taken with her.

The little girl, Sun Qiu, returned home to the grand mansion on Yu Hu Street. Her elder sister, Sun Zao, who had become a sword cultivator early on and was quite proud, rarely initiated a conversation with her sister. But now, she was curious about the young Hidden Officer’s martial arts, asking if they were really as formidable as rumored. She wondered how that fellow had single-handedly driven off five talented sword cultivators from the wild world, and if he really fed them punches every so often. 

Sun Zao’s questions were plentiful, leaving Sun Qiu somewhat flustered, and when Sun Zao grew impatient, she rolled her eyes at her sister, exclaiming that after practicing martial arts, she still acted so demure. The two sisters eventually sat side by side on the railing, with Sun Zao commanding her flying sword to whirl around them, while Sun Qiu answered her sister’s myriad of questions, as if a student facing her teacher.

Sun Qiu tentatively suggested, “Shall I tell you a story about a cunning fox marrying off its daughter, or about a mountain god’s wedding?”

Sun Zao appeared skeptical but replied, “I’ll listen.”

However, they waited until a family elder called for Sun Zao to practice her swordsmanship, prompting her to jump off the railing, dismissing the story as dull before running off to train.

The tomboy Yuan Zao Hua returned home, discussing the martial arts training with her mother, recounting every trivial detail but omitting how arduous the training was. Eventually, Yuan Zao Hua grew a bit sentimental, expressing her envy for Jiang Yun and Xu Gong’s smooth martial arts training, as well as for the Guo sister who carried a bamboo box. The woman didn’t know how to console her daughter, so she embraced her tightly, gently laughing and softly calling her daughter’s name.

The three childhood friends gathered for a meal at Xu Gong’s residence in the twilight alley. Xu Gong’s home had no elders, while Zhang Pan and Tang Qu from Copper Coin Alley still had family members working in the Dan Workshop. Xu Gong was also friends with Zhang Jia Zhen, who had quietly left the Sword Qi Great Wall, often doing odd jobs together. Zhang Jia Zhen was several years older than the three of them.

Although they were very good friends, their personalities differed. Xu Gong had always been steady, Zhang Pan came from the best family but was the most timid, while Tang Qu was the most cunning.

Tang Qu asked with a grin, “When can we drink some wine?”

Zhang Pan quickly said, “Those who have just trained in martial arts absolutely must not drink. If Granny Bai finds out, we’ll certainly get a beating, or even worse, be kicked out.”

Tang Qu pouted, “Every time Mr. Chen sits far away on the railing and watches us practice, he looks so carefree while drinking. It is said that his wine gourd only holds sword-fostering wine. I’m dying of envy.”

Xu Gong replied, “That’s Mr. Chen; we can’t compare to him. Let’s first learn the martial arts and talk about drinking when we’re older. But why don’t we drink?”

After a brief pause, the three burst out laughing together, “Because we’re broke!”

Old sword immortal Dong San Geng stood outside his residence, once the home of his grandson Dong Guan Pu, who had been killed by Chen Qing Du. Dong Bu De and Dong Hua Fu stood behind their ancestor, unsure why he had summoned them.

Dong San Geng asked, “Isn’t San Qiu doing well? Why can’t you seem to like her?”

Dong Bu De replied, “Actually, I do like her.”

Dong San Geng nodded, unfazed. 

Only the confused Dong Hua Fu didn’t understand why his sister’s feelings had changed so suddenly.

Dong San Geng said, “Then go tell San Qiu directly; there’s no need to feel embarrassed about it.”

Dong Bu De shook his head, “I don’t want to; I still like her when we don’t meet, but being in front of her annoys me.”

Dong San Geng turned to glare, “Stop being so stubborn. You’re acting like a girl.”

Dong Bu De rolled his eyes. 

Dong San Geng laughed, “What can I say? When I see you and San Qiu, I just feel like you’re the man and she’s the girl.”

Afterward, the old man restrained his humor, “Since you’ve come to your senses, don’t hide away anymore.”

Dong Bu De shook his head, stubborn as ever.

Dong San Geng decided not to pressure him further, believing that each generation has its own fortune. These children’s fleeting gatherings and partings were not comparable to those of the elderly.

Dong San Geng looked at Dong Hua Fu and asked, “Do you have a girl you like?”

Dong Hua Fu shook his head, answering bluntly, “No time.”

Dong San Geng chuckled, “Every day you mooch off food and drink, yet you claim you have no time?”

Dong Hua Fu nodded, “A Liang once said he has encountered countless extraordinary people in his life, but he’s never seen anyone travel the rivers and lakes without spending a single coin, a feat never achieved in history. I’ve managed it and must maintain it.”

Dong San Geng asked, “Are you feeling proud of yourself?”

Dong Hua Fu nodded.

Dong San Geng clicked his tongue, “Being so stingy, if you ever find a wife, I’ll take your last name.”

Dong Bu De truly didn’t want to hear the two of them chatter, asking, “Why are we here?”

Dong San Geng replied, “You’re both too young. Young or old, it’s easy to forget things, which is why I called you both here to take a look.”

Dong Bu De said, “The prestige the Dong family has lost, I, a mere girl, can’t earn back. It’s barely manageable with charcoal.”

Dong San Geng laughed, “It’s not like that; the Dong family isn’t so fallen that two kids must support the facade. It’s just that I want you both to remember not to take everything for granted when doing things in the future.”

At the Diedong Tavern, a new face among the drunks shouted “Quickly!” to a group of sword cultivators.

This irritated the drunkard, who ordered several jars of bamboo sea cave wine, cursing that these old bachelors didn’t even have a chance at the bed.

The young waitstaff at the tavern were confused; they had heard many drunken tales and lewd stories, but this scholarly way of speaking was a first.

The young man, familiar with the tavern’s regulars, asked one, only to realize, while the girl was curious and discreetly inquiring, the boy’s cheeks flushed slightly as he shook his head, claiming ignorance.

An old sword cultivator, who had recently been inspired by poetry, expressed to a new drinking friend, “A certain scoundrel once said there are two types of people to be cautious of: those who have never been drunk but drink regularly, and those who have been bullied but never plead for mercy. Do you think there’s truth to this?”

The friend, not quite understanding, asked, “Which scoundrel? A Liang or the second shopkeeper?”

The old sword cultivator pointed dismissively, “What nonsense! Diedong, another jar of wine, I need to drink a few bowls with my friend.”

The sword cultivator who had unwittingly contributed to the wine bill nodded, “At the table, whether drinking or being drunk, we should all be quiet. On the battlefield, the ones who take hits without a sound are the ones we’re talking about. It’s obviously referring to our second shopkeeper; thus, the one with such wisdom must be A Liang. These scholars love to twist words and make it hard to grasp. Come on, while those two aren’t here, let’s drink and curse; I won’t pay for the wine, but every curse will go on my tab. Even if A Liang and the second shopkeeper stood in front of me, I’d still say the same! In terms of drinking capacity, those two together can’t match me!”

The old sword cultivator was taken aback, “Are you too?”

The drunkard smiled knowingly, pretending to be profound.

Outside the Ning residence, an old man appeared conflicted, unsure whether to knock on the door. Eventually, he sighed and returned to the Yao family.

On the battlements, Wei Jin felt a mix of thoughts arise and decided to stop deliberately nurturing his sword.

The Grand Sword Immortal stood nearby, laughing, “I’ve never understood what’s so good about drinking.”

Wei Jin quickly replied, “Drinking may not be so great; it’s probably just a habit.”

Chen Qing Du gazed toward the northern city, saying, “Do you know why the taverns at the Sword Qi Great Wall do the best business?”

Wei Jin nodded in agreement, “Too many sword cultivators, too little space; it seems the only way to relieve stress is through drinking. In the Haoran world, in a place this small, it can hardly accommodate more than one or two sword immortals.”

Wei Jin asked, “Grand Sword Immortal, why did you want me to return to the Baoping Isle instead of going to Fuyou Island? Is it because my realm isn’t sufficient? I could assist a certain sword immortal, after all.”

Chen Qing Du replied, “It’s both yes and no.”

Wei Jin sighed helplessly.

The Grand Sword Immortal did not wish to elaborate, so Wei Jin didn’t dare to pry further.

Chen Qing Du walked with his hands behind his back, taking a solitary stroll.

Earlier, when the ten individuals gathered on the battlements, there had actually been a sequence to their arrival.

Qi Ting Ji arrived first.

Chen Qing Du had told him, “You can retain your realm and head to Fuyou Island to establish a sect. Before leaving, show some real skills. If you just keep muddling through, there’s no need to go to Fuyou Island.”

Qi Ting Ji inquired why he wasn’t heading to Beiju Lu Island.

Chen Qing Du laughed, “You have the nerve to go to Beiju Lu Island?! Let’s not even mention Han Huai Zi; can you really compare to Li Cai, who is merely at the Jade Purity realm? What can you offer besides a little extra in your pants? What can you compare to that woman?”

Qi Ting Ji fell silent for a moment before declaring, “Among all the descendants of the Qi family, I will only take Qi Shou with me!”

“He will follow Nalan Shao Wei elsewhere; you cannot take him with you.”

Qi Ting Ji sighed heavily.

He truly dared not haggle over this with Chen Qing Du.

In Chen Qing Du’s eyes, Qi Ting Ji resembled a mountain-top cultivator of the Haoran world. Choosing Qi Shou meant preserving the lineage. It was clear he valued Qi Shou’s talent.

But besides bargaining, Qi Ting Ji had some words he couldn’t keep to himself.

For the first time in his life, he addressed the Grand Sword Immortal by his name, “Chen Qing Du, do you not feel any guilt watching so many sword cultivators die here, simply because they’re sword cultivators?”

Chen Qing Du scoffed, “If I weren’t here, would you all be? Do you really not understand the order of arrival? You should really consider changing your surname to Dong.”

Then, Chen Qing Du no longer wished to waste time with Qi Ting Ji and called the second person over to speak with him.

Chen Xi departed for the fifth realm. However, he needed to undergo a transformation, born with knowledge. As a member of the Chen family, he had to report to the Sword Qi Great Wall.

At that moment, Chen Xi had only one question, “What about San Qiu?”

Chen Qing Du replied, “She will go to the Haoran world.”

“Who will San Qiu accompany?” Chen Xi asked again.

Chen Qing Du did not answer.

Next up was Dong San Geng, whom Chen Qing Du asked if he truly had no regrets.

Dong San Geng only said that since he first drew his sword in his youth, he had no regrets in this life.

Chen Qing Du smiled and asked, “I heard A Liang say that while you wandered the wild world, you had many female friends and fathered numerous illegitimate children?”

Dong San Geng cursed loudly.

Then Chen Qing Du remarked, “If you can’t even curse, it’s no wonder your achievements are limited.”

Afterward, Lu Zhi, the old deaf man, and Nalan Shao Wei were summoned to the battlements by the Grand Sword Immortal.

Nalan Shao Wei also needed to undergo a transformation, but he would go to the Qing Ming realm.

The old deaf man, during the great war, could drop a realm and return to the wild world. If he wanted to go to the Haoran world, no one would stop him.

The old deaf man stated he wished to go work for the old blind man, as it was easy and stable.

As for Lu Zhi, she had already made plans; she would take the blushing lady to Nan Po Sha Island, while Tong Ye Island had its arrangements, and Fuyou Island had Qi Ting Ji.

Finally, there were A Liang and Chen Ping An.

At this moment, Chen Qing Du recalled something. The young Hidden Officer at the Sword Qi Great Wall was still too relaxed, which was quite strange.

The old man then spoke to the currently residing Chen Ping An at the Summer Retreat Palace, “You should visit the old deaf man, and take care of your responsibilities. Don’t worry; it’s a good thing. Otherwise, if you have nothing to do, you might accidentally find your Dao heart collapsing.”

Just as Chen Ping An was about to ask what it was about, he found himself tossed to the entrance of the old deaf man’s prison.

Seeing the old deaf man’s compassionate gaze, Chen Ping An knew it wasn’t what A Liang had claimed was simply training martial arts.

He felt that something ominous was definitely afoot.

The old deaf man said nothing, opened the restrictions, and led the young Hidden Officer into the prison. 

A Liang rushed over, agitated, “Have you gone mad?! At this rate, he will be crushed by the entire wild world’s Dao!”

Chen Qing Du laughed, “Such trivial matters are nothing; I’ve endured for over ten thousand years.” 

(End of Chapter)

 ### Chapter 786: Cold Weather, Extra Clothes (Part 1)

At the humble abode of the Grand Sword Immortal, there were hardly any visitors year-round, yet the three great sages often received sword cultivators. 

For instance, Chou Miao frequently discussed economic strategies with the Confucian sages, and those gentlemen of the Confucian School—Lishi and Yasheng—who served as officers and recorders on the Sword Qi Great Wall, were well-acquainted with the Sword Immortal Chou Miao. 

In his younger years, Pang Yuanji often visited the Buddhist sages to discuss the profound meanings of Zen koans. 

It wasn’t just the exceptional sword cultivators like Chou Miao and Pang Yuanji; even ordinary sword cultivators were eager to exchange a few words with the sages at either end of the city wall. As Ah Liang would say, it was about soaking in the aura of immortals and the righteous spirit. In other realms, such powerful figures were often not so easily encountered. 

Only the Daoist sage, stationed at the highest point of the canopy, practiced quietude, resulting in fewer visitors. Typically, sword immortals would casually fly over to inquire about the customs and culture of the Qingming realm. 

Today, high above the sea of clouds, the old Daoist, with a whisk resting across his lap, brushed away impurities and the heat of summer, embodying humility. However, the whisk had now only a long jade handle left. 

It was not only a divine weapon but also a personal artifact. 

The other two sect sages also faced a similar bleak situation; after three attempts to forge the Golden River, aiding the Sword Qi Great Wall in dividing the battlefield, one had to pay a price—was it truly believed that the great monsters on the wild, with their thrones, were mere idle creatures? 

As the old Daoist opened his eyes, he spotted Ah Liang arriving. 

The old man forced himself to muster some spirit. That guy looked downcast, likely having come up short against the Grand Sword Immortal. 

Ah Liang lay across the sea of clouds, lightly punching the air until a small hole appeared, just enough to glimpse the city's outline. Then, he pulled out a handful of ordinary pebbles that seemed to have been picked up from who knows where, tossing them one by one, each with a different force, all intentional. 

The Sword Immortal Sun Juyuan, who was dozing in the corridor, heard the sound of pebbles striking the roof. 

A female sword cultivator, who was grooming herself in front of a mirror, also heard a pebble clink against the curtain. 

A young sword cultivator from Yuhu Street practicing in the courtyard was startled when a pebble struck the tip of his sword. 

At a nearby tavern table, an elderly sword cultivator, who was spitting and cursing, suddenly found a pebble in his wine bowl and switched from cursing to praise, speaking smoothly without a hitch. 

The old Daoist was unfazed by this; after all, a hundred years ago, even more outrageous things had happened. 

Once, a pair of immortal lovers, caught in a precious moment of spring, were interrupted by a slight disturbance on the roof, the tiles rippling slightly. In the next moment, subtle movements elsewhere suggested someone sensed their presence and immediately fled. The man, enraged, threw on his clothes, grabbed his sword, and leaped onto the courtyard wall, only to find remnants of ripples left behind in one courtyard. As he pursued, he unexpectedly stumbled upon another couple, just as lost in their own world. Without saying a word, he first cursed their ancestors for eighteen generations, and the two parties ended up in a fierce brawl. 

At that time, a man had been watching the commotion from above the clouds, much like now. 

Ah Liang clapped his hands, flipping them to smooth the surface of the sea of clouds. 

The old Daoist asked a question he had always been curious about, “Ah Liang, how is it that someone like me, or even the sword immortals here, as we age, find little interest in worldly matters outside of cultivation? How do you manage to be so… bored?” 

The more one sought a path in cultivation, the more one would wish to immerse oneself in it. Moreover, to cultivate the arts of immortality with a focused heart was only natural. 

Ah Liang leaned back, lying on the sea of clouds, and crossed his legs. “After all the hard work to cultivate for immortality, what can we do once we achieve it?” 

This was a question with a high threshold. 

It wasn’t something one could discuss with ordinary Qi Refiners, nor could one discuss it with the local sword immortals here. 

However, there was still plenty to talk about with the old Daoist. 

After all, this Daoist master was the foremost disciple of the Great Teacher of the Qingming realm and the lord of the city of Baiyu. The great celestial lord from the Overturned Mountain, though of equal standing, was still lacking in Daoist attainment. 

The old Daoist chuckled, “My time is short.” 

Ah Liang sat up, tossing a small Daoist talisman-like object toward the old Daoist. It was a token that Chen Ping’an had entrusted to Ah Liang for delivery. 

Shaped like a long wooden paperweight, it was very light in hand, adorned with images of the sun, moon, and stars, inscribed with a line of text: “The Marshal commands, grant a measuring and cutting of essence, according to the heart’s pointing, mountains and peaks shall be crushed, hastily as per the law.” 

The old Daoist took the token and, after some calculations, nodded. “Understood, understood, it should be as such.” 

Ah Liang smiled, “Can you really calculate it?” 

The old Daoist nodded, “I’ve grasped the general meaning.” 

Ah Liang then relayed the details in a voice only the old Daoist could hear, who committed everything to memory. “I’ll inform the Overturned Mountain when I return.” 

This aged Daoist, apart from being adept at divination, was also skilled in the art of Mohist reasoning and Buddhist logic. 

The old Daoist’s expression turned serious. “Ah Liang, I have a small request.” 

Ah Liang grinned, “A small matter.” 

The old Daoist stood, bowed respectfully, the gesture not minor. Ah Liang could only rise and return the salute. 

The old Daoist looked around, no longer consciously restraining the aura rippling above the sea of clouds, and sighed, “After all, how many can truly see the deer? Unaware of dreaming each day as a fish. The day has passed, and so has life; like a fish with little water, what joy is there?” 

The Buddhist sage smiled and said, “In the quiet night, the cold water denies fish their meal; why rejoice in vain? A full boat returns under the moonlight, how can one not rejoice?” 

The Confucian sage nodded, “Shaking off dust, one can still see the blossoming branches in spring. Standing in the mud, is it not also the heart of heaven, full moon?” 

Ah Liang pretended to understand, nodding lightly, and then wracked his brain to squeeze out a line, “What night is this, to meet such a good person?” 

The Grand Sword Immortal scoffed, “Ah Liang, can you leave some face for the scholars?” 

Ah Liang burst into laughter; did the Grand Sword Immortal really not know he was the one with the thinnest skin in the Sword Qi Great Wall? 

Suddenly, Chou Miao, the Sword Immortal, took charge, saying that during this time while the Hidden Official was away from the Summer Palace, all matters of the Hidden Official lineage would be handled entirely by him, Chou Miao. 

No one among the sword cultivators at the Summer Palace objected; Chou Miao was trustworthy, with exceptional realm, character, and methods, recognized as the second-in-command of the Hidden Official lineage. With Chen Ping’an absent, it was only natural for Chou Miao to take on the burden. 

Gu Jianlong, Wang Xinshi, Cao Jun, and Xuan Can, these four who had been unofficially appointed as the Hidden Official's loyal subordinates, inevitably felt a bit worried. 

After years of close companionship, they had grown accustomed to the presence of the Hidden Official in that position. No matter how precarious the battlefield circumstances were, even when Chen Ping’an was silent, his presence brought some peace of mind. Seeing the current situation, it seemed the young Hidden Official would not be returning to the Summer Palace anytime soon. 

As Chen Ping’an’s direct disciple, Gu Zhujiu merely asked Chou Miao if her master had gone to stealthily slay a great demon of the Ascending Realm again. 

Chou Miao could only say he wasn’t sure. 

He only knew that Chen Ping’an had gone to the old deaf man's prison. 

Chou Miao also said he would treat everyone to drinks, and not return until they were drunk. 

Among the Hidden Official lineage, aside from Lin Junbi—who had returned home ahead of schedule—and the derelict Hidden Official, all the sword cultivators had gone to the tavern in the stacked peaks. 

The out-of-town sword cultivators understood that Chou Miao was simply advancing the farewell drinks; once the battle began, the sword cultivators of the Hidden Official lineage would become fewer and busier, making it a luxury to hold farewell drinks for the four of them. 

Coincidentally, Ning Yao, Chen Sanqiu, Yan Zhuo, Dong Huafu, and Fan Dache were also drinking at the tavern. 

In fact, apart from Dong Buduo and Gu Zhujiu, the Hidden Official lineage had rarely interacted with the sword cultivators of that small mountain. 

Upon seeing Dong Buduo, the Chen family’s young master, who had been speaking loudly with a neighboring drinker, immediately lost his flirtatious demeanor, becoming as restrained as a young lad drinking for the first time. 

Dong Huafu hesitated, his words caught in his throat. 

Dong Buduo glanced at his brother, who looked like he wanted to speak up, and Dong Huafu had no choice but to keep quiet. Then, looking at Chen Sanqiu, who was almost hiding his face in his wine bowl, he felt an unprecedented guilt. He’d let Chen Sanqiu off the hook for today’s drinking expenses, and instead, let Fan Dache settle the bill. 

Mi Yu, who slept soundly among the clouds, Wu Chengpei, who sat stiffly at the city wall, Pang Yuanji, who was slightly tipsy from drinking, and Chen Sanqiu, who was pushing the walls with his drinking—all were famous handsome men from the Sword Qi Great Wall. 

After the sword cultivators of the Hidden Official lineage, led by Chou Miao, took their seats, the atmosphere in the tavern momentarily turned strange, with much less clamor. 

Firstly, Chou Miao’s reputation was significant; he was the youngest sword immortal of the upper five realms in the Sword Qi Great Wall, with remarkable achievements, and had set out early with Ah Liang to travel deep into the wild world. 

Moreover, Luo Zhenyi and Xu Ning, the “money-collecting” sword cultivators, were notoriously unsociable. Their status in the Sword Qi Great Wall was akin to scouts on the fringes of a mundane dynasty, somewhat elevated above ordinary sword cultivators. 

Furthermore, the current Hidden Official lineage held more authority and insider knowledge than any previous Hidden Official sword cultivators in the history of the Sword Qi Great Wall. 

No one liked their secrets, big or small, casually exposed on paper for others to peruse. 

Lastly, the key reason lay in Pang Yuanji's presence. 

The previous Hidden Official, Pang Yuanji's master, Xiao Xian, had chosen to leave the Sword Qi Great Wall in the most disgraceful manner, taking two sword immortals, Luo Shan and Zhu An, with him. 

Xiao Xian left behind a desolate Pang Yuanji, much like leaving behind that Hidden Official jade tablet with no care. 

When Pang Yuanji fought his way out of the city, every time was a narrow escape, and as a top-tier genius, he was never particularly targeted by the great demons, which inevitably raised suspicions. 

There were quite a few sword cultivators in the Hidden Official lineage; the tavern’s stacked peaks even personally helped join two tables together. 

Two people, one long bench. 

Luo Zhenyi casually glanced over at Ning Yao. 

Ning Yao felt a stir in her heart and returned a glance at Luo Zhenyi. 

Gu Zhujiu ordered a portion of strong liquor, and the stacked peaks specifically brought a small pot of rice wine for the young girl. 

Gu Zhujiu disdainfully rejected the so-called “young lady’s wine,” showing no bravado; if she was going to drink, she’d drink the kind that “only drinks and says nothing.” The stacked peaks smiled and said it was her master’s intention; here, she could only drink this. 

Gu Zhujiu immediately changed her mind. 

After the tavern's business expanded, it not only sold the existing bamboo sea cave wines but also offered strong liquor, and later introduced a type of rice wine brew. The second shopkeeper named the strong liquor “Mute Lake Wine,” and it had no worries about sales; whether rich or poor, everyone liked it. It was inexpensive and had a strong flavor, truly deserving its name of strong liquor. However, that soft and fluffy rice wine brew sold for no high price; the stacked peaks were even more worried it wouldn’t sell at all. The women of the Sword Qi Great Wall, as long as they drank, did not fall short of the men—they consistently preferred strong liquor. If the tavern aimed to attract female customers, they would surely be disappointed. At that time, Chen Ping’an had not explained the specific reasons, only saying that this rice wine brew was merely a small business that added a bit of flair; even if it lost money, it wouldn’t lose much. He had connections with the ferry from Guohua Island in Old Dragon City, which helped bring some hometown rice wine brew; it cost him barely a few immortal coins. 

As it turned out, the second shopkeeper’s business acumen meant losing money was impossible; those who weren’t bachelors would always take home a few jars of rice wine brew before returning home drunk, telling their families this was wine from the Baoping Continent of the Hao Ran realm, from the young Hidden Official's hometown, and insist that the second shopkeeper guaranteed the drink would nourish a woman’s appearance! Some women would laugh and ask, “Do you believe that?” The men would sulk; the second shopkeeper’s tall tales couldn’t be taken off the table, which was widely accepted in the Sword Qi Great Wall; yet the women would still laugh and drink. 

Thus, the female sword cultivators who often came to drink at the tavern later only drank rice wine brew. 

Gu Zhujiu went over to the master’s wine table to toast; after one round, a whole pot of glutinous rice wine brew was gone. Ning Yao couldn’t stop it, and Gu Zhujiu returned to her own table, swaying as if she were practicing drunken boxing. 

The group with Ning Yao finished their drinking and prepared to leave. Fan Dache settled the bill; he was much more well-off now and no longer needed to borrow money from Chen Sanqiu. Ning Yao asked the stacked peaks to keep an eye on Gu Zhujiu. 

Gu Zhujiu had indeed drunk too much and had fallen asleep on the table. She couldn’t hold her liquor, but she was quiet and peaceful when drunk. 

Chou Miao laughed, “Some things that used to be unsuitable to discuss in the Summer Palace can now be openly talked about.” 

Cao Jun swayed as he stood, raising his wine bowl first, saying, “Pang Yuanji, Qi Shou, and Gao Ye Hou have all successively entered the Nascent Soul stage. If in the future, you still don’t enter the upper five realms, I’ll scold you.” 

Pang Yuanji didn’t drink much, but he rose with a smile, clinking wine bowls. “Scold away first; if you’re wrong, when we meet again, I’ll scold you back.” 

Cao Jun looked at Pang Yuanji, shaking his head vigorously. “Pang Yuanji, in my eyes, you hold the same potential for the Dao as the Hidden Official. I hope that many years from now, when you look up, you’ll see the highest point in the world, with the green-clothed swordmaster Chen Ping’an and the white-clothed sword immortal Pang Yuanji.” 

Pang Yuanji smiled helplessly, “I’m nowhere near the Hidden Official.” 

Both drank heartily. 

Xu Ning turned to Xuan Can and said, “It’s about the matter, not the person.” 

Xuan Can followed suit and drank, his eyes bright. “Well said.” 

Song Gaoyuan drank a bowl by himself, propping one foot up on the long bench. “It’s a pity we can’t use the identity of the Hidden Official lineage’s sword cultivators to guard the Sword Qi Great Wall; otherwise, it would be extremely interesting! Looking back, these out-of-towners, young as they are, truly are a bunch of annoying little geniuses.” 

Gu Jianlong said, “Let me say something fair: the most annoying of all is the youngest, who broke through the fastest, Lin Junbi.” 

Wang Xinshi nodded, “Let me also speak a word of conscience; it’s actually Lin Junbi who is the most sycophantic towards the Hidden Official.” 

Gu Jianlong lamented, “If Lin Junbi were to cover a woman’s face, he would actually outshine our Hidden Official.” 

Dong Buduo smiled and said, “Wrong! Lin Junbi doesn’t need to change his appearance; he just has to switch into a woman’s clothes.” 

Everyone nodded in agreement. 

Dong Buduo added, “If Junbi gets drunk, with his little face all rosy, and clings to the Hidden Official, tsk tsk tsk, it would be a sight to behold.” 

Chang Taiqing jolted and quickly poured himself a bowl of wine, grabbing some pickled vegetables, only to jolt again. “Calm down, calm down.” 

Chou Miao laughed, “Are you all bullying the Hidden Official and Lin Junbi because they’re not here?” 

Deng Liang suddenly said, “Have we forgotten someone?” 

At the large table, there was a moment of silence, then everyone burst into laughter. 

Of course, it was that great sword immortal Mi Yu, who had just returned from the Sword Qi Great Wall and was now heading to the Overturned Mountain. 

Pang Yuanji drank modestly but didn’t hold back. 

The youth felt somewhat dazed, inexplicably feeling that the current Hidden Official lineage was truly lively, and it wasn’t bad. 

The drinking session lasted a long time, and everyone returned to the Summer Palace. 

Luo Zhenyi carried Gu Zhujiu on her back, walking side by side with Dong Buduo. 

Deng Liang slowed his pace to approach them. 

Luo Zhenyi, sensing the atmosphere, wanted to leave but was stopped by Dong Buduo. 

Deng Liang didn’t mind and straightforwardly said, “Miss Dong, I like you.” 

Dong Buduo’s gaze was clear as she replied, “I don’t like you.” 

Deng Liang nodded, “I know.” 

Deng Liang paused slightly, his expression carefree, his gaze sincere as he smiled, “I know Dong Buduo doesn’t like Deng Liang, but Deng Liang is just afraid Dong Buduo doesn’t know Deng Liang likes Dong Buduo.” 

Dong Buduo felt somewhat helpless; twisting around like this, but since you, Deng Liang, are so rude, I won’t hold back either. After all, I’ve put up with you for quite some time. “In the Summer Palace’s council hall, a place no bigger than a palm, I’m not a fool; of course, I can see you like me. Moreover, I also know you can’t help but steal glances at Luo Zhenyi’s face and keep your eyes fixed on her back.” 

Deng Liang threw caution to the wind. “Looking at Luo Zhenyi? I’m not the only one; didn’t Wang Xinshi look? Didn’t Chang Taiqing take a look?” 

Luo Zhenyi, a beautifully cold girl, had her demeanor even more frosty at that moment, but suddenly smiled, pretending to be angry was a bit difficult. 

These matters were trivial. 

Dong Buduo and she could say anything privately; what couldn’t they discuss? 

Dong Buduo remarked that Chou Miao had an excellent figure; though he looked thin in clothes, he was actually muscular. Dong Buduo asked Luo Zhenyi, “Have you touched him?” “Never touched, but have seen him, right?” 

Luo Zhenyi held great respect for Sword Immortal Chou Miao, viewing him as an elder, and wouldn’t allow Dong Buduo to joke about him. 

Dong Buduo also said that although Cao Jun was still a young lad, his little face was actually quite handsome, and he would definitely be a graceful young gentleman in the future. Especially his eloquence, soft and pleasant to hear, boosted by his crisp articulation, often sprinkled with rural dialects, chewing on their words, “In the old days….” In the future, when he and his celestial partner were under the flowers and the moon, if he were to affectionately call her by name, lifting her chin with his fingers, it would undoubtedly be quite charming. At this point, Dong Buduo tried to lift Luo Zhenyi’s chin, mimicking Xu Ning’s voice to say, “Zhenyi, Zhenyi,” which made Luo Zhenyi’s charming face flush slightly, enhancing her allure. 

Initially, Luo Zhenyi hadn’t paid attention to Cao Jun’s voice, but after Dong Buduo’s reminder, she seemed to realize it was indeed the case. 

Every time she saw Dong Buduo propping her chin in one hand, casually chatting with Cao Jun, Luo Zhenyi found it amusing. 

Dong Buduo even showed her a booklet filled with words from brothels and love stories, with the women being fox spirits or flower goddesses, while the men were mostly down-and-out scholars. Many phrases were truly indecent, comparing women’s waists to the way a man stood on the beach like a heron; if they hugged, they would either die or have their souls snatched away. Luo Zhenyi only read one page before feeling embarrassed and threw it back at Dong Buduo. 

Suddenly, Luo Zhenyi felt somewhat envious of Deng Liang. 

At this moment, with Dong Buduo’s interruption, Deng Liang lost the heroic spirit he had managed to accumulate. 

Moreover, as Deng Liang himself said, today’s words were just for Dong Buduo to know. 

Deng Liang clasped his fists and said, “Miss Dong, when you get married in the future, be sure to send me a wedding invitation. If the man is a sword cultivator, I will challenge him to a duel.” 

Dong Buduo merely smiled and remained silent. 

Deng Liang turned and strode away, rejoining Gu Jianlong and the others, only to receive an elbow from both Wang Xinshi and Chang Taiqing. 

Luo Zhenyi teasingly said, “Deng Liang is actually not that bad.” 

Dong Buduo smiled with her eyes narrowed, “How do you know if Deng Liang is good or not?” 

Luo Zhenyi felt helpless; she walked slowly, carrying Gu Zhujiu on her back, with the girl’s small bamboo box closely following. 

Dong Buduo understood why Luo Zhenyi had taken the initiative to carry Gu Zhujiu. 

Some things could be joked about, with no restrictions. But some things, not a single word should be mentioned. 

Fan Dache returned home alone, his steps unsteady as he drank and thought of the one he loved. 

Dong Huafu wandered about, keeping a tally of the things he liked and the food he encountered, placing the tab on Chen Dazhao and Yan Pangzi. 

On Taixiang Street, Chen Sanqiu squatted by a wall, his head resting against it, gently knocking as he murmured for it to make way, or he would go mad from drinking. 

The stacked peaks sat resting at the counter, while the young boy Qiulong and the young girl Liu E were busy, and the children Tao Ban and Feng Kangle were also helping. 

Outside, it was bustling and noisy. The stacked peaks looked up, seeing the rows of spirit tablets on the wall, silent and still, like a row of little mutes. 

“Drank the wine, killed the demons, composed poems; my talent doesn’t lose to the second shopkeeper, my looks fall short of Wu Chengpei, my life is quite complete, just lacking a wife.” 

“Money in my pocket, drinking down the tavern.” 

“My swordsmanship is acceptable.” 

“With Ah Liang as my partner, we can slay great demons of the Ascending Realm.” 

“Nalan Caihuan, I’ll be right back.” 

“Flute and camel bell, both are sounds of the wind.” 

“Good mountains and waters are given to idle people, good women are taken away.” 

“In this life, I’ve never been drunk; I resent the wine.” 

“I’ve never been to the Overturned Mountain.” 

“Chen Li, with a dull sword, dreams of flying swords. A hundred years of sword immortals, easily within reach.” 

“There’s no good drink in the world; damn, give me back my money.” 

“Lu Zhi is indeed beautiful.” 

“Life is short; practicing swordsmanship is too difficult.” 

After the old deaf man opened the restrictions, like a host welcoming guests, Chen Ping’an found himself within, his vision suddenly wide open. The world was vast and empty, with little to see, only a towering stone tablet inscribed with the words “Zha Zha Tian.” 

Chen Ping’an steadied himself and quickly adjusted his breathing, blocking the surging spiritual energy from overwhelming him. 

The prison managed by the old deaf man was a broken cave sky, reminiscent of the Overturned Mountain's Huang Liang tavern, with particularly abundant spiritual energy and no sword energy suppression at all. 

There were no other sword immortals present here, not even a single sword cultivator; ever since the old deaf man took over, he was the only one watching over this place, a former demon of the Ascending Realm. 

The old deaf man wasn’t truly deaf; as a being of the Ascending Realm, how could he be hard of hearing? However, the sword cultivators of the Sword Qi Great Wall had always looked down upon him, and he was a soft target who wouldn’t retaliate or respond to insults, rarely showing himself, which had kept him out of major trouble. 

Additionally, the Dong family controlled the Sword Workshop, the Qi family managed the Clothing Workshop, and the Chen family was responsible for the Alchemy Workshop, making the Sword Qi Great Wall the true meaning of a restricted area. 

There were few records in the archives of the Summer Palace regarding the prison; the texts only vaguely noted the identities and origins of the demons imprisoned over the generations, and the deceased were merely a line crossed out. 

The old deaf man chuckled, knowing it was normal for the young Hidden Official not to trust himself, but did he also not trust the Grand Sword Immortal? However, he soon felt relieved; if he didn’t have this nature, he wouldn’t have been able to become the Hidden Official, nor reach this point. At that time, on the city wall, it wasn’t himself that the Hidden Official lineage didn’t trust, but rather Lu Zhi. At this moment, he didn’t trust himself. Would he end up doubting even Chen Qing in the end? Regardless of the answer, the old deaf man found it somewhat amusing. 

Chen Ping’an and the old deaf man moved forward almost simultaneously, and Chen Ping’an discovered that the stone tablet, appearing merely a hundred or so yards away, would take quite a while to reach if they just walked straight ahead. 

The old deaf man, not wishing to be misunderstood as taking advantage of others, respectfully referred to the Hidden Official and then revealed the secret, “The smaller we make our minds, the smaller our thoughts, the smaller our steps, the faster we actually go.” 

Chen Ping’an followed his advice and, sure enough, within a few blinks, he had arrived before the stone tablet. 

The old deaf man was slightly surprised, inevitably comparing Chen Ping’an to the previous two Hidden Officials. The temperamental girl with the braided hair had refused to believe in the supernatural and insisted on rushing to the stone tablet, only to find herself thousands of miles away in an instant. As for Xiao Xian, he had always flown down, reveling in it, and as a result, after a period of time, by the pace of an ordinary person, he had crossed continents, guzzling down plenty of immortal brews each day, running further and further away from the stone tablet—he had seen many bored sword cultivators, but none as bored as her. As for the earlier Hidden Official, he wasn’t bored, just lacked excitement; however, the merit under the table was not small. That mirage was something he had paid to have built, but unfortunately, his cultivation aptitude was too poor, and his lifespan was short. Otherwise, the Hidden Official of the Sword Qi Great Wall would not have been Xiao Xian, nor would this young man beside him. 

The old deaf man accompanied the young Hidden Official, both gazing up at the stone tablet. 

The old deaf man raspily spoke, “Zha Zha Tian, these three characters were penned by a pair of ancient immortal lovers who were sword immortals, of high lineage, only slightly younger than the Dragon Lord and Guan Zhao, yet they didn’t have much fame in the Sword Qi Great Wall.” 

The old deaf man smiled, “I believe with the Hidden Official’s discerning eye, you should have seen the trend early on. The characters for ‘Zha’ and ‘Tian’ were engraved by the male sword immortal, with excellent strokes, while the character ‘Zha’ was written by the female, with sharp sword intent, still unable to hide a hint of softness. At that time, she had sustained serious injuries and was slightly fatigued, so the male remedied it. In the end, the last character, appearing spirited and rigorous, saved the middle character, but it was already tinged with pain for the lovers; compared to the character ‘Zha,’ which should have been the most imposing, the character ‘Tian’ instead felt heavy, lacking in sword intent—a real pity, a true pity.” 

Chen Ping’an sincerely replied, “I didn’t notice these.” 

How strange it was; how did he become a disciple of the Literary Sage? 

The old deaf man asked, “The Hidden Official should not be unfamiliar with the River of Time?” 

Chen Ping’an nodded, “Not unfamiliar.” 

The old deaf man reached out, and the three characters “Zha Zha Tian” seemed to disassemble, each stroke separating from the stone tablet, and the sword light gathered together like streams merging into a river. The old deaf man led Chen Ping’an, wading through the water; when they reached the end of it, there was another world inside. 

*(End of Chapter)*

 **Chapter 787: Add Layers Against the Cold (Part 2)**

Chen Pingan's surroundings shifted abruptly; the ground was littered with corpses, a scene of tragic devastation. Some of the bones were pale and enormous, stretching like a mountain range, while others gleamed golden, remnants of divine beings.

It appeared to be an ancient battlefield where gods and demons had fought fiercely in the distant past.

There was a large pit, carved with stairs.

The higher-ranking demons were imprisoned at the top.

As he descended the steps, Chen Pingan suddenly asked, "If it weren't for the Grand Sword Immortal and the Sword Qi Great Wall, how many sword cultivators would you have killed, senior?"

Old Hearing-Impaired Child did not hide his smile. "Everyone in sight would be dead."

He then added, "Not because I'm angry at those little brats' backbiting. It's not worth it."

Turning to Chen Pingan, he asked, "What about you, senior?"

Chen Pingan replied, "Anyone older than me, with a higher cultivation level, and without any grudges against me, counts as a senior."

Old Hearing-Impaired Child nodded. "Good habit."

He continued, "According to the Grand Sword Immortal, he wants Lord Hidden Official to act on my behalf."

Chen Pingan nodded in agreement. He had already figured it out on the way here.

The stairs continued to twist and turn as he went down. Chen Pingan's vision became blurred; all he could see was the staircase, with no other scenery in sight. However, upon encountering various cages of different sizes, his vision would clear somewhat. He noticed the cages were lined with solidified sword light as bars. As they passed several empty cages, Old Hearing-Impaired Child stopped and pointed to one. "The one inside has already had its head cut off by the Grand Sword Immortal.
