Lianxin continued discussing the plague god, which was not purely righteous or evil. A natural victim, loathed by gods and demons, suppressed by the Dao, almost everyone’s fate was not in their own hands. They could either be imprisoned by righteous Qi cultivators, isolated from the world, or raised by evil cultivators from a young age to serve as puppets, threatening the imperial court and acting as cash cows. Once thrown onto the battlefield, they wielded immense destructive power, leading to endless future troubles, with epidemics spreading, and the common folk suffering immensely, leaving no life in a hundred years.

There were also the pigeon immortals, adept at taking over nests. Any Qi cultivator could be used by them as a nest, planting their thoughts and seeds in others' hearts without anyone noticing. There were also ferrymen who could traverse between the mortal realm and the underworld, remaining the most secretive. Additionally, there were debt-collecting ghosts, targeting the foolish in rural areas, capable of shifting karmic burdens onto enemies while secretly gathering offerings from families or temples.

Finally, there were the mirror sellers, who traveled far and wide, capturing and refining the shadows of ordinary people, arbitrarily binding souls and determining fates, draining fortunes for their own use.

Regarding the mirror sellers, Lianxin shared a dubious tale. There once was a remarkably gifted mirror seller in the history of the Hao Ran realm who attempted to refine the luminous moon into a makeup mirror.

If successful, the entire realm, whether ordinary or cultivators, would have to look up to the "mirror surface," and the consequences would be unimaginable.

After listening to these strange tales of the mountains, Chen Ping'an sighed softly, "Those who attain enlightenment live long lives. As long as they are willing to move around and traverse the world, they will encounter endless wonders and oddities."

Throughout their conversation, Chen Ping'an also witnessed Lianxin's innate artifact, the ten sewing needles held by her yin spirit, each glowing with a delicate multicolored light trailing from the needle's end, precisely targeting the three souls and seven spirits.

Once Lianxin completed her task, her yin spirit returned, and she stood up, saying, "I've roughly calculated it. If you manage to kill all sixty or so demons, I can sew up thirty-two places for you. You're purely a martial artist, so the lines in your palms, the back of your hands, and your fingers will all need extensive work. The face and vital points will focus on the eyes, and the heart will naturally be the main event. I'll thread them together and grind the heart a bit, which might take a while. For the back, the emphasis will be on the spine. After skinning, I’ll need to pull the entire spine out to a height of an inch. These are still manageable. The three souls and seven spirits are crucial, and after sewing and dressing, the real suffering begins. Just to clarify, the five demons will serve as your wedding dress; if your realm isn’t high enough, there will be more unexpected mishaps. Once the three souls and seven spirits are lit, don’t say you can’t punch or even move slightly. If the wick flickers, your heart will be unsettled."

At this point, Lianxin pulled her lips into a slight smile, "But since the Hidden Official mentioned ‘a settled heart’ before, I imagine you shouldn’t be afraid."

Chen Ping'an maintained a blank expression.

Lianxin nodded, "Not very old, but quite bold."

Then, the young Hidden Official took up the sword-raising gourd and took a large swig of liquor.

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 790: A Good Experience

Chen Ping'an and Nianxin arrived at a cage.

Inside sat a middle-aged man, cross-legged, barely breathing, his body emaciated and resembling a skeleton. Yet, he exuded an undeniable force of fist intent, which coiled around him like countless tiny dragons, nesting upon the mountain of his form. He was a genuine Wanderer of the Beyond.

Before Chen Ping'an arrived at the Sword Qi Great Wall, this pure warrior from the wild had killed six sword cultivators, including one Earth Immortal sword cultivator.

The man opened his eyes and asked, "Have you come to kill me?"

Chen Ping'an nodded.

The man glanced at the seamstress behind Chen Ping'an and said calmly, "You brought your own head on a platter."

He recognized he was no match for that hideous woman; her methods were vicious, and she had caused him considerable suffering.

Chen Ping'an said, "Let's have a duel and see who lives or dies."

The man scoffed, "A mere pure warrior from the Sword Qi Great Wall wants to use me as a whetstone? I fear that one punch from me will have you groaning in pain while clutching that woman's waist. Haha, too bad she isn’t much to look at."

Chen Ping'an replied, "Nianxin, close the cage door. Let’s wait until one of us is dead before opening it again."

Nianxin shut the door, and sword lights formed a barrier, enclosing the two warriors.

The man stood up. "Well, that’s straightforward."

Chen Ping'an clasped his fists and introduced himself, "In the name of righteousness, I am Chen Ping'an."

The man was momentarily taken aback but returned the gesture, "From the wild, Jinxi City, I am Hongyin."

One was a Wanderer of the Beyond, the other a bottlenecked Gold Body Realm cultivator; both struck at the same time.

Inside the cage, the force of their fists surged.

In an instant, they exchanged dozens of blows. Chen Ping'an primarily used his fists and feet to counter Hongyin's attacks, defending more than he attacked. Eventually, a kick from Hongyin landed on his waist, causing Chen Ping'an to slide back over ten feet. Yet, he remained firmly rooted to the ground. As Hongyin pushed forward, Chen Ping'an sidestepped, raising a leg to strike Hongyin's abdomen. The force shifted, pinning Hongyin to the ground.

Rather than follow up with an attack, Chen Ping'an retreated two steps, placing one hand behind him and transforming his fist into a palm in front of him.

His fist stance sank slightly, yet the intent behind it gradually rose.

Unharmed, Hongyin pushed himself off the ground and asked, "Are you holding back?"

Chen Ping'an replied, "I know your foundation, but you don’t know mine. So let’s see how you fare against a hundred blows from me. After that, we’ll see."

Hongyin twisted his wrist, the joints in his spine and ribs cracking like a dragon turning over. His fist intent exploded forth, his spirit surging.

Earlier, he had been testing the waters, and now he laughed, "If you truly have confidence, you’d need to be at the Ninth Realm to back it up."

He had only heard of the pure warriors from the Righteous World, limited by their innate physiques, and considered them weak.

Chen Ping'an shook his head. "I am not yet a Wanderer of the Beyond. However, I fought and killed Hou Kuimen on the battlefield, which cost me dearly, and I'm still not fully healed. But to be straightforward, when I face an enemy, whether injured or not, it makes no difference."

As Hongyin moved closer, Chen Ping'an remained still, not even shifting his gaze as Hongyin walked a short arc in front of him.

As a dominant Wanderer of the Beyond, Hongyin had certainly heard of that flamboyant Hou Kuimen, though he had never met him. He had only heard tales of the man, adorned in bright red armor, wearing a purple-golden crown with long feathers, and draped in treasures. Thus, he held little respect for Hou Kuimen. A true warrior should be unencumbered by possessions, relying solely on his fists, like the barefoot, rolled-sleeved young man before him—pure and straightforward.

Hongyin asked, "Is it customary for warriors in the Righteous World to explain themselves before fighting? Is there some strange custom in this?"

Chen Ping'an shook his head. "I just want you to throw your punches with a clear conscience before you die."

After a pause, he continued earnestly, "You haven’t fought in a long time; your skills are rusty, and you’re too concerned about the woman outside the cage. Your fist intent isn’t at its peak. I could easily kill you with a few blows, but what would be the point?"

Hongyin ceased his words.

In a duel between warriors, regardless of the size of the principles, it all came down to the weight of their fists and the height of their techniques.

For the next hundred blows, Hongyin struck fiercely, his momentum like a whale swallowing a rainbow, living up to his name.

A knee strike crashed into Chen Ping'an's chest, sending him sliding back ten steps. He merely assumed a stance without retaliating, his spine like a dragon pulse trembling, absorbing all the force.

Hongyin simultaneously struck hard at Chen Ping'an's shoulder, taking advantage of the young man's slight shift in position to surge forward. He nearly slammed Chen Ping'an against the sword-light barrier.

Yet, the young man’s expression, complexion, and even his fist intent remained eerily calm and unmoving.

Hongyin's last kick struck Chen Ping'an’s neck, flipping him around several times until he caught himself with a hand, head down, feet up, and froze in position.

His eyes were tightly shut, and his left hand formed a sword seal before him.

In the last few punches of their hundred, Hongyin twisted his body, his long arms delivering a crushing blow that sent Chen Ping'an flying. The young man’s energy plummeted as he used his fingers to touch the ground, flipping repeatedly to avoid the barrage of punches from Hongyin, finally standing in a straight line between Hongyin and Nianxin.

The sparring session came to an end; it wasn't that Hongyin didn’t want to determine their lives in an instant, but his warrior instincts warned him against carelessly approaching Chen Ping'an again.

He stopped in his tracks, quite surprised, while Nianxin looked on curiously.

As a half-wild cultivator from Gold Armor Continent, Nianxin had traveled for hundreds of years and was quite familiar with pure warriors from the Righteous World. Even among Ninth Realm warriors, there had been a rapid and intense clash. 

When did a young man in his thirties acquire such a masterful demeanor? The Wanderers of the Beyond and mountain-top masters she had seen before all exuded overwhelming presence, even when their divine radiance was restrained. Once they unleashed their fists, they embodied a heroic spirit that could shake mountains and shatter the earth; none had the calm and composure of this young man.

As the two continued their spar, Nianxin noticed some peculiarities; Chen Ping'an’s choices seemed increasingly odd, as if he had changed his mind.

Hongyin was fighting with great gusto, while Chen Ping'an remained restrained, mostly focusing on defense rather than evasion.

After about half a stick of incense had burned, Hongyin suddenly withdrew his fists, puzzled. "I've already exchanged two full breaths of true warrior's energy, yet you’ve only used one breath to counter?"

Chen Ping'an wiped the blood from the corner of his mouth with his thumb, answering evasively, "I'll come back in a few days for another spar."

Hongyin shook his head and took a deep breath, speaking seriously, "It’s one thing to look down on Jinxi City’s Hongyin, but if a warrior’s skills are lacking, that’s understandable. Yet, do you, Chen Ping'an, think you can look down on warriors?!"

Chen Ping'an fell silent for a moment before nodding. "You have reason, senior."

Finally, he allowed a pulse of pure true energy to flow through him. On the surface, his stance appeared relaxed, like a monkey, but internally, it was like a great dragon bracing itself, directly adopting a divine drum-like stance.

As he faced death, Hongyin's expression changed, akin to a fish caught on a hook, suddenly freed.

As was customary, Nianxin collected the corpse.

However, this time, Chen Ping'an did not observe; instead, he sat outside the cage, taking a sip of wine.

Having long mastered various sewing techniques, Nianxin seemed to have time to spare, asking, "How did you cultivate this fist technique?"

Chen Ping'an, with his back to the cage, slowly replied, "The one who taught me the fist technique didn't like to discuss fist theory, only imparted a few words, one of which I have never forgotten: 'My fists reach the heavens, and before me, there is no one.'"

Nianxin nodded, "That warrior has quite the spirit."

After that, Chen Ping'an moved on to the next cell, where a demon clan member was held—a bottlenecked Gold Dan sword cultivator.

This sword cultivator hailed from a sword sect known as the Ascendant Sect.

In the wild, sword sects were few and far between, unlike in the Righteous World. It wasn’t just any Fifth Realm sword immortal who could establish a sect in the wild. Even if a sect’s banner could be raised, it would not withstand the harsh reality. Great demons roamed freely, mercilessly; they particularly despised sword sects, and while they might spare human lives, they would wreak havoc on the natural formations, leaving no one unscathed.

Thus, every sword sect in the wild that managed to survive its first hundred years became a formidable power.

According to secret records from the Summer Palace, the Ascendant Sect had once harbored a sword immortal from the Sword Qi Great Wall. When this was later discovered, a massacre ensued. The Ascendant Sect employed various sinister methods to imprison the sword immortal's spirit, forcibly extracting sword techniques from him. Ultimately, the sword immortal was refined into a puppet with diminished intelligence, bound to obey others. He had appeared during a siege and was slain by the chief offering of the Yan family, Li Tui, thus gaining liberation.

Upon entering this cage, after Nianxin opened the door, Chen Ping'an introduced himself and simply uttered the words "Ask for the sword," before summoning the caged sparrow.

Unexpectedly, the Gold Dan bottleneck sword cultivator immediately knelt, fervently vowing loyalty to Chen Ping'an in exchange for his life.

Seeing the young man remain unmoved, this sword cultivator grew even more resolute, offering to sacrifice his foundational path by severing his life-bound flying sword to gift it to Chen Ping'an, hoping to prolong his existence in this cage.

This direct descendant of the Ascendant Sect’s ancestral hall was unpredictable in battle, wielding his life-bound flying sword, "Celestial Melody," which possessed two unique abilities. Wherever the flying sword passed, there was no sword to see, only the delicate sound of buzzing wings. If this sound reached a person’s ear, it would resonate violently within their meridians, carrying a tremendous killing force. Furthermore, the thunderous sound of the flying sword inherently contained the true essence of the Five Thunders, making it exceedingly difficult for enemies to defend against. Upon realizing the presence of the flying sword, one had to discern its location by sound, but once the sound was heard, the sword would swiftly pierce the sword cultivator’s body.

The moment the sword intent moved, the minuscule universe within his body would erupt with wind, thunder, clouds, and rain.

It was precisely because this demon sword cultivator’s flying sword was so aberrant that it had been specifically targeted by two sword immortals from the Sword Qi Great Wall, leading to its imprisonment.

After acquiring the "Celestial Melody," Chen Ping'an stored it away and inquired about the Ascendant Sect's sword techniques, finding some records in the Summer Palace. He asked a few additional questions to fill in the gaps.

Chen Ping'an exchanged a knowing glance with Nianxin, who immediately understood and stepped into the cell.

At the same time, a small but exquisite Yin God emerged, holding ten shimmering “embroidery needles.”

Realizing his imminent demise, the sword cultivator cursed and spat at Chen Ping'an.

Nianxin felt satisfied; earlier, Hongyin’s death had been too fulfilling, leaving the young Hidden Official with too little resentment, which was not a good thing.

Nianxin's sewing methods not only involved the three souls and seven spirits but could also gather grievances.

Chen Ping'an stood at the entrance, taking another sip of wine, savoring it sparingly. He thought he shouldn’t wait until he truly faced hardship before he could no longer drink.

Nianxin toyed with the sword cultivator’s Gold Dan and casually remarked, "One must pursue their responsibilities while in their position; it’s impossible for everything to go smoothly."

Chen Ping'an shook his head. "I’ve long come to terms with this. Killing demons at the Sword Qi Great Wall doesn’t require justification. Whether one is a Hidden Official or not, it’s all the same. The discomfort comes from my own low realm; facing any of those king-level demons now would mean death. Not to mention, confronting a Yuan Ying sword cultivator would be extremely taxing. Facing a sword immortal, I would undoubtedly perish. Becoming a sword immortal is incredibly difficult."

Nianxin laughed, "You’re a Fifth Realm sword cultivator at such a young age; I don’t see that as too difficult."

Chen Ping'an was left speechless.

It was rare for the seamstress to make a joke, and it felt quite chilling.

Earlier, the old deaf man had asked for three portions of blood essence from the mud eel spirit. Now, the young Hidden Official was conducting business that seemed unearthly.

The old deaf man had also obtained a few pounds of blood and flesh from the younger generation of the Yalu River, after all, he had taken in a so-called master boy, who, by the looks of it, was someone who could cook. With a good jug of wine and a pot of the young Hidden Official’s so-called mud eel tofu stew, it truly felt like a heavenly life.

As for the title of the honest young master, would the old deaf man take it seriously? Did he truly think he was a transcendent being who ascended after devoting himself to Buddhism?

The great sword immortal acted this way, merely providing a chance for the melancholy figure, at most just a protective charm. As long as the young man couldn’t seize the opportunity, the deadline of a hundred years would be the pinnacle of clarity regarding life and death. If it were that clever Du Shanyin, the old deaf man could already contemplate how to handle matters a century later, which is to say, the foolish would have their fortunes, and the melancholy child was simply too naive; the old deaf man felt embarrassed to take action since it lacked any interest.

And as for the melancholy boy, he didn’t take the master-servant relationship seriously; it was merely the young man’s true path to survival.

Thus, reading more books was indeed a good thing. As the young Hidden Official had said, one should never underestimate a transcendent being.

The melancholy boy was grabbed by the old deaf man and led out of the suffocating dungeon, winding past several demon corpses and broken divine beings, toward a place that brought peace to the young man’s heart. The gentle stream flowed, and in front of a thatched cottage by the creek, a massive grape trellis was built, lush and verdant, covering an expanse of land, where one could walk among the greenery, their attire turning azure in the shade.

With every breath the melancholy boy took, he felt a refreshing sensation, as if both the spiritual and sword energies had been refined, enabling one to bypass the Qi refining stage. The more this was the case, the more the reserved young man dared not breathe deeply. After all, he was a guest visiting.

The old deaf man smiled, "Just breathe and direct your energy; it won’t hurt your spiritual energy. A small fish swimming in the river can still drink the water without drying it up."

The old deaf man paused. "The master hasn’t returned yet; let’s wait a moment."

The melancholy boy nodded vigorously, feeling quite nervous.

This was because the elder had mentioned the identity of that sword immortal, the Executioner.

An ancient position in the history of the Sword Qi Great Wall that had disappeared for many years, on par with the Hidden Officials.

The old deaf man didn’t elaborate, only mentioning that the Executioner sword immortal felt guilty and believed he had no face to show others.

In another direction, the two walked slowly along the creek. It was indeed the sword immortal, whose face was obscured, walking alongside the young Du Shanyin.

Du Shanyin had several small bags woven from silver threads tied around his waist, gleaming like gold, radiant as the morning sun.

The old deaf man chuckled, "No wonder."

In this realm, the corpses of great demons and deities lay in an unseen river of time, their bones gradually decaying, eroding, and peeling away. However, those divine golden bodies occasionally yielded surprises, such as heaps of golden sand or fragments of their golden bodies. The young Hidden Official had been particularly unfortunate in his explorations, finding nothing, while the young Du Shanyin, accompanied by the sword immortal, returned laden with treasures.

The sword immortal certainly wouldn’t actively seek to destroy the divine corpses, merely waiting for treasures to fall from the sky, then bending down to pick them up.

It was likely that this journey with Du Shanyin was to observe the young man’s fortune.

By the creek, a woman was beating cloth on a blue stone slab, and when Du Shanyin called out, she suddenly looked up, her beauty radiant and captivating.

Du Shanyin was momentarily entranced, while a young maid holding a bamboo basket stood beside the woman, her bright eyes sparkling. Seeing the young man in a daze, she couldn’t help but laugh even harder.

The sword immortal Executioner and the old deaf man nodded at each other.

Only then did the old deaf man lead the melancholy boy toward the grape trellis.

Under the trellis, cups of exquisite porcelain hung at various heights, seemingly awaiting the grapes to fall into them.

The twelve-colored flower god wine cups depicted twelve graceful women and inscribed with twelve corresponding poems.

The old deaf man said, "In the Righteous World, aside from the flower god women, there are actually twelve flower god men, all favored and celebrated by the blessed lands of flowers. Many are immortals and literary masters who, through fortuitous encounters, were inspired to write historically renowned poems for various flowers. A Liang once let slip that the birth of these ancient masterpieces wasn't just a stroke of genius; it also involved the flower god maidens’ influence—many enchanting nights spent under the flowers and moon, which can make one envious."

The young melancholy boy felt as if he were listening to a celestial tale.

Over at the Sword Qi Great Wall, the old deaf man occasionally ventured to the city’s battlements, feigning deafness and silence, only occasionally conversing with A Liang.

In reality, just by observing the inscriptions on the Zha Zha Tian stele, along with the old deaf man’s discussions with Chen Ping'an, it was clear that this ascended demon possessed profound knowledge.

A small white-haired boy, carrying a skeletal frame as white as jade, dashed across the creek bank.

The bones clattered against the ground.

Clearly, it was an immortal's lost husk, though it was uncertain where it had been unearthed.

The Executioner, shrouded in clouds, turned to glance at the external celestial demon.

The white-haired boy immediately halted, standing across the creek, grinning widely. "This is just a small gift for the two esteemed sons of heaven, a congratulatory gesture. Today I’ll deliver one, and tomorrow I’ll bring another."

The old deaf man chuckled.

The sword immortal remained silent.

The white-haired boy said earnestly, "I swear, as the grandson of the Hidden Official and the elder's grandson! I only wish to take a peek into your hearts and minds; if I make any sneaky moves, I’ll be struck by the heavens with five bolts of lightning."

He added with a tone of grievance, "I just want to see a few sights; it’s been so long since I’ve seen the wild world and the Sword Qi Great Wall."

The celestial demon turned to the two young men. "My surname is Wu, with 'Tian' as my character, and 'Die' as my name, meaning incessant chatter. This elder has no airs; you can just call me by my full name."

Both the old deaf man and the Executioner did not underestimate this celestial demon.

He was indeed an extremely bothersome neighbor.

The white-haired boy seemed intent on lingering, but the sword light flashed.

The white-haired boy dropped the skeletal frame and fled. Each time he coalesced into human form, the sword light would shatter him, and after dozens of times, he had to run over ten miles before the sword light ceased pursuing him.

Suspended in the wind, he felt deeply sorrowful.

Because a sword light, barely a foot long, hovered not far away.

This was the Executioner’s flying sword technique; if the sword immortal wished, the sword light could pursue the celestial demon for many years.

The white-haired boy raised his hands, "Alright, I’ll head home. I won’t bother you, I’m just going to find the Hidden Official."

He departed in a flash, appearing on the steps of the prison.

The sword light did not follow.

The "child" adorned with a green snake and a short sword walked slowly, failing to enter the hearts of the two young men, which left him greatly disappointed.

He viewed the memories of others as if reading through a book; the hazy memories were like rough sketches. The shallower the memory, the blurrier the image, while deeply ingrained memories were vividly colored, resembling real-life entities.

The celestial demon’s methods didn’t stop there; he also had a technique to manipulate memories. The higher a cultivator’s realm, the greater the celestial demon’s power, allowing him to freely alter and paint over the cherished images stored in one’s heart. He could make people forget certain things or suddenly remember others.

The lord of Bai Di City was feared by the mountain-top cultivators of the Righteous World precisely because he was proficient in this art.

However, that city lord had many more unreasonable methods. This celestial demon also longed to visit the Central Divine Continent to meet the city lord and discuss techniques.

But here in the cage, he could not escape.

Time to find some fun.

After all, Chen Qing had already promised him that as long as he didn’t directly attack that young man, he could borrow his power, and after testing him, he would still have two chances.

The white-haired boy had chosen two targets: a fox charm with mediocre charm skills and a lower Fifth Realm demon cultivator who was undoubtedly doomed.

The Hidden Official, after all, was a man, and by his attire, he also seemed to be a scholar.

Among life’s many desires, the most entangled was that of love, common to both men and women. Everyone had their obsessions, but the most binding was moral obligation, akin to chains, indistinguishable between gods and mortals.

That fox charm came from a den of foxes in the wild, but sadly had only seven tails and shallow cultivation.

The white-haired boy entered the cell holding the fox charm, and before she could sense anything unusual, he had already entered her heart's lake, freely flipping through her memories.

Moments later, he swaggered out of the fox charm’s body, only using an illusion technique. Shaking his head, he lamented, "How dreadful. No wonder that young man was unaffected."

The fox charm remained oblivious.

The white-haired boy muttered to himself, "Next time I see that Chen Ping'an, you should restore your true appearance, barefaced and tidy."

"I’ll help you craft a heart-wrenching, sincere story. For instance, you came to the Sword Qi Great Wall to meet a certain lover."

"Then I’ll gift you an additional technique, using the enchanting corpse method to cultivate the vibrant refinement technique, and secretly create a charming tent, giving you a fighting chance. You can only blame that boy for being too composed and his state of mind too peculiar."

No matter the material, the final form of the enchanting corpse’s life-bound object, whether it be a red veil, a bed, or a handkerchief, was referred to as a charming tent, also known as the land of tenderness.

The celestial demon casually occupied the heart of a seven-tailed fox charm and began to draw.

Suddenly, he burst into laughter.

In the realm of cultivation, did one’s fate truly belong to oneself?

Wasn’t that a bit too high an estimation of oneself?

After a fierce battle with a non-sword cultivator in the Yuan Ying realm, Chen Ping'an lay on the ground, gasping for breath, blood soaking his clothes.

Nianxin tossed him a porcelain vial, then busied herself nearby, saying, "Haste makes waste; starting from the Gold Dan is the right approach."

Chen Ping'an replied, "I need to find a place to settle down here, one that allows for quiet cultivation."

Nianxin said, "Then you should seek that celestial demon; he excels at turning the unreal into the real."

Chen Ping'an nodded. "If I can’t avoid it, I won’t run."

Nianxin continued to tidy up, saying, "We’ll start working soon. I’ll share some insights on the sewing techniques so you can be mentally prepared and avoid unnecessary hardships."

Chen Ping'an immediately sat up.

Nianxin explained, "The first task is to start from sculpting the eyeball. However, that sounds quite unpleasant, so let me tell you something lighter first."

Chen Ping'an couldn’t help but smile bitterly but nodded anyway.

Nianxin slowly spoke, "According to the seamstress's rules, the human body is divided into three channels: mountains, water, and air. The bones represent the mountains, the blood represents the water, and the spirit energy merges with the soul to represent the air."

Chen Ping'an spoke solemnly, "I ask Senior Nianxin to elaborate in detail; the more meticulous and detailed, the better."

Being able to corroborate with Senior Li Er would greatly benefit his martial path.

The minutiae of the human body were filled with obstacles, much like a vast geographical map.

Nianxin recounted the details, speaking at length, then raised a hand, spreading her palm. The skin grew rapidly, soon resembling that of an ordinary person. "For example, the five fingers represent the mountains, and the lines on the palm represent water, intertwining and merging, forming the pattern of mountains and rivers. If you only look at the palm lines, they can also represent the entire universe within a hand, following its channels, the five organs and six intestines are clear at a glance. Otherwise, how could a practitioner perceive the mountains and rivers?"

Before Chen Ping'an could inquire about the techniques related to controlling mountains and rivers, a technique he had long desired, Nianxin shifted the topic. She had already raised her palm, fingers spread wide. "You can sew the true form of the Five Mountains, draw the Five Thunders’ orthodox cloud seals, write yellow talismans, refine the five elements, or compose divine decrees. Just with my fingers, I specialize in six different techniques. It is said that our seamstress ancestor was extraordinarily gifted, unmatched by anyone, and through the layered array techniques, fused various secret arts into one, turning clouds with a flip of the hand and controlling storms. Once, while facing the Dragon Tiger Mountain, just by using one palm, the power of the Five Thunders could darken the heavens."

Chen Ping'an tentatively said, "I once saw in a literary text that someone tattooed a few hundred verses from a great poet on their body. Isn’t that related to the seamstresses' techniques?"

Nianxin fell silent for a moment before replying, "That’s a sign of madness."

Chen Ping'an could only nod in agreement. "Indeed, I thought the same back then."

Nianxin continued to elaborate on various secret arts of the seamstresses.

Chen Ping'an took out the Sword Nourishing Gourd but did not drink.

Nianxin casually asked, "Why do men often enjoy drinking? Especially for cultivators, drinking can be detrimental to their progress."

"In the Sword Qi Great Wall, unlike our Righteous World, even if one breaks through, it doesn’t guarantee a long life. There are several Earth Immortal sword cultivators who sit by the roadside, drinking and eating pickled vegetables."

Such scenes would not exist in heaven and earth again.

Chen Ping'an hesitated, thinking of her in his heart, then smiled and said, "Women are like wine; there’s no need to drink."

Chen Ping'an leaned back, forgetting who had said it. When a young man likes a young woman, it is like tasting sweet rice wine; the flavor is not strong, but the first sip can indeed intoxicate. As he matures, a man liking a woman is akin to drinking strong liquor; a moment's carelessness can lead to heartbreak. In old age, a man reminiscing about a woman is like warming a pot of yellow wine in the dead of winter.

Nianxin turned her head and teased, "In the future, avoid saying such things to women."

Chen Ping'an laughed, "Then I’ll change my ways."

After all, aside from Ning Yao, there were no romantic words to speak.

Chen Ping'an closed his eyes. He knew that the sewing process in the prison could not be rushed, yet he ultimately wished to leave early.

At this moment, the celestial demon was locking eyes with a lower Fifth Realm demon cultivator.

Meanwhile, a great battle loomed at the Sword Qi Great Wall.

The sun shone brightly upon the city walls.

The old priest gently patted the enormous cloud sea beneath him, which resembled the world’s largest mat, while waving at the suspended sun. "My merits are not yet complete, and my pockets are shallow. Truly, I am a poor priest, and all I can do is borrow some light."

The vast cloud sea scattered before coalescing into numerous golden divine beings, which the old priest swept down onto the battlefield with a wave of his sleeve.

In the line of confrontation, massive demon beasts revealed their true forms, crashing against the golden divine beings.

A monk clad in robes shook his shoulders, shedding a body of transformed lion insects that had become Buddhist scriptures.

The Confucian sage sat upright, the sun shining perfectly, suitable for reading.

The title of his book bore a life-bound word, establishing the doctrine and revolving around that life-bound word.

The attacking demons from the wild were countless.

On this day, Chen Ping'an sat cross-legged outside a prison.

Nianxin stood with her hands behind her, gazing into Chen Ping'an's eyes.

Her Yin God was carefully sculpting the young man's eyeball with embroidery needles.

This had already lasted for a tea's worth of time, causing small beads of blood to accumulate and trickle from the corners of his eyes.

Nianxin observed the mental state of the young man and casually remarked, "If you can’t withstand this trial, you might as well give up on sewing. Don’t close your eyes; if even a slight movement of the eyeball occurs, all your previous efforts will be in vain. You should weigh the consequences."

As long as he could endure, the seamstress possessed mysterious means to heal.

Moments later, Nianxin expressed mild surprise, saying, "Not bad; it seems we can do two things at once. The eyeball will be handled with the most basic techniques—yellow application and finishing—slowly inserting the needle, primarily inscribing clouds and seals. The inscriptions will be the shallowest. However, your spine will not be so easy; primarily, the knife techniques will be applied to your spine's joints, using the Nine Layer Seal, Bird Insect Seal, and Dripping Seal, each inscribed on your spine's joints. These are the techniques for peeling clothes, and more importantly, the techniques for wearing clothes. It’s still too early for that. If you think you can’t hold on, or if you believe you can wait a bit longer, now is the time to speak up and let me know."

Chen Ping'an remained silent.

Nianxin approached Chen Ping'an from behind, her hands shaped like knives, slowly slicing through the green shirt and skin, pulling out a portion of his spine with extreme caution.

The girl curved her fingers, gently tapping, listening intently, and expressed regret, "You made me miscalculate; there are so many hidden injuries? Why didn’t any of this show up before?"

Nianxin casually returned the spine to its original position, her tone somewhat reproachful. "Let’s not apply any medicine for now; you need to adapt to this pain. Aren’t you able to endure it? Just take it well."

Chen Ping'an could only remain silent, struggling to maintain a state of intense focus and the "dead water state" with his soul, otherwise, he would have wanted to twist this woman's head off.

Inside the prison, a structure resembling a square space had suddenly appeared a few days ago, with only four pillars and no other coverings.

It resembled a small pavilion commonly found on earthly roads, yet not entirely.

Chen Ping'an walked barefoot inside, gradually slowing his pace.

Within, his vision was open, though he could see no scenery.

The white-haired boy of the green snake hung outside the structure, asking, "What’s wrong with you?"

Chen Ping'an continued walking, countering, "What do you mean?"

The white-haired boy shouted, "How can a cultivator’s mental state be so fragmented, like a battlefield?! It’s making things difficult for me at every turn…"

Chen Ping'an slowly punched the air, smiling and saying, "Where clarity exists, there are laws; where obscurity rests, there are spirits. Both clarity and obscurity are muddled, but conscience still exists in the heart. In the vast heavens and earth, the sun and moon shine brightly. What’s so strange about it?"

Nianxin stood at a distance, on the staircase, reminding him, "Let’s begin."

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 791: Bearing the True Name

On the Upside-Down Mountain, the entire Plum Blossom Garden had vanished into thin air, turning into a tale of divine mystery that people spoke of with great interest. Then, one day, a large group of sword cultivators arrived from the Ape Ruler Manor, led by two sword immortals: the sociable Sun Juyuan and Mi Hu, who was rumored to have already reached the divine realm. They arrived on foot, but left in a flurry of carriages and boats, causing quite a stir both in the sky and on the ground. Yet, despite the sword cultivators’ grand display, the locals of the Upside-Down Mountain pretended not to notice, and the traveling outsiders dared not approach.

If they were separated from the Sword Qi Great Wall by thousands of mountains and rivers, which sword immortal would not dare to curse? But once they were up close with the sword cultivators, what could they do? They could only remain silent.

Only one wandering immortal, a register master who had traveled far, did not believe in omens. He secretly used his power to observe the mountains and rivers, and what he saw in the Ape Ruler Manor was a terrifying scene: pavilions and towers had been demolished beyond recognition. This old Nascent Soul cultivator from the White Cloud Continent sensed danger and was about to retract his palm and withdraw his divine power when a brilliant sword light suddenly appeared from the darkness, piercing through his palm. The sword light flashed again, stabbing through his left cheek and exiting through the right, vanishing as quickly as it had come, the flying sword returning to the Ape Ruler Manor.

In pain, the old cultivator understood: his eyes should not see, and his mouth should not speak.

Having suffered such a heavy loss without a voice, it was only natural for him to harbor resentment against the sword immortal’s tyrannical actions. In his homeland, how could a dignified Nascent Soul suffer such humiliation?!

The sword cultivators had emptied the Liu family's Ape Ruler Manor in the White Cloud Continent and returned to the Sword Qi Great Wall that very night. Meanwhile, the bustling Mirage City, a trade hub of the Sword Qi Great Wall, gradually fell into decline over the following months. Shops were continuously relocating, gradually moving to the Upside-Down Mountain. If one had no ancestral place to settle in the Upside-Down Mountain, they could only return to their respective sects across the vast world, since land there was incredibly valuable. Moreover, with the Sword Qi Great Wall now serving as a boundary, everything to the south was a forbidden area, having long since been sealed off by a grand mountain and water formation, obscured from view. Thus, the towering city of the Sword Qi Great Wall was no longer a place to explore, making business on the Upside-Down Mountain increasingly bleak. Now, ferries traveling between the Upside-Down Mountain and the eight continents saw very few visitors; they were carrying more cargo than passengers. Consequently, many intercontinental ferries were now heavily loaded, like the ferry from Old Dragon City to Osmanthus Island, which had completely submerged its original dock under water. Many ferries that used to swiftly traverse clouds and rain had also slowed down considerably.

The war was intense, and the situation was perilous. This siege by the barbaric world was unusual, and the Upside-Down Mountain was keenly aware of this. However, historically, the Sword Qi Great Wall had entered closed-door cultivation more than once or twice; it wasn't enough to incite widespread panic. Many register masters had previously sold their property and shops at low prices during the great closures of the Sword Qi Great Wall, only to regret their decisions deeply afterward.

Among the four private residences on the Upside-Down Mountain was the Water Spirit Palace, presided over by a female cultivator of the Jade Purity realm named Yun Qian. She was one of the founders of the Rain Dragon Sect. One of her most favored disciples had taken a liking to a down-and-out wild cultivator named Fu Ke, who, due to a fortuitous encounter, was rapidly breaking through and became a remarkable figure in the Rain Dragon Sect's history of talented individuals.

Yun Qian was concerned not only for the future of her own sect but also for the war involving the Sword Qi Great Wall. After all, the Water Spirit Palace was unlike the Spring Banner Studio or the Plum Blossom Garden; it had not been refined and could not be relocated. It was also not like the Liu family’s Ape Ruler Manor, a treasure worth its weight in gold, which was merely optional to possess.

Yet now, the Sword Qi Great Wall was on high alert, especially with the current authorities belonging to the Hidden Officials faction, known for their meticulous and ruthless methods. Any cultivator who broke the rules, whether intentionally or not, was doomed to face dire consequences. Several individuals had previously sought out the Water Spirit Palace, all of whom had some connection to the Rain Dragon Sect. Two were Nascent Soul cultivators, and one was an old immortal from the Talisman Sect at the Jade Purity realm, all hoping that she could help mediate a bit with the Celestial Lord of the Upside-Down Mountain or plead for leniency from a sword immortal familiar with her. However, the Celestial Lord had long entered closed-door cultivation. Yun Qian attempted to visit a secluded peak to find the old immortal who had refined the dragon to forge a dust-raising immortal weapon, but she was met with a cold reception. When she tried to send a message to the sword immortal Sun Juyuan, with whom she had maintained good relations over the years, that letter disappeared without a trace, as if Sun Juyuan had never received it.

Feeling unsettled in the Water Spirit Palace, Yun Qian could no longer focus on her cultivation. She hurried to the Rain Dragon Sect's Ancestor Hall to convene a meeting and proposed relocating the sect, only to be met with ridicule. Although Yun Qian had prepared for this, understanding that it was no easy matter and perhaps quite far-fetched, seeing the Ancestor Hall members shift their conversation to various business dealings made her feel disheartened.

As the sword cultivators departed from the Ape Ruler Manor, a message-carrying flying sword from the Spring Banner Studio quietly arrived at the Water Spirit Palace.

Upon opening the secret letter, Yun Qian found only two words written on the paper.

**Northward Migration.**

The letter bore the signature of the sword immortal Sun Juyuan, which she recognized very well. It also featured two ancient seal characters, "Hidden Officials." Yun Qian had heard of them for a long time but was seeing them for the first time. 

With "Hidden Officials" inscribed above and the sword immortal's signature below, it adhered to the proper protocols. It should not be a forgery.

Yun Qian did not dare to linger and quietly left the Upside-Down Mountain, hastening back to the Rain Dragon Sect, where she was only able to find her senior sister, the sect leader. To her surprise, her senior sister casually tossed aside the letter, scoffing, "What? After dismantling the Ape Ruler Manor, you want to tear down the Water Spirit Palace too? The young Hidden Official is certainly calculating well. Yun Qian, do you believe if you go to the Spring Banner Studio, where Shao Yunyan is now a trusted confidant of the Hidden Official, he’ll discuss the Water Spirit Palace with you?"

Yun Qian was skeptical but did not forget to carefully tuck the letter away in her sleeve.

Seeing her actions, the sect leader grew even more furious and emphasized, "Now, our Rain Dragon Sect's ancestral estate has not come easily; you and I both know the hardships involved. Yun Qian, neither of us has made any achievements in expanding our territory. Now, are we unable even to hold onto what we have? Have you forgotten why you were demoted to the Water Spirit Palace? Those Nascent Soul worshippers dare to point fingers at you, not because you angered everyone in the Ancestor Hall, but because you couldn't even handle that small Luohua Island. If you lose the Water Spirit Palace now, how will you face the ancestors of the Rain Dragon Sect? Do you know what everyone says behind your back? A woman's kindness! A Jade Purity realm immortal, do you think this is acceptable?"

The sect leader did not want to demean her junior sister too much, knowing that the Water Spirit Palace needed Yun Qian's leadership. If Yun Qian were to get angry and randomly concoct an excuse to venture out to visit immortals or travel to Tongye Continent for leisure, the sect leader would not be able to stop her. Thus, she softened her tone, saying, "And don't forget, we made a deal with the founding ancestor of the Water Cave in the Fuyun Continent. That old account has been recorded by the Sword Qi Great Wall. The new Hidden Official holds great power, and what about that vast Water Cave in the Fuyun Continent? Is the Ancestor Hall still intact? Yun Qian, are you trying to lead our Rain Dragon Sect to follow in their footsteps? This Hidden Official has a hidden agenda and is not to be underestimated, especially skilled at using influence to pressure others."

Yun Qian nodded lightly in acknowledgment.

The sect leader pressed her point further, "Yun Qian, I’ll say this just once more: the Sword Qi Great Wall has a grudge against our Rain Dragon Sect. Does the new Hidden Official have any old ties with you? Why would he plan an escape route for our sect? Is it really about repaying kindness with kindness? Yun Qian, I’ve said all I can; think carefully!"

Yun Qian left the Rain Dragon Sect in silence and returned to the Water Spirit Palace. She had indeed taken her senior sister's words to heart. The intrigue among the register masters on the mountain left her feeling apprehensive. Throughout her journey in cultivation, she had suffered greatly from such betrayal, having faced three major calamities in her life. Aside from a natural disaster, the rest were man-made, all stemming from those around her. Yet, she remained unconvinced and visited the Spring Banner Studio. The sword immortal Shao Yunyan seemed to have anticipated her visit and handed her another secret letter, stating that the Hidden Official had reviewed the Rain Dragon Sect's records and greatly admired her kindness.

Yun Qian furrowed her brow. Shao Yunyan smiled and added that the Hidden Official did not expect her to believe his suggestion, but he urged her to read the letter and then dispose of it. Otherwise, it could lead to unforeseen complications, which would not be good for either the Hidden Official or Yun Qian herself.

Upon returning to the Water Spirit Palace, Yun Qian spent a sleepless night contemplating the detailed content of the letter. At the end of the letter were eight words: "Sect divided north and south, firewood in Qing Mountain."

Meanwhile, at the Spring Banner Studio, after Yun Qian left, Mi Yu and Nalan Caihuan appeared simultaneously. Mi Yu asked with a smile, "Brother Shao, do you think Yun Qian will really migrate north? If she has the courage and means, how many disciples from the Rain Dragon Sect could she save?"

Shao Yunyan replied, "In sects with the word 'sect' in their name, people are often grouped together. Yun Qian has become accustomed to business dealings in the Rain Dragon Sect and is not very popular, so even if she is willing to relocate, she wouldn’t take many people with her."

Mi Yu remarked, "What Yun Qian can't take, she shouldn’t need to take at all."

Nalan Caihuan's expression soured. "How dare you speak of Yun Qian's kindness! Do you believe that if Yun Qian really migrates north and the Rain Dragon Sect splits, the southern immortals who escape will not harbor resentment towards the Sword Qi Great Wall for their indifference? Especially our kind-hearted Hidden Official! If Yun Qian accidentally reveals the contents of the two letters, she could provoke enmity."

Shao Yunyan nodded, "So, asking Yun Qian to destroy the letter is likely because he is aware of this fickleness in human nature. I believe Yun Qian, when focused on her cultivation, should be able to recognize the implications of these gains and losses."

Mi Yu chuckled, "But what if Yun Qian doesn’t realize? Will our Hidden Official care about that?"

Shao Yunyan sighed, "It seems that the Rain Dragon Sect, which believes that everything in the world is simply a transaction, has not only one or two individuals in the Ancestor Hall harboring thoughts of becoming a dragon’s aide, still thinking it’s merely a business deal."

Nalan Caihuan snorted coldly, "Without the wisdom of the Hidden Official, who dares to speak of business under such circumstances?!"

Realizing her slip of the tongue, the woman left in haste to continue her calculations.

Shao Yunyan and Mi Yu exchanged smiles.

At the ferry dock on the Upside-Down Mountain, a cross-continental ferry from North Julu Continent had just arrived with sixty-two sword cultivators, who were taciturn and headed straight for the gate, making their way to the Sword Qi Great Wall.

In a seemingly floating pavilion, Chen Ping'an sat cross-legged on the floor, supporting his fists on his knees, breathing deeply. The object he was sitting on was the bamboo mat he had picked up from the Plum Blossom Garden. It not only helped cultivators focus and calm their minds but also had remarkable uses, allowing Chen Ping'an to refine the abundant green water pearls more quickly. Additionally, perhaps due to the bamboo mat’s material, in addition to benefiting the Water Mansion, the wooden residence was also significantly aided. The water pearls he refined, with excess water spiritual energy, could be drawn toward the wooden residence's Qi Mansion, a continuous flow of water energy that nourished his internal organs.

In the mountain, while such immortal artifacts might not be of high grade, they were indispensable. Little by little, over the course of a few years, the results might not be immediately apparent, but once one dedicated themselves to cultivation, spending decades or even centuries in the mountains, the transformation would be monumental. Thus, the register masters of the large sects, as Lu Tai mentioned, must possess a similar life-enhancing item. If the immortal’s resources were sufficient, they would seek, beyond their life-enhancing items, something that would ensure a long-lasting future, like building a skyscraper from the ground up.

Depending on different times, different immortal caves, and corresponding cultivation realms, one must constantly switch items, as there were many details to consider.

A foreign celestial demon drifted around the building without uttering a word, seemingly more worthy of investigation than the young sword immortal obscured by clouds.

The young Hidden Official had just returned from a secret realm; otherwise, he would not be so relaxed. Previously, he had been dragged by that thorny entity to a place where the remains of an ancient deity were refined into a realm. Located in the heart of that area was a forbidden zone where the old deaf man, the foreign celestial demon, and the seamstress could not enter. There was a small door symbolically locked, and only the old deaf man could extract the key and pass through, allowing the thorny entity to cast the young Hidden Official inside.

Inside was a golden pond bubbling with magma, and the inner chamber was blindingly bright with golden light. 

Every time Chen Ping'an was thrown into the golden magma by the seamstress, he would emerge after just a few hours, completely restored and healed. 

Yet, he had to leave behind his sword nurturing gourd in the floating pavilion.

Chen Ping'an asked, "Do ancient deities also have Qi Mansion openings, similar to our human structure?"

The white-haired boy paused, "Generally similar, but your human race is ultimately not as closely knit with the heavens and earth as the deities, after all, they crafted these puppets themselves. What they seek is merely incense offerings. Your human bodies, as small worlds, naturally won't be too exquisite from birth; however, compared to other beings, you are already quite fortunate. Otherwise, why do mountain spirits, ghosts, and the demon race of the barbaric world tirelessly strive to transform into human forms?"

Chen Ping'an caught a key phrase, "Close-knit? Is there some relation to the Daoist pursuit of purity?"

The foreign celestial demon spun slowly, answering indirectly, "Sword cultivators wield flying swords that can break myriad laws. A common kitchen knife can chop vegetables and firewood. But what exactly did the flying sword break? What did the kitchen knife cleave through? Do you understand the profound truth behind it?"

Chen Ping'an shook his head.

His student, Cui Dongshan, might understand the underlying reasons better.

Chen Ping'an finally opened his eyes and asked, "In exchange, I promised you that you could enter my heart lake three times. What did you see during those visits?"

The white-haired boy, who was the Er Qing Snake, sat cross-legged and suddenly flew into a rage, gritting his teeth but refusing to speak.

Having done four trades with this person, helping to construct buildings and gifting a set of a female sword immortal's shed skin, plus two short swords, he felt he had been taken advantage of.

Curious, Chen Ping'an picked up the nurturing gourd and took out one of the short swords. "If you’re willing to speak, I’ll return the short sword to you."

Inside the nurturing gourd was also the sword immortal from the Ascendant Sect's life sword "Tianlai," being nurtured.

The white-haired boy reached out, snatching the short sword from Chen Ping'an's hand and securing it at his waist. One sword remained, still being nurtured in that low-grade nurturing gourd, and he said, "The first time I visited, I met a middle-aged Taoist who wanted to spar with me. I nearly got scared to death."

"The second time, I didn’t go to that shabby little residence, but I encountered a youth with a weary appearance, wearing straw sandals and carrying a kitchen knife, wandering around. When we crossed paths, he wanted to discuss Buddhism with me, and just as he said 'please sit,' I was frightened again."

After recounting the two visits, the white-haired boy fell silent for some reason.

Chen Ping'an asked, "What happened the last time?"

The white-haired boy retorted, "Do you just love discussing principles?"

Chen Ping'an was confused. "What do you mean?"

The white-haired boy jumped up and cursed, "There was a guy who spoke to me for what felt like several years, based on the different speeds of time flowing in the river of light, and he wouldn’t let me leave! I truly couldn’t escape!"

Chen Ping'an smiled, "So I’m that annoying, even a foreign celestial demon can’t stand me?"

The white-haired boy cast a meaningful glance at the four pillars supporting the building.

After that, Chen Ping'an continued his cultivation, and the foreign celestial demon continued to wander, both remaining silent.

On this day, Chen Ping'an removed his upper garments, exposing his back.

The thorny entity casually withdrew a spine and began skinning it, stitching it up while inscribing several ancient seal characters, including the Nine Folding Seal, onto the young man's spine and skin, engraving one "true name" after another. Each name belonged to a mighty demon that had perished under the sword immortal’s blade, all intricately connected to the ancient ferocious beings now imprisoned in the cage. The closer the relationship, the greater the causality, and naturally, the better the stitching effect. Of course, the suffering endured by the young man would also escalate.

To prevent the young Hidden Official from being overwhelmed, collapsing his Dao heart, and his flesh and blood dissolving, leading to failure, the thorny entity had to impart a secret technique to Chen Ping'an that would allow him to slightly divert his focus.

This was truly a last resort. After all, Chen Ping'an had not yet reached the realm of wandering, and even after the tempering in that golden magma, his martial body could not bear too many true names of great demons. The thorny entity could only inscribe three each time—already the limit.

The young man had only one hand left to control; in fact, during the later stages of stitching, after the thorny entity inscribed the second great demon's true name, Chen Ping'an couldn't even dare to entertain a single thought. Even without any mental support, he still found his fingers writing in the air repeatedly: "Ning Yao, Ning Yao..."

The thorny entity, confined in the prison, never inquired about the matters of the Sword Qi Great Wall, so he did not know who this Ning Yao was.

During occasional breaks, the thorny entity would sneak a glance at the young man's writing, curious about which woman could inspire such affection in him. But was it really that deep?

*(End of Chapter)*

 **Chapter 792: Finally Entering the Realm of Far Travel**

Among the sixty-one demon races imprisoned here, only a few remained. Today, the work of sewing the thread was particularly crucial, marking the final stages at the spine.

Old Hearing stood with his hands behind his back, having hurried over to observe the sewing. As a demon, he found it far more comforting to watch others endure suffering than to see them enjoy themselves. The white-haired boy beside him called out to his grandson, and Old Hearing responded with a nod, pretending to be deaf.

Chen Ping'an had already settled into a meditative state, his mind deeply immersed. Every part of his being felt as if it were pinned down by an embroidery needle, tightly bound by the thread to prevent him from succumbing to pain and ruining the critical sewing process, which relied on an intricate chain of events that could not afford even the slightest error.

Nianxin, the seamstress, was pouring her heart into this sewing, essentially crafting a wedding gown for the young Hidden Official. The reasoning was simple: such an opportunity to practice her skills would never come again in her lifetime. Moreover, once successful, at least two realms of Qi cultivators—especially those hypocritical sect leaders and immortal teachers—would come to know her as Nianxin, the seamstress who had accomplished an unprecedented feat.

Just as discussions around chess invariably led to mentions of Baidi City, so too would discussions of Dao inevitably circle back to the Taishi. Thus, Nianxin was even more eager for success than Chen Ping'an.

After a prolonged period of cutting and stitching, she often found her eyes feeling dry and sore. To alleviate the strain, she picked up a nearby sword-raising gourd, poured out a dense, verdant pearl, tilted her head back, and let the drops land in her eyes.

In addition to the sword-raising gourd borrowed from the young Hidden Official, after two rounds of sewing, Nianxin took out two treasured artifacts—namely, a golden talisman and a jade book. 

Old Hearing looked down at the golden talisman and jade book, nodding in approval. "Good stuff," he remarked.

The white-haired boy lamented, "What a pity. Once used, they'll become useless. Otherwise, my grandfather, the Hidden Official, would surely have his eyes shining with delight."

Both artifacts were tied to Nianxin's Dao connections. She had once confided in Chen Ping'an that her path of cultivation relied not only on the secret arts and mystical powers of a seamstress but also on the golden talisman and jade book, both of which were highly orthodox treasures of the immortals, complementing her sewing technique. Without them, she would not have survived to this day.

Ordinary cultivators, even those at the same Jade Purity level as Nianxin, could not decipher the contents of the golden talisman and jade book, as if they were trapped within a natural mountain and water formation. However, Old Hearing and the white-haired boy were anything but ordinary.

The jade book was a sacred tome from an ancient dynasty in the Central Land, consisting of twenty-four bamboo slips connected by golden threads. Each slip had been meticulously polished by secret techniques. The golden talisman was a volume of the "True Scroll of Talismans," also known as the "Talisman Assignment Diagram," divided into three parts. The first part comprised sixteen grand characters—eight characters at the front from the three cave gold texts of true immortal slips, written in cloud script, swirling like mist. The latter eight characters represented the eternal Dao and were blessing words penned by a great Master of Dragon Tiger Mountain. The second part depicted portraits of sixty-one immortals, while the third part contained the main text of the entire "True Scroll of Talismans," recounting the tale of a queen who aspired to become a transcendent Daoist immortal. It was said that after the dynasty's downfall, she devoted herself to cultivation and eventually ascended.

The jade book was manageable, merely a foot in size when laid out. However, the true scroll, when unfurled, extended over ten feet long.

The reason Nianxin took out these two treasures was that using her unique sewing techniques, she could extract text, peel off charms, or imprint cloud patterns, and then reinforce them onto the young Hidden Official's skin and bones with the yellow paper method.

Thus, it could be said that Nianxin had reached a point where she was willing to risk everything for this sewing.

As for the suffering and calamities the young man would endure, Nianxin was entirely indifferent. Since he dared to come here and undertake this task, he should be prepared to accept it.

At that moment, glancing at the golden talisman and jade book on the ground, Old Hearing suddenly remembered a small matter. Earlier, he had promised the young Hidden Official a deal to ensure the safe exit of his three disciples from prison.

The terms had been settled; Old Hearing needed to provide a Dao technique suitable for demon clan cultivation, along with two rare artifacts with low thresholds for both refining and use.

Giving away two artifacts was a minor issue, but finding an appropriate Dao technique posed some challenges.

A methodical mountain Dao technique would undoubtedly come with numerous restrictions, much like certain rare charms that had specific methods for opening and closing.

For example, a certain ancestral talisman from the Dragon Tiger Mountain Master’s estate had been enhanced by successive generations of masters. Even for those not of the master’s lineage, unless they were immortal realm cultivators, it would be impossible to even lift it.

The profound arts of the immortals, often recorded in secret texts, naturally aligned with the great Dao. Once compiled into written form, they contained inherent mysteries. First, the materials used to inscribe the Daoist texts were not ordinary. Second, even if great cultivators lifted various restrictions, lower-tier Qi cultivators would still be incapable of deciphering them. Thus, sect families often treasured their Dao texts, with much of the knowledge transmitted orally, referred to as "intimate teaching."

Moreover, the oral teachings by a preacher were no easy task. A single misstep could ruin a disciple's Dao heart.

After some thought, Old Hearing decided that keeping that Dao text for himself would serve no purpose since he had no intention of establishing a sect. Instead, he would remove all restrictions and give it to the young Hidden Official. After that, how Chen Ping'an taught others was no concern of his. Handing out toilet paper to someone squatting in the restroom was already quite a gesture; after all, one couldn't wipe their backside as well.

The white-haired boy chuckled and asked, "If it were You Yu and Du Shanyin, would they be rolling all over the ground after just one cut?"

Old Hearing shook his head. "If they could manage to endure two cuts, they still have a chance. After all, those two kids don’t rely on suffering to cultivate; their luck is better than anything else. Otherwise, they wouldn't have the chance to enjoy themselves here."

Nianxin set down her knife and took a moment to rest. Having felt slightly sluggish earlier, her mood appeared to have soured. Hearing the noise from Old Hearing and the outlandish demon, she frowned and snapped, "Get lost!"

Known for his good temper at the Sword Qi Great Wall, Old Hearing indeed moved away, climbing the steps. "It’s one thing to be ugly, but a bad temper? No wonder she can't get married."

The white-haired boy floated beside Old Hearing and asked, "Does You Yu's Dao heart need your help to sharpen? You don't need to thank me for such a small favor."

Old Hearing chuckled, "I advise you not to. The Great Sword Immortal is watching this way. If I fail to protect my master, before I get crushed, I’ll surely settle accounts with you—both old and new debts."

After those two left, Nianxin exhaled a breath of frustration and continued to focus, gently bringing her knife down.

What appeared to be a horrific sight to ordinary mortals was, in her eyes, a masterpiece. The method of engraving was delicate; the Yang script prized clarity and lightness. After carving the inscription, mist swirled upward, producing five-colored auspicious fungi, while the Yin script favored richness and heaviness, resembling the long, winding dragon veins at the foot of the Great Mountain. Clarity resembled the heavens, while heaviness represented the earth.

For instance, using four-character Yang script cloud seals, she inscribed not the true names of the great demons but the法印 (fa yin) of the "Dao Sutra Master’s Treasures." Once the seal was completed, auspicious phenomena emerged, lingering like clouds around a mountain.

She also engraved the eight ancient small seals of "Taiyi Zhuangbao" and "List of Immortals," requiring extreme precision, stacking each character with utmost care, consuming Nianxin's heart and spirit.

The knife techniques, the talisman patterns, twisted and intertwined to the utmost. When she sheathed her knife, the pen held like a droplet of dew, hanging low yet not falling, as if water droplets condensed from morning mist.

There were also cutting techniques that resembled a carpenter's woodworking shavings. Nianxin lowered her head and gently blew away any useless shavings, all of which came from the young Hidden Official's spine.

After wrapping up for the day, Nianxin dragged the young man to a small door, complaining, "Chen Ping'an, you can barely withstand this; it's only about thirty cuts at most. If I hadn't stopped in time, your entire spine would have been ruined. Do you want to break the Bridge of Eternal Life again?!"

The barely conscious young man couldn't utter a word, merely moving his lips, likely cursing.

Blood was splattered everywhere, not a drop wasted. The blood would naturally weave into threads, eventually being collected into the embroidered pouch at her waist.

Old Hearing stood by the small door, unlocked it, and Nianxin tossed the young Hidden Official into the golden magma-filled "furnace" inside the room.

Old Hearing shut the door.

Just as Nianxin was about to leave, Old Hearing spoke up, "How did the Hidden Official manage to kill at the fifth realm? The Great Sword Immortal didn't mention it; how do you plan to resolve this?"

Nianxin shook her head. "He didn't say."

Old Hearing laughed. "Was today smooth sailing?"

Nianxin's brow furrowed, "Chen Ping'an still hasn't entered the Realm of Far Travel; this isn't a long-term solution. The pain he's enduring is quite severe, and he bears three parts of it himself. If I were in his position, I'd have asked the Great Sword Immortal to use some unconventional methods to break through first. Since he's so eager to leave, why not be in a greater rush?"

Old Hearing nodded. These troubling matters had nothing to do with him. "Miss Nianxin, having been neighbors for so many years, how about I treat you to a meal of mudfish stew? My young master is truly skilled in cooking. It's better than your internal organs chewing on each other."

Nianxin brushed him off and floated away.

Old Hearing went to the cage of the Great Demon Qing Qiu. Without needing to say a word, the Great Demon obediently offered three drops of its life essence and a large piece of flesh, tremblingly asking, "Could you please convey a message to the Hidden Official?"

At this rate, it was becoming unbearable.

Old Hearing chewed on the raw flesh of the blue catfish, which was very chewy but lacked the flavor of cooked food. He chuckled, "Didn't the Hidden Official come to see you again? How come you still couldn't reach an agreement last time?"

The Great Demon Qing Qiu's smile was bitter.

Earlier, it had indeed met with the young man again, but at that moment, it had nearly yanked the fellow into the prison again and "politely" declined the offer.

The young man had mentioned that catfish were fond of dark, murky waters and were most afraid of sunlight. Then he tossed a piece of yellow paper talisman resembling a ghostly drawing into the cage. The Great Demon Qing Qiu snatched it up and mocked the young man's talisman technique.

After that, the young man stopped visiting, while Old Hearing came by every few days.

Old Hearing had cleaned out the cage, hands behind his back. "What took you so long?"

Perhaps today was a fortunate day for the Great Demon Qing Qiu; Chen Ping'an strolled through the prison of the fifth realm Great Demons.

As the young man passed, the Great Demon Qing Qiu appeared near the sword light fence and asked, "How can I prevent Cheng Shan from causing me trouble?"

Chen Ping'an froze for a moment; Cheng Shan was the alias Old Hearing used in the wild lands. The summer resort’s file on Old Hearing consisted of two pages, each word smeared into ink blocks by the previous Hidden Official, Xiao Xian, who had carefully blotted each character without tearing the pages or carelessly smearing large areas, as if she was engaged in a very interesting task.

Chen Ping'an paused, locking eyes with the Great Demon Qing Qiu. "It's simple. Tell me all the inside info about the great demon who fell into the Yeluo River; the more detailed, the better."

The Great Demon Qing Qiu remained silent for a moment, a mocking smile crossing its face, and retreated back into the mist barrier.

Chen Ping'an did not press further and went to the first cage where Yun Qing was held. He often visited this place to chat with the Great Demon, and it was genuinely just idle talk about the customs and flavors of their respective worlds.

Today, they sat facing each other, separated only by a fence.

Chen Ping'an had not expected Yun Qing to be well-versed in knowledge, rivaling even the scholars of the Confucian school. For instance, when discussing the "Monthly Ordinance," she had unique insights, particularly about the phrase stating that in autumn, one should hunt the giant flood dragon, which implied that the flood dragon could be hunted while the dragon could not.

After inquiring, Chen Ping'an learned that Yun Qing had spent several years studying in Zhou Mi's territory, though they had no official teacher-student relationship.

Moreover, Yun Qing enjoyed wandering the world, traveling to various places, and had even compiled a poetry collection that was widely circulated in several dynasties of the wild lands.

At the end of their idle chat, the Great Demon Yun Qing smiled and took out a bamboo flute from her waist, inscribed with the words "Fallen Celestial," holding it in her hand. "This semi-immortal weapon is useless to keep, so I present it to the Hidden Official."

The flute, inscribed with the words "Fallen Celestial," also bore a line of smaller characters indicating it had once been gifted to Lu Zhi Feng Xuan. 

Yun Qing explained that this item had been a token of love for a great demon who had ascended. If it weren't for the severe damage rendering it unreparable, it would have been a genuine celestial weapon.

Chen Ping'an shook his head. "I can't accept it."

Yun Qing was puzzled. "Why not?"

Chen Ping'an replied, "Even if we meet with affinity, we ultimately belong to different factions. It wouldn't be appropriate for you to kill me later."

Yun Qing nodded and smiled. "Likewise, that's why we resonate."

Within the suspended building, Chen Ping'an walked in circles, unconsciously hunching his back, one arm hanging limply by his side.

Nianxin sat on the distant steps and said, "If you don't enter the Realm of Far Travel soon, the aftereffects will be significant. Even if you eventually succeed, the results will be greatly diminished."

Chen Ping'an nodded gently. "I know."

Nianxin felt helpless.

The white-haired boy appeared beside Nianxin, morphing into the scholarly form of Great Demon Yun Qing, smiling as he said, "Miss Nianxin, I must confess I've harbored feelings for you for a long time. What a captivating beauty, free from earthly constraints, unlike any rich adornment in the mortal world."

Nianxin ignored him.

The outlandish demon shifted forms again, raspy-voiced, "Nianxin, would you really mind that I'm deaf, blind, and old?"

Nianxin continued to disregard him.

The outlandish demon transformed once more, "Miss Nianxin, one cannot judge a person by their appearance. In my eyes, you are a beautiful lady. Among countless attractive women, there's only one Nianxin."

Chen Ping'an, still practicing his stance, said, "That's enough."

It turned out the outlandish demon had taken on Chen Ping'an's appearance in a blue robe.

Nianxin was focused solely on the follow-up to her sewing.

The outlandish demon resumed its favorite form and sat on the steps, "A lone man and a solitary woman, without a hint of affection—how absurd! What’s going on between you two? Such a dampener on the mood."

After finishing his stance, Chen Ping'an began holding his sword to practice, breathing and calming himself to nurture his life sword.

Nianxin left.

The outlandish demon, unwilling to depart, fixed its gaze on the sword-raising gourd beside Chen Ping'an. 

His short sword, "Dragon Qiu," was inside it, while the sword he had returned was now at his waist, named "Jiang Du." 

Both held significant origins, perfect for nurturing the two little things dangling by his ears.

In fact, anything that could long endure in this world would not be of low quality.

However, for an outlandish demon, it held little meaning—it was all about the eye affinity.

Suddenly, it exclaimed, "What about that celestial shed skin? How about I just give you my robe too, let her dress up and wield her sword?"

Chen Ping'an replied indifferently, "The deceased take precedence."

After rising, he leaned back, supported himself with one hand, closed his eyes, and pinched his sword formula with the other.

The white-haired boy kept his promise, not intruding into that building, but instead wandered around, constantly transforming into various demons that had perished under Chen Ping'an's fists and swords. He only asked, "The deceased take precedence? What of the living?"

Chen Ping'an opened his eyes, aligning his fingers against the ground, slightly elevating his feet.

The now-reverted white-haired boy smiled at him, saying, "Your heart and mind are not in sync. You’ve been too hard on yourself—the strong are one with heaven and earth."

Chen Ping'an shut his eyes again, stating, "There are no fixed laws."

The outlandish demon suddenly transformed into a woman, smiling sweetly.

Chen Ping'an hesitated for a moment, then opened his eyes to find a face that could easily deceive anyone.

What he thought was reflected in what he saw.

This was the terrifying aspect of the outlandish demon.

Chen Ping'an closed his eyes again and said, "Bear the consequences yourself."

The white-haired boy immediately shouted, "Hidden Official, what if your future inner demons take the form of this lady? What then?"

Chen Ping'an chuckled softly and replied, "I would actually welcome that."

The white-haired boy raised his hands and lightly flicked his fingers beside the blue snake, making a subtle sound that echoed through the heavens. He asked, "Shall we put on a performance?"

Chen Ping'an spoke sternly, "Get lost!"

The white-haired boy complained, "I lost a level for no reason; this deal with the Hidden Official is certainly a loss."

In the next moment, the outlandish demon fell silent, shrinking its neck.

It turned out Chen Qingdu had already caught hold of its head, lifting it up.

The elder was merely using his sword intent to overpower it, causing the outlandish demon's face to twist in pain, its whole body melting away like a wax candle, its features unrecognizable, and it immediately wailed, desperately pleading for mercy.

Chen Ping'an spun around, standing elegantly.

Chen Qingdu tossed the outlandish demon far away, looking at Chen Ping'an and frowning. "You didn't carve out a single true name of the key great demons?"

Nianxin appeared again on the steps, "Don't blame me; I can carve, but it would have to be on the dead."

Chen Ping'an sighed, "The martial artist's bottleneck is truly difficult to break. Even when confronting the outlandish demon in a contest of fists, it yields no results. What I lack now is that mysterious divine intent. Otherwise, just enduring Nianxin's sewing would be enough for me to enter the Realm of Far Travel."

Chen Qingdu said, "Where do I find a complete tenth realm martial artist for the Hidden Official?"

Chen Ping'an replied, "Don't ask me."

Chen Qingdu was slightly annoyed but also amused.
