The white-haired boy was wide-eyed in amazement.

With Old Hearing's arrival, he was utterly impressed.

The outlandish demon curled up on the steps felt that the repeated calls for the Hidden Official had not been in vain.

As a result, the Hidden Official was overpowered by the sword intent, first bending at the waist, then kneeling, finally collapsing onto the ground, nearly becoming a puddle of mud.

Fortunately, the Great Sword Immortal was somewhat honorable, directly tossing Chen Ping'an into the magma furnace.

Once Chen Ping'an disappeared, Chen Qingdu waved his hand, and Nianxin's group simultaneously left.

The elder stood within the pavilion, surveying the surroundings, his gaze slowly sweeping over the four pillars of the pavilion.

Chen Ping'an had rarely left the prison, taking the opportunity to breathe some fresh air.

The white-haired boy soon appeared, urging the young Hidden Official to visit the place where the execution officer cultivated, saying that there were many treasures there—unclaimed items to be found.

Just looking was free, and if one could gather, it was even better.

Under the guidance of the outlandish demon, Chen Ping'an arrived at a stream, feeling somewhat dazed, as if he were back in his hometown, ready to gather snake gallstones, though he lacked a large basket.

The white-haired boy was like a gossiping spirit, detailing the recent circumstances of two master-servant pairs, saying that You Yu was a bit slow-witted and could not compare to the three disciples Old Hearing had taken in. However, Du Shanyin had decent sword talent and good fortune but was a considerable lecher. All these characters could become the masters of Old Hearing and the execution officer, and he genuinely felt for the Hidden Official.

Suddenly, Chen Ping'an stopped in his tracks; not far from the stream, he spotted two women—one pounding clothes and the other washing silk.

He gazed intently, filled with disbelief. Having roamed the rivers and lakes, he had encountered those who lived by incense and offerings, even seen Cui Dongshan's insect silver, yet he had never seen the two women before him.

The white-haired boy exclaimed, "The Hidden Official has truly good eyes, instantly recognizing their true identities as the ancestral incarnations of Jin Jing Qian and Gu Yu Qian. Du Shanyin couldn't possibly see beyond their pretty faces, ample bosoms, and slim waists. Poor You Yu didn't even dare to take a good look; only the Hidden Official is truly remarkable."

The clothes-pounding woman looked up, brushing back her hair, and smiled faintly at Chen Ping'an.

The silk-washing girl noticed the young Hidden Official and rested a finger on her cheek.

Chen Ping'an returned the gesture with a fist salute.

The white-haired boy stomped his feet. "Hidden Official, they don't deserve your great courtesy; it would embarrass them."

Chen Ping'an pretended not to hear and walked toward the thatched cottage, pondering over matters of wealth.

The golden copper coins had three types in the Great Li: the Welcome Spring Coin, the Offering Coin, and the Suppression Coin. They were once the tolls for entering the Li Pearl Cave. Chen Ping'an was quite familiar with them, having bought a few bags of golden copper coins with the first batch of mountain heads.

It was said that the three types of golden copper coins sold to various immortal forces by the Great Li dynasty were crafted with the help of the Mo family, who first produced the three types of casting mother coins, which were of the finest quality and then mass-produced.

Even the ordinary copper coins crafted by the secular dynasty were highly sought after by many mountain cultivators, treasured by collectors willing to pay top dollar.

Along with the golden copper coins, the treasury issued new coins, including the three types of divine coins, such as the Snowflake Coin, Little Heat Coin, and Gu Yu Coin, all linked to the casting mother coins. Among them, the ancestral coin of the Snowflake Coin was naturally preserved by the Liu family of the White Snow Continent, but the whereabouts of the ancestral coins for the Little Heat Coin and Gu Yu Coin had always remained unclear. Little did he expect that the ancestral coin of Gu Yu Coin had actually been collected by the execution officer, manifesting as a person.

In the world, as long as a being could transform into a human form and awakened spiritual intelligence, regardless of their origins, they were considered practitioners of the great Dao. Treating them with courtesy would never be wrong.

Young Du Shanyin, having nothing to do today, stood under the grape trellis, watching the two visitors from afar.

The white-haired boy was still feeling indignant on behalf of his "Hidden Official," retreating alongside Chen Ping'an while pointing at the two women who spent their days pounding clothes and washing silk. "How reckless! How brazen!"

The clothes-pounding woman and the silk-washing girl, originally no different from rural beauties, transformed unexpectedly when the outlandish demon spoke the words "reckless," their skin shimmering with golden and green hues, faint words appearing—especially on the forehead of the silk-washing girl, which had opened like a delicate little window, likely due to the marks left during her birth.

However, they were entirely oblivious, continuing to work.

The white-haired boy whispered, "In the world, ancestral coins often come in pairs. If both become spirits and then partners, tsk tsk, that would be an extraordinary fortune. Wealth breeds wealth. Hidden Official, if you promise to take me to the Hao Ran world, I’ll help you seek them from the execution officer. Once we get to the Hao Ran world, we can keep our eyes wide open and find their Dao partners for you! How about that?"

Chen Ping'an replied, "No how about that."

The execution officer was inside the thatched cottage, and even if the Hidden Official came to visit, he showed no intention of opening the door to receive guests.

Chen Ping'an was merely out for some fresh air, so the execution officer's attitude did not matter to him, provided he didn't get hit by a sword light.

Du Shanyin bowed, "Greetings, Hidden Official."

Chen Ping'an smiled, "Be at ease."

Du Shanyin suddenly recalled something, smacking his head and fetching two bags of gold powder, first offering one bag. "I kindly request the Hidden Official to accept this."

Chen Ping'an genuinely accepted it.

Du Shanyin offered another bag of gold powder, "I humbly request the Hidden Official to share a tale of mountains and rivers."

The white-haired boy wore a playful smile.

Chen Ping'an reached out and pressed down on the tall young man's head, smiling, "Even if you become the legitimate master of the execution officer in the future, don't do such things again."

Du Shanyin looked up, his expression calm, "May I ask why?"

Chen Ping'an fell silent, brushing past the young man to admire the brightly colored flower vase suspended in the air.

The white-haired boy jumped up and slapped the young man on the shoulder, saying, "You’re truly capable; keep it up! My Hidden Official is just jealous of your good fortune. Being too pleased with oneself is a compliment for cultivators."

Du Shanyin grinned, "Just kidding."

The white-haired boy questioned, "Why aren't you the least bit afraid of me?"

Du Shanyin's thoughts shifted, and a streak of sword light suddenly hovered on the young man's shoulder, like a bird perched on a branch.

Du Shanyin said, "The execution officer gifted me this."

The white-haired boy immediately exclaimed, "With this, I’ll call you dad from now on!"

Du Shanyin's smile abruptly froze.

Chen Ping'an was gazing up at a flower vase, chuckling, "Go ahead and stir up trouble."

The white-haired boy burst into laughter. 

Chen Ping'an turned his head to look at the tall young man’s retreating figure. "Within your own rules, why don’t you dare draw your sword?"

Du Shanyin turned back and smiled, "To me, you are all transcendental beings, playing around in the mortal world. That's not excessive."

Chen Ping'an merely chuckled, continuing to examine the vase, appreciating its exquisite poetry, finally accepting it.

The white-haired boy asked, "Du Shanyin, has the execution officer ever told you that once you master your sword techniques and have the opportunity to travel the Hao Ran world, you must kill all the mountain flower thieves? Did he shower you with countless treasures you never even dreamed of? Among them, was there a book solely about the characters 'immortal'? In your heart, you might regret that the two ladies weren't included, so you feel a bit let down?"

"Don’t worry, just as well I know my Hidden Official has no thoughts about them. I’ll help you beg for them from the execution officer; you don’t need to thank me! Alas, I say this, and your thoughts about them will become shallow, feeling that they are no longer esteemed treasures in the mind of the Hidden Official. They no longer possess that celestial quality in your eyes, or else it would overshadow the Hidden Official, wouldn’t it? Rest assured, this is human nature; there's no need to feel embarrassed. In the pursuit of the Dao, to reach the peak, one should be like you—take what you see; if you dislike it, discard it; if you love it, seize it..."

Du Shanyin felt a chill within, his face increasingly uncomfortable, leaving him with no choice but to remain silent.

Chen Ping'an hesitated but ultimately said nothing.

Opportunities offered too much without consideration of one's capacity to receive; the giver was indifferent, and so was the receiver.

However, Chen Ping'an turned his thoughts elsewhere, realizing that such a mindset was likely the foundation of Du Shanyin's path; who said that one's success depended solely on depth of thought?

Moreover, Ah Liang was right—what mattered, and what could be cared for? Was it manageable? 

The white-haired boy seemed delighted, having rambled on for so long without a word from the execution officer inside the thatched cottage. What a good omen! Truly, the execution officer was indifferent to everything, so different from the Hidden Official.

He walked over to Chen Ping'an, pointing at a white jade table outside the grape trellis. "A treasure! It's a pity that the book on the table, the one about immortals, already belongs to Du Shanyin. Inside, a whole bunch of little critters have been nurtured, of a value far beyond ordinary bookworms."

Chen Ping'an stepped out from under the grape trellis and went straight to the stone table, casually flipping open a page of the book. It was filled with various forms of the characters 'immortal,' written in different styles—from cursive to regular to seal scripts.

The white-haired boy whispered, "You’re looking at the book without even greeting Du Shanyin; that’s not your usual style, Hidden Official."

Chen Ping'an feigned ignorance, merely flipping through the pages, searching for traces of the bookworm.

He recalled that Li Huai seemed to have a bookworm of his own, but he wasn't sure if it had since transformed.

The white-haired boy muttered, "The Hidden Official wouldn't stoop so low as to compete with a simpleton. What is going on? Has his state of mind shifted, or is he trying to scare me? Trying to swindle me out of my short sword?"

Having finished flipping through one book without spotting those so-called "little critters," he had to give up.

Ancient texts recorded a tale about a bookworm that fed on the characters 'immortal.'

When a bookworm entered a tome containing Daoist texts, consuming the characters 'immortal' for long, it would manifest five colors. If ingested, it could lead to immortality, or at least inspire literary genius for eloquent writing.

One was a mere casual remark from literary scholars, while the other was the oral tradition of Qi cultivators. 

Yet, even among those on the mountain, the profound meaning behind the characters remained elusive. They only knew that the bookworm's previous form was a kind of wallfish, existing solely in scholarly households, hiding among writing brushes, inkstones, or shadows of lamps. However, the scholars below asserted that if one wrote the characters 'immortal' on expensive letter paper, shredded it, and tossed it into a bottle, a wallfish would surely come to consume the scraps, offering hope to grow into a bookworm.

The white-haired boy slapped the white jade table, "How dare you? Do you believe I won’t write the character for wine on the book and watch you all get drunk?!"

Upon focusing, Chen Ping'an noticed that between two lines of 'immortal' characters on the page, tiny figures, the size of fingernails, were emerging, scaling the pages from various directions, huddling within the lines, looking pitifully at him and the white-haired boy.

Chen Ping'an chuckled, apologizing for the disturbance, and gently closed the book.

The white-haired boy knelt on the stone bench, placing his hand over the book, explaining, "Once they become bookworms, they can consume anything written within. They can shift forms based on various writings. For example, if one wrote poems related to wine, they would sway drunkenly. If one wrote about beautiful maidens or sorrowful verses, they would take on those forms within the book, but it wouldn't last long; they would quickly revert back."

The white-haired boy casually flipped through the book, likely due to its large presence; every page he turned had the little critters scurrying to follow.

Chen Ping'an pondered, "What if I wrote about excrement and urine?"

The little critters froze, feeling despondent, unable to comprehend how there could be such a lunatic in the world.

The white-haired boy gave a thumbs up, loudly declaring, "The Hidden Official's ingenious ideas are rare in the world! If you ever meet the ancestor of novelists, you'll surely hit it off with him, wishing you had met sooner! After following the Hidden Official to the Central Divine Continent, you must visit that place of white paper fortune!"

Chen Ping'an sat on the stone bench.

The white-haired boy no longer cared about the book, pointing toward the stream, which actually belonged to the source-less waters. "This is extraordinarily rare water fire; it appears like water but is actually fire. The Hidden Official can use it to refine into the final piece of his five-element life item. Chen Qingdu is generous; the execution officer is even more so. I can help move it to the pavilion."

Chen Ping'an remained unmoved and rose, saying, "Inviting oneself is already rude enough."

As Chen Ping'an departed, the white-haired boy could only follow.

Mixing with Du Shanyin held no appeal; it was far more exciting to accompany Chen Ping'an.

For instance, during this visit, the young Hidden Official had entered the thatched cottage without greeting and left without bidding farewell.

The white-haired boy skipped beside Chen Ping'an, saying, "Hidden Official, today feels different; your heart is open, truly following your desires, relaxed and methodical—this is worthy of celebration."

Both walked side by side.

Clearly, the young Hidden Official was not in a rush to return to the prison.

Chen Ping'an smiled, "Are you hoping to achieve your wish through that stream? Why beat around the bush? Just say it directly."

The white-haired boy asked, "Can it be accomplished by speaking directly?"

Chen Ping'an replied, "Of course not."

Etiquette mattered; whether as a dragon kiln apprentice or a youth from the mud bottle lane, one must do what a person wearing straw sandals and wielding a machete should do while crossing mountains and rivers.

The Hidden Official, the tavern owner selling wine, the pure martial artist engaging in contests, the sword cultivator nurturing their blade—all had different identities, doing different things, and speaking different words.

Ultimately, they were still the same person.

The white-haired boy sighed, "My Hidden Official, you’re not this harsh with people."

Then the childlike outlandish demon sighed, "Forget it; I’m not human."

Chen Ping'an remarked, "Whether one is human or not is beyond the appearance; it depends more on whether they possess a human heart."

The white-haired boy scoffed, "A person with ulterior motives is still a person."

Chen Ping'an replied, "A person with a benevolent heart is still a person."

They reached a site where the remains of an ancient great demon lay, spanning like a mountain.

"Let’s go!" 

Chen Ping'an took a heavy step forward, suddenly punching the decayed corpse, which had lost its resilience, and thus, with a casual strike, created a 'valley' in the ground.

The white-haired boy clapped in approval.

Chen Ping'an glanced at the outlandish demon, whose behavior seemed mischievous, and slowly said, "The sorrowful tale of that fox spirit really lacks originality. If you were to write a book and sell it, it would be difficult to make money."

Having traveled far and wide, he had witnessed fox spirits bumping into bells, female ghosts scratching doors—one was an annoyance, the other a fright. He had also seen birds listening to the Dharma from the treetops, an old ghost wearing a raincoat riding a fox, singing "Pan Mountain Child."

The white-haired boy replied, "No worries; I’ll make some revisions."

Then, pretending to realize something, he added, "I forgot her fate also lacks novelty."

Chen Ping'an suddenly said, "I've figured out your origins."

Looking up, it seemed as if he were gazing at the white jade capital in another world.

The white-haired boy sighed, "Including the suppressive items from the Western Buddhist nations, does that count as a variant of the unity of the Three Pure Ones?"

Chen Ping'an, however, changed the subject, chuckling to himself, "A down-and-out literati typically only engages in three things: serving as a backdrop, teaching, and selling literature."

When the last Hidden Official in the history of the Sword Qi Great Wall told mountain and stream stories on the streets, he combined all three endeavors, yet regrettably, none earned him any money.

The white-haired boy appeared dispirited.

Chen Ping'an leapt into the air, wearing a blue robe, rushing straight into the clouds, then soaring through the cloud sea, his sleeves billowing loudly.

In fact, now, besides riding the sword, he could barely ride the wind, relying solely on pure true Qi for support, consuming it rapidly.

He summoned the four flying swords: the first and fifteenth, pine needles, and thunder, each hovering in various locations.

Over the cloud sea, he leaped into the air, landing precisely on the flying swords, floating around.

The white-haired boy watched, yawning.

Chen Ping'an withdrew the four flying swords, leaning back and plummeting towards the ground.

Still in high spirits, he glanced at the fine stream in the distance.

Was water in the sky? Or was the sky in the water?

Chen Ping'an dove headfirst into the ground.

In the cloud sea above, the white-haired boy felt a stir in his spirit, somewhat surprised. He abruptly looked up, sensing the world changing colors.

Moments later, the outlandish demon stood up, its aura completely transformed. Having received Chen Qingdu's "mandate," it finally displayed the demeanor of an ascending outlandish demon.

It scooped a handful of water from the cloud sea, waving its sleeve to bring the clouds into its sleeve, then tossed it towards the heavens, creating a bright moon suspended in the air, thus cupping the moon’s reflection in its palm.

With a single slap, it shattered the moon reflected in the water.

The world changed once more.

The white-haired boy had already vanished.

In an instant, the cloud sea roared, as if someone had casually stirred up a massive pit. Dimly, one could see a vague figure of a celestial being in the clouds, looking down at the earth and laughing, "Little Confucian, don't overestimate yourself. Would you like to play with me?"

Then a giant golden figure slowly extended a fist, sneering, "Do you dare to take a punch?"

Chen Ping'an stood firmly on the ground, looking up.

He spat heavily, rolled up his sleeves, then smoothed them back out.

A young man in white, traveling far beyond, stood alongside a young man in a blue robe, exclaiming, "Staying in a cage for too long is truly unpleasant."

Chen Ping'an smiled, "Speak plainly."

The young man in white waved his large sleeves, appearing carefree, his gaze fervent, laughing, "Dammit! Let them bow down to me!"

Very good. This was it.

No doubt it was Chen Ping'an!

The earth trembled violently.

A blue robe shot towards the cloud sea.

The martial artist questioned the heavens with his fists.

Then the young man in white soared upward, the ground beneath him his domain, countless flying swords heading towards the cloud sea.

The swordsman challenged the celestial being above the clouds.

To the north of the Sword Qi Great Wall, and to the south, streams of martial energy surged wildly, blocking the sun and the moon, all searching for that unknown figure challenging the heavens. 

(End of Chapter)

 ### Chapter 793: Give It a Try

The seemingly idle foreign demon, once granted permission by Chen Qingdu, finally lifted all restrictions that had bound it. It tasted a brief moment of freedom, unleashing its true ascendant powers, allowing the world and all things to flow according to its whims, nearly comparable to the “truth.”

The old deaf man, following the orders of the Grand Sword Immortal, opened the forbidden gates of the prison's small world, accepting the martial fortunes gifted from the Sword Qi Great Wall and the Wilds. In an instant, a torrent of martial fortunes surged into the ancient battlefield ruins like a throng of dragons.

Beside the stream, the Executioner Sword Immortal stepped out of the thatched cottage, moving towards a stone table, where he placed his hand on a divine book infested with bookworms.

The women washing clothes continued their repetitive labor.

Du Shanyin stood beneath the grapevine, peering through the lush green leaves at the scene before him, his expression complex.

As the Executioner pressed down on the book, the atmosphere in the small world near the stream fell into tranquility.

The old deaf man stood at the prison entrance, stroking his beard and chuckling, “The heavens and earth are turned upside down.”

The young boy, brought here to witness the spectacle, felt his spirits sway, growing even more in awe of the young Hidden Official.

Nianxin quietly appeared, whispering, “That foreign demon actually possesses such powers?”

The old deaf man laughed, “You don’t really think it’s just a little trickster, do you? Its ascendant cultivation is merely suppressed too much here, giving it a showy appearance. It fears the Grand Sword Immortal; otherwise, with your level of cultivation and Dao heart, you would have long been reduced to its puppet. The skill in sewing, even if it touches upon the soul, cannot compare to the depths of the foreign demon's influence on the human heart.”

Nianxin asked, “It has always hoped to leave this place through Chen Ping’an.”

The old deaf man shook his head, “Chen Ping’an will never allow it to escape the forbidden ground. Once the Grand Sword Immortal’s suppression is removed, Chen Ping’an will be its best vessel. It would be like the pigeon immortal taking over, with its body and soul switched. At that point, it could roam freely in the Wilds, high up in the heavens and far across the earth. Both sides are aware of this; the foreign demon is meticulously unraveling Chen Ping’an’s heart, while Chen Ping’an remains steadfast, tempering his own Dao heart in return. On the surface, they seem to have a harmonious relationship, sharing laughter, but this life-and-death struggle is not much different from the grand battle of the Qi practitioners. You may not realize that the oaths sworn by these foreign demons are the lightest and most unbinding.”

The old deaf man wore a thoughtful expression, “With Chen Ping’an’s mindset and physique as a foundation, it’s likely that the Wilds will soon gain a new overlord demon, and the Grand Ancestor of the Moon-Embracing Mountain will surely be delighted by this. The two Hidden Officials from the Sword Qi Great Wall have already defected to the Wilds; this is the trend of the times. In front of the Grand Sword Immortal, I must utter such blasphemy: I am quite looking forward to it. A ‘Chen Ping’an’ who has ventured to the other extreme will still be Chen Ping’an, but not entirely the same Chen Ping’an, achieving the purest form of freedom, seeking only the utmost longevity in his cultivation. Nianxin, what do you think?”

Nianxin replied, “I have no preference.”

She added, “If that day truly comes, I might choose to align myself with that new Chen Ping’an and take root in the Wilds; perhaps I could even break through my current limitations.”

The old deaf man lightly rubbed his beard and chuckled, “A new Chen Ping’an, the seamstress Nianxin, and me, an ascendant—if the three of us join forces in the Wilds to establish a sect, we’ll surely have a remarkable presence and great potential.” 

He then self-deprecatingly continued, “But such a grand prospect can only be imagined.”

The young boy felt a chill run down his spine.

He could hardly conceive how terrifying it would be if that young Hidden Official chose to ally with the demon clan, especially for the Sword Qi Great Wall and that unfamiliar righteous world.

Deep within the boy’s heart, he even considered that if Chen Ping’an turned to the Wilds, it would have more severe consequences than the former Hidden Official Xiao Xian's betrayal of the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Nianxin curiously asked, “Aren't you afraid of being held accountable by the Grand Sword Immortal for being so candid?”

The old deaf man laughed heartily, “I am a demon myself; when have I ever hidden my true nature? When Chen Ping’an asked me what I would do if there were no taboos, did I not directly answer ‘Death to all who see it’?”

Nianxin gazed at the magnificent scene in the sky and remarked, “This is not the kind of momentum a gold-body stage martial artist should have. Even with the strongest title, it still seems unreasonable.”

The old deaf man shook his head, “You haven’t seen Cao Ci; he and Chen Ping’an are of the same generation. When Cao Ci returned to the Inverted Mountain, he broke through right at the entrance, causing immense stir across two realms. However, Cao Ci ultimately did not accept a single piece of martial fortune, which implicated six sword immortals from the Sword Qi Great Wall. They all drew their swords to repel the martial fortunes, and even two celestial lords from the Inverted Mountain personally intervened.”

The old deaf man glanced at the sky, “However, in terms of martial arts, Chen Ping’an is getting closer to Cao Ci. Other martial artists will likely only drift further away from him.”

This was a highly commendable evaluation from a prominent figure of ascendant cultivation.

When Chen Ping’an first met Cao Ci upon entering the city, the world only knew of Cao Ci, two similarly aged young martial artists.

The young boy cautiously said, “Senior Lou’er, if the Hidden Official is getting closer to Cao Ci, doesn’t that mean the Hidden Official is surpassing Cao Ci?”

The old deaf man nodded, “Who can argue with that?”

The white-haired boy had already returned from his long journey, and the unified form of Chen Ping’an landed heavily on the ground, bending his knees and bowing his head, gasping for air.

At that moment, the young man in the green robe, who had been silent, felt as if the sky and earth were vast, and anywhere was within reach. No matter if it was the Grand Sword Immortal or an ascendant demon, as long as they stood before him as enemies, he had fists and a sword enough to fight back.

The white-haired boy floated down, seeking credit, “I’m the one who put in the effort to create such a grand scene; you must be grateful, Hidden Official!”

The foreign demon merely saw the young man maintain his previous posture, only slightly lifting his eyelids.

It reined in its smile, locking eyes with Chen Ping’an.

Chen Ping’an slowly straightened his back, his movements slightly stiff, and smiled, “There is nothing in this world that cannot be discussed.”

It curled its lips, wrapping its hands around its head, “So there’s nothing to talk about, huh?”

Chen Ping’an tilted his shoulder, stamping his foot heavily on the ground, stabilizing his body.

His back trembled slightly, blood seeping from his arms and eyelids.

The foreign demon knew this was due to his unstable realm, compounded by the sewing technique's influence, which affected the Dao’s suppression. The current young Hidden Official was in a literal battle of heaven and man.

Those of higher realms are closer to heaven; climbing higher grants deeper insight into the operation of the heavenly Dao, bearing heavier burdens.

For Qi practitioners, the chance to step into the Jade Purity realm lies in merging with the Dao. To break through from the Immortal realm to the Ascendant realm, the fundamental principle of the Dao is found in “seriousness,” recognizing the essence of truth.

Chen Ping’an staggered forward, slowly making his way to the prison entrance.

The foreign demon, ever changeable in temperament, was now smiling and joking beside him, claiming it could protect the Hidden Official time and again, forging a bond of incense offerings, which was a great fortune indeed.

Chen Ping’an was focused on dual tasks: feeling the myriad mysteries of the distant traveler's physique while concentrating his mind into a seed, patrolling the small world within himself.

After enduring numerous trials of sewing from Nianxin and then verifying them against the boxing principles taught by Li Er, Chen Ping’an confidently felt that whether viewing the “mountains and rivers” of his body from the perspective of a pure martial artist or treating the “cave heavens and blessed lands” of his body from the view of a Qi practitioner, he had surpassed ordinary individuals.

As for the elemental items of his fate, he had already gathered four, with only the final piece missing.

The last piece he lacked was a fire-related item.

The stream, referred to as “water fire” by the foreign demon, tempted Chen Ping’an, but he remained unmoved. His reluctance stemmed from not wanting to take what others cherished. Of course, this was a more palatable explanation; bluntly put, it was due to his lack of confidence in dealing with the Executioner. Chen Ping’an always sensed that the experienced and high-ranking Sword Immortal had an innate prejudice against him. That seemingly casual visit only strengthened his conviction.

At the Ning residence, there were indeed fire-related items suitable for forging, although the treasures there weren’t of particularly high rank. Nonetheless, they would be more than sufficient to assemble the five elemental items of fate.

For a lower-level Qi practitioner, it would be difficult to match Chen Ping’an’s current level of elemental item configuration, even those who were first-rate direct descendants of established sects.

Moreover, Chen Ping’an had been tirelessly supplementing his collection to support the five elemental items of fate, such as the green bricks from the mountaintop Taoist temple, the Thunder Law Seal from Li Zhen, the imitation white jade capital tower, and the Sword Immortal’s pennant. Among these, the Thunder Law Seal had been refined by Chen Ping’an and hung at the entrance of his wooden house, serving as a talisman against evil, while the tower and pennant were placed at the mountain shrine.

Even the sword named “Little Fengdu” and the two swords from the Sword Immortal of the Hate Sword Mountain were often taken by that little bald head for fun, all kept together in the sword sheath.

The four flying swords connected end to end, resembling the most peculiar “long sword” in the world.

Only the earliest crafted Water Mansion had not received any embellishment from Chen Ping’an.

Back then, he first used the water seal as his fated item, performing refining work above the clouds of the Old Dragon City. The protector at that time, who later became the Southern岳 Mountain Lord, Fan Junmao, successfully forged a Water Mansion. With the assistance of the green-clothed boy managing the water currents and spiritual energy, the murals of the water gods on the walls were brought to life, as if the true deities were alive. However, after several fierce battles and the fluctuations in Chen Ping’an’s cultivation, the Water Mansion suffered several bouts of desiccation, with its murals peeling away and ponds drying up, which was a serious taboo in cultivation.

Within the small pond beneath the water seal, a water dragon coiled, as the water seal poured forth like a waterfall, causing the pond to resemble a dragon pool, aligning with the saying, “Water doesn’t need to be deep; with a dragon, it is spiritual.”

The white-haired boy glanced over, instantly perceiving Chen Ping’an’s state of mind, casually saying, “Dragon pools have always been the first choice for raising dragons. The sage interprets this character; ‘pool’ means gathering energy, and ‘bottom’ means stopping energy—all implying stagnation. Hidden Official, the problem with your Water Mansion’s dragon pool is simply too small; why don’t you deliberately expand its territory? It’s not as if you can’t do it. If it were me, I’d have that clever grandson of mine gather all the water pearls and toss them into the pond, exhausting those little Water Mansion folk.”

At this point, the foreign demon feigned a pitiful expression, lamenting, “The ‘pool’ signifies a state of sorrow. I’m deeply worried for you, Hidden Official.”

Chen Ping’an, still heavy-footed, replied, “I prefer water; I’m not troubled about the Water Mansion.”

The foreign demon shook its head, “For cultivators, the quality of the energy in their alchemical chambers is paramount. If all goes well, Hidden Official, your future alchemical chamber is highly likely to be the Water Mansion. However, you’re placing a few shabby items… oh no, I mean a few opportunities, just sitting at that mountain shrine, which is quite a loss. If it were me, I’d not care about anything, refining all treasures and accumulating them in the Water Mansion, preparing ahead is the best strategy. Forming the Golden Core is the top priority for cultivators, and the quality of the Golden Core directly determines a Qi practitioner’s future achievements.”

Chen Ping’an’s Water Mansion, aside from the troublesome water seal and the transient green-clothed boy, had other aspects that were naturally birthed, not unsatisfactory, but indeed insufficient.

Unfortunately, it was clear that Chen Ping’an did not heed his golden advice.

The foreign demon did not mind; if Chen Ping’an chose to pursue that path, it would only be a small matter with little significance.

In the eyes of an ascendant, all prodigies and talents are illusions. Unless the other party can one day become an ascendant, otherwise, to those who have already reached the peak, the so-called opportunities in the mountains, all struggles for the Dao and life, are merely a group of cats and dogs playing outside, amusing enough to glance at a few times, but if they become bothersome or noisy, they would simply be disposed of.

This foreign demon had been observing Chen Ping’an for quite some time and was quite eager to strike a big deal with the young man.

Chen Ping’an’s mind, like a seed, wandered to the mountain shrine, gazing upward from the foot of the mountain. The shrine, built from the five-colored soil of the New Five Sacred Mountains of Dali, was constructed atop a small mountain, later reinforced with the true meaning of the Tao contained in the green bricks.

The white-haired boy curiously asked, “Hidden Official, why do you have no greater aspirations regarding cultivation and enlightenment? Do you truly have no desire for immortality?”

As he walked, Chen Ping’an employed a six-step stance to continuously adjust his boxing frame, fine-tuning the minutiae of his muscles and bones to better adapt to his current physique. Upon hearing this question, he replied, “It’s too far; I can’t see it clearly, so I can’t imagine it.”

The white-haired boy exclaimed, “So you need a bit of light to guide your path. It’s a pity that you haven’t found it yet. It seems that among the enlightened ones in the righteous world, aside from knowledge, boxing, and swordsmanship, no one can truly capture your heart.”

Chen Ping’an did not wish to dwell on this matter, changing the subject, “That Executioner senior isn’t a local sword cultivator, right?”

The reason for this question was not only that there were no records in the Summer Palace but also that there were many clues: the colorful Twelve Flower Spirit Cup hanging under the grapevine, the bookworms consuming the divine characters, and the Executioner’s insistence that Du Shanyin learn swordsmanship to kill the flower thieves on the mountain, along with the two ancestral coins made of gold essence and the Grain Rain coin, which formed the figures of the sewing woman and the washerwoman. Even the Sword Qi Great Wall had elegant sword immortals like Sun Juyuan, yet they were still different from that enigmatic Executioner.

Local sword immortals of the Sword Qi Great Wall rarely have such concerns for outsiders.

What Mi Yu did cannot be called concern; it’s purely a penchant for attracting bees and butterflies, a nuisance amidst the myriad flowers.

The white-haired boy, who shared a deep understanding with the Hidden Official, immediately replied, “He’s not from here; his hometown is a lower-grade blessed land in the Liuxia Prefecture, with terrifyingly good talent. He broke through the barriers of heaven and earth in a heavily restricted lower-grade blessed land, where it’s difficult for cultivators to even enter the cave realm, and the Executioner forcefully ‘ascended’ to the righteous world using his Nascent Soul sword skills. However, due to his overwhelming presence, the originally secluded blessed land attracted the covetous eyes of various forces. Within a hundred years, it turned from a paradise into a playground for fallen immortals, with everyone fighting over it. Eventually, the blessed land was devastated by a battle among two sword immortals and an immortal realm Qi practitioner, leading to near extinction for the locals. The Executioner wasn’t strong enough at that time to protect his hometown, so he bears a heavy guilt to this day. It seems that none of the Executioner's family members or disciples managed to escape.”

Chen Ping’an could only sigh deeply within.

His own Fallen Mountain had a lotus root blessed land.

Chen Ping’an then frowned.

Typically, every lower-grade blessed land’s reality would attract waves of bloodshed and turmoil.

The situation in Fuyun Prefecture is currently chaotic. Aside from a few immortal treasures emerging, there’s also a pure martial artist who ascended, leading to a previously peaceful hidden blessed land being discovered by mountain cultivators, sparking a rush among various immortal forces. Though it’s another lower-grade blessed land, due to its ancient tradition of martial prowess and lack of arts, it has accumulated an abundance of treasures. Nearly all the sects in Fuyun Prefecture cannot stand idly by, eager to carve a piece for themselves. Moreover, Fuyun Prefecture is one of the regions with the deepest connections between the mountains and the mundane world. Immortal masters have their own schemes, while secular monarchs harbor their ambitions, thus any small movement can affect the entire body, leading to constant bloodshed and turmoil over these years, with smoke of war rolling across both the mountain and mundane realms.

The white-haired boy asked, “A business deal?”

Chen Ping’an smiled, “Let’s hear it.”

The white-haired boy spoke more seriously than usual, slowly saying, “Under the witness of Chen Qingdu, let me fully merge with your shadow spirit. I’ll choose to sleep for a hundred years. Within that century, as long as you reach the Jade Purity realm, you must return me a form of freedom. As a return, I’ll provide you with my ascendant Nascent Soul as a source of your Dao method, which will be inexhaustible for mid-five realm cultivators, allowing you to fight without worry about the scarcity of spiritual energy.”

Upon reaching this point, the white-haired boy’s eyes sparkled with excitement, feeling this deal was mutually beneficial, bouncing up and down in joy, “Not only will you reach the upper five realms without a doubt, but with me around, it’ll be like having a guardian deity, making any inner demons no problem at all. Moreover, before that, opening caves, observing the vast sea, leaping through the dragon gate, forming the Golden Core, and nurturing the Nascent Soul will surely be smooth sailing. There’s even a shortcut to breaking through faster, which requires using a secret technique to drop your realm to the third stage. I might be able to make you have a big dream in one night, allowing you to ascend to the upper five realms. With either choice, you won’t lose out, and there’s not a hint of danger!”

Chen Ping’an replied, “No thanks.”

The white-haired boy grew somewhat anxious, saying, “Even if you don’t trust me, can’t you trust Chen Qingdu? That old fellow’s judgment is exceedingly high and accurate!”

Chen Ping’an shook his head, “The moment I entertain that thought and speak to the Grand Sword Immortal, regardless of your plans, the Grand Sword Immortal will agree.”

The white-haired boy thumped his chest and stomped his feet, “Why do I have to encounter someone like you, who is so unyielding to reason? Why not take a gamble? A small loss if you lose, but a huge gain if you win—what's there to be afraid of? Cultivators must have a bit of guts; decisive in their killings! Hidden Official, you’ve truly disappointed me this time, utterly disappointed! You’ve completely chilled your grandson’s warm heart!”

The foreign demon began to act foolishly, while Chen Ping’an remained serious, “The reason I declined is not that I’m afraid of danger but that I don’t want to put us both in a pit, as this would go against my true heart. If I ascend to the upper five realms, my inner demons will likely shift, and you could become one of them, making your self-proclaimed status as a guardian deity fundamentally ineffective.”

The white-haired boy caught the implication behind Chen Ping’an’s words and asked in confusion, “Are you saying that if we set aside that unavoidable issue, hypothetically, if you reached the Jade Purity realm, you could kill me? Hidden Official, no matter how wise and powerful you are in my eyes, isn’t that a bit too arrogant?”

Chen Ping’an stopped walking, smiling, “Don’t believe me? Why not give it a try?”

The white-haired boy was eager to try but still fixed his gaze on Chen Ping’an, somewhat doubtful. After contemplating for a moment, he decided to enter the realm of Chen Ping’an’s new idea, “Let’s give it a shot!”

Having traveled through Chen Ping’an’s “heart” four times, he had seen many strange things. If he could witness something truly extraordinary, it would be an eye-opener, and he considered it a bit of fun.

Once the foreign demon entered the heart lake, Chen Ping’an took a deep breath, held his breath, and focused his mind, trying to call out.

In an instant, the foreign demon rolled out, its face pale, not only returning empty-handed but seemingly having sustained some damage.

The once proud and spirited ascendant presence had vanished without a trace.

The white-haired boy murmured, “Good scheme! Hidden Official, you’ve played me as a messenger sword that traverses two worlds. In the vast Sword Qi Great Wall, it seems I am the only one capable of doing this…”

Chen Ping’an asked, “Want to try again?”

The white-haired boy plopped down on the ground, leaning back and flailing his arms and legs, crying out, “I can’t live like this anymore! Hidden Official, you’re just bullying honest people!”

Chen Ping’an continued moving forward. This long-planned business was indeed coming to fruition.

Otherwise, why would he repeatedly allow a foreign demon to enter his heart lake?

The white-haired boy got up, following closely behind the young Hidden Official, still shaken and speechless.

Earlier, he had rushed into Chen Ping’an’s heart lake, only to find a golden arched bridge. At first, he merrily dashed along, enjoying himself, until he glimpsed a tall figure in white standing on the bridge railing, propped up by a sword, seemingly in a long slumber. When Chen Ping’an softly called out, this figure, which should have been merely an illusory semblance, unexpectedly “awoke” without warning. Moments later, she turned to look at the foreign demon, who felt something was amiss and abruptly halted.

The white-haired boy vowed he had never seen such a gaze in his life.

He couldn’t even make out her features, just those golden eyes.

From a high vantage point, devoid of any emotion, pure as the legendary highest deity.

Looking down on an ascendant like an ant.

Beneath the golden arched bridge lay what appeared to be the once-complete ancient human realm, filled with countless beings. The heavens and earth were distinct, yet the deities remained eternal.

Just a glance was enough to send the foreign demon tumbling out of Chen Ping’an’s small world, depleting what equated to a century of painstaking cultivation accumulated by an ascendant.

The foreign demon’s realm stagnated at the limit upon its birth, neither increasing nor decreasing, with only life and death to contend with thereafter.

The white-haired boy lamented, “Hidden Official, isn’t she on the same level as Chen Qingdu? You should have mentioned it earlier; with such a background, calling you grandfather isn’t enough; I should have called you ancestor instead!”

Chen Ping’an replied, “I am not a reincarnation of anyone; you have misunderstood.”

The white-haired boy scoffed, “You even managed to deceive a foreign demon; you’re quite the scholar.”

Approaching the prison entrance.

Chen Ping’an was gradually adapting to the significant differences between the Gold Body and Distant Traveler physiques, yet he still moved with a stoop, struggling to breathe, and it was no feigned act.

This was the aftereffect of Nianxin’s sewing; the heavier the bones, the more resilient the physique. The true names of the great demons inscribed upon him would only grow heavier. 

This was while several key great demon names had not yet been inscribed; Chen Ping’an couldn’t imagine what it would be like once Nianxin’s sewing was complete—would he be reduced to walking bent over?

Passing by five cages that held upper five realm demons, Yunqing congratulated him on his breakthrough from the sword light barrier.

The great demon Qingqiu merely hid within a fog barrier, its icy gaze fixated on the heavily burdened young man.

Among the other three great demons, one who had remained hidden until now finally revealed itself. This great demon, known as Zhu Jie, sat atop an unrolled green landscape painting. Under the scrutiny of Qi practitioners, they would find it vastly different from ordinary art; this painting resembled a true blessed land, not only featuring undulating mountains and pavilions but also living flora and fauna. Additionally, the sky was adorned with a breathtaking display of stars. The great demon, seemingly perched upon the heavens, hoarsely spoke, “Little fellow, your fate is truly fortunate.”

Chen Ping’an paused, merely observing the painting. The Summer Palace had noted that this great demon could seize mountains and rivers with brushstrokes, having served as a horseman for the great demon Huang Luan for hundreds of years. It could draw landscapes on the battlefield, capturing mountains and rivers in the painting. Once the scroll was rolled up, it could crush and annihilate all living beings depicted within. Qi practitioners of lesser realms could directly depict their form, ensnaring part of their soul into the painting. Thus, in the Wilds, it was common for demon clans to carry portraits of their enemies, complete with names, birth dates, and locations of their ancestral halls, then find this painter to commission a piece, after which they would buy back the painting containing their enemy’s captured soul.

The fourth great demon appeared as a woman-like jade purity realm sword cultivator, though her fated flying sword had suffered heavy damage in battle. She was known as Meng Po, a rare grass and wood spirit who had managed to study swordsmanship, wielding great killing power. In the Wilds, she once held sway, known as the master of a sword sect, with a reputed connection to the ascendant great demon, yet they were indeed partners in reality.

The last upper five realm demon, imprisoned yet continuously breaking through, had now reached the Immortal realm. According to the old deaf man, Chen Qingdu had once promised this demon that should it reach the ascendant realm, it could replace the old deaf man in overseeing the prison.

The white-haired boy appeared even more worried than Chen Ping’an, his face filled with concern, “Even if the Hidden Official has reached the Distant Traveler realm, dealing with these five seems to be a hopeless endeavor.”

Chen Ping’an nodded, “For now, yes.”

Descending the steps, most of the cages were already empty. Among the sixty-one mid-five realm demons, aside from the two disciples favored by the old deaf man, there remained five—each a tough opponent.

Chen Ping’an suddenly remarked, “It seems I need to reach the mid-five realm; otherwise, walking with a limp is too severe. Don’t mention upper five realm demons; even those five Nascent Soul demons are beyond my capacity to battle.”

The white-haired boy agreed, “The Hidden Official must hurry.”

Chen Ping’an sat down in the pavilion, while the white-haired boy maintained his decorum, floating outside the building.

Chen Ping’an smiled and asked, “Has that thought of hiding in my shadow spirit disappeared?”

The white-haired boy replied helplessly, “Though I treat others kindly, I’m not foolish.”

Chen Ping’an hesitated before fully summoning his fated items from the Qi mansion: a water seal, a five-colored mountain, a wooden deity statue, and a page of golden scripture.

The four key fated items orbited around Chen Ping’an, slowly rotating, their radiance differing, illuminating the surroundings of the chaotic void.

The white-haired boy drifted to the steps, asking, “What’s the order of these?”

Chen Ping’an replied, “Water seal, five-colored mountain, wooden statue of the Daoist, Buddhist scripture. However, I haven’t been able to find a suitable method yet. Moreover, the refining of the five elemental fated items was initially intended to rebuild the Longevity Bridge, so over the years, my battles and techniques have remained my weak points. However, Senior Nianxin suggested I rearrange a few of the fated items. For example, that Thunder Law Seal can be moved to my palm.”

The white-haired boy nodded, “Gathering the thunder will command all laws. Having all laws at your fingertips is an excellent suggestion. The key is to intimidate others; it’s much easier to conceal both your martial artist and sword cultivator identities than with your half-baked talismans.”

Chen Ping’an asked, “Aside from the Executioner’s stream, is there any other fire-related item in this realm suitable for refining?”

The white-haired boy nodded, “Yes. And it’s of extremely high quality. The reason I didn’t mention it earlier is simply because there’s no profit to be made, not comparable to that stream I can converse about.”

Three “extremely high” praises.

Chen Ping’an fell into contemplation.

He knew it was that magma furnace.

For matters devoid of personal gain, the white-haired boy had no interest, beginning to count on his fingers, “First, use talismans to feign weakness, if the situation turns unfavorable, then summon the pine needles and cough thunder, ‘disguising’ as a sword cultivator. If that gets seen through, annoyed, and they create distance, then strike down with an authentic Thunder Law. If the opponent is tough-skinned, then close the distance and unleash a few punches as a Distant Traveler martial artist. If I can’t win and can’t escape, I’ll casually release the caged sparrow while throwing a few punches. If that’s still not enough, then I’ll pull out the Moon at the Well… Hidden Official, I’ve run out of fingers!”

Chen Ping’an remarked, “You’re truly shameless.”

The white-haired boy beamed, “I’ve recognized a good ancestor.”

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 794: The Fifth Item

Chen Ping’an put away the four personal items and asked, “What’s your real name?”

“Shuangjiang,” Wu Die replied, a name concocted by the outside demon, which neither You Yu nor Du Shanyin believed.

The white-haired boy paused for a moment before continuing, “I come from a humble background in the Aiai Continent, so it’s better not to mention the surname of my wealthy patron. My original name was actually ‘Xiao Cao’ (Little Grass). Later on, after my life stabilized, I became a scribe for a wealthy young master. A private tutor helped me come up with the name ‘Shuangjiang’—it sounds imposing, but it’s not a particularly good name. Back then, I didn’t know much and was quite happy, thinking it tied me to the world of books.”

The white-haired boy leaned back, propping his legs up casually. “That old tutor was half a preacher to me—a Daoist in the Cave Dwelling realm, considered quite a remarkable figure in that small vassal state. In his youth, he dabbled in some rudimentary dragon-summoning techniques, helping people behind the scenes. Unfortunately, he was unlucky and never achieved much. Eventually, disheartened, he became a teacher, occasionally selling poems to make a bit of pocket money. One time, he set off on a journey, telling me he was going to explore the mountains and rivers, and never returned. Years later, I found out he went to a notorious brothel to settle a score for an official friend, but ended up losing his life and his soul was captured in a water lamp. In my fury, I risked my life to smash that river god’s shrine and statue, and still wasn’t satisfied. I even ate some fragments of the statue in anger, but the resulting chaos flooded a hundred miles, leading to a chaotic chase by the authorities.”

The demon with the name Shuangjiang chuckled, “Little Grass is not self-important; it has already forged a mountain of errors.”

Chen Ping’an had never heard of a great cultivator named “Shuangjiang” in the history of the Aiai Continent.

As for all the cultivators above the Fifth Realm, including those at the Jade Purity, Immortal, and Ascended levels, Chen Ping’an didn’t know many, aside from those from Baoping Continent, Tongye Continent, and Beijulu Continent. He couldn’t claim to have heard of them all, but after becoming a Hidden Official, he had made it a point to learn about the ascended beings in the Haoran realm, especially since the archives of the Summer Palace were vast, making it easy to follow the clues.

The white-haired boy sprung up like a carp, laughing heartily, “This is a fresh story I just made up. If the Hidden Official ancestor has heard it, that’s good enough.”

Chen Ping’an replied, “I can’t be certain of the truth of your story, but I can guess that you mostly hail from the Qingming Heaven.”

The white-haired boy replied, “I see where I slipped up. I shouldn’t have said I was being hunted by the authorities. In the Qingming Heaven, officials must have their registration certificates, while the Haoran realm’s officials wouldn’t have the guts or capability to do that.”

That realm, unlike the Haoran realm where various factions contended, was dominated by the Daoist sect, with a majority of officials and Taoists. Therefore, one wouldn’t see scenes of officials praying for rain; local officials could summon wind and rain themselves using techniques, and the status of the local mountain and water gods was quite low. Though they weren’t reduced to mere laborers, they couldn’t compare to the grandeur of the river deities and mountain gods in the Haoran realm.

Chen Ping’an mentioned, “I was fortunate to have traveled with Daoist Sun from the Daxuandu Sect in Beijulu Continent, and we had a fruitful journey together. If there’s a chance, I must go and express my gratitude.”

Daoist Sun, as the leader of the Daoist sword cultivators, had profound knowledge in both Daoism and swordsmanship. However, Chen Ping’an admired the old Daoist’s skill at playing tricks even more.

“Refined and extraordinary,” he mused.

Compared to Daoist Sun, he felt he was leagues away.

The white-haired boy nodded. “I figured it out. The middle-aged Daoist inside the wooden residence was indeed Daoist Sun’s junior. The wooden statue in the temple was crafted from the ancestral peach wood of the Daxuandu Sect, and the foundational intent of the Five-Color Mountains is also rooted in the Daxuandu Sect’s sword cultivators. I’m not blind, I can see that. So, when Zhu Jie said you were lucky, it’s both true and false.”

To visit another realm and pay respects to the Daxuandu Sect implied that Chen Ping’an would need to reach the Ascended realm.

Chen Ping’an then asked a crucial question, “Have you heard of the Three Mountain Refining Technique?”

The white-haired boy’s expression changed, “I’ve heard of it, but I’ve only heard of it.”

Chen Ping’an pressed on, “Can I use it to refine this divine heart? This corpse belonged to an ancient fire god’s assistant?”

The white-haired boy grinned, “Whether you can refine it, I can't say. As for the divine body, it’s not bound to any of the five elements; it encompasses everything. What’s lacking can be supplemented. This cage is meant for refining, but that furnace pool has never been tainted by the Sword Qi Great Wall, and it remains indestructible after ten thousand years. I’m not worried that you can’t refine it; I’m just afraid that after you do, your body and soul won’t withstand it. Both matters—fusing the five elements and true names—could end poorly. If you don’t believe me, ask Nianxin.”

Nianxin stood on the steps and crisply replied, “Unless I give up my Golden Talisman and Jade Tome entirely, using all the texts to construct the four walls of the heart chamber.”

Both treasured items were semi-immortal grade artifacts and the foundation of Nianxin’s Dao, a cost far from trivial.

Chen Ping’an inquired, “What are the conditions?”

Nianxin stated, “You’ve insisted on only sewing the upper body; I kindly ask you to abandon this absurd insistence.”

Chen Ping’an replied, “I refuse.”

The white-haired boy chuckled to himself, having waited a long time for this performance to begin.

Nianxin, irritated, responded, “Chen Ping’an! If you only focus on the limbs and upper body with the thirty-two sewing points, it’ll inevitably lead to imbalance. Do you think that’s sensible? As a seamstress, do you believe I’m the type of woman who cares about gender taboos? You, being the Hidden Official of the Sword Qi Great Wall, are a cultivator aspiring to the peak! Should you still care about these so-called gender defenses?”

Chen Ping’an nodded, “I care. In Nianxin’s eyes, I’m merely an object to be skinned, dismembered, and inscribed upon, but in my eyes, you’re still a woman.”

Nianxin’s face turned ashen with rage. “Chen Ping’an, you’re utterly unreasonable!”

The white-haired boy rolled on the ground, laughing heartily, though he struggled to suppress his voice.

What a delight, what a relief.

Chen Ping’an clasped his hands in apology. “I hope you can understand, Senior Nianxin.”

Nianxin vanished in a flash.

Chen Ping’an wasn’t particularly worried that Nianxin would throw in the towel, leaving the sewing matter half-finished. However, it was highly likely that the next round of sewing would bring him unnecessary suffering.

Once Nianxin departed, the white-haired boy straightened up.

Chen Ping’an smiled, “Senior Shuangjiang, why don’t you continue to enjoy the show?”

The white-haired boy lightly tapped his chest with his fist, “It pains me to see the Hidden Official ancestor misunderstood by Nianxin; the heartache is like a knife twist.”

You call your ancestor as you please; I’ll call mine, and we’re good friends.

Chen Ping’an asked, “If I refine it, will it affect the prison?”

The white-haired boy nodded, “Of course, the prison will lose half of its suppressive power. But it doesn’t matter; even if it’s all gone, there’s still an old deaf man nearby and a magistrate far away. Those demon clans won’t cause any chaos.”

Excluding the likes of Yunqing, the middle-level demon clans in the prison had only five nascent sword cultivators left, all seasoned and quite tricky.

Chen Ping’an remarked, “Yunqing will most likely break the restrictions and choose to leave the prison. Even if it’s only for a moment of freedom, he’d want to step out and see the ancient battlefield ruins. Meng Po would rather die under the magistrate’s sword than be killed by an unknown little figure like me.”

The white-haired boy rubbed his chin. “That’s true. What should we do?”

Chen Ping’an looked at him, recalling how he had acknowledged a good ancestor earlier.

The white-haired boy sighed, “I’ll keep an eye on those prison gates for the Hidden Official ancestor.”

Chen Ping’an said, “Senior Chengshan, please help me greet the old sword cultivator; I need to refine this item.”

The old deaf man’s voice echoed in his heart lake, “Do you need to prepare some heavenly materials and earthly treasures?”

Chen Ping’an shook his head, “Not needed.”

Besides the Five-Color Golden Cauldron, Chen Ping’an also possessed the “Guidance” opportunity gifted by the Fire Dragon True Person. After entering the Far Travel realm, it became increasingly clear that he merely needed Nianxin’s help to separate it, along with the Three Mountain Refining Technique—enough.

The white-haired boy’s expression turned gloomy. “Are you really not planning to transition from the Three Realms right to the Jade Purity?”

Once Chen Ping’an successfully refined it, he might very well cross a major threshold and enter the Cave Dwelling realm.

Chen Ping’an feigned ignorance.

The white-haired boy said seriously, “Then I’ll step back, giving up those little tricks. I no longer have plans to seize your skin; I only seek a place to reside to escape the prison, hoping one day to return to the Qingming Heaven. Besides, the conditions remain; I’ll consider it buying my life.”

Chen Ping’an still shook his head.

The white-haired boy slowly stood and transformed into a Daoist wielding a whisk, wearing a robe that was neither from the Bai Yujing Three Schools nor the Daxuandu Sect. Instead, it was a purple robe Chen Ping’an had never seen or heard of before, adorned with a front opening, long sleeves, and embroidered with sun, moon, stars, Taiji, Eight Trigrams, cloud patterns, and various celestial beasts—almost as if the robe itself was a vast, bounteous paradise.

Now cloaked in this heavenly attire, the Daoist’s eyes seemed to hold the shifting of constellations, his expression calm as he smiled, “Chen Ping’an, you schemed against me, made me send a sword message once, costing me a hundred years of cultivation. But you, as a Fifth Realm cultivator, have such wit; after five journeys, observing your mindset, how could I not leave behind a backup plan?”

Not only did the old deaf man arrive instantly, but even the sword light bestowed to Du Shanyin by the magistrate also flashed in, piercing through layers of spatial barriers, dazzlingly bright.

This might just be the “true form and essence” of the Ascended demon Shuangjiang.

Chen Ping’an waved his hand, signaling the old deaf man not to act, and locked eyes with the outside demon, asking, “Are you really forcing a sale?”

The Daoist “Shuangjiang” smiled, “Why not give it a try?”

Chen Ping’an nodded, “Let’s give it a shot.”

The old deaf man frowned.

Even if the trial ended with that demon’s demise, what benefit would it bring Chen Ping’an? Wasn’t it better to maintain a facade of cordiality like before? There was no gain in tearing the mask off for either party. However, for Shuangjiang, it was clear he was at his wits’ end. If Chen Ping’an left the prison without pleading for mercy from the old sword cultivator, and allowed the outside demon to escape, it would mean Chen Ping’an had made up his mind to let the old sword cultivator strike.

If Chen Ping’an hesitated, harboring thoughts of muddling through without either saving or killing, knowing the old sword cultivator’s temperament, he would let Chen Ping’an suffer the consequences.

An Ascended demon naturally had means to follow and escape, and in Chen Ping’an’s journey of cultivation, before returning to the Haoran realm, he would face endless troubles.

Of course, this was all contingent on whether Chen Ping’an could survive long enough to meet his own teacher, the Literary Saint of the One with Heaven.

Nianxin, returning, silently cursed Chen Ping’an for his impatience. Why, after reaching the Far Travel realm, did he seem to have changed completely? That scheming outside demon should be delayed. First, refine the item and break through; then, when successful, he could bring out the old sword cultivator. That would be much better than hastily engaging in a contest of wills with an Ascended demon.

Cultivators excel at refining items, while outside demons enjoy refining hearts.

Suddenly, the old sword cultivator appeared, “Can’t you let me have a breather?”

Every time that outside demon saw Chen Qingdu, it was like a mouse spotting a cat. This time, however, instead of reverting to the white-haired boy’s appearance, it asked, “Chen Qingdu, does our agreement count? Am I allowed to leave the Sword Qi Great Wall?”

The old deaf man wasn’t surprised.

Chen Qingdu had no interest in entertaining an outside demon.

As expected, he remarked, “You could try switching to a higher realm, like Hou Changjun, or simply find a naturally gifted vessel, like the disciple chosen by the old deaf man. As for whether you can survive leaving? Don’t ask me.”

Nianxin couldn’t help but laugh. Those last three words were so familiar.

The old deaf man’s expression darkened. He didn’t dare question Chen Qingdu’s decision, only regretting that his deal with Chen Ping’an had come too early.

Shuangjiang shook his head.

Chen Qingdu smiled and asked, “You’re just going to be shameless, huh?”

Shuangjiang remained silent.

Chen Qingdu turned back to Chen Ping’an.

Chen Ping’an stated, “As a Fifth Realm cultivator, I need to sew while also dealing with an Ascended demon’s schemes. Old Sword Cultivator, you have no reason to stand idly by.”

Nianxin felt that this young Hidden Official was bound to face misfortune again.

Unexpectedly, Chen Qingdu nodded with a smile, “Finally, you’ve learned to ask for something yourself. Rare.”

In the Haoran realm, Chen Ping’an sought everything for himself and asked nothing from others; Chen Qingdu couldn’t be bothered to intervene. But since he had become the Hidden Official of the Sword Qi Great Wall, it was only reasonable to ask him for a few things. Was the old sword cultivator merely a decoration?

---

**Mounting the Upside-Down Mountain**, Mi Yu begged Shao Yunyan to take him to that famous tavern, to drink the renowned Worry-Free Wine.

To his surprise, after much anticipation, when Shao Yunyan finally agreed, Nalan Caihuan insisted on joining them to enjoy the spoils.

The three entered the tavern, and Shao Yunyan noticed that, aside from the old shopkeeper and the young assistant, there was now a young woman with an unremarkable appearance, who was staring vacantly at the table. A stack of books was laid on the table, with one open beside her. The assistant, Xu Jia, sat next to her, keeping her company in her stupor.

Shao Yunyan recalled that the first time he came to the tavern, the girl looked somewhat like this, and now she hadn’t changed much. Women who practiced cultivation often had beauty-enhancing techniques, making them alluring.

After Mi Yu took a seat, he grabbed the wine and drank heavily, getting drunk without saying any drunken words, looking somewhat lost.

Nalan Caihuan took small sips, her gaze distant, as if recalling sad memories.

The old shopkeeper was teasing the sapphire-caged martial sparrow, laughing, “After the dismantling of the Yuan Ruofu and the relocation of the Plum Blossom Garden, even the Water Crystal Palace is now unsettled. Master Yunqian intends to take people north to select a site for a residence, and the Rain Dragon Sect’s master has come to the Upside-Down Mountain, causing quite a scene between the senior and junior sisters. This is all thanks to your new Hidden Official, right?”

Shao Yunyan nodded with a smile. “The Hidden Official has a kind heart. If it were me, I wouldn’t wade into these muddy waters. For common folks, it’s one thing not to understand fate; for cultivators, not to seek protection, isn’t that asking for trouble?”

In the paradise of Huangliang, drinking and speaking without restraint.

Mi Yu staggered to the wall and shouted, “Bring me a pen!”

Xu Jia stood up to hand him a pen, and the drunken Mi Yu wiped his face and wrote a line: “When the night falls and the lamp is lit, I dream of home, awakened by the oriole’s call, a pillow of Huangliang.”

Nalan Caihuan also approached and wrote a line: “The closest people are the hardest to get along with.”

Shao Yunyan glanced at the wall where the lines were written, noticing the differences in temperament between the two sword cultivators—one flowery and adorned, the other practical.

The girl suddenly raised her head and asked Nalan Caihuan, “Now that the Sword Qi Great Wall is on high alert, I cannot go to the southern city. How is that Ah Liang?”

Nalan Caihuan returned to her seat and replied with a smile, “What can be expected? Same old story.”

The girl looked forlorn, her eyes filled with sorrow like a spring pool brimming with feelings. “Everyone has returned to the Sword Qi Great Wall, yet no one has come to drink with me. With me at the tavern, at least you wouldn’t need to pay for the drinks. It’s a shame I rushed back from the Bai Zhi Paradise, only to not even meet anyone.”

The old shopkeeper chuckled, “You still have to settle your debts; the money owed still needs to be paid.”

The girl retorted, “Ah Liang said that debts aren’t really debts.”

The old shopkeeper nodded, “Ah Liang’s face isn’t really a face either.”

She flopped back down on the table, smacking it with her palms. “So boring! Had I known, I wouldn’t have come back to the Upside-Down Mountain. In that Bai Zhi Paradise, I would have had many children with Ah Liang by now.”

The old shopkeeper was too lazy to comment on this girl anymore.

Shao Yunyan didn’t want to listen to this tavern gossip and asked, “What are your plans, shopkeeper?”

The old man replied, “There’s a secret realm in the Fuyou Continent that hasn’t been around for long, a remnant of the Huangliang Paradise. I plan to go check it out. Once a sect takes it over, I’ll see if I can negotiate to buy it and expand the tavern. I’m about to set off, so if all goes well, you might be the last batch of guests at the Upside-Down Mountain tavern.”

The girl declared, “I’m not leaving. I won’t go anywhere without seeing Ah Liang.”

Xu Jia pointed upward and said softly, “Miss, not going anywhere might not work out; you might end up going over there all of a sudden.”

The girl shot him a glare, and the young assistant shrank back.

Mi Yu smiled and asked, “May I ask this young lady, how are the views in the Haoran realm?”

The girl glanced at Mi Yu, who, while not bad-looking, couldn’t compare to Ah Liang.

She casually replied, “Passable.”

Mi Yu murmured, “How can it be just passable?”

---

After leaving the demon army’s gathering place in the Wildlands, the little girl with the braids didn’t hurry to the ancient well that held the fourteen thrones.

Instead, she wandered leisurely, unafraid of taking detours.

Grabbing her two braids, she swayed in the wind, soaring through the skies. She went to the mountain peaks to enjoy the views and sought water palaces by large bodies of water. Unfortunately, it was said that the mountain and water deities in the Wildlands were not as flamboyant as those in the Haoran realm. After visiting several mountain shrines and water palaces, she felt somewhat disappointed.

With a punch, she killed a group of useless beings, and with a kick, she crushed a swarm of ants.

There were no rules to bind her; she acted according to her whims, and it felt great. When there was no wine, she used side dishes as substitutes, crunching on soybeans.

Then she was caught up with by two sword cultivators from the Hidden Official lineage, Luo Shan and Zhu An, who chose to follow her through the Wildlands. They had defected from the Sword Qi Great Wall alongside Xiao Xian, and with nothing to do in the military camp, they naturally wouldn’t turn their swords against the Great Wall. The Haoran realm was where their hearts truly lay, and once there, they would challenge any sword sect that hadn’t sent a sword cultivator to the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Above the sea of clouds, Luo Shan watched as the Hidden Official spun around in the wind, grasping her braids like a bamboo dragonfly, feeling somewhat helpless.

Zhu An laughed, “The Hidden Official should have left the Sword Qi Great Wall long ago.”

Next, they planned to tour a grand city in the Wildlands, the capital of a certain dynasty. The threshold was extremely high; to settle or enter the city, one had to be in human form. This meant that within that city, there were many demon cultivators skilled in techniques. Of course, there were also many shortcuts; one could pay to have the insufficiently powerful demon servants disguise themselves with talismans.

Such rules were rare in the Wildlands.

At the same time, it indicated that this dynasty was incredibly powerful.

The emperor and empress were both at the Immortal realm, and one of them was even a sword cultivator. This time, neither side had gone to the battlefield of the Sword Qi Great Wall. According to rumors from the Jiazi Account, it was a case of losing money to avert disaster, draining the national treasury.

A group of cultivators stationed in the capital rose on the wind, their armor resplendent, blocking the three from reaching the capital’s skies. An infant realm cultivator shouted angrily, “Who goes there?!”

Xiao Xian merely kept spinning, circling around the demon cultivators, and moments later, it sounded like firecrackers going off, with clouds of blood mist scattering in the wind.

A rainbow light shot up from the palace of the capital, pausing at a distance. It was a handsome man with long hair, dressed in a robe of striking bright red and gold, intricately embroidered with dragon patterns using peacock feathers, making the robe dazzling and eye-catching. Upon seeing the little girl with the braids, he immediately bowed and clasped his hands, “Hidden Official, your arrival is a great honor; I apologize for not welcoming you properly.”

Xiao Xian continued to spin, including the man, Luo Shan, and Zhu An in her circle. “I’m no longer the Hidden Official. Are you scolding me?”

The man bent even lower, “I would never dare offend the Hidden Official. In my heart, the Hidden Official of the Sword Qi Great Wall will always be you.”

Zhu An smiled knowingly; as a demon sword cultivator, he had picked up many bad habits from the human rulers of the Haoran realm.

Xiao Xian punched the great demon back into the capital.

When the great demon crashed through a palace roof, Xiao Xian followed, landing a kick on its back before delivering a final punch that sent the demon, now in its true form, deep underground.

Above the clouds outside the capital, Luo Shan remarked, “You’ve mentioned three Hidden Officials.”

Zhu An nodded, “Forgetful.”

---

**In the depths of the Ten Thousand Great Mountains**. 

An old blind man, guarding a thatched hut and vegetable patch, kicked an old dog that lay by his feet. He then lifted his head to gaze into the distance, scratching his face.

The old man’s cheeks were sunken, skin stretched tightly over bones.

The old dog spoke up from afar, “It’s hard to separate the Sword Qi Great Wall and the sword path’s fortune. Once the Moon-Trapping Mountain brings it into their fold, they can attack or retreat at will, and for the next ten thousand years, it should be the Haoran realm’s turn to worry.”

The old blind man slowly replied, “If even a dog knows this, how could Chen Qingdu not?”

Chen Qingdu wouldn’t let the Wildlands gain too much; achieving that would already be quite a feat.

To leave nothing behind for the Wildlands would be a fool’s dream. The question was how to move that wall that had stood for ten thousand years. Who could possibly move it? Those sword cultivators burdened with fortunes, both big and small, where would they be placed? It wasn’t as simple as just throwing them away; especially since Chen Qingdu likely still hoped that the young sword cultivators would carry the thought of the Sword Qi Great Wall in their hearts, willing to pass this thought down through generations—this was even more challenging.

Those young people from the Sword Qi Great Wall, once scattered far and wide, would soon understand one thing: without Chen Qingdu and the Sword Qi Great Wall, life and death would make even less sense than on the battlefield of their hometown in earlier years.

The Sword Qi Great Wall, a tavern, was desolate and empty. As long as a sword cultivator was present, no matter their rank, they would head to the city wall to fight.

Feng Kangle and Tao Ban sat side by side on a long bench, sharing a bowl of spring noodles. Suddenly, Feng Kangle asked, “Do you think we will die?”

Tao Ban thought for a moment and laughed, “No way! We’re still young, we haven’t made any money or drunk any wine—there’s no reason for it. Besides, we still have the second shopkeeper here!”

Feng Kangle nodded vigorously, then laughed, grabbing a huge mouthful of spring noodles.

---

Outside the small door of the prison, the old deaf man asked, “Are you really willing to part with the Golden Talisman and the Jade Tome?”

Nianxin nodded.

The old deaf man sighed, “Divine partners, just like that.”

Nianxin retorted coldly, “Watch your mouth.”

The old deaf man scratched his head, flipping his attitude faster than he could turn a page. Women’s thoughts were, in truth, no different from those of outside demons.

The white-haired boy squatting at the door shouted, “Clear the way! Let me guard the gates and protect the path for the Hidden Official ancestor alone!”

---

Within the pavilion, Chen Qingdu was surrounded by a view of the surroundings.

Confucianism, Buddhism, Daoism. Pure martial artists.

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 795: Travelers of the Human Realm

Nianxin wasn't someone who enjoyed watching the excitement, but for the first time, she felt a sense of curiosity towards this demon from the Outer Heavens of the Qingming World. The “true immortal appearance” of this Outer Heaven demon had profoundly shocked her, especially with the “Daoist Shuangjiang” draped in that astonishing celestial robe.
