Nianxin thought that if she could dissect the tens of thousands of “threads” woven into it, it would elevate her sewing skills to the next level. With a bit of luck, it might even bring her the opportunity to grasp the Great Dao that had eluded her for so many years.

“You're called Wu Shuangjiang,” Nianxin declared.

The white-haired boy crouching on the ground lifted his head. “And what else?”

Nianxin continued, “Wu Shuangjiang was a military cultivator in life, not a Daoist.”

At this point, she added, “Now, Wu Shuangjiang may not necessarily be dead.”

The white-haired boy chuckled, “Why a military cultivator? What’s your reasoning?”

Nianxin replied, “Wu Shuangjiang, the unparalleled general—sounds like a name fit for the battlefield, don’t you think? It would be a waste for someone who isn’t a military cultivator.”

Old Deaf felt that this little girl was truly not very bright. By her logic, if he was called Old Deaf and there was an old blind man in the southern mountains, then perhaps they were long-lost brothers? Indeed, if the little girl had any sense, she wouldn’t have stuck to sewing for so long. Those notorious demonic cultivators—like the Lone Rider of the South Sea, the Passerby, the Plague God, and the Seductive Corpse—were all on paths that couldn’t be changed. However, the seamstress, the executor, and the mirror seller had the option to switch paths midway. With proper operation, it wouldn’t be difficult to secretly turn into a celestial teacher of the charts. But no matter how Nianxin had become a seamstress, whether she was willing or not, she had made up her mind to walk this path to the end.

The white-haired boy spat on the ground, rubbed his face with both hands, and looked utterly bewildered. “Is that even possible?!”

Old Deaf asked, “Did Nianxin really hit the nail on the head?”

The white-haired boy imitated his ancestor, clasping his hands in his sleeves, his eyes filled with pity as he glanced at Nianxin, then at Old Deaf. Two fools—why not just admit they were father and daughter? If not for the current worries about the Great Dao and possibly losing their lives, he could have easily spun a series of thrilling tales about Wu Shuangjiang flooding the Water God Palace, burning the Fire Temple, stepping on the Mysterious Capital, striking the Celestial Drum, and attacking the White Jade Capital, ensuring every detail was tightly woven together with logic and evidence.

He turned sideways, lifting his butt, pressing his hands and ears tightly against the small door. “Why is there no sound? I’m so worried about Master Yinguang. With his penchant for holding grudges, if the alchemy fails, he will surely come after me. Grandson, granddaughter, you two hurry up and pray to the gods, be sincere. If it works, I’ll remember your contributions. From now on, the three of us will establish our own sect and worship Master Yinguang as our ancestor, so we won’t have to envy the many followers of the Justice Officials. By then, I’ll deal with that sewing lady and the washing maid, and Old Deaf can fight it out with the Justice Officials while Nianxin just stands by holding a water bucket…”

Nianxin pressed her foot against the white-haired boy’s head, gradually applying more force until half of his cheek was stuck to the door.

The white-haired boy didn’t seem annoyed at all.

Old Deaf felt somewhat envious of Nianxin. In the early years when he first encountered this Outer Heaven demon, they had clashed quite a bit. As for the ongoing rivalry with the Justice Officials, it had only escalated over the years. For some reason, Shuangjiang seemed particularly unconcerned about Nianxin. Old Deaf wasn’t afraid of the Outer Heaven demon causing trouble, but the lack of peace was ultimately bothersome. Back when the Outer Heaven demon had followed Old Deaf for eighty years, it had been difficult for him to find a moment of quiet for cultivation, until he finally had to call it “grandfather” to shake off its clinginess.

Nianxin removed her foot.

The white-haired boy maintained his position and said, “You greet Master Yinguang, and let him greet me back. I’ll promise to transform that ‘Crimson Purple’ robe for you, let you see it to your heart’s content.”

The white-haired boy seemed worried that Nianxin, being a Qi cultivator from the Haoran World, wouldn’t understand the profound nature of the “Crimson Purple” robe. He explained, “That feathered robe of mine is one of three replicas worn by the Dao Ancestor when he rode out on his ox. Although it was woven in later generations, it still contains boundless Dao intent. It’s one of the treasures of the Year-End Palace, the core of the mountain-water formation. Once the Ancestor shakes the robe, the mountain will look like it’s draped in a feathered garment, and even if a sword immortal strikes a thousand times, it remains unbreakable.”

At this point, the white-haired boy sneered, “The Year-End Palace is on par with the Great Xuan Capital. Nianxin, think carefully for yourself.”

Nianxin thanked him and no longer lingered at the door, ready to begin peeling away the words on the golden talismans and jade tablets.

Old Deaf praised, “Good skill.”

Shuangjiang stood up and shook his sleeves. “Good grandson.”

This act helped Nianxin, allowing her to gain a connection to the heavenly path. It also helped Chen Ping’an, as he wouldn’t have to suffer extra hardships under Nianxin while simultaneously repaying the debt of the golden talismans and jade tablets. As for Shuangjiang, he was also helping himself. He had previously received secret guidance from Chen Qingdu; rather than choosing to be adversarial with Chen Ping’an, it was better to befriend those around Chen Ping’an. It was clear that the guidance was a pretense, while the threat was genuine, clearly indicating that he needed to back off and not interfere with Chen Ping’an’s cultivation or lay traps.

Earlier, Shuangjiang wasn’t just scaring Chen Ping’an. After several journeys, using the Three Mountains and Nine Lords technique as a foundation, and subsequently deriving the Twenty-Four Mountain Methods known as Dragon Seeking, he had identified a “lucky spot,” termed as “pointing the vein.” In a secluded corner of the human realm’s void, he excavated a round pit the size of a mirror, termed “gold well,” then covered it with a wooden box shaped like a calabash. After that, the heart pit resembled a covered and dead water well, no longer seeing the “sun, moon, and starlight.”

Dragon Seeking, pointing the vein, breaking ground, and covering the box—each journey accomplished one step, while avoiding the patrolling fire dragon, especially that little golden figure who carried a dragon-horned sword and hung books. Every time they entered Chen Ping’an’s heart lake, the Outer Heaven demon would play hide-and-seek with that little fellow.

This was a deeply hidden ploy that wouldn’t affect Chen Ping’an’s current cultivation level at all. However, once this scholar’s mind became clouded, if there was a spot devoid of light, even if it was subtle, when Chen Ping’an’s realm became higher, it would grow as large as a mountain. Or Shuangjiang could simply break the gold well right now, leaving a flaw in Chen Ping’an’s heart realm, making the fundamental Dao incomplete. Could it be repaired? Of course, it could, as long as Chen Ping’an gifted this gold well to the Outer Heaven demon as a cave, not only would it patch the leaks, but it could also benefit his cultivation, becoming a source of Dao for a Qi cultivator.

As for refining the Three Mountains method, Shuangjiang was certainly not unfamiliar with it. 

Yet, Shuangjiang still hadn’t figured out one thing: from Chen Ping’an’s active inquiry about his name to the mention of the Fire Dragon Real Person’s teaching on the Three Mountain Refining Method, was Chen Ping’an doing this on purpose? Did he already sense the oddity, prompting him to tear his face and call in Chen Qingdu for support?

The white-haired boy couldn’t help but sigh, “Only able to create a Dao stage within a snail’s shell, restricting grandfather’s great divine powers.”

Chen Ping’an had refined four items of his fate consecutively: the Cloud Sea of the Old Dragon City, the immortal inn at the estuary of the Great Lake, the Dragon Palace’s cave heaven, and the hidden chamber in the Ning House of the Sword Qi Great Wall.

The last one belonged to the Five Elements, with two optional guardians: a flying ascendant demon and the Outer Heaven demon, Shuangjiang.

The small door slowly opened, revealing Chen Ping’an.

The white-haired boy immediately fawned, “Master Yinguang, your talents are so outstanding that it’s staggering! Refining items so quickly, even that Cao Ci wouldn’t be worthy of carrying your shoes… Huh? Why hasn’t Master Yinguang started refining yet? Is it because there’s too much martial fortune on you, and you haven’t thoroughly tempered it? How many martial artists in the world can understand such worries?”

Old Deaf felt that calling it a few times “grandfather” wasn’t a bad thing when it came to flattering someone.

Chen Ping’an said, “Let’s go out for some fresh air.”

Walking down the steps, the surroundings were all shrouded in dark, natural shadows, visibility relying solely on cultivation level.

Since the young Master Yinguang was heading down, the white-haired boy walked ahead, bending down and stretching out his hands to remind Master Yinguang to watch his step.

If they were ascending, the white-haired boy would follow behind, also extending his hands to prevent Master Yinguang from accidentally falling backward.

In terms of flattery, it seemed that among the followers of Master Yinguang, the likes of Mi Yu, Gu Jianlong, and Cao Gun would not compare to this Outer Heaven demon.

It seemed both entertaining and boring, but the white-haired boy silently counted in his heart, curious how long it would take for Chen Ping’an to deny this matter, which was indeed amusing yet dull.

Chen Ping’an paid no mind to the absurd behavior of this Outer Heaven demon, letting it stir up as it pleased.

Chen Ping’an truly hadn’t refined that magma furnace. The martial fortune within him wasn’t the reason; Nianxin had previously helped extract two fire seeds from that fire dragon, which were the two eyes of the fire dragon. Compared to a pure martial artist’s true energy that formed the roaming fire dragon, those two fire seeds were external items. After Nianxin had skinned them away, it didn’t harm the fire dragon’s essence at all. However, the process of “extracting the eyes” had been somewhat unexpected. As a seamstress in the Jade Purity realm, she was unexpectedly unable to suppress that unruly true energy fire dragon. If she had forcibly skinned away the two eyeballs, it would have likely caused a huge uproar, harming Chen Ping’an’s fundamental essence. This was probably the inherent discord between Qi cultivators and pure martial artists.

Chen Ping’an had to negotiate with that golden little figure. After much persuasion and receiving countless insults, the latter finally stepped on the fire dragon’s head, making it docile and allowing Nianxin to retrieve the items.

Up until this point, everything had gone smoothly. However, once Chen Ping’an entered the small door and began operating the ancient immortal formula taught by the Fire Dragon Real Person, he found himself in an awkward situation. This was due to the rain-summoning stele outside the Water God Temple of the Bi You Mansion, which had evolved into a refining mantra that faintly resembled a disappointed person hiding away, wallowing in self-pity, operating the technique solo and causing ripples in his heart lake. Under normal circumstances, this would be a good omen of success in cultivation and communication with the heavens, a sign of great fortune. However, at this critical moment of refining fire attribute items, it became a troublesome issue. By the time Chen Ping’an sensed something was off and sent his mind to the Water Mansion, he indeed saw those green-clad boys all restless, curled up beneath a mural resembling a water fairy’s worship. It was evident that within Chen Ping’an’s microcosm, there was a budding conflict between water and fire. This was because Chen Ping’an had an affinity for water and aimed to refine an unimaginable divine heart of the fire attribute, hence the conflict became most pronounced. 

Previously, there was the Water Mansion, then the Mountain Shrine. Since they were mutually dependent on each other, it instead aided the refining process. Subsequently refining the wood attribute fate item, both water and earth assisted, and the atmospheric phenomena within his microcosm also posed no hindrance.

Afterward, regardless of how Chen Ping’an suppressed the atmosphere of the Water Mansion, the effects were minimal.

Chen Ping’an stood outside a prison cell, which held a Yuanying sword cultivator of the demon race, under the alias Huang He, whose fate sword was named “Lin Li.” His true form was that of a scorpion, categorized under the “searching mountain” entries. 

Chen Ping’an often stood here without saying a word, while Huang He was deeply focused on nurturing his sword, treating the young man outside as if he were invisible.

Chen Ping’an asked, “Do you have a method to suppress them? Use the Mountain Sealing Technique to close the Water Mansion’s doors.”

The white-haired boy wore a mournful expression and replied, “Master Yinguang, ranks are ranks, and business is business. Right now, we have a clean break, so don’t take advantage of me, alright?”

Chen Ping’an said, “Why not do business? Starting now, we’ll truly start doing business. As long as what you give is enough, you could earn yourself a life. Your oath means nothing, but my oath is absolutely true. When the time comes, I’ll plead with the big sword immortal for you. However, there’s a bottom line: if you scheme against others, I already have an agreement with the big sword immortal. You scheme against me, and I’ll chop you down with one sword.”

The white-haired boy asked, “Are you really willing to change your mind and let me leave the prison?”

Chen Ping’an replied, “It’s a matter of order; you schemed against me first, wanting to seize my spirit and soul, coveting my entangled karma and some of my fortune, hoping to hide deeper. Once you succeed, even the big sword immortal might find it hard to kill you completely. You’d take all the advantages, so why should I let you leave the prison alive? Do you really think I’m your grandfather or ancestor? If you were my ancestor, with your character, I would have long since executed you for treason.”

The white-haired boy pouted and said, “Aren’t you trying to get me to pave the way for you, to tell you more about the insider rules of the Qingming World, preparing for your future ascension to the Qingming World, and making plans for that sword challenge at the White Jade Capital?”

“Did I say otherwise?” Chen Ping’an smiled as he rubbed the white-haired boy's head. “Why not call me ancestor anymore?”

The Outer Heaven demon cheerfully responded, “Alright then, ancestor!”

Chen Ping’an turned his palm into a fist, and with a bang, the Outer Heaven demon shattered. Then, in another location, it reformed into a humanoid shape, wearing a blue snake pendant and a Daoist robe, bouncing back, excitedly exclaiming, “This punch from Master Yinguang truly showcases the elegance of the Traveler Realm!”

Chen Ping’an lightly twisted his wrist, stepping into the Traveler Realm, clearly much stronger than in the Golden Body Realm. He just didn’t know where Cao Ci was currently situated in terms of realm.

The white-haired boy slyly revealed, “For refining items, Master Yinguang holds two immortal formulas, and both sides claim they can refine all things. So, the method of refining formulas?”

Chen Ping’an thought for a moment but shook his head. “If I must choose one over the other, it’s truly difficult to decide. Moreover, once refined into one formula, I’m unsure what the outcome will be. Additionally, there are too many uncertainties in this process. The two immortal formulas have too high a rank, and my cultivation level as a Qi cultivator is too low. So, you can say your true thoughts now. How do we calculate this first deal? Let’s sum it up?”

The white-haired boy held up two fingers, saying, “Actually, this is the second deal. Nianxin will be looking for you soon.”

Chen Ping’an folded his hands in his sleeves, smiling, “This doesn’t count as a deal; it’s your recognition of your ancestry.”

The white-haired boy also folded his hands in his sleeves, his eyes twinkling, nodding, “That makes sense.”

Chen Ping’an said, “I told you before, there’s nothing that can’t be discussed in this world; you just didn’t believe it.”

The white-haired boy candidly responded, “At least I’m a transcendent being of the ascended realm, easily swayed.”

The Yuanying sword cultivator, Huang He, who was imprisoned, stopped nurturing his fate sword and opened his eyes to watch the “harmonious” duo of grandfather and grandson outside the sword light barrier. Suddenly, a thought arose in his heart: if the young people from the Haoran World were all like this, perhaps our demon race should refrain from causing a ruckus over there. Literate and educated, their hearts were steeped in ink, their guts and intestines were dark as well.

After leaving the prison, the white-haired boy understood why Chen Ping’an had remained for so long. But having seen the young man’s two heart realm scrolls, he dared not act cheekily in such matters.

Chen Ping’an then inquired, “Are there any corresponding local customs regarding the Five Poisons in the Qingming World?”

Shuangjiang nodded, “There are many. For instance, in the marketplaces, colorful paper is cut into five-colored small gourds and pasted upside down on doors, known as disaster-repelling gourds. In the government offices, clean officials who handle documents will wear Daoist robes bestowed by the Daoist sect with illustrations of the five poisons, and then they will go to all the water sources in their jurisdiction to drop in several Grain Rain talismans.”

Chen Ping’an remarked, “In the southeastern part of the Northern Jiulu Continent, there are also customs of posting Grain Rain notices up and down the mountains. For wealthy families, having a divine hand-written notice at the door is something to be proud of, not inferior to hanging the plaque of their main hall.”

Shuangjiang stated, “Once your realm is high, new troubles may follow closely behind. However, there’s one good thing: the realm of cultivators can genuinely resolve many troubles. As one's realm rises, many troubles will naturally disperse. Good fortune comes unbidden, and evil guests will leave without dismissal.”

Chen Ping’an seemed enlightened, nodding in acknowledgment, “That’s a good saying. I appreciate the lesson.”

Shuangjiang raised his hand to wipe away a tear of bitterness, sobbing, “Your words, Master, are truly touching.”

Nianxin arrived shortly, and with matters of the Great Dao at hand, there was no need for shyness. 

She wasn’t like Chen Ping’an, a big man who felt shy about anything; women shouldn’t be so indecisive.

Chen Ping’an was very interested and decided to observe from the side. 

A celestial robe, of which there were many in the Qingming World, Nianxin began to meticulously dissect the thirty-six thousand intricately woven threads with her sewing skills. Just this process was an encounter with the Dao that was hard to come by.

Nianxin first presented the golden talismans and jade tablets, saying, “I originally planned to wait until you succeeded in refining the items, let you suffer a little first, then help you create a heart chamber.”

Suddenly, she asked, “Do you have any talisman paper of higher quality? Otherwise, it won’t be able to hold these words. If the quality isn’t good, they’ll need to be stacked together, which wouldn’t be a small number.”

Chen Ping’an took out a piece of blue talisman paper from his belongings.

The white-haired boy’s eyelids twitched slightly.

Nianxin nodded, instructing Chen Ping’an to place the talisman paper beside the golden talismans and jade tablets.

She took out the law knife “Willow Muscle,” which was to be refined into her fate item, and began to peel away the words from the golden talismans and jade tablets one by one. It looked like an ordinary short knife, but the blade tip was incredibly slender.

Every time a word left the talisman, Nianxin would immediately flick it onto the blue talisman paper, and the words would embed themselves into the paper, slightly sinking down without breaking it.

Finally, Nianxin’s complexion turned pale, as if her internal organs were churning and grinding against each other, blood and flesh a muddled mess, resembling a quagmire.

Nianxin opened her sewing bag, took out some crimson pills of unknown origin, stuffed a handful into her mouth, and chewed them recklessly before swallowing them down.

Chen Ping’an folded that piece of talisman paper, feeling its weight, and carefully tucked it into his sleeve. After standing up, he solemnly clasped his fists in thanks.

Nianxin ignored him completely.

From beginning to end, despite suffering greatly, even to the point where her Jade Purity realm was beginning to teeter, her brows had never once furrowed.

Chen Ping’an felt that Nianxin could actually switch to martial arts.

Being carved by someone else’s knife and remaining unyielding was one realm, while being carved by one’s own knife and remaining unmoving was another.

Nianxin looked towards the white-haired boy.

The white-haired boy hadn’t transformed into the true appearance of the “Ascended Realm Master Shuangjiang,” but instead glanced at the expressionless Master Yinguang beside him, then shrank back, extending two fingers to pinch a corner, slowly pulling it, causing a burst of light to flow, illuminating the celestial robe. Then the white-haired boy suddenly yanked it, grabbing the robe in his hand. It was an ethereal Daoist robe, shimmering with colors like a waterfall, the clouds and mist surging.

Chen Ping’an asked curiously, “The form is fake, the robe is also fake, so why is it so real?”

Nianxin’s eyes were fervent as she felt that Chen Ping’an was too much of a novice, saying, “It contains Dao intent; in the world, it nearly manifests the Great Dao. How can one speak of authenticity?”

Chen Ping’an was amazed. His own robe, Golden Nectar, although raised to an immortal weapon by continuously “feeding” it with golden coins, was nothing compared to the profundity of this robe.

The white-haired boy angrily scolded, “Hey, little girl, how can you speak to my ancestor like that?! Show some respect!”

Nianxin responded with a cold smile, glancing at Chen Ping’an. Chen Ping’an looked at the white-haired boy, who was looking around and laughing.

Nianxin took the robe, which felt extremely light, almost weightless, opened her palm, and caressed it gently, her expression like a drunkard savoring fine wine, like a lover caressing a beautiful woman’s skin.

Chen Ping’an felt somewhat intimidated. Earlier, the lewd remarks of the female sword immortal Xie Songhua, and now Nianxin’s gaze towards her beloved items, made it hard for Chen Ping’an to withstand.

The white-haired boy informed Nianxin of the numerous restrictions on this robe. She sat down gently, placing the robe softly on her knees, summoning ten fate item embroidery needles, combining efforts to lift a thread, slowly pulling it into a ball of thread, which she placed at her feet.

Just pulling out a single thread consumed a whole incense stick’s worth of time.

Nianxin expended a great deal of mental energy, closed her eyes, and began to breathe and circulate her energy.

During this time, a tiny error in the needle’s position could trigger multiple restrictions. The sun, moon, and stars, as well as mountains and rivers on the robe, would change color. Ultimately, the robe unexpectedly put itself on Nianxin’s body, causing her soul to tremble, as if she had been thrown into a forbidden world. Shuangjiang quickly maneuvered the robe away from Nianxin’s body, showing the danger inherent within. Nianxin spat out a mouthful of congealed blood, which she then stored back in her sewing bag.

Chen Ping’an sat on the steps and silently left after watching for a while.

Until then, it felt like being in a common household, watching a woman sew under the lamp.

The white-haired boy inquired with his heart, “No need to close the Water Mansion anymore?”

Chen Ping’an shook his head. “Not necessary. The heart is calm now.”

The white-haired boy unusually didn’t follow him out. He propped his chin on his hands, watching Nianxin’s needlework, softly saying, “If this were real, the moment you start to pick the needle, it would trigger the restrictions. If no one helps you take off the clothes, you’d die.”

Nianxin was completely focused, treating it as if it were the wind passing by her ears.

The thread balls around her feet continued to accumulate, clustering together like miniature suns and moons snuggling against each other.

Suddenly, the white-haired boy frowned and stood up, his expression unusually serious.

Nianxin had just planned to pick the needle when she halted her motion.

Someone stepped out from behind the door, and the sound of his heartbeat resonated like a drum of a deity.

With each thump of the heartbeat, the entire prison microcosm trembled.

The Summer Retreat Palace received a flying sword message.

Sword Immortal Qiumiao handed the secret message to Song Gaoyuan, coming from the Upside-down Mountain Water Crystal Palace. The envelope bore only a seal with an insignia, without a signature, making it impossible to identify the owner of the seal.

Song Gaoyuan was accompanying Xuan Can, both focused on a certain battlefield within the ground scroll. After reading the secret message, he hesitated to speak.

Currently, the sword cultivators of the Hidden Official lineage felt much more relaxed. If they wanted to go fight on the city walls, there was no need to adhere to the three-person rule; whether alone or in groups of three or five, they could go whenever they pleased. At that moment, Dong Buding, Guo Zhujiu, and Luo Zhenyi, three female sword cultivators, set off together from the Summer Retreat Palace. Additionally, Xu Ning and Gu Jianlong, along with Cao Gun, also set off together.

Qiumiao chuckled, “What are you hesitating about? Learn from Lin Junbi.”

After some hesitation, Song Gaoyuan said, “I’ll write a reply to send to the Upside-down Mountain Water Crystal Palace. I want to wait until Sword Immortal Xie Zhi withdraws from the battlefield before going to the Upside-down Mountain with this senior.”

Qiumiao questioned, “Are you really going to leave your sect’s senior waiting at the Upside-down Mountain? That doesn’t seem right.”

Song Gaoyuan replied, “Master Rongguan won’t mind. She intended to travel to the Upside-down Mountain anyway.”

Qiumiao let him be.

The next day, Dong Buding and the three female sword cultivators returned to the Summer Retreat Palace. Luo Zhenyi suddenly remembered something and informed Song Gaoyuan that she had brushed past Sword Immortal Xie Zhi on the battlefield and asked her to relay a message that he shouldn’t wait for her.

Pang Yuanji stood up, striding over the threshold, ready to fly his sword to the city walls, saying, “Song Gaoyuan, I won’t see you off.”

On this day, Song Gaoyuan left the Summer Retreat Palace, and before leaving, Qiumiao handed him a package from Master Yinguang.

Song Gaoyuan slung the package over his shoulder and set off alone. After passing through the gate, he reached the Upside-down Mountain and found the Water Crystal Palace, where he saw his sect’s female ancestor, Master Rongguan.

The young sword cultivator, upon seeing his ancestor, didn’t care that there were several female immortal teachers from the Rain Dragon Sect beside Master Rongguan. With reddened eyes, he trembled as he said, “So many have died. Senior Xie Zhi has also not returned home.”

Master Rongguan sighed, unsure how to comfort this junior.

The young sword cultivator, Xuan Can from the Golden Armored Continent, crossed the gate with the female sword immortal Song Ping, heading straight for a ferry.

Song Ping was filled with a heavy aura of killing intent, as though her mind hadn’t truly departed from the battlefield.

Also accompanying them were two young girls from the Sword Qi Great Wall, both of whom were young cultivators. The one with a stern face was named Sun Zao, while her sister Sun Qu was practicing martial arts. Unlike Sun Zao, the other girl, named Jin Luan, was looking around curiously.

They would follow Sword Immortal Song Ping in her training, and once they reached Song Ping’s sect, they would be formally accepted as direct disciples in the Ancestor Hall.

The group reached the ferry near the Mi Lu Cliff, where they would board a ferry to cross over to the Golden Armored Continent.

Song Ping and Xuan Can were returning home, while the two girls were leaving their home for the first time, traveling thousands of miles away.

At the ferry, the female sword immortal bought two boarding jade tokens. When it came time to board, the ferry attendant questioned why the two little girls didn’t have jade tokens, as that was against the rules.

Of course, Song Ping recognized them; he wasn’t blind. Such stunningly beautiful girls carrying a long sword rumored to contain a vast amount of sword energy, cultivators from both the Golden Armored and the Fuyao continents could easily identify them.

Song Ping said, “I’m giving you face, so take it well.”

Xuan Can remained calm, feeling that Song Ping’s words were entirely justified.

In the end, the ferry attendant rushed over, personally paving the way for them to board.

Jin Luan’s mouth dropped open slightly, as she was somewhat bewildered. This was not how Sword Immortal Song Ping usually interacted with them; she was always smiling and gentle, with an excellent temperament.

The ferry provided several good rooms, and Song Ping took the two little girls to a scenic viewing platform, smiling, “This is the scenery of the Haoran World.”

Jin Luan whispered, “There’s too little sword energy.”

Sun Zao rolled her eyes, “Of course. Can it compare to our Sword Qi Great Wall?”

Jin Luan fell silent, not because she was afraid of Sun Zao, but because she was intrigued by the various stories of the mountains and rivers that Sun Zao had shared.

Song Ping gently said, “So you need to adapt quickly. Once you reach the sect on the Golden Armored Continent, your master will reserve two peaks rich in spiritual energy for you, and when you reach the Golden Core Realm, a peak-opening ceremony can be held, and that will be your residence. From that moment on, you will finally have stable footing in the Haoran World.”

On the viewing platform of the adjacent room, the young sword cultivator stretched out his hand, lightly waving, greeting the two little girls.

Jin Luan stood on tiptoe, smiling brightly, “Brother Xuan Can!”

Xuan Can made a face at her.

Sun Zao suddenly became sad and gently tugged at the female sword immortal’s sleeve, sobbing, “Master, I miss home.”

Song Ping held the little girl’s hand, softly saying, “In the future, apart from your master, don’t say such things to anyone else.”

Sun Zao, unaware of the context, quickly wiped her tears away, nodding with a smile.

As night fell, a gaunt and tall old man stepped through the gate, immediately stopping to close his eyes, tilting his head to sniff the air, chuckling, “Long time no see.”

It was the Jade Purity realm sword immortal Pu He, though now he had regressed to the Yuanying realm. Even dressed in a robe, he couldn’t hide the lingering stench of blood on him.

Following Pu He into the Upside-down Mountain were Cao Gun and a pair of young sword cultivators from the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Cao Gun had only become a sword cultivator of the Hidden Official lineage when he was still at the Dragon Gate realm, but now he was a guest at the Golden Core level.

The youth and girl Pu He had taken from the Sword Qi Great Wall were not particularly outstanding talents; the boy was merely at the cave dwelling level, having ordinary aptitude among the sword cultivators. 

However, they suited Pu He’s taste.

As for the sea-viewing realm girl, she had better aptitude, but Pu He planned to have a close friend from the mountain teach her; as a sword immortal known for his fighting prowess in the Liuxia Continent, he naturally had several cherished female friends. Although the other party now outranked him by a realm, even if she still looked like a young girl, once they met, she would still have to call him “Big Brother Pu” in a roundabout way.

The boy complained, “Pu Laoye, when will you become a sword immortal again? Otherwise, I’d be too embarrassed to have you as my master.”

Pu He scoffed, “Taking you as a disciple at the cave dwelling level—do you think that would bring me honor? Do you know that at the drinking parties in Liuxia Continent, Golden Core cultivators aren’t even qualified to sit? They can only stand and drink?”

Cao Gun had nothing to retort.

After all, what Pu He said was absolutely true. A proud Golden Core Earth Immortal would often avoid attending banquets where Pu He was present, but many were willing to go otherwise.

The boy angrily shouted, “Don’t call me ‘old man’ again!”

Pu He, unfazed, laughed, “Just as I expected from my disciple. When you don’t drink, you talk nonsense; after you drink, you’ll unsheathe your sword at the slightest disagreement, making everyone in the continent look at you!”

However, the boy refused to appreciate it, saying, “A little Yuanying, acting so tough. If it weren’t for your familiar face, people would think a Transcended Realm practitioner is yawning here.”

Cao Gun felt increasingly speechless.

What kind of master had what kind of disciple—it was a family affair.

The quiet girl envied her peers’ boldness. She wouldn’t dare speak to the sword immortal Pu He like that.

The boy remarked, “I’ve heard you have many enemies in the Liuxia Continent. Now that you’ve regressed, won’t it endanger me being butchered by your enemies?”

Pu He pressed down on the boy’s head, pushing him away, “Stop saying such ominous words.”

The ferry they were riding would stop at the ferry near Lingzhi Zhai. Pu He had just planned to visit that immortal shop to buy a few items, but he had very little money left in his pocket, so he could only choose the cheaper items. If that didn’t work, he’d have to borrow money from that brat Cao Gun; the depth of friendship in the Sword Qi Great Wall was determined by lending money and inviting drinks, after all—it was a one-way trip.

At Lingzhi Zhai, the girl was lively and spirited, while the boy didn’t want to enter, merely sitting on the steps. 

Cao Gun accompanied him, sitting beside him.

A group of people boarded the ferry overnight. The boy leaned on the railing, weakly saying, “Pu Laoye, is this really your Haoran World? It doesn’t look that impressive.”

Pu He chuckled, “Remember this: practicing sword on the Sword Qi Great Wall is different from practicing sword in the Haoran World. Therefore, if your realm stagnates in the future, it’s perfectly normal; you don’t need to be anxious. I, Pu He, will eventually have a great sword immortal as my disciple!”

The ferry attendant stood nervously not far away.

Even though the youth from the Liuxia Continent hadn’t heard from Pu He for a long time and had only heard that Pu He had been defeated at the Sword Qi Great Wall, Pu He’s reputation, especially his eccentric temperament, still made many five-realm cultivators and Earth Immortals feel apprehensive.

There’s a saying that when Pu He smiles, someone will die.

Damn, that must mean he’s going to draw his sword!

Pu He was the sect’s elder ancestor, a proper chart immortal, but he acted without restraint, capable of murder, robbery, and deception, skilled in disguise, and especially good at framing others. His methods were so wild that even the wild cultivators had to call him “ancestor,” so his reputation wasn’t great on the mountain, but among the rivers and lakes, he was extremely well-known. 

Not long ago, Jiang Shangzhen had caused a stir in the Northern Jiulu Continent, and he had once been hailed as the second Pu He, both being the sort of scoundrel who’d mess around and be on the run while still in their own pants.

Yet, the ferry attendant found it hard to reconcile the current old man with the sword immortal Pu He from his memories.

Arriving at the door, Pu He tossed two bottles of pills to his disciple, instructing the boy to apply one externally and swallow the other. Once the boy closed the door, he took off his clothes, gritting his teeth, revealing a massive scar on his body that had yet to heal.

It was Pu He who had pulled him out from a pile of corpses.

After applying the ointment and swallowing the pills, the boy redressed, sitting cross-legged on the bed, diligently cultivating, nurturing his fate sword.

Moments later, there was a knock on the door, and Cao Gun announced his name.

The boy, who had been candid with Pu He, was quite respectful towards this sword cultivator from the Hidden Official lineage, even though Cao Gun’s realm wasn’t high.

The boy quickly opened the door. Cao Gun saw the somewhat restrained boy and smiled, “Let me tell you some important points about cultivating in the Haoran World. Don’t find it bothersome. As a chart immortal, there are tedious formalities—might not be charming, but you should listen.”

The boy perked up, listening intently.

Cao Gun finally said, “In the future, when following Sword Immortal Pu He, cherish it.”

The boy, named Ye Du, nodded vigorously, “My master… is this one!”

Cao Gun looked at the spirited boy, giving a thumbs-up, suppressing a laugh. 

The elderly Pu He, who had been lingering outside the room, nodded with a smile and went to find some wine to drink.

In the Ailong Continent, the sword cultivator Deng Liang, alone and downcast, left the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Having practiced there for many years, he had only managed to bring his realm to the brink of Yuanying, never breaking through to the upper five realms.

Previously, the sect had asked the ferry to help send two messages to the Summer Retreat Palace from the Upside-down Mountain, inquiring when he would return. Deng Liang had ignored them.

Though Deng Liang hadn’t stood out as much as Cao Gun and Xuan Can, making it easy for people to forget one fact: Deng Liang was an extraordinarily young Yuanying realm sword cultivator!

Not only did he have a seat in the Ancestor Hall of his Ailong Continent sect, but his position was also quite prominent.

Having come from the wild cultivators, Deng Liang had crawled and struggled for many years, becoming a chart immortal. He was meticulous in dealing with people, thus well-liked, and was someone the sect leader valued and relied upon greatly.

Before leaving the Sword Qi Great Wall, Deng Liang visited a tavern, writing on a blank slate, “Arrived as Yuanying, leaving as Yuanying, never breaking through. I’m ashamed to face the fine wine.”

With his package slung over his shoulder, he boarded the ferry.

The ferry attendant personally welcomed him, and Deng Liang exchanged polite laughter with him.

Deng Liang first sent a message to his sect via flying sword, simply stating that he had set off on his return journey.

Once inside the cabin, he took off his package, and aside from a few blank slates that had become relics, he also had some miscellaneous items. Deng Liang took out a letter, which Sword Immortal Qiumiao had told him to open after boarding, claiming it was a personal letter from Master Yinguang. The handwriting was very familiar, and the letter mentioned several matters, one of which was a request for Deng Liang to send a letter to Sword Immortal Xie Songhua, and another was to help take care of some sword cultivators that Xie Songhua had brought away from the Sword Qi Great Wall. The letter also mentioned a secret matter concerning the fifth world, asking him to bring it to the sect’s Ancestor Hall. If Deng Liang’s sect truly had intentions on this, they could prepare early.

Deng Liang put away the letter, left the room, and went out to enjoy the night view—the sky was high and the moon bright.

He missed the Summer Retreat Palace, feeling admiration for the young Master Yinguang.

At the Spring Banner Hall of the Upside-down Mountain, Yan Ming rose from his desk after a discussion about an important matter, smiling, “These days working with everyone has been very enjoyable.”

Mi Yu, Shao Yunyao, Nalan Caihuan, and Wei Wenlong all stood up simultaneously.

Mi Yu said nothing, only clasping his fists in farewell.

Shao Yunyao smiled, “Being able to spend day and night with Sword Immortal Yan is a great honor.”

Nalan Caihuan clasped his fists, saying, “Yan Ming, the head of the household, is good at making money. I may not lose to you, but as a sword cultivator, I am not as good as you.”

Mi Yu’s expression dimmed. “I’m even less so.”

Yan Ming smiled and nodded, striding out of the room, only saying to Mi Yu and Nalan Caihuan, “Those who are alive, why not feel relaxed and content? There’s no need for guilt.”

At the Summer Retreat Palace, the outside sword cultivators had already returned home. Sword Immortal Qiumiao stood up, saying, “From today, before the Hidden Official returns, Dong Buding and Xu Ning will jointly be responsible for decision-making matters.”

Luo Zhenyi hesitated to speak but ultimately couldn’t say a single word of farewell.

After Qiumiao crossed the threshold, her back to the crowd, she smiled, “I’ll make the first move.”

The armless Yan Ming pinned a seal to his waist and returned to the Sword Qi Great Wall, reestablishing himself at the city walls as a sword cultivator.

The nine-realm female martial artist, Bai Lianshuang, no longer taught the children to punch and kick, leaving the Summer Retreat Palace and returning to Ningfu, tidying up every corner before pausing at the main entrance for a long time, murmuring to herself before heading to the city walls.

The Yuanying sword cultivator Yin Chen left the realm of cultivation for the first time, flying his sword out towards the battlefield, never to return.

In the Wild Continent, dragging a full moon from the sky, he arrived on earth, crashing into the Sword Qi Great Wall.

On the city wall, the old sword immortal Dong Sangeng scoffed, “I go to your mother’s,” then flew his sword towards the moon.

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 796: Breaking the Contract

Standing on the steps, Shuang Jiang watched the young man staggering down, pounding heavily on his chest.

With each punch Chen Ping’an threw, golden light surged from his chest, like a blacksmith wielding a hammer to forge a sword. Each strike sent sparks flying, disrupting the flow of time around him and causing the light surrounding him to twist and fluctuate.

Despite being at a lower elevation, Shuang Jiang could still clearly see those extraordinary golden eyes of Chen Ping'an, even with his gaze lowered.

Chen Ping’an stumbled as he walked, the commotion from his heart was overwhelming. After refining the heart of the divine relic, it felt as if he had moved an entire molten furnace into his chest.

The characters peeled from the Golden Talismans, despite their high grade and the profound truths they contained, melted away in golden light after just one of Chen Ping’an’s punches, dissipating into the air.

“Shouldn’t it take longer to refine successfully? Are you hiding something?” Shuang Jiang asked.

Chen Ping’an remained silent, unwilling to speak, and in truth, unable to do so. He continued to pummel his chest, desperately trying to suppress the drumming sound resonating from his heart.

Shuang Jiang stepped aside to let him pass, walking alongside him. She kept her gaze on the profile of his face, using her divine sense to meticulously examine the inner atmosphere of Chen Ping’an’s microcosm.

Eventually, he stopped, covering his mouth, and coughed up a mouthful of golden blood. He tilted his head slightly, swallowing all the blood before continuing his punches against his chest.

Shuang Jiang felt a pang of anxiety; it was strange, far too strange. Even though Chen Ping’an used two dragon eye fire seeds as a catalyst for his refinement, and was aided by martial luck, the divine relic's heart should not have accepted him so smoothly. According to her calculations, even if he managed to unravel thirty-six thousand threads of fate, he would barely have made it through the small door.

It was akin to a gifted scholar flipping through a sage's text; at first glance, they might grasp the hidden meanings within, but they could never truly understand the deep, essential principles contained therein.

There were only two possibilities: One was that Chen Qingdu had secretly intervened, manifesting his will and drawing upon the entire Sword Qi Great Wall to assist Chen Ping’an in his refinement.

The other was that Chen Ping’an was the reincarnation of a deity with a deep connection to this divine relic, a half legacy, half refinement.

Yet Shuang Jiang felt both possibilities were slim. Chen Qingdu was not one to casually lend a hand. If Chen Ping’an were indeed a reincarnated ancient deity, the disruption caused by the Long Life Bridge in his early years would have left some traces behind, which Shuang Jiang, having traveled through it multiple times, should have noticed.

As time passed, Chen Ping’an’s eyes gradually returned to normal, the golden light slowly fading, and the commotion in his chest lessening.

His punches became lighter, his steps steadier, and his mind more tranquil.

The entire prison began to quiet down as well.

Chen Ping’an turned to ascend, and the white-haired boy had no choice but to follow.

As they passed by prison cells, five great demons of the upper realms and five sword cultivators of the Nascent Soul realm appeared, although no one spoke.

They looked at the young man as one would look at a demon.

When Chen Ping’an reached the entrance of the prison, he sat on the top step. The realm was a duality of day and night, with perpetual daylight outside the prison.

Unable to contain herself, Shuang Jiang asked again, “Old Ancestor Hidden Official, can’t you say anything? If you do, consider it a trade, and I’ll owe you three snowflake coins.”

Earlier, the two had reached an agreement on a trading rule. One snowflake coin equated to one Earth Immortal cultivator. One minor summer coin could be exchanged for the life of a Jade Purity realm cultivator. Once enough coins were gathered, Chen Ping’an could plead with Chen Qingdu to spare this alien demon’s life. Shuang Jiang had everything prepared—spiritual herbs, talismans, and treasures of all sorts. While in this prison, she had accumulated some possessions, but she had always relied on luck. Soon, she would need to take risks to seize opportunities. If she was truly cornered, she would gather everything, including those maids of the executioner, plus the godly texts and that sword pellet from Du Shanyin—all of it would be hers to exchange for currency with the Old Ancestor Hidden Official!

The young Hidden Official had one admirable trait that put Shuang Jiang at ease: once Chen Ping’an made a sincere promise, he would never go back on it. It was more reliable than any vow.

Suddenly, Shuang Jiang burst into laughter, saying, “You speak with conviction, yet you’re being insincere, how amusing.”

Chen Ping’an smiled knowingly, not minding the alien demon's roundabout insults, only saying, “You know I used to run a tavern on the Sword Qi Great Wall, where sword immortals drank without credit. And only three snowflake coins? That’s too much of a loss for this deal.”

Shuang Jiang turned her back, stealthily producing a handkerchief that seemed like a keepsake, gently laying it on the ground, her fingers deftly pulling out a cherished item she had kept for years.

On the handkerchief, ripples trembled as Shuang Jiang conjured a long, narrow knife. Transitioning from holding the hilt to a two-handed grip, she positioned the knife’s sheath against the handkerchief.

It was taller than the childlike appearance of the alien demon.

Shuang Jiang tucked the handkerchief away, stood up, and on tiptoe, pushed the knife slightly out of its sheath. In an instant, it burst forth with radiant brilliance, displaying a spectrum of colors as dazzling as the morning sun.

The hilt was wrapped in delicate golden threads, and the narrow blade featured an exquisitely crafted circular guard. Outside the ring was a series of ancient golden inscriptions, flowing light, clear as the moon, reflecting the water, eternal and unchanging, illuminating the heart and soul. The last two words read, “Slay the Blame.”

After pushing the knife back into its sheath, Shuang Jiang held it with both hands. “How about this? I’ll trade you this knife for the answer from the Old Ancestor Hidden Official.”

Chen Ping’an extended his hand with a smile. “Deal.”

Without hesitation, Shuang Jiang handed the narrow knife to Chen Ping’an.

He gripped the knife across his knee; it felt heavy in his hand. With one hand on the hilt and the other pinching the base, he slowly pushed the knife out of its sheath, focusing intently, but soon pushed it back, recalling the somewhat familiar words “Slay the Blame,” and asked in confusion, “Is this an execution tool from the Ancient Dragon-Slaying Platform?”

Shuang Jiang squatted beside him, nodding. “Indeed! It’s just that it has lost some of its quality before being discarded. It’s probably chopped off quite a few evil dragons and vile serpents’ heads, hence the heavy malevolence. But since the Old Ancestor Hidden Official isn’t afraid of it, I’ll consider this noble blade a gift to a hero! To be fair, while it’s not the best on the Dragon-Slaying Platform, it still competes fiercely among upper realm martial practitioners in the Haoran world.”

Chen Ping’an laughed, “A gift?”

Shuang Jiang immediately slapped her own face, correcting herself, “I meant to sell it!”

With both hands resting on the blade, Chen Ping’an gently said, “The truth is, I’m not even sure about the answer. I’m not lying to you.”

Shuang Jiang felt as if struck by lightning.

Chen Ping’an lifted the narrow knife a few inches. “In my dealings, I’m always honest and fair, so I can’t accept this. Just take it back.”

Both fell silent.

“Give it back, will you?” 

Chen Ping’an lifted the knife slightly, but there was no further response. Shuang Jiang couldn’t just snatch it back, especially seeing the Old Ancestor Hidden Official's demeanor; his fingers tightly gripped the handle, showing no sign of letting go. Shuang Jiang wouldn’t dare say a word of thanks, as any politeness would surely be met with rudeness from him.

Chen Ping’an tossed the narrow knife to the alien demon. “This is for helping me leave a token at the entrance.”

Otherwise, he would have to go to that pavilion naked, encountering that troublesome thread.

Shuang Jiang stood there, cradling the knife, and asked, “Is it really such a trivial matter? Worth trading a knife that’s already in hand for?”

Chen Ping’an extended his hand, smiling. “A minor summer coin. A good omen for starting afresh.”

Shuang Jiang passed the narrow knife to him, overjoyed.

Chen Ping’an stood, fastening the knife to his left side, and walked away without returning to the prison.

Shuang Jiang inquired, “So you plan to step into the Far Travel realm first, then refine your life-bound item, while also tempering your martial luck? Is that why you’re not in such a hurry about the sewing?”

Chen Ping’an shook his head. “Honestly, I haven’t thought that far ahead. With you around, I was intentionally holding back my thoughts earlier.”

Suddenly, Shuang Jiang knelt with both knees, hitting the ground with her fists, lamenting in a flowing manner, “What great sins have I committed!”

Chen Ping’an didn’t find it funny; instead, he felt a deep concern.

The alien demon was free-spirited, unrestrained.

A beam of sword light approached in an instant, hovering not far in front of Chen Ping’an, before darting toward the thatched cottage by the stream.

The executioner was inviting him for a visit?

Chen Ping’an found himself, for the first time, traveling on wind at the eighth realm of martial prowess.

Shuang Jiang whispered beside him, “That sword pellet the executioner delivered to Du Shanyin can also be worth a minor summer coin.”

Both the sword pellet refined by the executioner and the narrow knife just acquired by Chen Ping’an were valuable treasures, but the accounting methods differed in the dealings between him and the alien demon. Inside the prison, opportunities and treasures were abundant; Shuang Jiang’s life at the Ascension realm was even more precious. Chen Ping’an had once heard of a very hidden demonic sect on the Central Divine Continent, which only accepted the most treasured items from others in their trades. This could be the beloved of someone, or even a principle held dear, like someone who cherishes their life must offer up their life in exchange.

Chen Ping’an gracefully descended near the grape trellis, where the executioner, still shrouded in mystery, stood among the verdant foliage, saying, “We’re about to leave here. Say goodbye to the Hidden Official; you may choose one of the two ancestral money incarnations to stay by your side.”

Chen Ping’an replied, “I won’t accept a gift without merit.”

The executioner said, “Staying in this place too long can be stifling. The Hidden Official has demonstrated his martial prowess and refined items; I’ve witnessed a few good shows, so I should offer some gesture of thanks. More importantly, they feel a kinship with you. They’re all willing to serve the Hidden Official, but Du Shanyin will need one of them to assist in her future cultivation; otherwise, you could take them all.”

At the stone table, the laundry maids and the silken attendants looked reluctantly at Chen Ping’an, yet they smiled brightly, their eyes sparkling.

Upon hearing this, Chen Ping’an suddenly understood why this elusive executioner sword immortal seemed to hold a grudge against him.

Money.

For the cultivators in the Haoran world, the vast majority looked at every cave paradise with eyes filled with visions of divine wealth. Especially those oblivious to the greater world beyond, they were seen as worthless by the exiled immortals.

Chen Ping’an couldn’t be bothered to explain; he simply shook his head. “The executioner should keep them close.”

With a swift motion, the executioner used his sleeve to gather the thatched cottage, the stream, the grape trellis, and the white jade table and stone stool, flying away on his sword, with Du Shanyin and the silken maiden following behind.

Only the laundry maid remained, bowing to Chen Ping’an with grace, her demeanor elegant and captivating.

Chen Ping’an didn’t want to be overly sentimental, and he couldn’t just snatch the maid and toss her to the executioner, so he returned her bow, then turned his attention back to the white jade table, softly saying, “Not even a single stool left behind.”

Not even leaving a chance to scavenge.

Accepting gifts and favors inevitably leads to owing debts. Picking up scraps is risky business; one must rely on their abilities to earn money.

The laundry maid, born of golden coins, smiled even more charmingly at his words, softly saying, “I am called Chang Ming, my humble name. If you don’t like it, you may give me another name; I would be most honored.”

Chen Ping’an turned and waved his hand, smiling at her. “Friend Chang Ming, we are of equal standing. To be honest, I do have a place in mind, in the Treasure Bottle Continent, called the Lotus Root Paradise, suitable for you to stay and cultivate. But after you leave the Sword Qi Great Wall, where you go is entirely up to your own desire.”

She blinked, raising a hand to the heavens, and from the scattered remains of the divine corpses, the decayed and colossal bodies began to crumble and break apart. Golden sand, like a continuous thread, gathered around Chang Ming, forming a golden mountain as large as the Dragon-Slaying Cliff of Ningfu.

Shuang Jiang whispered, “This golden mountain, in the Qingming realm, could refine three or four Water Gods or Water Immortal Lords’ golden bodies. In the Hidden Official’s paradise, it’s still just a middle-tier paradise, but it will yield more divine bodies.”

Chen Ping’an struggled to suppress his laughter, ultimately unable to hold it in, cupping his fists. “Alright then, I sincerely invite you, Chang Ming, to visit the Treasure Bottle Continent. At the very least, you would be a registered devotee with minimal constraints.”

The golden sands, polished by the flow of time, slowly adhered to the laundry maid’s garments without a trace of strangeness.

In his heart, Chen Ping’an agreed; wealth should not be flaunted. It was just as it should be. Truly, she was a fellow practitioner. The white-haired boy beside him, who showed off everywhere, could not compare.

Curious, she asked, “Old Ancestor Hidden Official, aren’t you returning home?”

Chen Ping’an smiled. “Not yet.”

She ceased to inquire further, still presenting herself as a maid.

Then, Chen Ping’an wandered alone. Before parting, she reached out, touching her forehead, and produced a golden copper coin, handing it to Chen Ping’an.

Shuang Jiang pulled the laundry maid to search for treasures. They had discussed it; Shuang Jiang initially intended to keep everything she found, of course. What she discovered would be theirs to share, but unexpectedly, that lowly girl, not knowing whose audacity she borrowed, actually wanted a fifty-fifty split. Although her cultivation was negligible, the ancestral coin would still manifest even if she killed her own avatar, and it would appear in Chen Ping’an’s possession. She figured she couldn’t afford to provoke him; with his temperament, he would likely ask Chen Qingdu to end her life over such trivial matters. So, she had to negotiate gently with her, and after much effort, they finally agreed on a forty-sixty split, with Shuang Jiang gaining a slight profit. She felt more exhausted than dealing with a stubborn old man for eighty years. Yet, she didn’t expect that the maid would still be dissatisfied, lamenting that she was truly useless, causing her master to lose a tenth of the profit.

Shuang Jiang nearly knelt down to bow to this lady.

Chen Ping’an arrived at the sea of clouds, where the natural waters nurtured raindrops, lying there with his hands folded on his abdomen, closing his eyes to nourish his spirit.

In the microcosm of his mind, he roamed freely.

Eventually, in the heart lake of his microcosm, he felt a stirring and created a remarkably stable arched bridge.

His true self rested peacefully above the clouds.

In the microcosm, Chen Ping’an stood at one end of the Long Life Bridge. Once he crossed it, on the other side, there would surely be a Qi Refinement realm cultivator added to the world.

The golden little figure riding the fire dragon arrived beside Chen Ping’an’s mind, arms crossed, looking up.

The fire dragon beneath him had thrived after tempering martial luck; if before it was as thin as a chopstick, now it was as thick as an arm, exuding an intimidating aura.

Chen Ping’an softly said, “Don’t start cursing.”

The golden little figure sneered, “Haven’t you been cursing yourself all along? It’s annoying, and I can’t avoid listening.”

Chen Ping’an replied, “They say human strength has its limits, and I believe that, so cursing makes no sense, right?”

The golden little figure said, “You’re afraid of being unable to leave, scared of becoming a second Chen Qingdu, while lacking his abilities. You fear that every action you take will lead to no reward.”

Chen Ping’an jumped a few times, clapped his hands, and performed a set of movements, then exhaled, gazing at the bridge. “It’s only natural for anyone to feel this way; there’s no need to feel embarrassed.”

The golden little figure remained silent for a moment, then used a string of curses to express a sense of comfort.

Hearing the familiar dialect of his hometown, Chen Ping’an instantly felt happy, his eyes clear like the stream back home, with a hint of sorrow like a small fish that flicked its tail and darted into the underwater weeds, never to be seen again.

Ultimately, Chen Ping’an’s mind withdrew from the microcosm. He stood up from the sea of clouds and flew toward the prison entrance.

Crossing the bridge was not an urgent matter; he would wait until the martial luck of the Sword Qi Great Wall and the Wild World were completely refined and integrated into his body’s landscape before proceeding.

His own cave abode was inevitable.

When the cave opened, the microcosm would connect with the greater world. The rich spiritual energy mixed with the sword intent from the prison would surge into various vital energy centers.

However, the pain of flesh and soul might be seen as a terrifying threshold by ordinary lower realm Qi Refiners, but for Chen Ping’an, it wasn’t a significant issue.

As Chen Ping’an passed through the prison, the great demon Yun Qing appeared again, smiling as he joked, “Earlier, you had martial luck at your side, now you’ve refined the divine relics, and soon you’ll be congratulating the Hidden Official again. When you step into the cave realm, there’ll be another round of congratulations. You’re quite busy. Good thing it’s not in the Wild World; otherwise, just the celebration gifts would require three portions.”

Chen Ping’an halted, smiling, “In Haoran, the arrival of a mountain-top celestial being at the upper fifth realm is the best visiting gift.”

Yun Qing glanced at the narrow knife, admiring it. “Good knife.”

Chen Ping’an pressed his palm against the hilt, saying, “It’s hefty enough; it’s indeed a good knife.”

Yun Qing sighed, “It seems there won’t be many more chances to converse with the Hidden Official.”

Chen Ping’an replied solemnly, “It’s a pity we didn’t meet in the Haoran world.”

Yun Qing laughed, “It’s a regret not inviting the Hidden Official for fine wine in the Wild World. My old mountain top has an exquisite view.”

The white-haired boy returned, accompanied by the maid Chang Ming.

The golden sand was easy to come by with her around, but what required more effort from Shuang Jiang were the remnants of the ancient demon corpses, scattered and difficult to gather. Heavenly treasures are often more spiritual; unlike divine relics or massive demon bones that refuse to budge, even with Shuang Jiang putting in great effort to search, it would still be troublesome. Thankfully, that maid, true to her nature as an ancestral coin incarnation, had extraordinary luck and ultimately collected much more than Shuang Jiang had anticipated. Having gained experience, Shuang Jiang deliberately kept her distance, waiting for the maid to stumble upon an opportunity before pouncing on her, diligently capturing those treasures that darted about like flying swords.

They agreed that today they would only scrape the surface in one direction, and in the following days, they would visit one place each day, completing a rough search within the span of ten days, and then thoroughly check for anything missed in the next ten days.

It was the maid’s first time entering this prison, so she was inevitably curious.

The great demon Qing Qiu saw the lovely and graceful maid beside Chen Ping’an, exclaiming, “Old Ancestor Hidden Official, you’re quite the womanizer, but your tastes are peculiar. First, you had a skinned woman, and now you’ve changed to a creature with both flesh and blood lacking substance. What’s the matter, Old Ancestor Hidden Official? Aren’t there seven-tailed fox spirits locked up here? If I remember correctly, there are still a few other female cultivators; isn’t that enough for you?”

Chen Ping’an laughed, “If they’re nearing death, can’t they say a few flattering words?”

The true form of that azure cat demon mocked, “Just you? With that broken knife? Stretch your neck and let me see if you can cut!”

Chen Ping’an pushed the knife out of its sheath slightly, “Want to give it a try?”

The great demon Qing Qiu instantly vanished into the mist.

Shuang Jiang burst into laughter.

The maid Chang Ming took her leave, unwilling to continue wandering in the overly polluted atmosphere of the prison.

Arriving at the thread, Chen Ping’an waited for her to pull out a strand before saying, “I need to borrow your magical knife.”

The thread handed the knife directly to Chen Ping’an.

Upon receiving the knife, Chen Ping’an smiled, saying, “Back in my hometown, when offering scissors or axes, the blade always faces you.”

The thread feigned ignorance, asking, “Have you decided?”

Chen Ping’an nodded and took out the blue talisman paper that bore the characters of the Golden Talismans. Due to the sheer volume and weight of the text, the paper appeared uneven.

He pulled out the narrow knife—the prized possession of the alien demon—and cut into his left palm, staining the entire sheet of talisman paper with blood, faintly laced with golden threads.

Then, with one hand holding the talisman paper and the other gripping the short knife, he pierced his chest, letting the essence blood, akin to true energy, drip from the knife tip onto the paper. Using the water refining technique from the Green Floating Water Temple, he maneuvered the blood droplets, writing with precision, each stroke and dot orderly, the divine meaning rich and full. Ultimately, he “wrote” out a contract dissolution letter, clear and concise in content, yet articulated with precision.

Especially at the end, when signing, he separated a particle of his life spirit from his three souls and seven spirits and infused it into the name “Chen Ping’an.”

Chen Ping’an returned the magical knife to the thread.

The thread frowned, “Had I known, I wouldn’t have revealed this to you.”

Previously, upon first meeting this young Hidden Official, she was puzzled as to why he was so entangled with the dragon family. After some effort, and a chat with the alien demon, she uncovered a shocking secret. Chen Ping’an bore a deeply hidden contract; the two parties were equal in status, neither master nor servant, but their lives were intertwined, the effects akin to the contracts formed between cultivators when they become immortal couples. Of course, Chen Ping’an’s contract didn’t involve any love, and the one writing it had all the advantages, with almost no restrictions.

Chen Ping’an’s face turned pale, yet it seemed he felt a great burden lifted, resolving a significant cause-and-effect grievance.

This was for himself, to find peace of mind, as well as for his student, allowing her to exert her full potential in the Treasure Bottle Continent.

Shuang Jiang squatted beside him, lamenting, “Old Ancestor Hidden Official, you’ve made a huge loss in this transaction. You shouldn’t have been so straightforward; had it been me, I would have squeezed a hefty sum from it.”

Chen Ping’an handed the talisman paper to the alien demon, saying, “If I had known sooner, I would have done this long ago. Shuang Jiang, pass this to the old deaf man; once he leaves the prison, have him send it to Wei Jin at the Snow Temple, to be delivered to someone named Cui Dongshan in the Treasure Bottle Continent.”

Shuang Jiang teased, “Let the thread deliver it to the old deaf man; they’ve just recognized each other as relatives.”

Chen Ping’an smirked slightly, maintaining his posture.

He had known that this alien demon had already recognized the origin of this blue talisman paper.

Years ago, when Chen Ping’an first obtained the “True Records of the Pill Book” and these talismans, he hadn’t yet cultivated and was merely learning to punch, so to him, they were just some yellowed pages. However, at that time, Chen Ping’an could easily identify the rarity of the talisman paper thanks to the amount of talismans he had. One was used up in the Dragon-Slaying Gorge, another given to Zhong Kui in Tongyezhou, and now another was used.

Shuang Jiang raised both hands. “Stop testing me; I promise I won’t touch this talisman paper. If I do, I might accidentally fall into your trap, losing a hundred years of cultivation.”

When the alien demon didn’t address him as ‘Old Ancestor Hidden Official’ or ‘Old Ancestor,’ it often meant she was speaking sincerely.

Eventually, Chen Ping’an handed the talisman paper to the thread.

In a flash, she disappeared to deliver it to the old deaf man, returning almost instantaneously. “Good thing I went early; the old deaf man was just about to leave the prison.”

Some words lingered in the thread’s mind, but she chose not to voice them. Initially, she had wanted to urge Chen Ping’an to hurry with the task of slaying demons and sewing, but the words died on her lips.

Chen Ping’an nodded, heading toward the pavilion alone, sitting with his arms around his knees.

Shuang Jiang stood on the distant steps, watching that building with that person inside.

This place represented the manifestation of the young man’s state of mind.

Thus, Chen Qingdu could go to the pavilion, and even the thread could go if she wished, for deep within Chen Ping’an, he accepted the alien demon as one of his own, but he would never permit this alien demon.

He stood in the pavilion of heaven and earth.

The foundation was made of the principles, both major and minor, that Chen Ping’an sincerely recognized.

The four pillars of the pavilion represented the four fundamental veins he gradually transformed into his own as he traveled through life.

And the pavilion’s peak symbolized the great sword immortal that Chen Ping’an constantly envisioned.

The young man viewed life as a temporary guest at a pavilion, eventually destined to part ways with all, some with farewells, others without a word. 

He remained in place, willing to perform small acts of kindness to shield others from the wind and rain.

The higher the realm, the more separations one would endure. Perhaps that’s why the young man had always held no ambition regarding achieving immortality. While he feared death, he also did not desire to live forever.

Shuang Jiang called out loudly, “Old Ancestor Hidden Official, does that beloved lady of yours know about this contract?”

Chen Ping’an snapped back to reality, feigning calmness. “This contract has nothing to do with me.”

Shuang Jiang leapt high, giving him a thumbs up. “Old Ancestor Hidden Official, you’re quite the bold one, especially for a scholar!”

*(End of Chapter)*

 ### Chapter 797: The Purpose of Hard Training

Frostfall tentatively asked, "What if I exchanged a large piece of gold body fragment for a little story to bind with the Hidden Official Ancestor?" 

The story was not trivial at all.

Just for the matter of the contract dissolution, Chen Ping'an had to use the ancient executioner's sword from the Dragon-Slaying Platform, employing a blue talisman to carry blood, extracting a drop of his heart's essence, and even separating strands from his three souls and seven spirits to infuse them into the signature at the end. 

Ordinary practitioners wouldn't need to make such a fuss to form or dissolve contracts. If she didn't engage in such transactions, Frostfall felt that she might invite divine retribution. 

However, Chen Ping'an wasn't interested in this deal. With that ancestor in the form of the golden coin old man, she could very well serve as a registered offering at Falling Fortune Mountain, which had a treasure-gathering basin. Chen Ping'an felt indifferent to fame and fortune now; he certainly wouldn't be blinded by money. 

Once the executioner left, the old deaf man also departed. All the heavenly materials and earthly treasures here, no matter how many legs they grew, couldn't escape from this prison realm. Chen Ping'an had always wanted to ask the senior sword immortal why he didn't clear out the wealth here and hand it over to the Summer Resort to manage, or move it to the alchemy shop for disposal. Unfortunately, the senior sword immortal never gave him the chance; every time he appeared, Chen Ping'an's fate was not very good. 

Even the mud Buddha had some anger. Why couldn't the Packing Studio open elsewhere? Besides, in the endless future, there might not be an end, so he had to find something to do, like counting money or refining objects.

Chen Ping'an flipped his wrist and summoned the strange five-thunder talisman, cradling it in his palm. Though it was only the size of a jujube pit, it faintly emanated thunder, shimmering with colorful light, creating an imposing atmosphere that naturally overpowered any malevolent spirits or filth.

Similar to the imitation of the white jade capital's pagoda and the sword immortal's banner, Chen Ping'an didn't dare to refine it into his life-bound object directly; he only performed a middle-tier refinement. First, there was no need for heavy refinement, and second, he didn't dare to act recklessly. After all, it was something obtained from Li Zhen, and he worried about what could happen if he acted carelessly. Just like the pine needles and cough thunder, he had only been able to transition from middle-tier to heavy refinement after a long time. 

Of course, it wasn't that he didn't trust Liu Jinglong and Yuan Lingdian; it was just that heavy-refined items were not ordinary. Besides occupying a whole life-bound aperture, they would also siphon off the practitioner's spiritual energy. For a Qi Practitioner of the lower fifth realm, who had not opened many apertures and lacked deep spiritual reserves, these two issues were monumental challenges. 

Now as a fifth realm practitioner, Chen Ping'an actually had quite a few apertures, but just for the sake of the Eternal Life Bridge's five-element refinement, he had to allocate five of them to diligently refine, and how much surplus spiritual energy could he use to "reward his vassals"? This was what they called "a clever housewife can't cook without rice"; otherwise, if he just opened a water residence, then with all the opportunities he gained on his journeys, the little green-clad boys would not be so idle. For example, the replenishment from that bottle of water spirit elixir; every time the water residence faced a long drought, the spiritual energy still needed to be shared with places like the mountain shrine and wooden residence. 

Even with just a middle-tier refinement of this talisman, Chen Ping'an believed that relying solely on this treasure from the mountain, in that small nation under the jurisdiction of the Treasure Bottle Continent, becoming a god-like figure capable of slaying demons and performing miraculous spells would be no problem at all. Moreover, even when traversing the mountains and wilds, he would be regarded as a renowned celestial teacher because practicing the Five Thunder Technique, if the method and principles were not authentic, could easily harm one's internal organs, and over time, lead to irreversible physical damage. For instance, the blind Daoist Jiu Cheng was blinded because he practiced a side technique of thunder. 

Thinking of this, Chen Ping'an couldn't help but chuckle to himself. 

Suddenly, he asked, "Isn't that gold sand?" 

Frostfall pulled out a piece of gold body fragment, about the size of an orange, tossing it lightly. Such a treasure was rare, and mining it took considerable effort. 

With his left hand controlling the five-thunder talisman, Chen Ping'an reached out with his right hand to grab the fragment from the hands of the external celestial demon, clutching it in his palm. After a moment, he used the Three Mountains Refining Technique to refine the gold body fragment into a droplet of golden water, then caught it with his finger, gently applying it to the "Gather" character of the five-thunder talisman, much like how temples and Taoist shrines gild idols. 

During this gilding process, the five life-bound apertures within Chen Ping'an each had a trace of spiritual energy flowing autonomously, as if receiving a command, circulating in his palm and rising to surround the five-thunder talisman. This helped to accelerate the refinement of that droplet of golden water into the talisman, much faster than just gilding using the Refining Objects Immortal Technique. This illustrated the advantage of a practitioner pouring their five-element life-bound objects into the task; the intricate processes were ineffably profound. 

After putting away the talisman and gold body fragment, Chen Ping'an said, "My hometown is in the Li Pearl Cave Heaven. When I was little, on a snowy night, I happened to wake up from a nightmare and then heard some noises at the door, almost as if I heard a faint voice. The wind and snow that night were fierce, so I couldn't hear clearly; it felt quite eerie. At that moment, I hesitated, unsure whether to go out or stay hidden under the covers. I also wondered if Song Jixin might have heard it too; he was bold and would likely go out first." 

At this point, Chen Ping'an suddenly didn't know how to define Zhi Gui. 

Frostfall, who was familiar with Chen Ping'an's various mental processes, revealed the truth, "There are two possibilities why she didn't seek out the prince Song Jixin. One is that she chose to walk into the alley from the west of Mud Bottle Lane, finding it difficult to enter; even though it was just one door away, she was already exhausted, so she collapsed at your door, unable to knock on Song Jixin's courtyard. This is the fateful connection that exists in the universe. The other possibility is that she entered Mud Bottle Lane from Gu Can's house, arrived at Song Jixin's doorstep, and changed her mind at the last moment because, being bound to a dragon of the Great Li Song clan, she had too many restrictions. She might have been forced to sign a genuine master-servant contract, with her life and death in others' hands, which is not a comfortable choice for the last true dragon's remnant in this world. After being saved by you, she secretly formed a contract with you because your life-bound porcelain was shattered, and your spirit was frail; the contract was formed without anyone knowing. She could then enjoy her life in peace, whether standing, sitting, or lying down!" 

Chen Ping'an nodded and said, "That's indeed the case." 

"My Hidden Official Ancestor, how could you engage in such transactions?" 

Frostfall lamented, "You and that girl called Zhi Gui have an equal contract; the more you suffer at the beginning, the more you will enjoy later. What are you thinking, Hidden Official Ancestor? It’s clear that if you just hold on a bit longer and don’t write such a definitive dissolution in the contract, your later years could be smooth sailing! It's as if you are lying down and breaking through, in that Book Lake, how could that ungrateful mud snake of a child that you despise not return the favor to Gu Can’s body and soul? Don’t you know that?" 

The white-haired boy spoke passionately, gesticulating wildly, "No matter what that Prince Zhu did to steal your destiny, the more he achieves, the more he will speak of reciprocity in the world.
