This is a universal truth. So as long as she truly transforms into a dragon, you will be credited for it, and it would be a genuine act of helping a dragon. From now on, you will earn a steady stream of income. Every time she breaks through, she will return benefits to the person she contracted with, forming Golden Pills and nurturing Original Infants; how is that a difficult thing? Just considering the natural superiority over the attributes of the dragon and even the water god lake lord, which practitioner wouldn't yearn for that?" 

Chen Ping'an stood up and began to stroll, smiling, "I only know that when bestowing kindness upon others, one should not expect anything in return. Back then, I didn’t understand the matter of contracts; I only knew that saving her was a casual act." 

The monk's alms-gathering is a form of forming connections. Daoists also believe that every sip and every bite has its destiny.

Frostfall cautiously said, "Hidden Official Ancestor, you are a Confucian disciple. A gentleman bestows kindness without expecting rewards; I can barely understand that. But she has harmed your fortune for many years; are you still willing to repay evil with kindness? Could it be that you have the suspicion of being too kind-hearted?" 

Chen Ping'an shook his head and said, "There are priorities and weights to things. First of all, Zhi Gui is, in my heart, just a neighbor and far less important than the Great Li's situation. Moreover, repaying evil with kindness? You know very well that this is actually contrary to my fundamental teachings. Priorities and severity must be clarified before discussing forgiveness and absolution." 

Chen Ping'an paused for a moment, resting his palm against the hilt of the Dragon-Slaying Executioner's sword, and smiled, "Assuming that the big matter is resolved, how about you let her stand in front of me now?" 

Frostfall felt a headache at the mere mention of "let's try." 

Chen Ping'an continued, "If we set aside right and wrong and conspiracies, just focusing on the matter of me being neighbors with Song Jixin and Zhi Gui, it’s not as bad as you imagine. In fact, I can say that having them living next door gives me some extra hope for survival. At least I know what a good life for common folks looks like; they don’t lack money, and there’s no worry about food and clothing. Have you ever heard the sound of a kitchen knife slicing fish scales on the cutting board, or the sun shining while a wooden stick gently taps on a thick quilt on the bamboo pole? It’s all very pleasant. I never learned to read or write, but I’ve heard plenty of words from books, thanks to Song Jixin's boring recitations." 

In those days, Chen Ping'an was completely in the dark. His thoughts solely revolved around the daily meals, fears of heatstroke in summer, cold in winter, and lacking the festive atmosphere in spring and the worries of insufficient harvests in autumn. 

In dealing with that neighborly master and servant, the boy from Mud Bottle Lane would help whenever possible, such as helping Zhi Gui carry water or drying books on the wall between their two houses. At that time, Song Jixin, as the "illegitimate son of Lord Supervisor Song," seemed to have endless money, as if it fell from the sky, and he spent it without a care. 

The lane was too narrow, and Song Jixin, being someone who enjoyed luxury and avoided trouble, would always just let Zhi Gui buy firewood and charcoal in bulk, solving the problem for the entire winter. 

If Chen Ping'an saw it, he would help too. At that time, it was as if the exhausted Zhi Gui would lift her skirt to run to the house’s door and call for Chen Ping'an to come out to assist. 

Chen Ping'an would never refuse; doing these trivial things wasn’t out of any ulterior motives. To the contrary, it was precisely because he treated everyone around him with respect that he felt it was a matter of course, doing these things would leave his clothes dusty and sooty, but his heart was pure. Moreover, compared to helping the neighbor, Chen Ping'an had done even more for Gu Can’s family. 

Besides, at that time, that grass shoe boy was completely ignorant of matters between men and women. 

So, Song Jixin, a petty and small-minded peer, never suspected that Chen Ping'an had any thoughts about Zhi Gui; he was only sensitive and hostile towards Liu Xianyang and Ma Kuxuan. 

Occasionally, when Zhi Gui was picking vegetables in the neighboring yard, she would also tentatively converse with Chen Ping'an, saying that he had helped the Gu family so much, he should at least ask for some reward, even if it wasn’t money. Her family’s farmland was managed by him, so it was only reasonable to ask for a few sheng (a measure of rice), and if that vixen of a woman didn’t agree, then that would be a problem with her character, always wanting to take advantage of Chen Ping'an. In the small town, there were plenty of opportunities for long-term and short-term labor, helping with joyous and sorrowful occasions, where money could be earned. 

Song Yushao once drunkenly said something while having hot pot; at that time, Chen Ping'an didn’t think much of it. Now, as a man in his thirties, he was no longer a boy from many years ago. 

Upon reflecting carefully, he discerned many aftertastes. It was like drinking a bowl of aged rice wine, with a strong lingering effect that remained in his heart for years. 

In his youth, his memory was sharp. Whenever he thought of home, everything was vividly clear in his mind; his heart would stir, and he felt as if he was back home. 

As he aged, his memories grew hazy; whenever he thought of home, it felt even further away. The helplessness of life probably lay here. 

Frostfall smiled and nodded, "I actually understand quite a bit about the trivialities of life." 

Chen Ping'an teased, "A dignified ascended master knows about these things?" 

According to what it had previously shared with Chen Ping'an about its life story, as a wandering orphan, "Little Grass" had drifted about, always at risk of freezing to death in the frost and snow, and by chance, was taken in by a wealthy family to serve as a servant, later becoming a scribe after being recognized by a hidden tutor in the market, receiving the name Frostfall, thus embarking on the path of cultivation. During this time, it indeed should have learned about many hardships faced by common people. 

But Chen Ping'an didn’t believe its narrative at all. 

Frostfall rubbed its cheeks, "People like me with such a miserable fate in ascended realms are rare, like pitiful worms raised on mud and filth." 

Chen Ping'an nodded, "For a Qi Practitioner of the fifth realm to call an ancestor is indeed unfortunate."

 # Chapter 798: On the Edge of a Blade

A ferry from the Central Lands of the Divine Continent docked at the Upside-Down Mountain under the cover of night. However, it did not unload any cargo. Instead, over a hundred Qi Cultivators disembarked, each exhaling long breaths, all accomplished individuals in their own right, adhering strictly to the rules.

At Chunfan Lodge, Nalan Caihuan and Shao Yunyan personally welcomed them, escorting them all the way to the main entrance. These cultivators belonged to the Yin-Yang School and the Mo Family’s Mechanists, but they would not engage in any bloodshed within the city.

They split into several groups, heading towards the Mirage City, the Summer Resort Palace, and the Winter Retreat Palace, as well as a few private residences of sword immortals. Among these was the Elm Fairy Pavilion, whose foundation was built upon a poetic inscription by a sword immortal. Nearby resided several women dressed as sword cultivators, who had received permission from a temporary "Supervising Officer" from the Hidden Officials to leave the forbidden grounds set by their master. 

Three Golden Core sword cultivators were just about to take flight on their swords towards the city wall. After years of being confined by their master, they had only ever practiced swordsmanship, to the point that they had forgotten to ask for appropriate robes to wear. However, they were stopped by a small girl, who wore a bamboo box on her back and had a small inkstone tied at her waist. She informed them that they could only go to the Mirage City and must return to their residence to continue practicing swordsmanship if they did not comply.

Five Yin-Yang cultivators and Mo Family Mechanists, after receiving a geomancy map and a detailed explanation gifted from the Summer Resort Palace, began to decipher the restrictions of this private residence one by one. The door opened smoothly, and soon a luminous mirror inscribed with the phrase “Clear Moon” appeared above the residence. Within the ancient mirror, four auspicious beasts danced around the knob. Once the formation was activated, the surrounding scenery of the residence was illuminated, revealing every detail.

The group responsible for moving the Elm Fairy Pavilion and this residence consisted of foreign cultivators, who stole glances while watching the small girl confront the three Golden Core sword cultivators. She spoke rapidly, like beans pouring from a bamboo tube. Although the foreign cultivators had picked up some dialect from the Sword Qi Great Wall during their journey, they could only grasp the general meaning; her imposing presence completely overwhelmed the three Earth Immortals.

No amount of reasoning or emotional appeals could sway the three Golden Core sword cultivators. One of them, exasperated, shouted, “Guo Zhujiao! Don’t think that just because Lord Hidden Official is your master, we can’t do anything! We three brothers are at least Golden Cores and your seniors on the path of cultivation…”

In truth, the little girl often came here to sneak over the walls, so both sides were quite familiar with each other.

Guo Zhujiao crossed her arms, her expression stern. “If you dare to go to the city wall, my Hidden Official’s flying swords will arrive even faster, and you’ll be thrown back here by a certain sword immortal. You won’t even get to go to the larger Mirage City.”

One of the more composed Golden Core sword cultivators forced a smile and asked, “Is there really no room for negotiation?”

Guo Zhujiao nodded but added, “There is!”

The three Golden Core sword cultivators, along with the onlooking foreign Qi cultivators, were taken aback.

Guo Zhujiao continued, “As long as you don’t go to the city wall, you can ambush any rogue monsters that cross the wall. But you must not die. If one of you dies, the other two will be confined by a certain sword immortal for a hundred years.”

She pointed toward the Mirage City. “With the Executioner and our Hidden Official’s leader, Sword Immortal Mi, here, there’s no need for you small Golden Cores.”

The three sword cultivators exchanged glances and chuckled. It was certainly better than being mere spectators at the Mirage City.

Guo Zhujiao suddenly added, “Just don’t die.”

Three streaks of sword light flashed and vanished.

The foreign Qi cultivators, who were not low in cultivation, felt heavy-hearted and puzzled. 

How could the sword cultivators of the Sword Qi Great Wall treat their lives and their paths so lightly? While it was not uncommon to die without remorse for the greater good, where were the cultivators who actively sought death when they could avoid it?

Guo Zhujiao turned her gaze back towards the three streaks of sword light, lingering long without pulling her gaze away. 

She feared that, in a moment of impulse, they might rush to the city wall. She thought to herself that if they went, she might as well go with them.

Guo Zhujiao continued to look toward the city wall, secretly searching for her parents' figures, but she could not find them.

Masters, parents, children, partners, ancestors, juniors, friends.

Which sword cultivator from the Sword Qi Great Wall lacked a justifiable reason to slay monsters? Many sword cultivators below the level of sword immortals were willing to kill monsters but were averse to dying. The top sword immortals and the Summer Resort Palace no longer insisted on defending the city. They could retreat if they sensed danger, and if things seemed stable, they could return to the city wall. At present, the scholars and virtuous individuals of the Sword Qi Great Wall had already relinquished their positions and the Hidden Officials' flying swords rarely sent messages to the city wall.

Guo Zhujiao turned back with a smile. “You’ve all worked hard, seniors.”

Upon arriving here, the oppressive sword energy was overwhelming, and the foreign Qi cultivators who had initially expressed some grievances found themselves momentarily at a loss for words when faced with the little girl’s sincere gratitude. After all, they had come to earn a few hard-earned coins. But that was not the most important thing; the key was that their actions would be recorded in the academy, earning them a good deed.

At the Winter Retreat Palace, a group of foreign individuals arrived.

With no one left to teach them martial arts, a dozen children now practiced boxing on their own. According to Jiang Yun’s instructions, aside from practicing stances, they engaged in sparring matches, beating each other to their hearts' content.

When the Qi cultivators passed the training ground, all the children stopped their practice, gazing indifferently at the divine beings of the Sword Qi Great Wall.

The temporary supervising officer of this place, Sword Cultivator Gu Jianlong, did not bother explaining anything to the children. He was disinclined to do so, and besides, if he were to speak a few words of fairness, it might provoke a fight between the two groups, given the age difference. Gu Jianlong had always believed that even with the Hidden Official present, friends like Lin Junbi and Xuan Shen, and the foreign sword cultivators, the Sword Qi Great Wall remained the Sword Qi Great Wall.

At the sword workshop.

Luo Zhenyi sat on a set of steps, eyes closed, nurturing his flying sword.

A young foreign Golden Core cultivator, busy with his elder’s tasks, mustered the courage to speak to the girl, but before he could say anything, she simply said, “You’ve worked hard,” followed by a “Get lost.”

Two statements, one addressing the situation and the other the person.

At the clothing workshop, Wang Xinshui gazed towards the city wall. An elderly foreign cultivator chuckled and asked, “Young brother, may I inquire about your age and cultivation level? I’m genuinely curious.”

Wang Xinshui responded politely, turning to smile. “In the Sword Qi Great Wall, it is nothing worth mentioning.”

Seeing that the old man did not believe him, Wang Xinshui added, “It’s not a modesty statement.”

The old man laughed. “Being able to speak amicably with you, young brother, is already a pleasant surprise on this journey.”

Wei Wenlong had already returned from the Mirage City to Chunfan Lodge. He spoke of the fierce tactics of the king-level monsters, particularly one named Huang Luan, who seemed to have gone mad, smashing many pavilions and towers into the city wall. The small realms meticulously refined by Huang Luan also concealed numerous Earth Immortal monsters. One of them, a monster sword cultivator who shouted “First to cross the city wall, whoever,” was struck by a sword immortal after a certain observatory was destroyed. He barely managed to cross the city wall and fled onto the city’s great formation, only to be struck down by Mi Yu with a single sword, cleaving him in half along with his Golden Core and Nascent Soul, before casually waving his sleeve and disappearing, a fine display of a sword immortal’s charm.

Nalan Caihuan glanced at Wei Wenlong’s adoring expression and retorted, “No matter how good Mi Yu is at embroidering pillows, he’s still at the Jade Purity realm. Dealing with a heavily injured Nascent Soul is more than enough.”

Shao Yunyan asked with a smile, “Who was that ‘whoever’?”

As for this sword immortal, his real combat power was slightly inferior to Mi Yu, and while Shao Yunyan had a decent reputation in the Upside-Down Mountain, Mi Yu was subjected to mockery from Nalan Caihuan, a mere Nascent Soul cultivator, in the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Wei Wenlong shook his head. “I don’t understand the dialect of the barbarian lands. Afterward, Sword Immortal Mi didn’t reveal the opponent’s name, only saying the phrase ‘First to cross the city wall.’”

Shao Yunyan sighed. “Master Yunjian from the Water Spirit Palace should be visiting soon.”

Nalan Caihuan scoffed. “Lord Hidden Official does have good foresight and means. Only cultivators like Yunjian would not treat their own Jade Purity realm as a top-tier realm. If it were other sects’ elders at the top tier, they wouldn’t be so restricted.”

Shao Yunyan, a gentle man who rarely expressed sharpness, finally went toe-to-toe with Nalan Caihuan today, saying, “Yunjian’s heart of Dao is higher than mine.”

Implying that he, Shao Yunyan, was a sword immortal while she was only a Nascent Soul, naturally, that made him superior.

Nalan Caihuan raised an eyebrow. “What does it matter if one has a higher realm and a higher heart of Dao? When it comes to life and death, can Yunjian escape?”

Shao Yunyan smiled back, slowly saying, “So what? It doesn’t prevent her from having a higher heart of Dao than you.”

Wei Wenlong silently cheered for his master, thinking that this “so what” was truly brilliant.

Nalan Caihuan scoffed, “Shao Sword Immortal has spent little time with Lord Hidden Official, yet you’ve learned seven or eight parts of the essence of conversation.”

Shao Yunyan laughed heartily, “I don’t dare claim that.”

But aside from their light banter, when Wei Wenlong faced the accounts on the table, he unknowingly fell into a daze. 

The Water Spirit Palace, one of the four private residences at the Upside-Down Mountain, remained the only one untouched by the Sword Qi Great Wall, and it seemed to be in constant argument with no conclusion in sight.

First, the sect leader of the Rain Dragon Sect visited the Water Spirit Palace but failed to persuade his junior sister Yunjian to abandon her plans to move north. Naturally, Yunjian could not convince her senior sister either. By the time Yunjian made the decision to make her northward relocation public, the Water Spirit Palace, with its many peaks, was rife with contradictions. It was apparent that many had received secret messages from the Ancestor Hall, leading Yunjian to hit a soft wall. As a Jade Purity realm immortal, Yunjian returned to her home peak at the Rain Dragon Sect, only to find dissent among many disciples, especially her direct disciple who had become Dao companions with Fu Ke. She was resolute, stating she wouldn’t leave the Rain Dragon Sect, even if it meant betraying her master’s kindness. This caused Yunjian to grow increasingly weary.

Yunjian could only hide her tracks and quietly visit Chunfan Lodge, taking a seat in the conference hall, where she met Sword Immortal Shao Yunyan and Nalan Caihuan, a Nascent Soul sword cultivator from the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Yunjian was indeed not adept at dealing with others. Arriving with a heavy heart, once seated, she didn’t know how to begin.

Shao Yunyan, unwilling to let the Rain Dragon Sect’s ancestor feel too uncomfortable, took the initiative to say, “Isn’t the Ancestor Hall of the Rain Dragon Sect considering that even if the Sword Qi Great Wall cannot hold, it wouldn’t be too hasty to discuss retreating and relocating later on? After all, the ancestral home of the Rain Dragon Sect is quite a distance from the Upside-Down Mountain. If the situation becomes dire, it wouldn’t be too difficult to gather some important belongings and packages to leave, just like those in the Jianghu. Furthermore, gathering important items and your sect leader’s hidden treasures would be sufficient to ensure the survival of the sect.”

Yunjian nodded lightly, maintaining her silence.

Shao Yunyan continued, “However, if you move now and disrupt the mountain’s foundational water flow, tearing down the grand formation, it would be difficult to restore it later. In any case, there are many difficulties and it’s not worth it to relocate; it’s best to observe the changes. This is what the Ancestor Hall of the Rain Dragon Sect has thoughtfully decided.”

Nalan Caihuan suddenly spoke up, “Shao Sword Immortal underestimates the Rain Dragon Sect’s business acumen. They’ve already begun secretly buying up shopfronts and properties in the Upside-Down Mountain. Well, many who initially wanted to abandon their ancestral businesses are now unwilling to sell.”

Shao Yunyan glanced at Nalan Caihuan, who leaned back against her chair, indicating to him to allow her to remain silent from here on out.

In truth, this wasn’t even harsh language; she hadn’t even uttered the truly piercing words. For example, it was clear that there were influential figures within the Rain Dragon Sect, not just one or two, who were looking to make a larger profit during these turbulent times. It wasn’t just about a piece of land that Yunjian couldn’t shamelessly seize; there were opportunities to carve out a large territory in Tongyezhou as a branch sect.

Shao Yunyan remarked, “At present, it seems that the ancestral home of the Rain Dragon Sect clearly won’t be moving north. The reason there aren’t many sect cultivators willing to follow Yunjian Daoist is not due to their short-sightedness, but rather their shrewd calculations. First, the cultivators who follow Daoist Yunjian northward will all bear the suspicion of splitting the Rain Dragon Sect. Once the Ancestor Hall is enraged, your senior sister can directly issue an order to expel them from the sect and reduce them to a group of mountain and wild cultivators. This is a very real danger close at hand.”

“Secondly, even if they take the risk and move north, where exactly would they go? Where can they find a spirit-rich island like the Rain Dragon Sect’s ancestral home? Would they need to rent land from others? When have the Rain Dragon Sect’s cultivators ever needed to depend on others? If they casually find a place with thin spiritual energy for cultivation, how many years would it set back the future paths of those cultivators who moved north?”

“Lastly, even if they find a barely suitable overseas immortal island, the expenses for building a residence, creating a great formation, and the required rare materials for cultivation would be astronomical. Yunjian Daoist is famously poor at managing finances and has limited resources. Moreover, Yunjian Daoist is known for her ascetic lifestyle and doesn’t enjoy socializing, so her connections are weak. Following such a great cultivator who possesses only the realm and not the means to make a living and wandering away from home is hardly a wise decision.”

Yunjian remained speechless, even sparing the effort to nod.

Nalan Caihuan finally spoke up, “What should we do then?”

Shao Yunyan rubbed his forehead, recognizing that if it were an ordinary top-tier cultivator, they would have stormed away in frustration by now.

Nalan Caihuan glanced at the indecisive upper-tier female cultivator and asked, “Yunjian, how many people can you bring with you?”

Yunjian replied, “Sixty-two people, including three Earth Immortals.”

Nalan Caihuan queried, “That many?”

Yunjian felt embarrassed.

She mistakenly thought that Nalan Caihuan was mocking her again.

Nalan Caihuan abruptly said, “I can lend you all the immortal money I’ve accumulated.”

Shao Yunyan was greatly surprised; it was unexpected for Nalan Caihuan to lend money to Yunjian.

Yunjian was puzzled. “Why would you do that?”

Nalan Caihuan explained, “When the world is in chaos, money on the mountain loses its value, but money in the mountains is worth more. I only have one request.”

Yunjian nodded. “Please, go ahead.”

Nalan Caihuan continued, “If you, Yunjian, one day leave the Rain Dragon Sect and establish your own sect, I will become the sect leader. Rest assured, by then, I will certainly be a sword immortal. If not, and you still cling to your identity as a Rain Dragon Sect cultivator, you will repay the money according to the mountain’s rules after a hundred years.”

Yunjian pondered briefly and nodded. “Then it’s settled!”

Finally, she displayed a bit of the determination expected from a top-tier cultivator.

Shao Yunyan knew that cultivators like Yunjian were naturally suited to sit in high positions but could not be sect leaders.

Nalan Caihuan turned to smile at Shao Yunyan. “If there’s an opportunity, how about becoming the chief supporter?”

Without hesitation, Shao Yunyan replied, “Sure.”

This bond formed at Chunfan Lodge with Nalan Caihuan was anything but ordinary. Shao Yunyan was already a sword immortal with a wide circle of friends, and while Nalan Caihuan was overly shrewd in business and lacked some integrity, she would indeed need someone like her to manage affairs if she were to establish a sect in the Sword Qi Great Wall in the future.

Yunjian felt a sense of relief.

Shao Yunyan had a great reputation at the Upside-Down Mountain. He could not simply be regarded as a Jade Purity realm sword immortal.

Moreover, in times of life and death, one’s true character shines through. Since Chunfan Lodge was willing to be so close to the Sword Qi Great Wall, Shao Yunyan’s true nature was laid bare. Compared to the profit-driven Nalan Caihuan, Yunjian actually trusted Shao Yunyan more in her heart.

Nalan Caihuan said, “I’ve completed my business. Brother Yunyan, you can continue discussing matters.”

Shao Yunyan, unconcerned about Nalan Caihuan’s name change, said to Yunjian, “Lord Hidden Official mentioned that if you encounter obstacles in moving north, there’s a compromise. You can make another trip to the Rain Dragon Sect’s Ancestor Hall, expressing your willingness to personally lead a group of sect disciples on a journey that will take about five years, and then seek a sum of money from your senior sister for the trip, of course, not too much. Besides visiting the Dragon’s Vein Ravine, there are many immortal secret realms to explore, such as Luohua Island and the Creation Cave, where Nascent Soul Qi cultivators can follow along. Furthermore, there will be visits to the Resting Dragon Stone and other places.”

As Shao Yunyan spoke, he smiled, “Lord Hidden Official originally thought you could only take thirty people. Who would have thought it would double, causing a bit of a headache. If sixty-two people leave the Rain Dragon Sect and the Water Spirit Palace together, your senior sister and the entire Ancestor Hall will undoubtedly lose face.”

Yunjian fell into another dilemma.

Nalan Caihuan, unable to bear Yunjian’s naivete any longer, remarked, “What’s the difficulty? You just need to reflect and repent at the Ancestor Hall, saying you’ve abandoned the absurd idea of moving north, and wish to make amends by fulfilling your responsibilities to your sect’s disciples. Then let those who were willing to follow you northward find some appealing reasons to take the intercontinental ferries from the Poshang and Baoping Islands, claiming to go on a journey to visit friends. Just remember to have them leave in batches, discreetly, without attracting attention. Otherwise, with your senior sister’s temperament, once you lead the team on a journey, she could easily imprison them secretly.”

Yunjian nodded lightly.

After settling the hundred-year agreement, Nalan Caihuan looked at Yunjian’s naive and bewildered demeanor and suddenly found her cute. Such a nonchalant great cultivator was less likely to bring trouble to a sect leader. In the immortal mountain ranges of the Sword Qi Great Wall, many sects had fallen to ruin through the actions of their own members. For instance, when a cultivator’s realm ascended to the pinnacle of their sect, ambition could blind them, leading to factional struggles.

Shao Yunyan said, “Mobilizing forces, tearing down houses, and relocating north are merely stopgap measures. The three matters I mentioned earlier were already concerns for Lord Hidden Official. At that time, neither of us had expressed our intentions openly, worrying that Yunjian Daoist might misinterpret our goals. In essence, we only sought to assist you, Yunjian Daoist, in leaving some seeds of cultivation for the Rain Dragon Sect. However, Lord Hidden Official candidly stated that there are no good strategies for relocating; we could only strive to avoid unfavorable outcomes. The next things I mention are what I hope you, Yunjian Daoist, will consider carefully. The so-called journey is merely a pretense; abandoning the northward relocation is the true goal. This way, the Rain Dragon Sect can be at ease in letting you go.”

Shao Yunyan sighed at this point.

Yunjian’s expression was focused. “I implore Sword Immortal Shao to enlighten me.”

Shao Yunyan smiled. “After your travels to Luohua Island and the Creation Cave, you will continue eastward, eventually landing at Tongyezhou. Previously, Lord Hidden Official wrote in the letter, ‘The firewood is in the green hills,’ implying that as long as the green hills remain, there is no worry about firewood. There’s also a deeper meaning that the firewood is on the green hills and not in the water. Afterward, you, Yunjian Daoist, and your disciples will have three choices. The first is to seek out the Great Lord of Taiping Mountain and say that you are friends with ‘Chen Pingan.’”

“Then, you would head north, landing at Old Dragon City, and seek out Fan Junmao of Southern Mount in Baopingzhou, as the Great Liyang Song family is currently digging a great canal. The Rain Dragon Sect’s cultivators are well-versed in water techniques, which can help cultivate their paths while accumulating goodwill. If this matter is accomplished, you can continue your journey northward to Baopingzhou, crossing at the Niujiao Mountain ferry, proceeding to the Bone Marsh, and then taking the Chunlupu ferry. Your destination will be the small Dragon Palace cave heaven in the central area of North Julu, which is jointly owned by the Water Dragon Sect, the Floating Duck Lake, and the Yang family of Yunxia Palace. Among those, the waters of the great canal are stewarded by Li Yuan and the Southern Xun Water Hall’s Madame Shen Lin, both of whom are friends of Lord Hidden Official. You may take residence at one of the Wu Water Islands for cultivation. Even if you borrow it for a hundred years, it would be acceptable. As for where you, Yunjian Daoist, ultimately wish to settle—whether it’s to affiliate with Taiping Mountain or establish a residence by the great canal of Baopingzhou, or remain in the rich waters of the Dragon Palace cave heaven—all depends on fate.”

Shao Yunyan paused for a moment, then said solemnly, “Lord Hidden Official once mentioned that this journey will inevitably be fraught with challenges, and it certainly won’t be smooth sailing. You must pay attention to the emotional changes of your disciples and offer guidance.”

Yunjian glanced at the chair at the head of the conference hall and asked, “I have one last question. I implore Sword Immortal Shao and Daoist Nalan to explain why that Hidden Official is willing to act this way?”

Shao Yunyan chuckled knowingly. “To be honest, I am also curious. Lord Hidden Official’s impression of the Rain Dragon Sect is… quite average.”

Nalan Caihuan spoke frankly, “I dare assert that he is helping others but also helping himself. A young person without enemies cannot achieve such accomplishments and possess such a heart of Dao today!”

Shao Yunyan joked, “Luckily, Wenlong isn’t the type to complain, and Mi Yu is used to being bullied by you. Otherwise, with Lord Hidden Official’s small-mindedness, heh.”

Nalan Caihuan suddenly fixed her gaze on Yunjian.

Yunjian was at a loss for why she would say that.

Nalan Caihuan chuckled, “Your Rain Dragon Sect has many female cultivators.”

Yunjian didn’t understand the basis for her statement.

Nalan Caihuan continued to amuse herself. “Fortunately, Lord Hidden Official, regardless of anything else, has always treated women with respect and distance. The more beautiful they are, the more he avoids them.”

Shao Yunyan, unwilling to let Nalan Caihuan continue with her unfounded remarks, stood up, cupping his fists. “I wish you, Daoist Yunjian, a smooth journey.”

Yunjian stood and returned the gesture, saying, “The kindness of Sword Immortal Shao’s planning and Daoist Nalan’s lending is remembered in my heart.”

After Yunjian left.

Nalan Caihuan and Shao Yunyan walked towards the account room together, and she asked, “Do you know how things are going with Chen Pingan back in his hometown?”

Shao Yunyan shook his head.

He was contemplating one thing: according to the young Hidden Official’s predictions, the likelihood of Yunjian and the Rain Dragon Sect’s cultivators ultimately choosing Tongyezhou was seemingly the smallest, yet in reality, it was the greatest.

The reasoning was simple. Tongyezhou, as a whole, was likely to be shattered, and most immortal forces would be lost. However, the other two islands would still be traversed by Yunjian first.

Nalan Caihuan laughed angrily. “I am neither friend nor foe with Chen Pingan; what you say will not kill me. Don’t forget, we may end up being part of the same mountain in the future.”

Shao Yunyan smiled. “Whether to be friends with Chen Pingan is a matter of personal preference, but as for being enemies, I think we can skip that.”

Shao Yunyan indeed knew quite a bit about Chen Pingan.

Because Shao Yunyan would follow Lu Zhi and Madam Tuo Yan to Southern Poshang Island, and Chen Pingan hoped that once Shao Yunyan arrived there, he would meet Liu Xianyang. Moreover, his direct disciple Wei Wenlong had already been firmly established as a supporter of the Fallen Rock Mountain, so both sides were quite honest with each other. During Chen Pingan’s last visit to Chunfan Lodge, he had shared more insider information about his hometown.

The young Hidden Official, residing in the vast territory of the Great Liyang Dynasty, raised the matter of seeking swords with Zhengyang Mountain. Once one side tore the veil, the Fallen Rock Mountain would become an enemy everywhere, nowhere to hide, and the Zhi Color Peak’s Ancestor Hall could not be moved.

However, if one were to expand the chessboard, Baopingzhou lay between North Julu and Tongyezhou. North Julu had the Bone Marsh and the Pi Ma Sect, the Tai Hui Sword Sect, the Floating Duck Lake, and Chunlupu, among others, while Tongyezhou was presided over by Jiang Shangzhen of the Yu Gui Sect and the Taiping Mountain, which had a promising connection.

The Song family of the Great Liyang had already immersed themselves in achievements and knowledge for over a hundred years, so they would naturally calculate this account carefully, considering the specific gains and losses, deciding whether it was worth acting as a talisman for a Zhengyang Mountain.

Liu Xianyang’s way of seeking swords was certainly viable.

Yet in the depths of Chen Pingan’s heart, he hoped that the mountain-moving ape would one day be hunted down by Zhengyang Mountain’s own hands.

At that time, he would only need to sit in the Ancestor Hall of Zhengyang Mountain, being treated as a guest of honor by a group of so-called sword cultivators. He could drink tea and wine freely, while watching that mountain-moving ape fall into disfavor and isolation.

Seeking swords in his heart.

Of course, directly climbing Zhengyang Mountain to seek swords and behead the mountain-moving ape to throw its head into the Ancestor Hall would also be a satisfying task.

“I won’t lose anything; you can do as you please.”

Arriving at the door of the account room, Nalan Caihuan suddenly said, “Looking at Yunjian’s retreat arrangements, Shao Yunyan, are you afraid?”

Shao Yunyan smiled. “Afraid? Afraid of what?”

Nalan Caihuan shook her head. “It’s nothing.”

---

Above the city wall, Lu Zhi overlooked the battlefield below, where the monsters were clustered like an anthill. This female sword immortal was recuperating, with half her face bloodied and disfigured, too preoccupied by the stalemate of the battle to care.

Moreover, Lu Zhi had never been concerned about her appearance.

Having ventured too far from the city, she had been struck by a powerful technique from the great monster, Heavy Light, as well as a flying sword from Sword Immortal Shouchen.

However, at this moment, within the world’s largest anthill, a tidal wave surged towards the south.

With the flying sword at the forefront, thousands of sword cultivators followed.

On the edge of a blade, the flying sword collided with the monsters first.

Countless monsters were instantly sent flying, splattering limbs and remains everywhere.

This was the sword formation led by the great sword immortals Nalan Shaowei, Yue Qing, and Mi Hu. Those willing to venture out of the city could unleash their swords without restraint.

In the distance stood A Liang, Chen Xi, and Qi Tingji, sword immortals inscribing characters on the city wall, each occupying a corner of the battlefield, forming a triangular formation.

Among them, after Qi Tingji exerted his full strength, each sword energy release left a clearing within a hundred-zhang radius, only to be swarmed by countless monsters.

Aside from the great monsters Huang Luan, Yang Zhi, and Bai Ying, who were responsible for disrupting the city wall, they would occasionally engage in battles with A Liang and the others, with other king-level monsters joining in from time to time.

High above, Dong Sangeng battled a king-level monster that had refined half of the moon spirit, using a great moon as the battlefield, fighting fiercely for an extended period.

Looking up, a clear thin black line was visible on the massive round moon.

From such a distance, one could still see the traces; if one were to enter the great moon, they would need to ride their sword to travel far and witness the sword scars on both ends.

That was the result of a sword strike from Dong Sangeng earlier.

Although Old Deaf was a monster, he was far more straightforward in killing monsters than many sword immortals, combining his massive true form with an imposing Dharma aspect through a unique secret technique, specifically tearing apart the heads and limbs of those colossal monsters, then hurling them as flying swords toward the southern battlefield.

The three teachings’ saints, the old Taoist’s robe, depicted an ancient map of the great mountains, far more than just five peaks.

The old man held a Dao artifact of the Immortal Treasure Realm in the clouds, which was as vast as a giant lake, reflecting scorched earth wherever its light reached.

The Confucian saint took out a scroll of the “Yellow River’s Giant Crossing” from his sleeve, aligning his fingers, gently brushing it open, and the long scroll unfurled, falling from the city wall, suspended between heaven and earth. The waters of the Yellow River come from the sky, crashing the monsters that clung to the city back down to the ground, drowning them in a flood, leaving countless skeletons in an instant.

The bloodied Buddhist saint, covered in golden blood, condensed into ten golden dragons.

This monk severed his fingers, using them as spines for the golden dragons, and with the blood from the severed fingers, he illuminated their eyes.

After severing all ten fingers, the monk clasped his hands gently, bowed his head slightly, and chanted a Buddhist verse.

On the battlefield, Li Cai was fighting alone, sword in hand, surrounded by monsters and magical techniques.

How could he keep killing endlessly? 

Kill again!

If I were to die here today, Jiang Shangzhen, you heartless bastard, remember to shed a few tears when that time comes, just for show!

Thousands of sword cultivators left the city wall, forming a tidal wave formation as the battlefield advanced continuously. Originally a straight line, it gradually became sparse and distorted.

A young sword cultivator named Chen Li followed that line of sword energy, weaving through the battlefield with ease, not lingering in battles, killing those monsters that were injured yet not dead with a single strike. If one strike failed, he would never entangle himself.

The young Chen Li wielded a dull sword, his innate flying sword called “Wu Mi.” That sword was a relic from a sword immortal, and when combined with the flying sword Wu Mi, it could create a miniature celestial realm. Though merely at the Sea Viewing realm, in the heat of battle, he was extraordinarily clever, adept in strategy, and had an almost instinctual grasp of the battlefield dynamics, taking advantage of opportunities and avoiding dangers. He also enjoyed frantically picking up spoils on the battlefield, darting about until he spotted treasure; he was the kind who prioritized wealth over life, earning him the nickname “Little Hidden Official.”

The boy had once left behind bold words on a signboard at that tavern, “The Hundred-Year Sword Immortal, within reach.”

As Chen Li slashed down a hefty monster, he simultaneously ran while wiping the blood from his face. With a roll, he dodged a flying sword from a hidden monster sword cultivator, while controlling his flying sword Wu Mi to fly straight ahead, both avoiding the opponent’s sword without any intent to pursue.

An elderly Golden Core sword cultivator, surrounded by monsters, had nearly lost his sword-holding arm to a monster’s axe, but unexpectedly, a wooden-clad young swordsman intervened, effortlessly severing the head of that monster cultivator. The Golden Core sword cultivator expressed his gratitude, although he had been struck by an axe, it wouldn’t be fatal. However, losing an arm on the battlefield meant he had to retreat for the time being. To his surprise, that sword cultivator tore off his disguise, revealing a faint smile. The Golden Core sword cultivator was stunned, then burst into laughter, “You rascal, the two-palm shopkeeper!” Soon, a sharp pain gripped his heart as the “young hidden official” pierced his heart with a sword energy, shattering the elder’s Golden Core. The figure quickly covered his face again and vanished into another area of the battlefield.

Amidst resting and recuperating, Wei Jin from the Snowy Temple immediately stood up, riding his sword away.

This person was deadly serious.

Otherwise, the future would be endless troubles.

He shared a similar approach to Chen Pingan and Shouchen, both being extremely decisive. Capable of self-preservation while possessing sufficient killing power, having both qualities made strategy and means meaningful. Otherwise, it would be better to strike straightforwardly and directly.

In the heart of the battlefield, a large armored figure rode a steed, holding a long spear that had impaled three sword cultivators.

This great monster, gripping the reins with one hand, spun the horse in place, while the burly armored figure, whose face was obscured by a mask, seemed to be patiently waiting for the sword immortals.

A young sword cultivator was struck down by a monster with a human head and monkey body, its fists hammering through his chest and causing him to plummet, only to have his head crushed underfoot by the monster. The moment the monster lifted its head, it was met with a sword light that exploded its head from afar.

A young female sword cultivator, whose innate flying sword had been shattered, retreated unsteadily. Just as she was caught by a monster rushing from the side, it struck her neck with a fist, tearing off her arm. The monster then chewed on her severed arm, gesturing to the two sword cultivators nearby to rescue her. The girl, covered in blood and struggling to see, glanced at the boys she had grown up with in the distance and then grabbed a broken weapon nearby, stabbing it into her heart.

The monster frowned, discarding the half-chewed arm, and was about to attack those two young sword cultivators when suddenly a punch crushed its body to pieces.

Even in death, it never witnessed the face of that martial woman, only knowing she was a seemingly inconspicuous frail old woman.

At the entrance of the account room, an old man in gray wore a calm expression as he gazed at the battlefield.

Standing beside the old man was the bearded Liu Cha, who asked, “Are we just going to allow the Sword Qi Great Wall to drag this out? Since the opponent has no intention of retreating to the Sword Qi Great Wall, Chen Qingdu clearly intends to abandon the Sword Qi Great Wall while leaving behind a significant number of sword cultivators as seeds.”

The old man in gray chuckled. “Abandon the Sword Qi Great Wall? I would gladly allow it, as long as they leave me this entire Sword Qi Great Wall. Let those sword cultivators go wherever they please; as long as they retreat from here to the Upside-Down Mountain, with the virtue of those Qi cultivators in the Sword Qi Great Wall, they might not even need us to intervene. They could end up fighting each other in the southern Poshang, Fuyun, and Tongyezhou. Unfortunately, Chen Qingdu isn’t foolish. Otherwise, if the sword cultivators of the Sword Qi Great Wall retreat today, the next day, the southern Poshang would retreat, and the day after that, Tongyezhou and Fuyun would follow suit. They might as well retreat back to the Central Lands of the Divine Continent without obstruction.”

Liu Cha said, “According to the messages from the dead soldiers who crossed the city wall, the Sword Qi Great Wall has deployed a significant number of Yin-Yang cultivators and Mo Family Mechanists, intending to elevate the entire city.”

The gray-clad old man nodded. “In that case, it’s a bit troublesome. Based solely on the foundation of the Sword Qi Great Wall’s formations, even with the Mirage City serving as the spearhead of the heavenly sword, and with the help of those sword immortal residences, it still wouldn’t be able to lift the entire city.”

The old man chuckled, “Chen Qingdu’s behavior, would you consider that desperate?”

Liu Cha fell silent.

At the Upside-Down Mountain, the young innkeeper at the Stork’s Nest sat at the door, basking in the sun year after year, finding no new excitement, yet it was still better than being battered by wind and rain.

At the old gate, the young Taoist boy continued to flip through books while the sword-wielding man squatted nearby, grumbling about how fast the boy was flipping the pages.

When the Great Heavenly Lord emerged from seclusion, he received a decree from his master.

The Sword Respect Pavilion had long closed its doors, while the shop at Mi Lu Cliff was still open, albeit desolate and quiet. The Lingzhi Workshop was nearly empty, and the Captive and Release Pavilion no longer saw bustling crowds.

Most of the Rain Dragon Sect’s cultivators still believed that the sky would not fall.

The children of Luohua Island were still pestering the old man with questions about the extraordinary individuals on land.

In the Fifth World, an old scholar urged the most accomplished student in the world to draw his sword more decisively, more forcefully, embodying the spirit of a sword immortal.

At the highest point of Bai Yu Jing in the Azure Underworld, a young Taoist who had just returned from traveling leisurely walked along the railing, cradling a pile of scrolls in his arms. They were all celestial paintings scraped together from various places. Once unfurled, they would immerse him in a spring dream, bursting with colors, featuring women partially veiling their faces with silk fans. There were images of summer relaxation, with a small yellow cat curled up on a rock enjoying the cool. There was also a painting with much blank space depicting a lone boat fishing against the cold river snow, a solitary figure casting a line alongside a straw-coated elder. There were also scenes of a literati in a green robe observing lumberjacks at Taiping Mountain.

In Baopingzhou, at the Ancestor Hall of Fallen Rock Mountain, ripples stirred as a tall woman in white suddenly appeared.

On the peak of the Cloud-Drifting Mountain, the great mountain lord Wei Bo feigned ignorance, closing his eyes once more.

In the backyard of the town’s pharmacy, Old Yang was puffing out clouds of smoke.

In the Sword Qi Great Wall, Chen Pingan, having restrained the innate divine ability of the caged bird, held a bloodied head of a monster sword cultivator. A golden whirlpool appeared where the sword had pierced his heart, yet there were no traces of injury or blood.

Nianxin began preparing to sew, reminding him to be cautious this time as the stitching of his true name was of great importance.

Frostfall squatted nearby, asking the young man who sat cross-legged with his bare back exposed, “Since you are a scholar, Hidden Official, do you have an innate character?”

---

*End of Chapter*

 ### Chapter 799: Where the Sword Does Not Inquire

In the Wind and Snow Temple, the Sword Immortal Wei Jin had finally traced the whereabouts of the green-clad swordsman. However, he was suddenly confronted by a handsome young lord, elegantly adorned with a sword nurturing gourd at his waist. With a swift motion, the young man raised his palm, blocking all of Wei Jin's sword light. He shook his wrist, revealing that his palm, which had turned to charcoal, instantly returned to normal.

This imposing figure, neither too high nor too low in the ancient well, was known as Qinghua.

His exquisitely charming face, captivating to women, was a patchwork of others' features meticulously combined. Inside the gourd, countless remnants of Sword Immortals' souls and broken flying swords were contained.

The great demon Qinghua chuckled at the young swordsman, the first among the hundred sword immortals of the Wildlands, behind him: “Little junior brother, have you had enough fun?”

The green-clad swordsman nodded, “You take care of yourself.”

Qinghua again blocked a distant strike from the Sword Immortal, as Wei Jin launched two successive attacks that surged past him. Qinghua had already been suspended above a massive pit, his voice soft and smiling, “What does my senior brother need to be cautious about? Haven't we yet gone to find Chen Qingdu?”

At that moment, Lu Zhi arrived riding his sword and spoke to Wei Jin: “Continue your pursuit. This effeminate one is mine to handle.”

Qinghua turned to gaze at the scarred face of the female Sword Immortal, “Is this the legendary Lu Da Jianxian from the Sword Qi Great Wall, renowned for her beauty?”

Lu Zhi did not respond verbally, but answered with a sword strike.

On one end of the city wall, a blood-covered monk stood like a golden Buddha, with the Sword Qi Great Wall as his lotus seat.

The middle-aged saint of the Buddhist sect, whose robe had fallen away, gently lifted it into the air with a hand that lacked fingers, causing it to expand like a sea of clouds. In an instant, winds whipped and clouds surged, the robe growing larger and radiating Buddhist light that illuminated the world.

Ultimately, that robe, immense enough to obscure the sun and glowing with brilliant colors, descended and enveloped the battlefield outside the city wall, transforming into countless particles of golden light that attached themselves to the sword cultivators of the Sword Qi Great Wall.

The monk sat cross-legged, and a lotus lamp appeared before him, with a stick of incense burning.

Then, within the timeframe of a single stick of incense, the numerous wounds of the sword cultivators on the battlefield were transferred onto the monk.

In the record of the Sword Immortal's seal, there was an inscription that the young hidden official had copied from the realm of Haoran.

“Buddha of Steady Light descends into the mundane world.”

As the incense was about to burn out, the monk joined his palms in prayer and gazed upward with a smile, passing away unexpectedly.

Yet the light from the lamp before him continued to shine, even brighter than before.

The three saints, including the monk, had been engaged in battle the entire time.

For instance, this Buddhist saint consumed his own life force to alter the heavens and assist the Sword Qi Great Wall in overcoming the Wildlands, collaborating with the other two saints to create a golden river thrice, shaking off the lion’s bugs and severing ten fingers to transform into a golden dragon, shedding his robe to protect the sword cultivators…

Amid the horrific slaughter of the siege, where blood flowed like rivers, along with the Confucian saint's grand diagram of the Yellow River, the crucial Buddhist powers enveloped the battlefield.

Having nurtured his sword for too long, Wu Chengpei finally felt it was time to unleash his life’s sword, the “Ganyin.”

This sword was ranked among the top three in the Sword Spirit Assessment of the Summer Palace.

On the battlefield outside the city wall, thousands of demons were shrouded in a torrential downpour of blood that surged from the earth, instantly stripping flesh and bone. Each droplet, infused with the essence of the sword, slaughtered souls.

The great demon Bai Ying's throne was positioned foremost, but there was still some distance from the battlefields of A Liang, Chen Xi, and Qi Tingji.

Perched atop a throne of dried bones, constructed from hundreds of thousands of skulls, this great demon was devoid of flesh, his white bones shining like jade, yet he still stood upon a severed head.

Upon witnessing Wu Chengpei summon his life sword from the city wall, Bai Ying kicked the head away, stood up, and with great interest, gazed at the descending rain curtain.

Bai Ying's gaze drifted slightly, and on the battlefield, a pitiful little Jade Purity realm sword cultivator had lost an arm and was wielding his sword with one hand. Not only that, but his ankle had also been cleanly severed. Nonetheless, he seemed oblivious to his plight as he navigated through the three sword formations created by Qi Tingji and the others, heading straight toward the throne.

The man halted, facing the throne of bones, raising his long sword. Yet, he did not look at the great demon Bai Ying but fixed his gaze intently on the severed head, declaring, “From the lineage of Dragon Monarch, the sword cultivator Gao Kui, with this final sword, I seek to question the ancestor.”

Bai Ying glanced at the head on the ground and laughed heartily, “I think not. A single slap could easily take you down, allowing your disciples to keep you company in death.”

An empty, gray robe floated down, gently landing upon the throne of bones.

As it appeared, Bai Ying immediately returned to his seat, no longer daring to utter a word.

The gray robe stood at the edge of the throne.

Before them was the young master who was determined to inquire about his final sword.

A hoarse voice rang out, “The Dragon Monarch leads the sword.”

The two thrones of great demons hovered near each other, both resembling women.

The great demon Yang Zhi revealed her true form, her body a dragon with a human head, wearing an imperial crown and draped in a black dragon robe, seated upon a dragon chair with a massive dragon tail trailing on the ground.

Beside her, the great demon known as Fiery Concubine did not reveal her true form. With a youthful appearance and crimson eyes, her robe was woven with thousands of threads, each representing a river she had refined. On her wrist was a bracelet made from the essence of dragon pearls, and her shoes were embroidered, with large black pearls adorning the tips.

Yang Zhi had just retreated from the battlefield and had taken a heavy blow from Qi Tingji’s sword, thus she had to reveal her true form to heal.

In the cultivation of demons, transforming into human form expedited ascension, but for healing, it was necessary to revert to their true form for quicker recovery.

Yang Zhi's expression darkened as she stared at Qi Tingji, who occupied a vast battlefield all by himself. This old sword immortal from the Sword Qi Great Wall bore the appearance of a handsome young man. According to the early predictions from Tuo Yue Mountain, Qi Tingji had a lofty ambition and would not willingly accept death, intending to follow the hidden official Xiao Xian in betraying the Sword Qi Great Wall. At a critical moment, he could deliver a treacherous strike against a certain great sword immortal, similar to how Xiao Xian had struck at his back.

Unexpectedly, Qi Tingji had changed his mind. Logically, this should not have happened. As long as Qi Tingji was willing to leave the Sword Qi Great Wall, only Chen Qingdu could kill him. But once Chen Qingdu chose to strike, the Tuo Yue Mountain’s ancient ancestor would also act, just as he had stood by during the battle at the Jiazi account.

The only explanation was that Chen Qingdu had offered Qi Tingji a better path to enlightenment.

Fiery Concubine hovered beside the dragon chair. Compared to the great demon Yang Zhi, she appeared diminutive. She glanced at the two young men standing on the armrest of the dragon chair and smiled slightly at one of them, then spoke to Yang Zhi in her mind: “You have failed to command the troops well. Do you not feel guilty? Look at Huang Luan; she knows how to be tactful.”

Yang Zhi's expression grew increasingly grim, the massive tail trailing behind her lightly struck the ground, sending tremors across a hundred-foot radius.

Her situation with Huang Luan was currently most dire.

Yang Zhi had once been the sovereign of the Falling River, so there naturally existed a conflict of interests between her and Fiery Concubine. However, under the witness of Tuo Yue Mountain, Yang Zhi had gifted the entire Falling River region to Fiery Concubine.

In exchange, Fiery Concubine needed to assist Yang Zhi in becoming the co-sovereign of the nine continents of Haoran, allowing Yang Zhi to become the mistress of all earthly kings, with authority over the five sacred peaks, earthly incense, life and death of deities, and the flow of martial fortune, all to be dictated by Yang Zhi's words.

Moreover, Yang Zhi also needed to help Fiery Concubine fulfill her greatest wish, which was to devour the last vestige of a true dragon, thus completing her path to enlightenment, allowing all waterway control in the Wildlands and Haoran to fall under Fiery Concubine’s command.

Thus, the two parties transitioned from a life-and-death conflict in the Wildlands to a future of mutual assistance and alliance.

Atop the massive armrest of the dragon chair stood two sword cultivators from the Jiazi account, Yu Si and the young Tan.

Yu Si had only discovered after the ambush that Tan was indeed Yang Zhi's direct disciple.

Tan also just learned that Yu Si was referred to as “young master” by the great demon Fiery Concubine.

After that, the atmosphere in the Jiazi account became somewhat strange.

Except for the wooden clogs, the other colleagues found it increasingly difficult to engage with them calmly. The gazes directed at them were laced with an unmistakable, hard-to-hide fear.

Thus, today, the two sword cultivators had come to this place for a little respite.

Tan remarked, “It seems there has been no sign of Chen Ping'an.”

Yu Si nodded, “That makes it difficult to avenge Liu Bai.”

Dressed in a black robe, Yu Si wore a white ribbon to tie back his hair, creating a striking contrast that made him appear brisk and handsome.

Tan's expression turned somber, “Sister Liu Bai has changed her body; her sword heart is somewhat unstable.”

Kneeling on one knee, Yu Si gazed toward the distant battlefield, “If it were me, I too would find it hard to maintain a clear sword heart.”

Tan gritted his teeth, “I will kill Chen Ping'an!”

Yu Si smiled, “Count me in.”

He turned his gaze to the great demon Fiery Concubine.

She smiled, “Once the rickety fence is broken, I will help find that young hidden official for you.”

Yang Zhi hesitated for a long time, glancing at the city wall where the Confucian saint had summoned the grand diagram of the Yellow River, causing continuous torrents of water to pour onto the battlefield, blocking the demon’s ant-like siege.

She took out a scroll from her sleeve with reluctance.

As the former sovereign of the Falling River, before relinquishing control over that domain, she had first refined three rivers spanning thousands of miles, one of which was the Uncertain River, swarming with bone demons.

Yang Zhi tossed the scroll toward the Sword Qi Great Wall, dodging several flying swords from the sword cultivators. It fell to the ground, and a torrent of the Uncertain River collided with the Yellow River, instantly stirring up waves.

In the preceding battles, the great demon Yao Jia, who had never intervened, lifted his gaze toward the ancient Daoist from the Azure Heaven who was said to be the master of one of the twelve cities in the Baiyu Capital.

The great demon Yao Jia stood upon a mountain that seemed to be hanging upside down, its platform smooth as a mirror, shining brilliantly.

This shattered mountain was compared in size to the mountain seal left in Haoran and was hailed as the Golden Throne of the Wildlands.

Crafted from countless fragments of historical mountains and water deities, it required iron chains made from demon bones to connect these various shards of golden stone, with the surface of the platform resembling the largest golden coin in the world.

Clad in a golden robe, the great demon Yao Jia, within this throne, did not intentionally employ illusions but was still enveloped in light as if overshadowed by the sun, his true form concealed.

Yao Jia, positioned at the center of the mirrored platform, swiftly navigated the mountain beneath him toward the battlefield, directly confronting the overwhelming power of the sun reflected from the old Daoist holding the multi-treasure mirror.

Previously, the old Daoist had utilized the multi-treasure mirror to connect with the sun of the Wildlands, targeting a demon soldier from the Jade Purity realm, burning away its resilient form while employing immobilization techniques. Ultimately, it was the top ten peak sword immortal candidate, Yue Qing, who severed the demon's head with the treasured sword “Xiong Zhen Wu Yue,” pulverizing its body and restraining its fleeing primordial spirit with his life swords “Bai Zhang Quan” and “Yun Que Zai Tian.”

Having earned a brief moment of respite, Yue Qing surveyed his surroundings. No demons were involved in this fierce battle, and he stood atop a demon's head, gently shaking his wrist to scatter the blood that remained on his sword.

Satisfying.

The great sword immortal, with his back to the Sword Qi Great Wall, raised his arm and forcefully shook it.

Yue Qing advanced southward.

This highly lethal sword immortal had previously scoffed at the incense of the Confucian lineage and had proactively sought out the young hidden official to express his gratitude and apologies in person.

He was straightforward.

The old Daoist nodded slightly, acknowledging Yue Qing's politeness.

Then, he frowned as he adjusted the angle of the multi-treasure mirror several times, still pulling the light toward the Golden Throne. The old Daoist sighed internally, realizing that his level of cultivation was no longer peak and feeling helpless.

The golden throne beneath Yao Jia was inundated with the molten gold from the multi-treasure mirror, constantly overflowing and splashing out, as fast as flying swords. Whether sword cultivators or demons, anyone touched by it would instantly disintegrate, meeting a deadly end.

Yao Jia inquired, “Old Daoist, you clearly still have much life to live, yet you choose to perish here. Is it for enjoyment?”

This esteemed old Daoist from the Azure Heaven, holding two essential life items, had cracks appearing on the mirror's surface like a spider web. With every new fissure, the old Daoist, who had once embodied purity, would lose a thread of his vitality, visibly consuming his life force, while his whisk had been largely destroyed, leaving only the handle.

The old Daoist raised one hand with the mirror aloft and stroked his beard, smiling, “Enjoyment? You old hag!”

He spoke the coarsest words with the demeanor of a venerable immortal.

It was hard to imagine that this was the same man who once remarked, “When the peach blossoms bloom, if a yellow oriole still adorns the flowers, it is particularly enchanting; one cannot dare look, yet the heart stirs.”

Moreover, it was unimaginable that when the old Daoist preached in his own city of Baiyu Capital, many high-ranking true immortals from other cities would sit on cushions, sharing knowing glances.

Yao Jia paid it no mind and ceased to speak.

The two sides continued to exhaust themselves, consuming the fragments of divine beings while this old Daoist was hastily depleting his own life force.

This notable achievement in slaying one of the three saints of the Sword Qi Great Wall would be a triumph for me, Yao Jia, to claim.

According to the contract, Tuo Yue Mountain had promised to deliver an entire continent of Haoran to the Sword Qi Great Wall, where all Confucian academies, royal decrees, and the divine figures of mountains and waters would be fused into one, leaving none alive.

Particularly since it was heard that many ancient deities had reincarnated in Haoran, this was crucial for Yao Jia’s path to enlightenment. By refining them all, he could attain the sun suspended in the sky, assuming the form of a supreme deity, gazing down upon all beings and achieving true immortality. Regardless of the flow of the Dao, the so-called heavenly net would have to make way for him!

The great demon extended a hand, slowly raising it. On the outer edge of the mirror appeared a series of golden inscriptions, each word immense. Every golden character transformed into a colossal divine being several tens of feet tall. Among them, the characters for sun and moon served as the eye of the formation, with the manifested divine beings towering over a hundred feet, particularly those born from the characters “sun and moon,” adorned with halos of radiance, with golden streams drifting about, reminiscent of celestial garments in water and land murals.

Suddenly, the old Daoist stood up and laughed heartily, “In the future, if any sword cultivator travels to the Azure Heaven, remember to come visit the poor Daoist in my city! The scenery is exquisite, and the fairies are beautiful! Spending years with you all has been delightful!”

After this declaration, the old Daoist's body dissolved into his spirit, ultimately transforming into a dazzling rainbow light, first heading into the suspended multi-treasure mirror, and then bursting forth, directly colliding with the Golden Throne.

Even Yao Jia, the great demon, could not maneuver the throne to evade the rainbow light, having to watch helplessly as the old Daoist's spirit and intent dissolved into the Golden Throne.

Then, across the entire mirror's surface, a fissure appeared that the old Daoist had forcibly torn through with his spirit, and his final true words were merely three characters:

“Drop the Sword.”

The great sword immortal Mi He struck forcefully with his sword along the fissure, cleaving the entire Golden Throne in two.

After this battle, the great demon Yao Jia, whose life items were damaged, had to withdraw from the battlefield, exerting all efforts to repair the heavily damaged Golden Mountain.

At the entrance of the Jiazi account.

A burly man stood side by side with an old man in gray.

Liu Cha remarked, “Chen Xi and Nalan Shao Wei seem a bit off.”

They shouldn't be fighting so desperately, not to the point of sacrificing their lives.

The gray-clad elder nodded.

In contrast, Qi Tingji, the old deaf man, appeared quite normal, showing fierce strikes on the battlefield while still leaving himself an escape route, at worst losing a realm.

However, both Chen Xi and that Nalan Shao Wei, the family heads of the Taixiang Street aristocracy, were charging toward a dead end.

As for Dong Sangeng…

The old man glanced at the distant moon, high in the sky, believing that Dong Sangeng did not intend to return to the city wall. Moreover, when this person ultimately fell, it would surely be a grand spectacle.

Despite the division between enemies and allies, the gray-clad old man couldn't help but feel regret for Dong Sangeng.

Such a hero.

As for the fate of the Lotus Blossom Temple's master, the gray-clad old man did not care. Carrying the burden of Tuo Yue Mountain, the unauthorized refining of half a moon's essence was a transgressive act that deserved death. Now facing Dong Sangeng, he had the advantage of timing and geography, yet it was still a cage.

Liu Cha asked, “According to the latest predictions from the Jiazi account, is the Confucian Temple planning to hand over half of the world to the sword cultivators of the Sword Qi Great Wall?”

The gray-clad elder nodded, “A grand gesture indeed.”

That young hidden official, with an extremely utilitarian strategy, had aided the Sword Qi Great Wall in regaining its breath, while also being forced into a corner for years, allowing the sword cultivators to vent their frustrations. That fellow who had fallen from the sky, making a trip to the Azure Heaven and then returning, further alleviated the pent-up resentment among the sword cultivators.

The Confucian lineage had saints stationed here. The Sub-saint lineage had A Liang, the refined Chen Chuan'an. The Literary Sage lineage had great sword immortals on either side, including the hidden official Chen Ping'an.

These scholars who traveled from afar were all reasoning in their own ways, prompting the Confucian Temple of Haoran to agree to this matter.

On the battlefield, Li Cai halted.

A hundred feet away, a celestial figure emerged, the great demon Huang Luan.

This great demon passed through the ranks of the demon army and directly approached the deeply embedded Li Cai.

Huang Luan smiled, “You are Li Cai? I heard you bought that Tingyun Pavilion. How fortunate, it is already mine. Sheathe your sword and kneel, and I shall spare your life.”

After a brief silence, Huang Luan narrowed her eyes and said, “Well, the term ‘servant’ doesn't sound appealing for a female sword immortal. Let’s call you a sword attendant instead.”

Along with Li Cai, the entire Tingyun Pavilion, crafted from pure jade, included numerous relics left by sword immortals, such as the Sounding Pines Retreat, the Xu Xian Pavilion, and the Jia Zang Armory. All of these should have been her spoils of war.

At this moment, Li Cai was covered in wounds, though mostly concealed by her robe. It was evident that her cheekbones had been shattered by a demon warrior, leaving her skin raw and bones exposed.

Li Cai coughed up a mouthful of blood, tugged at her lips, and forced a smile, “You know I bought Tingyun Pavilion?”

Huang Luan nodded, “There are indeed some sword cultivators who fear death and cherish their lives.”

Li Cai sheathed her sword, her movements swift, and the sword intent surged, creating ripples that spread outward. In an instant, the demon army rushing toward her and Huang Luan lost countless heads.

Huang Luan’s fingers came together, and with a gentle shake, she dissipated the invisible sword essence, “Since you’ve reached your limit, there’s no need to put on a show.”

Li Cai asked, “Do you not know that even if you go to Tongye Continent, you will be pierced by a sword?”

Huang Luan chuckled in surprise, “My mood isn’t very good right now.”

Originally, Huang Luan held a position of authority among the sword cultivators in the Wildlands and was clearly someone favored by the gray-clad elder from Tuo Yue Mountain.

On one hand, she held a transcendent status among the demons, rarely at odds with other great demons. On the other, when she ventured to the Haoran world, what she sought were those so-called useless items that held little value. Moreover, Huang Luan herself had no great ambitions. In the words of another great demon, Huang Luan coming to Haoran was akin to collecting scrap.

Thus, Tuo Yue Mountain entrusted this significant campaign to Huang Luan to oversee.

However, this battle, likely unparalleled in history, was originally intended to be a tumultuous clash, with tens of thousands of sword cultivators clashing in a grand scale, but the Wildlands failed to overpower the Sword Qi Great Wall and suffered heavier losses than anticipated.

This led to Huang Luan and the great demon Yang Zhi having no choice but to cut through the backlines of the Wildlands to eliminate those trying to aid the Sword Qi Great Wall, thus making up for their failures.

Not only that, but Huang Luan also had to hurl half of her painstakingly refined treasures, including pavilions and towers, toward the Sword Qi Great Wall.

It was evident that the gray-clad elder from the Jiazi account was quite displeased with Huang Luan's performance.

Li Cai glanced back and realized she had unknowingly drifted somewhat far from the Sword Qi Great Wall.

Clearly, her swordsmanship was quite impressive!

Huang Luan declared, “This is your last chance to survive.”

Li Cai thrust out a sword.

Huang Luan reached out to grasp the sword light, forcibly breaking it. The splintered sword light sprayed forth, leaving not a scratch on Huang Luan.

Li Cai bent down, darting forward, and in an instant, drew her sword from its sheath.

Huang Luan’s robe billowed as she unfurled her power.

The small world around them turned entirely white.

Li Cai's desperate final sword strike, driven to its peak, merely broke through Huang Luan's little world.

Huang Luan was indeed correct; Li Cai was at her last gasp.

Unable to draw a second sword, Li Cai retreated, spitting blood.

Huang Luan ignored the girl's pitiful state, raised a slightly torn sleeve, and gazed at her with some regret, then looked up with a smile, “Your sword intent is quite impressive. No wonder you’re a sword cultivator from the North Ju Lu Continent. I will definitely take you as my sword attendant. After capturing you, I will have Bai Ying help refine your soul anew. In the future, when we reach Tongye Continent, you can see if anyone can pierce me with a single sword…”

As her words lingered, Huang Luan pressed down with one hand.

In the blink of an eye, a massive vortex appeared in the sky, and a building the size of a mountain came crashing down toward Li Cai.

Just as Li Cai was about to draw her sword, she noticed an old man had already arrived beside her. He uttered a word of apology and pulled Li Cai back while simultaneously throwing his sword toward the building.

The long sword and sword light shot straight up, bracing against the building, as if single-handedly supporting a precarious structure.

Yao Chongdao, whose courtesy name was Lian Yun, perhaps cherished the phrase “Lian Yun” so much that he named both his longsword and life sword “Lian Yun,” a celestial being.

Before arriving here, the old man had exchanged a sword with the demon sword immortal, who had since retreated from the battlefield.

Huang Luan sighed, “I’m really not interested in military achievements. You're gravely injured; why come here to seek death? However, a free head thrown my way can’t be ignored.”

Above that building, another formidable structure descended, stacking upon the first. The “Lian Yun” sword light soared toward the sky, bending slightly under the pressure.

Huang Luan was using the losses of the mid-refined items in exchange for the wear and tear of Yao Chongdao's great refined items, and she saw no reason to hesitate.

Huang Luan's mind shifted, and a succession of celestial residences crashed down, causing the sword light “Lian Yun” to bend at its tip.

However, the old man's life sword had yet to make its appearance.

Huang Luan was curious to see if this injured Yao Chongdao could unleash a surprising move.

As Li Cai was about to rejoin the battlefield, the old man shouted, “Li Cai! It’s not that I look down on women; it’s that I look down on you, a Jade Purity realm. Retreat!”

Li Cai could only curse and decisively abandon her charge.

Huang Luan gazed up at the brilliant sword light that had already pierced through the building, laughing, “I initially thought you were merely sacrificing a long sword to save yourself. Fine, since you’ve made up your mind to waste your life, let it be your wish. Killing an immortal from the Sword Qi Great Wall can make up for your transgressions.”

The old man, donned in a robe of the Sword Qi Great Wall, his sleeves billowing, suddenly inquired, “Do you recognize my granddaughter-in-law?”

Li Cai, not wishing to complicate matters or distract Yao Chongdao, nonetheless did not want to retreat just yet. She created some distance while nurturing her flying sword.

After hearing the question, she nodded, “I know her, quite well.”

Yao Chongdao hesitated for a moment before saying, “Then please inform that young man that there’s no need to come to our house to propose marriage. I’m not concerned about it.”

Li Cai was speechless.

This Yao Great Sword Immortal was clearly not indifferent, but it was impossible for him to drag that fellow by the collar to propose marriage to the Yao family.

Li Cai had wanted to mention her direct disciple, who had been smitten with that fellow, but the words lingered on her lips, and she ultimately held back.

Li Cai said, “Senior Yao, I can switch places with you. There might be a chance to retreat together.”

Yao Chongdao could not be bothered to expose the true thoughts of this girl from the North Ju Lu Continent. She was still young; what was the point of dying here?

Yet the old man smiled, “You shouldn’t underestimate the hidden abilities of a great demon. If a little girl like you were to die alongside a decrepit old man, it would seem like a love sacrifice. What kind of nonsense is that?”

The old man lightly leaped, sitting cross-legged, clouds billowing beneath him.

He stacked his hands over his abdomen, and mist began to rise, slowly manifesting a small, pure white flying sword.

Huang Luan remained composed, observing that Yao Chongdao's life sword was suitable for large-scale battles, akin to Wu Chengpei's “Ganyin” and Yue Qing's “Yun Que Zai Tian,” focused not on one-on-one combat.

Huang Luan gently exhaled a breath of multi-colored mist, vanishing in an instant without any grand display.

However, it sent chills down Li Cai's spine, who was quite a distance away from the battle.

Any great demon held within them the essence of time. Over prolonged periods, Huang Luan had refined over a hundred life items, continuously excavating and replacing until she possessed two celestial weapons and three half-celestial weapons.

As for those seemingly magnificent treasures, aside from three of them, the rest were merely mid-refined items, a hobby she indulged in to relieve stress.

Yao Chongdao spoke to himself, “Ning girl, from now on, you will be in charge of protecting. Don’t think that just because Ning girl is strong, you won’t protect her. What good man in the world doesn’t protect the woman he loves? If you can hold back Ning girl and help her escape the city to face Li Zhen, that’s wonderful. If you win against Li Zhen, even better.”

“So there’s nothing to worry about; I’m quite at ease.”

In an instant, the old man's forehead, temples, neck, heart, and abdomen seemed to be pierced by five colored flying swords.

Once pierced, his bones, flesh, soul, and sword intent were crazily drained through those five unremarkable holes.

Clearly, Huang Luan was displeased with Yao Chongdao’s sword light destroying too many structures.
